Tests (`test/sessions.test.js`): the #557 regression pin (oversized contract + continuity index + template cap → Resume guard, wrap sentinel, identity, and honest trim note all present; blind slice must not fire; verified failing pre-fix), budget-floor omission, no-cap full embed, event-driven guard line.

## [4.17.0] - 2026-07-13

### Added

- **Banner loop view + force-done — live loop observability lands in the session banner (MED-2K9P v2 Slice 1, chunk T4 — closes the TC side of Slice 1).** A new **⟳ loops chip** appears beside the ➤ launch button whenever the session knows of any loop; its **text carries the live status** (single live loop → `R{round}/{maxRounds}`, several → live count, none → ended count — never color-only), and the Medusa mark gains an ambient **live-loop glow** (suppressed under `prefers-reduced-motion`; the chip text is the surviving cue). Clicking the chip opens the **loops panel**: one row per loop — counterpart + direction, mode, honest state label, round count — plus a **force-done** kill-switch and an expandable **transcript**. Loop data rides the existing status poll (no new timer): `GET .../medusa/status` now returns `loops` via new `medusa.getLoops` (`lib/medusa.js`), with TC-side discovery because the Bridge exposes no `GET /loops` list — `openLoop` records ids, inbound loop-tagged messages re-learn them (the target side's only path), a Bridge 404 self-heals by untracking, and a mid-poll Bridge failure degrades to `loops: [] + loopsError`, never a silently-empty list. **Force-done** (`POST .../medusa/loops/:loopId/force-done` → `medusa.forceDoneLoop`) rides the contract's initiator-only close with a structured `closeSignal.reason: 'force-done'` — pinned against Bridge source: no external `halted` transition exists (that state is reserved for the server's own runaway guards), so the loop lands in `complete` with the reason recorded and the UI labels it "ended by force-done" from the closeSignal — honest, no fake "halted". Guard semantics surface both ways: a guard-halted loop shows "halted by guard — cannot be closed" (the Bridge's 400 passes through verbatim) and force-done is initiator-side only (Bridge 403 enforced + UI-gated). The **transcript is labeled for what it honestly is** — the rounds THIS session observed (opening task + inbound loop-tagged inbox messages); the Bridge retains no full round history (upstream feature filed). All Bridge-supplied text is `esc()`d (cross-session data is untrusted). `CACHE_NAME` v3-43 → v3-44. Tests: `getLoops` discovery/re-learn/404-untrack/sort + `forceDoneLoop` honest-close/guard-halted/initiator-only/unknown-loop matrix, status-with-loops + force-done routes against the fake Bridge's new stateful loop store (`test/api-medusa.test.js`); loop-view source-probes — XSS guard on every Bridge field, honest state labels, reduced-motion suppression, no-new-timer, delegation wiring (`test/medusa-control.test.js`).

### Fixed

- **TC server restart no longer silently drops every live session's switchboard listener (TC#550).** Listeners are in-memory and were started only at launch or via toggle/PATCH, so a TC restart deregistered every running session from the Bridge — the whole switchboard went dark until each session was relaunched or manually re-toggled (the TC#549 PATCH-sync was the manual heal, used twice on 2026-07-13). Server boot now runs `sessions.resyncMedusaListeners()` (`lib/sessions.js`, wired in `server.js` `onListening`): every live session whose project has `medusaEnabled` gets its listener re-started under the same predicate as launch, reusing the persisted registry workspace id (identity stable across the restart), non-throwing per project so one broken record never blocks the sweep — and with ACK-on-read (TC#547) the re-register redelivers only genuinely-unread mail. Tests: opt-in-only re-sync, id stability, idempotency, broken-project isolation, boot-wiring source pin (`test/api-medusa.test.js`).

### Changed

- **`openLoop` drops its out-of-band task notice — the Bridge's server-side loop invite supersedes it (TC#552).** Medusa#47 (loop open never notified the target — deadlock-by-design) was fixed upstream in Medusa PR #48: `POST /loops` now durably enqueues a full `loopInvite` to the target (pushed live over WS when online). TC's paired direct-message workaround therefore DOUBLE-notified every target and is removed (`lib/medusa.js`, with the `TASK_DELIVERY_FAILED` orphaned-loop path it existed to guard); the route response loses `taskDelivery`, and the launch toast now claims exactly what the contract guarantees — the Bridge delivers the invite (its open response reports no live-vs-queued, so the UI invents neither). `api-notes-medusa.md` T3 section marked superseded.

## [4.16.0] - 2026-07-13

### Added

- **Loop setup modal — launching a bounded agent-to-agent loop replaces the manual compose box (MED-2K9P v2 Slice 1, chunk T3).** The banner ➤ now opens a **Session Loop modal** (`public/session.{html,js,css}`; the compose popover is gone per the T3 acceptance, its send *plumbing* retained as the loop transport): pick a target from the live roster (self excluded, `(offline)` annotated, honest loading/error/empty states — a failed roster fetch is never disguised as "nobody home"), state the **task** and the **done criteria** the initiator will judge against, choose the **judge mode** (supervised default / autonomous — both selectable from the start per the ratified §8 decision), and set the **runaway guards**: max rounds + max minutes (converted to the contract's `maxWallTimeSeconds`). Only the two guards the Bridge actually *enforces* are offered — an unenforced token knob would be a dishonest control (deferred until Medusa enforces one). Launch calls new endpoint `POST /api/sessions/:project/medusa/loop` → `medusa.openLoop` (`lib/medusa.js`, `server.js`), which creates the Medusa loop object (`POST /loops`, initiator = the session's registered workspace id) **and delivers the task notice to the target as a direct message naming the loop id + how to respond** — live-probed 2026-07-13: the Bridge does NOT notify the target on loop open and bars the initiator from posting round 1, so without this out-of-band delivery a fresh loop deadlocks (filed upstream as Medusa#47; when loop-open delivers server-side this step drops). Results are honest end-to-end: task `delivered` vs `queued` (offline target) are distinct outcomes, a launch failure keeps the modal + form input intact with the real error, and a created-but-undelivered loop error names the orphaned loop id. `CACHE_NAME` v3-42 → v3-43 (exact-pin test in `test/openclaw-bridge-port-row.test.js` converted to the ≥-generation pattern — the exact pin snapped on every legitimate bump). Tests: `openLoop` validation/defaults/honest-failure matrix + route wiring against the fake Bridge's new `/loops` (`test/api-medusa.test.js`), loop-modal source-probes carrying over every compose-era security/honesty pin — roster-name `esc()` XSS guard, no-new-timer, off-state gating, compose-box-gone (`test/medusa-control.test.js`).

- **Project Medusa toggle now takes effect on the LIVE session (TC#549).** Flipping `medusaEnabled` in project settings previously only registered the session at its *next launch* — an already-running session stayed invisible in every other session's switchboard roster with no signal why (live-confirmed on two running sessions, 2026-07-13). `projects.updateProject` now syncs the flip immediately via new `_syncLiveMedusaListener` (`lib/projects.js`): ON starts the active session's listener (registers the workspace with the Bridge), OFF stops it (deregisters); no active session is a clean no-op, and a listener failure never fails the PATCH (the pref persists; the listener's own honest status carries any Bridge trouble). Tests: OFF→ON registers / ON→OFF stops a live session, no-session flip persists cleanly (`test/api-medusa.test.js`).

### Fixed

- **Switchboard listener now ACKs read messages — TC restarts no longer re-flood handled mail as fresh unread (TC#547).** Medusa's at-least-once retention (Medusa#46) keeps every delivered message queued Hub-side until ACK'd; TC's listener never ACK'd, so each reconnect/restart redelivered the entire handled inbox → stale unread badges and stale wake nudges (bit this session's own coordinator inbox on 2026-07-12). The listener now ACKs **on read, not receipt** (`lib/medusa-listener.js`): `markRead` sends one WS `ack` frame for every read envelope id, ids stay in an awaiting set until the Hub's `ack_response` confirms (never confirmed-by-assumption), and unconfirmed ACKs re-flush on the next `registered` handshake — a lost ACK frame degrades to a redundant retry while the existing `messageId` de-dup keeps the redelivered copies out of the inbox and off the badge. A message received but never read intentionally stays queued Hub-side and honestly redelivers after a crash. Tests: no-ack-on-receipt, batch ack-on-read, confirmed-ack multi-hop (markRead → reconnect), lost-frame re-flush with no re-badge, failed `ack_response` retry, id-less messages (`test/medusa-listener.test.js`).

## [4.15.0] - 2026-07-12

### Added

- **Medusa contract injection at launch — an opted-in session now boots knowing how to participate in the switchboard (MED-2K9P v2 Slice 1, chunk T1, closes Round 1).** The prime prompt of a `medusaEnabled` project carries a new "Medusa Switchboard" section with the three things design §3 says an LLM needs to participate natively ("the agent is the client"): **(1) the consumer contract** — Medusa's public `docs/CONSUMER-CONTRACT.md` embedded in full, resolved at launch via `MEDUSA_CONTRACT_PATH` env override → the registered Medusa project's checkout (`lib/medusa.js#readContract`); an unresolvable contract injects an honest UNAVAILABLE note naming every path tried, never a silent omission; **(2) its workspace identity** — the exact id the listener registers under, guaranteed by pre-minting: `launchSession` mints the id before the prime is generated (`medusa.mintWorkspaceId`, unpersisted) and threads it through `_maybeAutoStartMedusa` → `startSession({workspaceId})` → `registry.ensureWorkspaceId(..., preferredId)`, which adopts it (and supersedes stale debris under a recycled session id) so prime and listener can never diverge; **(3) the participant role** — act on inbox messages and reply until the initiator closes (initiator-only termination, per the ratified loop model), plus the division-of-labor guard: TC already runs the session's WS listener, so the agent is told to use TC's `/api/sessions/:project/medusa/*` endpoints and never open a second registration on its own id (two consumers on one workspace fight over the destructive-pop queue). Injection lives in the prime, not the engine config: the id is session-dynamic (minted per launch, forgotten at teardown), and the config route could not reach TC's own plugin-governed CLAUDE.md — which would silently exclude the primary dogfood session. Toggle/reconnect/webui paths pass no pre-minted id and keep their existing behavior. Tests: registry pre-mint/adopt/supersede + threading seam (`test/api-medusa.test.js`), contract resolution incl. env-override precedence and empty-file honesty, prime-section content + both off-gates (`test/sessions.test.js`).

## [4.14.0] - 2026-07-11

### Added

- **Idle-gated wake nudge — inbound Medusa mail can now trigger the receiving session's next turn (MED-2K9P v2 Slice 1, chunk T2).** New boot-time monitor `lib/medusa-wake.js` (wrap-sentinel lifecycle pattern): when a session with a live switchboard listener has fresh inbound messages, TC types a minimal fixed nudge into its tmux pane so the agent spends a turn reading its inbox via the existing `GET .../medusa/messages` + `POST .../medusa/read` API — the mechanical "wake a turn" primitive from switchboard-v2-design.md §4; drain/act/reply stay with the agent + the consumer contract (Medusa `docs/CONSUMER-CONTRACT.md`, #34). Safety spine: **(1) never interrupts a busy turn** — the T2 spike (live probe over 4 real sessions) found Claude Code's status line carries a deterministic in-flight marker (`esc to interrupt`), strictly more truthful than the 3-line output-age heuristic (a long quiet tool call reads false-idle under output-age); a pane is idle only when that marker is absent AND a bare `❯` input-prompt line exists (which also refuses pending permission dialogs — where typed bytes could answer the dialog — and half-typed operator input), debounced over 2 consecutive ticks; **(2) zero attacker-controlled bytes** — the nudge is a fixed template; cross-session message text is never typed into a terminal (it arrives over HTTP as data, not keystrokes); **(3) one nudge per fresh-mail edge** — a per-session watermark re-arms only on a genuinely new arrival, so a burst that piled up while busy drains FIFO on a single wake and an unhandled backlog never nudge-loops; **(4) opt-in per project** — new `medusaWake` preference (default OFF; a wake spends a real turn, which v1's passive badge never did), validated/persisted alongside `medusaEnabled` (`lib/projects.js`, `server.js` PATCH surface) with an "Auto-wake on inbound messages" toggle in project Settings (`public/ui.js`; `CACHE_NAME` v3-41 → v3-42), read live each tick — no relaunch needed; **(5) Slice-1 scope gates** — Claude-engine tmux sessions only (webui + other engines skipped with a once-per-session log, never silently). Tests: `test/medusa-wake.test.js` (pane-policy pinned byte-for-byte against the spike captures incl. dialog/typing/ANSI cases; debounce/watermark/burst/retry semantics; every gate blocking alone; prune-and-re-arm), `medusaWake` round-trip + rejection (`test/projects.test.js`).

## [4.13.1] - 2026-07-11

### Internal

- **Global rule made engine-agnostic: plans/design docs "openable from anywhere."** Reworded the operator-added Build-Plans rule in `data/global-rules.md` to state the *outcome* — a shareable hosted link the operator can open from any device — rather than a Claude-native "Artifact," so it degrades gracefully when injected into non-Claude engine sessions (Gemini/Codex/etc.). Verified the global- and session-rule injection path renders into every non-plugin project's config at launch (`lib/engines.js`). Filed #542 (TangleClaw-served plan/design doc links) to give every engine a hosting floor.

## [4.13.0] - 2026-07-10

### Added

- **Medusa switchboard resilience + lifecycle cleanup (MED-2K9P Chunk 04 — final).** Makes the switchboard trustworthy across failures: (1) a **socket-identity guard** in `lib/medusa-listener.js` `_connect()` — every socket handler is gated on the firing socket still being the current one, so a late `close`/`error`/`message` from a superseded (reconnected or post-`stop()`) socket can no longer flip a live listener's state, inject a ghost message, or set a stale error; (2) **inbox `messageId` de-dup** (bounded, FIFO-evicted) so a duplicate delivery — e.g. a re-`registered` drain overlapping a live push — isn't double-injected or double-counted; (3) **honest Bridge-down recovery** — a drop surfaces `state:"error"`/`connecting` then auto-reconnects (capped backoff) back to `listening` with the error cleared; (4) **deregister-on-session-end** — new `medusa.forgetSession` + `sessions._teardownMedusa` stop the listener (closing the WS; the Bridge auto-drops it from `wsClients`) and **forget the persisted `registry.json` workspace id**, wired into **every** session-end path (explicit kill, V2 + legacy wrap-complete, dead-tmux auto-complete, stale-wrapping recovery, and tunnel-kill of a webui session) so an ended session is never left as a ghost roster peer another session could "Deliver" to, and a future session mints a fresh id. **Scope note (Chunk 04 verify-api, 2026-07-11):** true offline store-and-forward is **descoped/deferred** — `POST /workspaces/register` mints its own id and never persists TC's WS id, so a WS-only id is never in the Bridge's `workspaceRegistry`; an offline send to it honestly 404s (the sender is told, not silently dropped) and `DELETE /workspaces/:id` is a no-op for it. Queued delivery is gated on a Medusa change (register must accept a caller-supplied `workspaceId`) and filed upstream; v1 remains "badge-receive while listening" (operator Option A). `lib/medusa-listener.js`, `lib/medusa.js`, `lib/medusa-registry.js` (existing `forgetWorkspace`), `lib/sessions.js` (kill + wrap teardown). Tests: socket-identity guard / messageId de-dup / Bridge-drop→recover (`test/medusa-listener.test.js`), `forgetSession` + `_teardownMedusa` stop-and-forget (`test/api-medusa.test.js`).

- **Medusa outbound send + target picker in the session banner (MED-2K9P Chunk 03).** Completes the switchboard's send half: a small **➤ compose button** beside the unread badge (shown only while the listener is on — you must be registered to have a truthful `from`) opens a **compose panel** with a **target picker populated from the live roster** (`GET /workspaces`, proxied by TC, self excluded, each option annotated `(offline)` when the peer isn't connected), a message field, and Send. The result is **honest, never a blanket "sent"**: delivered (`received`) vs queued (recipient offline — "they'll get it on reconnect") vs failed are surfaced distinctly via the reused methodology-action toast; on success the **outbound (right) head lights** (`flow-out`, mirroring the inbound glow) with an `aria-live` announcement (the non-color/-motion a11y cue). TC always passes the session's own registered workspace id as `from` (the Bridge trusts `from` verbatim — never let the browser set it), and validates a non-empty message client-side because the Bridge does not (verify-api 2026-07-10: a missing body still queues). New endpoints (thin Bridge pass-throughs — the browser never calls Medusa directly): `POST /api/sessions/:project/medusa/send` (`{to, message}` → `{status, id, to}`; honest `400`/`409`/`502` on validation/not-listening/Bridge-failure) and `GET /api/sessions/:project/medusa/roster`. Bridge HTTP base URL resolves from `MEDUSA_BRIDGE_HTTP_URL` (default `http://localhost:3009`). `lib/medusa.js` (`sendMessage`/`getRoster`), `server.js`, `public/session.{html,js,css}`; `CACHE_NAME` `v3-40 → v3-41`. Tests: send/roster mapping (received/queued/404-failure/empty-reject/self-target/not-listening/Bridge-unreachable) + route wiring against a fake Bridge (`test/api-medusa.test.js`), and frontend source-probes for the honest-result contract, roster-name `esc()` XSS guard, off-state gating, and no-new-timer (`test/medusa-control.test.js`). Interaction-design §3.7 + `api-notes-medusa.md` updated with the compose spec and re-verified send/roster shapes.

## [4.12.1] - 2026-07-10

### Fixed

- **V1 Prawduct playbook no longer injected where it is noise or explicitly disabled; the V1 methodology is now visibly deprecated (#536).** TC never fully migrated off its V1-internal `prawduct` methodology: `writeEngineConfig` injected the full "Session Playbook: Prawduct" (incl. the Independent Critic protocol) into **every** non-plugin-governed project's generated config — 19 CLAUDE.md files fleet-wide, including non-Claude engines (codex/antigravity/aider, where the Claude-harness governance it describes cannot apply — `governanceState` → `not-applicable`) and regardless of `independentCritic: false` (the render mismatch the TiLT v2 session hit: it ran V1 playbook prose and hand-rolled a Critic instead of the plugin's `critic-reviewer`). Fix is **template-declared, generator-enforced** — `template.json` reconciles additively into live installs on boot (#136), while `playbook.md` is user-owned after first copy, so live stale copies can never gain bundled edits: new `playbookEngines: ["claude"]` gates which engines receive the playbook (absent = all engines, so `tilt`/`minimal`/custom playbooks are unaffected), and new `playbookRuleSections: { independentCritic: "### Independent Critic Review" }` strips that section by heading when the project rule is **explicitly `false`** (absent/`true` keeps it — the template's `defaultRules` declare it enabled). Both implemented in a single `_renderPlaybook` helper replacing the four per-engine `getPlaybook` call sites (`lib/engines.js`; builders gain a defaulted `engineId` param). The V1 template is also marked **`deprecated`** with a `deprecationNote` pointing at the V2 plugin (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`), surfaced by `methodologies.listTemplates` (`lib/methodologies.js`) and badged "(deprecated)" in the create-project methodology pills + detail panel and the Settings methodology select (`public/ui.js`, `public/style.css`; `CACHE_NAME` v3-39 → v3-40, exact-pin test updated in `test/openclaw-bridge-port-row.test.js`) — it stays fully functional as the fallback for the 12 unmigrated drift/vendored projects ("bugfix now, migrate later" per the operator decision; plugin-governed projects were already correctly skipped by `isPluginGoverned`, regression-pinned since #330). Template-field docs updated (`docs/methodology-guide.md`). Tests: `test/prawduct-playbook-gating.test.js` (template declarations, `_stripPlaybookSection` heading/EOF/absent cases, `_renderPlaybook` engine-gating + explicit-false-only stripping + absent-field default, `generateConfig` integration across all four engines, `listTemplates` deprecation projection).

- **`attachProject` now applies the detected methodology's `defaultRules` to a fresh project config, same as create and methodology-switch (#536 Critic finding).** The config skeleton ships extension rules `false`; attach wrote it verbatim, so an attached auto-detected prawduct project silently carried `independentCritic: false` — which, with the playbook-section gating above, would strip the Critic section with no operator having chosen that (the asymmetric-gate class from #103/PR #125). Existing attached configs are untouched (an explicit rule state stays operator-editable in the Project Rules modal). Also from the same review: `_renderPlaybook` now `log.warn`s when a disabled rule's declared heading is missing from a (drifted, user-owned) playbook copy — the silent re-creation of the #536 mismatch — and omits the playbook entirely when stripping empties it (`lib/projects.js`, `lib/engines.js`). Tests: attach default-rules materialization (`test/projects.test.js`), stripped-to-empty → `null` (`test/prawduct-playbook-gating.test.js`).

### Internal

- **README refreshed for the 4.12 surface.** The storefront had drifted since its last update (Jul 3, #461): the **Session Switchboard** was listed as a future roadmap item even though its receive side and session-banner control shipped in v4.10–4.11 (MED-2K9P Chunks 01–02). Reframed the Switchboard as **functionally in beta** — added it to "What TangleClaw Does" and the "All features" Sessions section (listener state, unread badge, per-project auto-enable toggle), and narrowed the roadmap entry to the remaining outbound-send piece. Also corrected the engine list from "Five built-in engines … and OpenClaw" to "four local engines, plus remote OpenClaw," reflecting #459's removal of OpenClaw from the project engine picker (it portals to a remote agent, not a local LLM), and folded in three shipped-but-undocumented surfaces: the auth config-vs-live drift warning (#508), the Tailscale-tailnet HTTPS ingress site (#476), and the per-connection ClawBridge port affordance (#490/#492). Doc-only; no behavior change.
- **Screenshots reshot for the green-serpent rebrand + 4.x features.** The README embeds and the `project-assets` screenshot set were still the Mar-30 v3-era captures (old logo, no continuity/Master/Switchboard UI). Replaced the two embeds and rebuilt the Screenshots section as a **2×3 grid of click-to-enlarge thumbnails** (rendered via an HTML table for cell separators) — dashboard, project detail drawer, **Session History & Search**, the in-session view showing the **Switchboard** control, **Project Master** (captioned as the in-session drawer), and per-project **settings** (incl. the Medusa toggle) — plus a fuller `tangleclaw-screenshots/` set (rules, PortHub, groups, OpenClaw connections). Sensitive infrastructure (Tailnet/LAN IPs, SSH user, key path) and un-launched business-idea project names are blurred; images downscaled to 1920px. Assets live in the public `Jason-Vaughan/project-assets` repo per convention.

## [4.12.0] - 2026-07-10

### Changed

- **Session-banner logo enlarged to match the Medusa crest (29px) and de-padded.** The banner serpent rendered at 22px with ~5–8% transparent margin baked into the shared icon, so it read smaller than the Medusa heads beside it. Added a tight-cropped banner-only asset (`public/logo-banner.png`, margin removed so the serpent fills the frame) and bumped `.banner-logo` to 29px — matching the crest heads. Still clears the 32px back-button row, so the banner height is unchanged. Session + OpenClaw-view banners both updated; the shared PWA/favicon/apple-touch icons keep their safe margin untouched.

- **New TangleClaw logo — the green serpent — applied to every in-app icon.** Replaced the favicon, PWA icons (192/512), Apple touch icon, dashboard + session-banner mini logo, and the fallback (`public/logo-icon.png`, `public/logo.png`, `public/icons/icon-192.png`, `public/icons/icon-512.png`, `public/icons/apple-touch-icon.png`) with the new transparent green-snake emblem — a straight file swap at the existing paths, so no HTML/manifest edits. Downscaled from the operator-supplied 1024² transparent PNG (favicon **2.5 MB → 256 KB**). The "TangleClaw" text wordmark (`logo-text.png`) is unchanged (the new art is icon-only). The GitHub README emblem lives in the separate `project-assets` repo and is refreshed to the same transparent version alongside this change (the README previously showed a flattened black-background variant). Browser favicon caches are sticky — a hard refresh surfaces the new icon.

- **Medusa banner control now uses the real Medusa artwork (MED-2K9P art upgrade).** Replaced the hand-vectored placeholder head SVG with the production gold art — **two facing heads flanking the MEDUSA emblem** — as per-head `<img>` pieces (`public/medusa-head-left.webp`, `medusa-head-right.webp`, `medusa-wordmark.webp`), downscaled from ~475 KB of source PNG to ~17 KB of alpha-preserving WebP. Status is now carried by **state, not a flat recolor** (approach B): the gold art stays the brand at rest (`listening`), **dims + desaturates** when `off`, glows amber on `error` (alongside the "!"), and the inbound head still glows on a received message — so the artwork survives while the status read stays honest and distinct per state. Keeping the heads as separate images preserves the per-head status the control needs (inbound left / outbound right in Chunk 03). Dropped the placeholder's central "bridge" element in favor of the emblem centerpiece, and removed the now-dead `--medusa-color` CSS variable left from the recolor approach. `public/session.html`, `public/session.css`; `CACHE_NAME` bumped `v3-38 → v3-39` (edits `session.*`). New source-probe assertions in `test/medusa-control.test.js` (per-head art present, emblem centered between the heads, no bridge, placeholder SVG gone, assets ship).

### Fixed

- **The Medusa inbox panel could not be dismissed once opened (MED-2K9P Chunk 02 bug).** Opening the inbox marks it read → `unread` drops to 0 → the badge that toggles the panel **self-hid**, leaving no close control and no Escape handler — a hard trap on touch (the only remaining path, an outside tap, is undiscoverable once the badge vanishes). Added an explicit **✕ close** button in the panel header (delegated handler, since the panel's `innerHTML` re-renders on each open), **Escape-to-close**, and a dedicated `closeMedusaInbox()` (`public/session.js`, `public/session.css`). Regression pins in `test/medusa-control.test.js` (close button rendered in both the empty and populated panel, and the close + Escape wiring).

## [4.11.0] - 2026-07-09

### Added

- **Medusa control in the session banner — receive badge + per-project auto-enable (MED-2K9P Chunk 02).** The UI slice of the switchboard: a two-head Medusa mark in the session banner that carries honest listener status (RED off / GREEN on, GREEN-pulsing while connecting, AMBER + "!" glyph on error — kept visually distinct from off so "off" never reads as "broken"). Click the heads to toggle this session's listener (register+connect / stop+drop); an unread badge counts inbound messages and the **inbound head lights transiently** on each `new_message`, fed by the Chunk 01 status endpoint over the **existing** session-status poll (no new UI timer, per the no-timer-UI rule #98/#268). Click the badge to open a read panel listing received messages (with `from`), which marks the inbox read; hovering the mark shows a recent-inbound-peers popover (desktop). Flow indication is never color-only — the accessible label carries the state text, the badge shows the count, an aria-live region announces arrivals, and the "!" glyph marks error (motion cues auto-suppress under `prefers-reduced-motion`, leaving the badge + announcement). Plus a **per-project "Enable Medusa session comms" toggle** in the project Settings modal (`medusaEnabled`, engine-agnostic, **default OFF**): when on, a newly launched session for that project auto-starts its listener; the banner control remains the per-session override. New TC endpoints (thin pass-throughs, browser never talks to the Bridge): `POST /api/sessions/:project/medusa/toggle` (`{enabled}` optional — idempotent, else flips), `GET .../medusa/messages`, `POST .../medusa/read`. Head shapes are the inlined `medusa-logo.svg` artwork (DECISION A), recolored per-head via CSS. Tests: toggle/messages/read routes + auto-start-on-launch wiring (`test/api-medusa.test.js`), `medusaEnabled` validate/persist/round-trip (`test/projects.test.js`), and frontend source-probes locking the `esc()` XSS guard on untrusted cross-session text + the no-new-timer + first-render-seed invariants (`test/medusa-control.test.js`).

## [4.10.0] - 2026-07-09

### Added

- **Medusa listener core — the switchboard's server-side spine (MED-2K9P Chunk 01).** New per-session in-TC-server WebSocket client that registers a workspace against the Medusa Bridge, receives inbound messages (the post-`registered` offline-queue drain plus live pushes, both as `new_message` envelopes), keeps presence fresh with periodic `listener_heartbeat` frames, and exposes an observable state machine (`off`/`connecting`/`listening`/`error`) over a bounded in-memory per-session inbox (most-recent 500). Three new zero-dep modules: `lib/medusa-listener.js` (the WS client + reconnect with capped exponential backoff, `EventEmitter` emitting `state`/`message`; malformed frames and `error`/`pong`/`heartbeat_ack` are tolerated, never crash the listener), `lib/medusa-registry.js` (mints/persists/reuses a stable `<slug>-<hex>` workspace id per session at `<project>/.tangleclaw/medusa/registry.json`; a missing/corrupt file is treated as empty, not thrown), and `lib/medusa.js` (per-session listener lifecycle + status/inbox pass-throughs). Surfaced read-only via `GET /api/sessions/:project/medusa/status` → `{ state, workspaceId, unread, lastError }` (thin pass-through; resolves the active session id via `store.sessions.getActive`, with a `?sessionId=` fallback). Uses Node 22's built-in `WebSocket` global — no new dependency. Trust model is trusted-local loopback (the Bridge WS path is unauthenticated at the workspace layer; verified in `.prawduct/artifacts/api-notes-medusa.md`). No UI in this chunk (Chunk 02). Tests: `test/medusa-listener.test.js` (register-on-open, `registered`→listening, `new_message`→inbox/unread + FIFO drain order, malformed-frame tolerance, heartbeat, `stop()`→off with no reconnect, reconnect-after-unexpected-close, id mint/reuse/persist/forget) via an injected `wsFactory` fake — no real networking; and `test/api-medusa.test.js` (service lifecycle: start/stop, per-session idempotency, workspace-id reuse across restarts, safe no-ops on unknown sessions; and the status route: 404 unknown project, off-status with no active session, `?sessionId=` fallback).

## [4.9.1] - 2026-07-09

### Fixed

- **The dashboard (landing.js) wrap trigger is now single-flight — no concurrent wraps, no mid-wrap dismissal (UI-3B8N).** `landing.js` `confirmWrap` (the project-card wrap trigger, distinct from the in-session one fixed in #519) awaited `POST /wrap` *without* disabling the confirm button, so a second click during the in-flight wrap launched a **concurrent** wrap (double commit / pipeline race), and Cancel or a backdrop click could dismiss the modal mid-wrap. Applied the same fix #519 landed on `public/session.js`: the first click sets a `wrapInFlight` flag, disables **both** Confirm and Cancel, flips the label to **"Wrapping…"**, and blocks every close path (`closeWrapModal` guards on a strict `force !== true`, so the Cancel handler's event-arg and the backdrop's no-arg close can't slip through) until the request resolves — all restored in `finally` so a failed or hung wrap re-enables cleanly. Driven purely by the request lifecycle, no timers (per the no-timer-UI rule, #98/#268). Regression pin in `test/landing-wrap-single-flight.test.js` (structural, matching the `session-wrapper.test.js` convention).

- **Wrap-drawer decision selects now expose an accessible name to screen readers (UI-7H4K, a11y).** The pr-check and plan-picker resolution widgets (`public/session.js`) rendered a standalone `<label>` with no `for`/`id` tie to their `<select>`s, so assistive tech announced the controls with no name. Fixed both: the **plan-picker**'s single select now carries an `id` its `<label htmlFor>` points at (a direct label→control association); the **pr-check** widget — whose caption spans N per-PR selects — marks its list a `role="group"` labelled by the caption (`aria-labelledby`) and gives **each** resolution select its own accessible name via `aria-labelledby` referencing that PR's title. Visual rendering and behavior are unchanged (CSS is class-based; the caption tag changed from `<label>` to `<div>` only for pr-check, where it captions a group rather than a single control). Structural regression pin in `test/wrap-drawer-select-a11y.test.js`. The Critic NOTE carried forward from #428/#519 that filed UI-7H4K is now resolved.

### Internal

- **Removed the dead "no parseable chunks" defensive branch from the commit-body builder (WRP-6C4M).** `commit.js` `_buildBodyLines` carried a branch rendering a `- Priming refreshed … plan has no parseable chunks` line for a staged priming pointer of shape `{current:null, allDone:false}`. Since #515, priming-roll's `run()` skips a chunk-less plan *before* it ever selects a pointer or stages (`_selectPointer` only ever yields `allDone` or a non-null `current` for a staged entry), so that shape can no longer reach the builder — the branch was dead code, and its unit test exercised an input the pipeline never produces. Removed both (branch + `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pin), leaving an invariant comment so the shape isn't re-added. This is the twin of the `priming-roll._renderPointerBody` dead branch dropped in #517; the Critic flagged it as a NOTE there. No behavior change — the drawer's generic `return null` fallback for the same case is a shared catch-all (with `test`/`lint`), not a shape-specific branch, and is retained.

## [4.9.0] - 2026-07-09

### Added

- **Inline plan-picker in the wrap drawer when priming-roll blocks on multiple in-progress plans (#428).** When `next-session-prime` can't auto-pick among several in-progress plans in `.claude/plans/` (#226), the drawer previously showed only a "How to fix this" blob telling the operator to hand-edit `.tangleclaw/project.json` in a terminal. Now it renders a **dropdown of the candidate plan filenames** + a **Set active plan** button — mirroring the affordance `pr-check` already proves. **Backend:** the multi-plan block now exposes the candidates as structured data (`output.candidates`, `lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js`) rather than only inside the blocker string; a new `activePlan` field on `updateProject` (`lib/projects.js`, PATCH `/api/projects/:name`) validates the pick (bare `.md` filename that exists under `.claude/plans/`; path separators rejected) and persists it via `store.projectConfig.load/save` — read back by `priming-roll._readActivePlan` next wrap. **Frontend:** `planPickerWidget` (`public/wrap-drawer.js`) + `renderPlanPickerWidget`/`setActivePlan` (`public/session.js`, `public/session.css`). **Persist-only by design** (operator decision): the pick is a durable config write and, because the block is non-fatal (the wrap already committed), it is *not* wired to a whole-pipeline Retry — so it "sticks" for the next wrap without a double-commit; the operator sets the plan and clicks Done. Tests: candidate exposure (`test/wrap-step-priming-roll.test.js`), `activePlan` validate/persist/round-trip (`test/projects.test.js`), widget descriptor (`test/wrap-drawer.test.js`).

- **Help affordances in the wrap drawer (what / how / why).** Each wrap step now carries a **tappable** `ⓘ` that reveals an inline description of what that step does and why it runs — a new `KIND_DESCRIPTIONS` map (`public/wrap-drawer.js`) covering all 13 pipeline kinds, surfaced as `kindTooltip` on the step row (`renderStepRow`) and toggled on tap/click (`.wrap-step-help` / `.wrap-step-help-text`) so it works on touch — iPhone Safari is the primary platform, where native `title=`/`:hover` never fire — with the `title` kept only as a desktop hover bonus. The inline plan-picker (#428) gains a plain-language **"Why: …"** explainer, a **"What happens: …"** note, and hovers on its dropdown + button, so an operator meeting it for the first time isn't guessing at an unfamiliar affordance. A drift-guard test asserts every canonical wrap-step kind has a non-empty description (`test/wrap-drawer.test.js`).

### Fixed

- **The `priming-roll` wrap step (`next-session-prime`) now skips — instead of blocking the wrap — when the resolved plan has no `### Chunk N:` headings (#515).** `lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js` treated a chunk-less plan asymmetrically: the single-plan resolve path (`.claude/plans/` holds exactly one `.md`) returned it and let `run()` hard-**block** on zero chunks, while the multi-plan path already **skipped** such a plan via `_isPlanInProgress`. So the same spec/design doc (or a not-yet-chunked plan) failed the wrap when it stood alone but was silently dropped when it had company — the `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates` class of gate asymmetry. Observed live 2026-07-09: TC's own wrap went BLOCKED on `.claude/plans/continuity-contract.md` (a Phase-0 spec doc, zero chunks) once the real build plan was archived. The `run()` zero-chunk gate now returns `status:'skipped'` with a reason (`… no ### Chunk N: headings — nothing to roll (add chunk headings if this is meant to be an active build plan)`) and stages no priming write — honest and visible in the drawer, never halting. Applies to explicitly-configured `step.planPath`s too (a pointer at a chunk-less file is a visible skip, not a wrap failure). Re-specified the prior block-asserting test to the new contract and added regression tests pinning single-plan/multi-plan symmetry and the explicit-planPath case (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`).

- **The wrap trigger modal no longer allows concurrent wraps or mid-wrap dismissal (re-entrancy fix).** `confirmWrap` (`public/session.js`) fired `POST /wrap` and awaited it *without* disabling the confirm button, so a second click during the in-flight wrap launched a **concurrent** wrap (double commit / pipeline race), and Cancel or a backdrop click could dismiss the modal mid-wrap — orphaning the request, which then resolved later and popped the results drawer unexpectedly. Now the first click sets an in-flight flag, disables **both** Confirm and Cancel, flips the label to **"Wrapping…"**, and blocks every close path (`closeWrapModal` guards on a strict `force !== true`, so the Cancel handler's event-arg can't slip through) until the request resolves — all restored in `finally` so a failed or hung wrap re-enables cleanly instead of sticking. Driven purely by the request lifecycle, no timers (per the no-timer-UI rule, #98/#268). Operator-verified (`VRF-wrap-single-flight`).

### Internal

- **priming-roll hygiene: own test file, dead-branch removal, citation fixes (TST-4X8N + #515 follow-up).** Extracted the `priming-roll` unit tests (~690 lines, both `describe` blocks) out of the 208 KB `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` into a dedicated `test/wrap-step-priming-roll.test.js`, matching every sibling wrap-step's convention (advances backlog TST-4X8N for the priming-roll slice; the pipeline-level ordering/commit/drawer tests that reference the step stay in `wrap-pipeline.test.js`). Removed the now-unreachable "no `### Chunk N:` headings" fallback branch of `_renderPointerBody` in `lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js` (+ its direct test): since #515 made `run()` skip a chunk-less plan before rendering, `_selectPointer` can only ever hand the renderer an `allDone` or `current` pointer, never an all-`null` one — the branch was dead code testing dead code. Repointed two provenance citations (`lib/continuity.js`, `FEATURES.md`) from `.claude/plans/continuity-contract.md` to `.claude/plans/archive/continuity-contract.md` after the spec doc was archived. No behavior change. (Left in place, noted for a future pass: the commit/drawer side carries a parallel "no parseable chunks" defensive render for the same staged shape — a separate consumer, out of scope here.)

## [4.8.0] - 2026-07-09

### Added

- **Session-rule version history is now pruned to the newest 200 versions per rule (SR-5T1J).** `session_rule_versions` appended a full snapshot on every mutation and never removed one, so under the self-improvement loop's autonomous edit volume (the high-edit-velocity trigger the D1b Critic named) a single rule's history could grow without bound. Each snapshot write now trims that rule's history to the newest `SESSION_RULE_VERSION_RETENTION` (200) versions — self-maintaining (no cron/wrap step), amortized on the existing `rule_id` index, and it bounds row count directly regardless of edit velocity (an age window would leave a fast-churning rule unbounded inside the window). Only versions **older than** the 200th-newest (by `version_no`) are dropped, so every restore target within the window, the rule's current state, and a deleted rule's tombstone (`op='delete'`, its latest version) are always preserved; `version_no` stays monotonic (`MAX+1`) and `restore` still resolves by exact `version_no`, so the harmless gaps pruning leaves are invisible to callers. Accepted trade-off: restoring to a version older than the window returns the same `NOT_FOUND` as any absent version (git, CHANGELOG, and the activity log remain the durable record beyond it); an operator wanting unbounded audit sets retention to `0` (the `_setSessionRuleVersionRetention` seam, mirroring `_setBasePath`). Requirement in `docs/session-rules-self-improvement.md`; +7 store tests in `test/session-rules.test.js` (default-200, exact-newest-N, monotonicity-after-prune, kept-vs-pruned restore, tombstone preservation, per-rule isolation, N≤0 opt-out).

### Fixed

- **`GET /api/ports` no longer throws on a request with no `Host` header (janitor).** The handler built its URL with `` new URL(req.url, `http://${req.headers.host}`) `` — the one call site (of 16) that had dropped the `|| 'localhost'` fallback the others carry, so a `Host`-less request (`new URL('/api/ports', 'http://undefined')` → `TypeError: Invalid URL`) crashed the handler. Consolidated all 16 sites into a single `reqUrl(req)` helper (`server.js`) that always applies the localhost fallback, so the fallback can't drift per call site again. Regression test in `test/server.test.js` (no-Host case + Host-present case).

### Internal

- **Janitor maintenance sweep (2026-07-09).** Removed dead public export `git.isDirty` (`lib/git.js`) — uncalled anywhere; the internal `_isDirty` it wrapped is retained. Corrected a stale doc-comment in `lib/wrap-pipeline.js` that still described `wrapV2` as defaulting `false` ("Chunk 11 flips the default") when it has defaulted `true` since #196. Added a Node-22 startup guard in `server.js` (clear abort message before the `node:sqlite` load, instead of a cryptic module-not-found on older runtimes). Deleted dead `tests/conftest.py` (Python/pytest scaffolding in a zero-Python, zero-dependency Node project — the entire `test/` vs `tests/` split). No behavior change beyond the `reqUrl` fix above.

- **Pruned the injected config surface — leaner CLAUDE.md and per-project engine configs (janitor).** The governance/API text TangleClaw injects into every project's config had accreted verbosity. Concised the four git-tracked sources — `data/global-rules.md` (190→118 lines) and `data/{porthub,shared-docs,session-memory}-guide.md` (154→~100) — **keeping every rule, rationale, and API endpoint** (verified: all `## ` headings, every `**Rule:**`, the version-bump table byte-for-byte, and all endpoints preserved; only prose was tightened and em-dash mojibake fixed). This shrinks the config injected into every non-plugin-governed project by ~126 lines. TC's **own** CLAUDE.md — which the Prawduct plugin governs, so TC never regenerates it — was hand-trimmed to match (423→248 lines): Global Rules + guides mirrored to the concised sources, and ~73 lines of vendored Prawduct methodology (Methodology/Session-Playbook/Governance) that the plugin already injects at session start collapsed to a one-line pointer. One `#212` round-trip test's obsolete `>10 KB` precondition (the bundled file is now just under the old cap) updated to assert the round-trip itself; the 256 KB upper-bound test still pins the cap.

## [4.7.1] - 2026-07-08

### Internal

- **Dedup the path-token matcher shared by the continuity Map and the features-toc wrap step (CON-8H3Z).** `lib/continuity.js` and `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js` each carried a character-identical `/([A-Za-z0-9_./-]+\.(?:js|jsx|ts|tsx|json|md|html|css|yaml|yml|sh))(?:\b|:)/gi`, and their extension allowlists had to stay in sync by hand — a type recognized by one but not the other would silently drift the Map's file coverage from FEATURES.md's. Extracted the pattern to `lib/path-tokens.js` (`makePathTokenRegex()` factory + a named `PATH_TOKEN_EXTENSIONS` allowlist); both consumers now build their own module-scope instance from the shared source, so `.lastIndex` stays isolated per consumer (no shared-mutable-regex cross-talk) while the allowlist lives in one place. Behavior-preserving — no existing assertion changed; a byte-identical regression pin against the historical literal plus fresh-instance / allowlist / capture-group coverage in new `test/path-tokens.test.js`.

## [4.7.0] - 2026-07-08

### Added

- **Dashboard warning when auth is configured but not actually enforcing (AUTH-2K9D).** An operator could persist `authEnabled=true` and believe TangleClaw was access-controlled while the runtime enforced nothing — two silent config-vs-live mismatches: `authEnabled` in `direct` mode is *inert* (only the Caddy cutover reads it; direct mode has no in-process gate — AUTH-2), and `authEnabled` in `caddy` mode with identity not arriving (e.g. a hand-edited live Caddyfile missing `header_up X-Auth-User` — AUTH-3) was indistinguishable from a healthy gate. `GET /api/server-info` now returns an `authStatus` enum (`off` / `live` / `configured-inert` / `configured-no-identity`) derived server-side from `{authEnabled, ingressMode}` plus the existing trust-gated identity resolution (new pure `authIdentity.resolveAuthStatus`, single source of truth). The dashboard renders an amber warning chip next to the login chip on the two mismatch states, naming the concrete remediation (run the cutover / fix `header_up`). **Surfacing only — it never enforces auth** (direct mode is deliberately trusted-LAN; the gate is Caddy's job) and doesn't touch the `resolveRequestUser` spoof-defense. The chip is state-driven and self-clearing (no dismiss control, no timer, per the no-UI-timers rule), amber + text for a11y. Unit tests (`test/auth-identity.test.js`), API wiring (`test/api-auth-identity.test.js`), and frontend structural tests (`test/auth-status-warning.test.js`); requirement in `docs/auth-status-surfacing.md`.

## [4.6.0] - 2026-07-08

### Added

- **Critic-gate provenance on session-rule version history (SR-7K2P).** Every version snapshot of a session rule now records a `criticGate` attestation — `passed` (an AI/autonomous edit attested as having cleared the in-session Critic gate), `not-required` (an operator or trivial edit that legitimately skips it), or `unknown` (a backfilled legacy row, or an AI edit applied with no attestation). This makes the self-improvement loop's central safeguard **auditable** rather than only inferable from cross-referencing `changed_by='ai'` against the activity log. Because the server can neither summon nor verify a Critic, this **records** the AI's apply-time attestation — it does not enforce it. Schema bumped v23→v24 (`lib/store.js`): the fresh-DB DDL carries a `critic_gate` CHECK, and a table-rebuild migration (mirroring SR-3MW8) applies it to existing DBs, defaulting every pre-existing row to `unknown`, with a `sqlite_master` postcondition guarding the version bump. The four apply-path APIs (`POST /api/session-rules`, `PUT /api/session-rules/:id`, `POST /api/session-rules/promote`, `POST /api/session-rules/:id/restore`) accept an optional `criticGate` (enum-validated, 400 on a bad value); absent an attestation the writer derives honestly from the author (operator → `not-required`, AI → `unknown`). `GET /api/session-rules/:id/versions` returns `criticGate` per version, and the version-history UI shows a per-version badge (`✓ Critic-reviewed` / `— not required` / `? unknown`). Store, migration, API, and UI tests added in `test/session-rules.test.js`, `test/api-session-rules-selfimprove.test.js`, and `test/session-rules-panel.test.js`; schema-version assertions across seven test files bumped to 24.

## [4.5.2] - 2026-07-08

### Fixed

- **Session-start banner (`*TangleClaw'd into existence.*`) now surfaces on every session, regardless of wrap tier or engine/model.** The banner lives in the hidden SessionStart prime (`lib/sessions.js` `generatePrimePrompt`); confirmed against Claude Code's hooks docs, a SessionStart hook can only inject *hidden model context* — it cannot render into the startup header or emit guaranteed-visible terminal output — so the sole visible path is the model re-printing the banner on its first turn. The "re-emit this visibly" instruction previously lived **only inside the Resume branch** (which fires only when a continuity index exists), so any session after a `mechanical-only` wrap took the legacy-summary `else` path and silently dropped the banner 100% of the time; even in the Resume branch it was coupled to a wait-for-confirmation directive, so a task-opening prompt often skipped it. Hoisted an **unconditional, engine-agnostic** banner-emit instruction into the header block every prime carries, explicitly split from any wait-for-confirmation directive (visible-output requirement only — does not authorize starting work). Regression tests in `test/sessions.test.js` assert the instruction is present in the clean/no-index path, the legacy-summary path, and the Resume path.

### Internal

- **CHECK constraint pins `session_rule_versions.op` to its enum `('create'|'update'|'delete'|'restore')` (SR-3MW8).** The version-history table backing the reversible audit trail for session-rule edits (D1b) never enforced its `op` enum at the storage layer — every insert routes through `_snapshotSessionRule`, whose only four callers pass exactly those literals, but a future writer bug or a manual edit could land a garbage op and silently corrupt the history. Schema bumped v22→v23 (`lib/store.js`): the current-schema DDL now carries the CHECK for fresh DBs, and a table-rebuild migration (SQLite can't `ALTER TABLE ADD CHECK`) applies it to existing DBs, preserving every row verbatim, with a `sqlite_master` postcondition that refuses to advance `schema_version` if the constraint isn't present (mirrors the v14→v15 rebuild pattern). No user-visible behavior change — a data-integrity guard only. New migration + enforcement tests in `test/session-rules.test.js`; schema-version assertions across seven test files bumped to 23.

## [4.5.1] - 2026-07-06

### Fixed

- **The ttyd attach script is now installed outside the TCC-protected repo, so sessions no longer black-screen after a ttyd restart (#500).** On 2026-07-06 the v4.5.0 update restarted ttyd and every session pane went black and unresponsive — new and reopened alike. Root cause: macOS TCC blocked the freshly-restarted **ttyd** (which is denied Full Disk Access) from reading its per-connection attach script `deploy/ttyd-attach.sh`, which lived under `~/Documents/Projects/TangleClaw/`; each connection's `bash` child **froze in the `open()` syscall**, so the websocket upgraded (101) but not one output byte ever flowed. The plist template had explicitly (and wrongly) reasoned the script was TCC-safe "because it is a ttyd arg, not the launchd program" — but ttyd's own per-connection read is a *separate* TCC path the earlier bash-inline-from-argv hardening never covered. The script is now installed to the non-TCC `~/.tangleclaw/deploy/ttyd-attach.sh` (new `lib/ttyd-attach.js#syncAttachScript`, idempotent + refresh-on-change), the plist points there via a new `__TTYD_ATTACH__` placeholder filled by `install.sh` and `scripts/ingress-cutover.js`, and the server re-syncs the copy at every boot so an update that bumps the repo script refreshes it on the ensuing restart. Mirrors the #463 Caddyfile boot-adoption pattern: the repo now generates exactly what the operator applied by hand during the incident (verified: the boot sync no-ops against the live hand-fixed copy). Same TCC-under-`~/Documents` family as #324 (launchd→node). **Failure signature for future diagnosis:** WS upgrade 101 but zero output frames; the attach child stuck in `open()`/`__open_nocancel` on a `~/Documents/…` path; identical black screen for new and reopened sessions; server restarts don't help. Tests: new `test/ttyd-attach-sync.test.js` (+8 — path resolution, copy / refresh-on-change / no-op / exec-bit / no-source, real-repo source, and an ENOTDIR error-branch fault injection) + updated pins in `test/ttyd-plist.test.js` (the `__TTYD_ATTACH__` template contract plus the install.sh copy/substitution assertions) and `test/ingress-cutover.test.js` (non-TCC path asserted, repo-path regression-guarded in both ingress modes). **Live install verification (a full `install.sh` run) deferred to an operator VRF** — running it on Cursatory now would regenerate the plist and re-break sessions.

- **The setup wizard's Admin Login step now explains why Next is disabled (#498, backlog AUTH-7P3M).** When the password failed a client-side rule the Next button was correctly disabled but silent — `setupAdminError` was only populated by `wizardAdminNext()`, which never fires while the button is disabled, so an operator with (say) an 11-character password was simply stuck (the exact elkaholic HITL repro from 2026-06-26). A live hint under the fields now names the FIRST unmet rule in gate order ("Enter a username." → "Password must be at least 12 characters." → "Passwords do not match." → "Password must not contain the username."), updating as the operator types, clearing when the rules pass, and suppressed while all three fields are still empty. The rules live once in a new pure `_adminRuleHint(user, password, confirm)`: the Next gate (`_adminCanAdvance`), the live hint, and the `wizardAdminNext` error path all consume it, so the gate and its explanations cannot drift. The server's weak-password denylist stays authoritative via the existing error surface. No CACHE_NAME bump (`setup.js` is not SW-precached). Tests: `test/auth2-wizard-admin.test.js` +6 (exact messages, first-unmet precedence incl. the 11-char repro, gate⇔hint single-source equivalence, pristine suppression, live-hint show/clear, error-path parity + structural sync-wiring pin).

- **Injected AI-guide API base URLs now carry the scheme the server actually serves (#496, backlog ENG-5R2W).** Engine configs and the master identity file derived the base-URL scheme from `config.httpsEnabled` alone, but the server's boot predicate is richer: caddy ingress mode always binds plain HTTP on the loopback (caddy owns TLS), and HTTPS additionally requires both cert paths (`createServer` falls back to HTTP otherwise) — and since `httpsEnabled` defaults to true, both caddy-mode and no-cert installs got an `https://` base URL nothing was serving. Every guided API call then failed with connection errors until the caller guessed the http fallback; on 2026-07-06 a live session's restart POST silently no-oped against the injected https URL while the stale server kept running. A new shared predicate `effectiveServerProtocol(config)` (`lib/https-setup.js`) mirrors boot reality (caddy override + the `willServeHttps` cert-paths conjunction) and both generators (`lib/engines.js` `_getRulesContent`, `lib/master.js` `buildMasterClaudeMd`) consume it — the same one-predicate consolidation the symmetric-capability-gates learning prescribes. The static PortHub guide prose no longer claims https-is-the-default; it now tells sessions to use the injected URL as-is. Configs pick up the corrected URL on their next regeneration (server restart / project sync). Tests: +5 (pure-predicate unit coverage in `test/https-setup.test.js`; caddy-mode + no-cert injection pins in `test/engines.test.js` and `test/master.test.js` — the master https fixture gains cert paths to match the served-protocol contract, assertions strengthened).

### Internal

- **The caddy adoption computation now has a single implementation shared by the real and dry-run paths (#494, backlog CAD-7X4V).** `applyDryRunAdoptionPreview` (`scripts/ingress-cutover.js`) was a hand-maintained 3-concern mirror of `adoptCredentialIntoConfig` (`lib/caddy.js`) — credential, remote-HTTP catch-all, and tailnet-host adoption duplicated across two files, with the original dry-run/real divergence itself a Critic-caught bug on the #476 review. The computation is extracted to a pure `caddy.computeCaddyfileAdoption(config, content)` (mutates the in-memory config, returns the `{adopted, changed, user, remoteHttp, tailnetHost, reason}` shape); `adoptCredentialIntoConfig` keeps the ingress-mode gate, Caddyfile read, and persist+log around it, and the dry-run preview delegates behind its unchanged exported signature. Pure refactor — no behavior change; all pre-existing adoption/preview contracts pass unmodified. Tests: `test/auth-credential-durability.test.js` +5 (direct helper coverage: full result shape, never-overwrite + no-op reasons, idempotence, publicDomain exclusion; plus an anti-drift structural pin that the cutover script no longer references the three concern extractors).

## [4.5.0] - 2026-07-06

### Added

- **The OpenClaw connection card now shows a Bridge Port row when one is set (#491, backlog OUI-4T9M).** The expanded card listed Host / Port / SSH User / SSH Key / CLI Command / Local Port / Version but not the bridge port, so a configured — or #490 auto-allocated — bridge port was only visible inside the Edit modal; during the VRF-489-bridge-auto smoke test the operator couldn't tell from the card whether auto-allocation had worked. The detail grid gains a conditional **Bridge Port** row (between Local Port and Version, with a tooltip pointing at the Edit-modal affordance) rendered only when `bridgePort` is set, so non-ClawBridge connections (null, the #160 default) stay clean. `CACHE_NAME` v3-36→v3-37 (ui.js is precached); exact-pin ownership moves to the new test per the established convention. Tests: new `test/openclaw-bridge-port-row.test.js` (+4 structural — conditional gating, grid placement, tooltip, cache bump).

- **The connection form's Bridge Port field now supports `auto` — server-side free-port allocation from the UI (#489, backlog OUI-2F8K).** The API has accepted `bridgePort:"auto"` since #352 (create: allocate from `[3201,3300)`) and #483 (update: idempotent — keeps an existing bridge port, allocates only when bridge-less), but the form field was `type="number"` with blank=null-only semantics, so ClawBridge users had to hand-pick a non-colliding port. The field is now a text input (`inputmode="numeric"`) accepting three shapes — blank = no bridge port (the #160 contract), a port number = sent verbatim, `auto` (any case) = server allocates — with an **Auto** button beside it that fills the literal in, tooltip explaining both the create and keep-existing semantics. Parsing lives in a new pure helper `tcParseBridgePort` (`public/api-helper.js`): invalid input (typos, port 0, > 65535) is rejected with a form error *before* the request is built rather than coerced to null, because a silent null on edit would clear the stored bridge port and release its lease (#483) — exactly the failure mode the old `parseInt || null` closure would have had once the field became free text. En route: the input's inert hardcoded `value="3201"` (contradicting its own #160 comment claiming it was a placeholder) is gone, and the stale "typically `3201`" hint in `docs/openclaw-setup.md` now documents `auto`. `CACHE_NAME` v3-35→v3-36 (ui.js/index.html are precached); the superseded exact pin in `test/master-drawer-frontend.test.js` converts to the floor pattern per the convention in `test/terminal-drag-copy.test.js`. Tests: new `test/bridge-port-input.test.js` (+21 — behavioral parser coverage incl. case-normalization for the server's exact `=== 'auto'` compare and the reject-don't-coerce typo cases, + structural form/wiring/propagation pins).

### Internal

- **`.prawduct/change-log.md` is now git-tracked, so the `check-change-log-entry` PR gate can actually pass (#485).** `.gitignore` excluded `.prawduct/` wholesale, which made Prawduct's REL-6C3W probe structurally always fail with `no-entry` — the change-log was written correctly on every branch but could never appear in the `merge-base...HEAD` diff (first observed on PR #484). The blanket ignore is replaced with `.prawduct/*` + a `!.prawduct/change-log.md` negation, so all other governance state (critic findings, session files, ledger, artifacts) stays fail-closed local while the change-log — an audit trail with the same publishability as this file — is committed. En route, two defects fixed in the change-log itself: the title still said "TangleClaw-v3" (stale pre-#183 repo name), and the 2026-07-04 #434-chunk-2 entry was missing its `## ` heading (the exact marker the gate greps for).

## [4.4.1] - 2026-07-04

### Fixed

- **`PUT /api/openclaw/connections/:id` now reconciles the PortHub leases when a connection's port changes (#483, backlog PH-4B7N, surfaced by the #352 Critic pass).** The create path leases `local_port`/`bridge_port` under `oc-direct-<id>` and DELETE releases them, but an update used to leave the old lease held forever and the new port unleased — reopening the #352 allocate→bind race for edited connections (a later create's `nextFreePort` could hand the edited connection's live port to someone else, while the abandoned port stayed blocked until DELETE). The PUT handler now mirrors the create/delete lifecycle: it 404s early on unknown ids, conflict-checks a *changed* `localPort` (as before) **and** a changed `bridgePort` (previously unchecked — parity with POST), then after a successful store update kills the now-misconfigured standalone tunnel (`tunnel.killTunnel('oc-direct-<id>')` — it was still bound to the old port while the record and HTTP/WS proxy pointed at the new one) and releases the stale lease(s) before re-leasing the connection's current ports. `bridgePort: "auto"` is now also honored on PUT (previously the literal string `"auto"` was written to the DB) with *idempotent* semantics: a connection that already has a bridge port keeps it — re-saving an edit form must not churn ports — and only a bridge-less connection allocates from `[3201, 3300)`. Lease reconciliation only runs when a port actually changed, so non-port edits touch nothing. Tests: `test/api-openclaw.test.js` (+8 — local/bridge swap release+re-lease incl. the bridge-only-change case guarding the killTunnel/localPort interaction, clear-to-null release, PUT-side conflict 409s for both ports, `"auto"` allocate + `"auto"` keep-existing, and no-port-change lease preservation; 6 of the 8 fail without the fix, the other 2 pin pre-existing contracts).

## [4.4.0] - 2026-07-04

### Added

- **New `learnings-db-write` wrap step mirrors captured learnings into the DB, so the D1 self-improvement loop finally has data (#466).** The D1 loop shipped its store, API, UI, and prime-injection surfaces, but nothing ever wrote a `learnings` row — `store.learnings.*` had no call site, so `generatePrimePrompt`'s "Active learnings" and the `POST /api/session-rules/promote` learnings→rule loop were permanently empty (`SELECT COUNT(*) FROM learnings` → 0 across every project, ever). The new step (`lib/wrap-steps/learnings-db-write.js`, kind `learnings-db-write`) runs right after the AI-driven `learnings-capture` step: it parses that session's **today-dated** `## YYYY-MM-DD — <title>` entries out of `.tangleclaw/memories/learnings.md` (which stays the human-readable source of truth), dedups by exact `content` against the project's existing rows (idempotent across wrap retries — a retry inserts nothing), attributes the active session best-effort (nullable), and inserts each via `store.learnings.create({tier:'provisional'})`. It writes directly to SQLite (the `learnings` table is not a git artifact, like the activity log / port leases), never stages to the working tree, and never blocks the wrap (parse/insert failures degrade to a skip). Registered in the prawduct pipeline after `learnings-capture` (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`, `schemaRevision` 3→4 so existing installs get the step at the correct position via the framework-owned-subtree resync; the additive merge-by-id path also appends it, and post-`commit` placement would be harmless anyway since the DB insert isn't part of the commit). `project-map`-style live-state steps are unaffected. Tests: `test/wrap-step-learnings-db-write.test.js` (+14 — today-entry parser incl. multi-entry/preamble/no-novel-sentinel/hyphen-separator, and handler insert / dedup-idempotence / partial-new / session-attribution / skip cases); pipeline + skills + sessions step-list/count assertions updated (11→12). Docs: `docs/session-rules-self-improvement.md` "Learnings ingestion".

### Fixed

- **`features-toc` wrap step now diffs the session (`<lastWrapSha>..HEAD`), not the branch (`<base>...HEAD`), so the Feature Index accrues entries under the merge-PRs-then-wrap workflow (#465).** The step computed drift with `git diff --name-only <base>...HEAD`, but under TC's own canonical workflow — feature branch → PR → squash-merge to `main` → wrap while checked out on `main` — that range is empty (HEAD *is* the base), so the step skipped with `no files touched against main` on every wrap and `FEATURES.md` never gained stubs (which in turn starved the downstream `index-describe` step of stubs to fill). New `_resolveSessionRange()` prefers `<lastWrapSha>..HEAD` (two-dot — every commit merged since the previous wrap, regardless of branch topology; `lastWrapSha` is already stamped by the commit step) and falls back to the prior `<base>...HEAD` on the first wrap or when the recorded SHA no longer resolves (rebase / fresh clone). The recorded SHA is shape-validated (`/^[0-9a-f]{7,64}$/i`) and peeled with `^{commit}` before it's interpolated into the range, so a malformed value degrades to the branch fallback rather than reaching a shell. `project-map` is unaffected — it reflects the live filesystem/store, not a branch diff. Tests: `test/wrap-step-features-toc.test.js` (+6 — `_resolveSessionRange` preference/fallback/malformed-SHA/null cases + a wrap-on-main handler regression proving files merged this session are stubbed even though `main...HEAD` is empty).

### Security

- **TC's router fails closed on auth-bypass paths Caddy and `new URL` normalize differently (#473, closes the normalization axis of the #472 residual-risk #2 leak class).** #434/#472 fixed the *case* axis of the Caddy-gate-vs-TC-router mismatch; this closes the remaining normalization axes. Caddy decides `basic_auth` bypass against the **decoded, path-cleaned** target, but TC's router parses the **raw** target with `new URL` — so three variant shapes were waved through *unauthenticated* by Caddy yet missed the OpenClaw proxy route in TC and fell through to the unauthenticated SPA shell: `/openclaw-direct//x` (duplicate slash → empty connId segment), `//openclaw-direct/x` (leading `//` → `new URL` host-hijacks the path to `/x`), and `/openclaw-direct%2Fx` (`%2F` stays encoded in `new URL`). New `caddy.caddyCanonicalPath(rawUrl)` reproduces Caddy's match-time canonicalization (percent-decode → collapse duplicate slashes → resolve `.`/`..`, preserving a literal trailing slash — **not** Node's `path.normalize`, which keeps a leading `//` and strips trailing slashes, both parity-breaking) and `caddy.isCaddyAuthBypassPath(rawUrl)` tests it against the single-source-of-truth bypass matcher. `server.js#handleRequest` adds a fail-closed guard after static-file serving: any request whose Caddy-canonical path is still a bypass path but reached the SPA fallback did **not** resolve to its intended handler (health via `/api`, the OpenClaw proxy, the manifest file), so it 404s instead of serving fallback content. Genuine bypass paths keep their handlers (the real `/manifest.json` file still serves; `/api/health` still routes); ordinary non-bypass SPA routes are untouched. The canonicalizer is verified byte-for-byte against a live `caddy run` (2.11.4) across 20 normalization variants incl. encoded `..%2f`, trailing-slash, and malformed-`%` cases. Tests: `test/caddy.test.js` (+21 canonicalizer/predicate parity cases), `test/server.test.js` (+5 guard integration cases, each a regression test that fails without the guard). WS-upgrade path was already fail-closed (`socket.destroy()` on unresolved connId — no content served). Related open thread: #470 (WS proxy header injection, same two-layer-auth family).
- **OpenClaw WebSocket proxy injects the gateway token instead of forwarding the browser's caddy Basic credential (#470, same two-layer-auth family as #473).** The HTTP proxy (`_openclawProxyHeaders`) and the WS-upgrade proxy (`handleUpgrade`, both the `/openclaw-direct/` and `/openclaw/` branches) handled `Authorization` asymmetrically: the HTTP path overwrote it with `Bearer <gatewayToken>`, but the WS path let an *incoming* `Authorization` win and injected the token only when none was present. Behind the caddy `basic_auth` ingress the browser attaches `Authorization: Basic <caddy creds>` to same-origin WS handshakes, so TC forwarded the operator's caddy credentials to the downstream OpenClaw gateway instead of the gateway token — harmless against current OpenClaw (≤2026.6.11 authenticates in-band and ignores the handshake header) but a latent credential leak to the gateway host and a break waiting for any OpenClaw version that validates the handshake `Authorization`. Both WS branches now share a single `_openclawWsRequestLines()` builder (so the auth rule cannot drift between them again — the symmetric-gates lesson the issue cites), and both proxy paths now apply the same rule: **always strip the incoming `Authorization`** (the caddy Basic header is meaningless to the gateway and must not leak downstream), then inject `Bearer <gatewayToken>` when a token is configured. `_openclawProxyHeaders` was correspondingly hardened to `delete` the incoming header even when no token is set (previously it forwarded the Basic header downstream in that case). Tests: `test/server.test.js` (+8 — HTTP/WS Authorization rules incl. the no-token no-leak case, WS request-line/origin/referer/header preservation, and an explicit HTTP↔WS symmetry assertion).

## [4.3.0] - 2026-07-04

### Added

- **Boot adoption + cutover now preserve the live tailnet HTTPS site (#434 Chunk 2 — completes #434).** New config field `caddyTailnetHost` (default null) + new extractor `caddy.extractTailnetHost(content)`: a top-level site block headed by a bare FQDN that carries a `tls` directive (which distinguishes it from the ACME public-domain site, whose block has no `tls`); returns null when absent or ambiguous (never guess, mirroring `extractBasicAuthCredential`). `adoptCredentialIntoConfig` adopts the host into config at boot/cutover, and `scripts/ingress-cutover.js` passes `tailnetHost` through to the generator — so a future cutover reproduces the 2026-07-04 hand-edit (tailnet HTTPS site + http→https redirect) instead of dropping remote OpenClaw access. **Design deviation from the build plan, recorded there (Decision 7 amendment): shape adoption is DECOUPLED from credential adoption.** The plan said "mirror the `caddyRemoteHttp` pattern", but an exact mirror nests shape adoption behind the `config-already-has-credential` early return — and on the live box the credential was already adopted (#463), so the tailnet host would have been orphaned forever. Shapes (remote-HTTP catch-all, tailnet host) now adopt independently, never overwrite a set config field, and a tailnet host equal to `publicDomain` is ignored. `adoptCredentialIntoConfig` gains a `changed` return field (any adoption persisted) alongside the unchanged `adopted` (credential adopted); the cutover keys its config refresh off `changed` so a shape-only adoption reaches the plan (dry-run preview `applyDryRunAdoptionPreview` mirrors the same decoupling — one preview test updated to pin the new contract, strengthened not weakened: it now also asserts the credential stays untouched while shapes preview). Extractors verified read-only against the real live cursatory Caddyfile (host, catch-all, and credential all extracted correctly). Tests: `test/auth-credential-durability.test.js` (+14: extractor unit coverage incl. the redirect-block false-positive and multi-site ambiguity, the live-cursatory credential-already-adopted scenario, overwrite/publicDomain guards, idempotence, cutover round-trip). The live Caddyfile stays hand-edited and load-bearing — running a cutover on cursatory remains a separately-VRF'd operator step.

## [4.2.1] - 2026-07-04

### Security

- **`buildCaddyfileContent` gates with a case-sensitive `path_regexp` matcher instead of the case-insensitive `path` matcher (#434, folds in #472 Critic residual-risk #2).** Caddy's `path` matcher is case-insensitive, so a request to `/OPENCLAW-DIRECT/x` (or `/API/HEALTH`) slipped past the `not path` bypass gate; TC's case-sensitive router then missed the proxy route and served the unauthenticated SPA shell. The bypass is now an anchored RE2 regex (`^(/api/health|/openclaw-direct/.*|/manifest\.json)$`, case-sensitive, `.` escaped literal) applied to every gated site block, so only exact-cased bypass paths are exempt. Verified with a live `caddy run` probe: uppercase variants → 401, correctly-cased paths bypass, path traversal (`/openclaw-direct/../api/system`) still 401 (Caddy canonicalizes before matching), authed requests reach the upstream. Tests in `test/caddy.test.js`.

### Internal

- **`buildCaddyfileContent` can now emit the tailnet HTTPS site + http→https redirect (#434, generator half).** New `tailnetHost` option: when set (with basic_auth — fail-closed guard, an ungated remote HTTPS site throws), the generator emits a gated HTTPS site for the tailnet FQDN (reusing the local mkcert cert, whose SAN must include the FQDN) plus an `http://<host>` → `https://<host>:<port>{uri}` redirect, and adds `auto_https disable_redirects` so the explicit redirect governs. This codifies the 2026-07-04 hand-edit that unblocked remote OpenClaw access (OpenClaw 2026.6.11+ Control UI requires a secure context). Not yet wired into config adoption or the cutover — that is #434 Chunk 2 — so no operator-visible behavior change yet; the generator is capability-only. Tests in `test/caddy.test.js`.

## [4.2.0] - 2026-07-04

### Added

- **Wrap commits no longer dangle: the commit step auto-opens a PR and arms auto-merge after auto-branching (#467).** Since #264, a wrap that fires on `main`/`master` auto-branches to `wrap/<ts>-<slug>` and commits there — but nothing landed that branch, so the wrap's version bump, CHANGELOG promotion, and self-healed index files (#423/#425) evaporated for the next session (the #447/#450/#453/#464 manual-rescue class; TangleBrain re-self-healed FEATURES.md/PROJECT-MAP.md on every single wrap). The commit step now closes the loop after an auto-branched commit: pushes the wrap branch, opens a PR back to the original branch via `gh` (What/Why body embedding the wrap commit's body lines; best-effort `chore` label), arms `gh pr merge --auto --squash --delete-branch` (branch protection still gates — this removes the wait, never the checks), and returns the checkout to the original branch on full success. Every sub-step is non-fatal: the commit already landed, so failures degrade to `output.autoPr.{skippedReason|error, remediation}` and HEAD stays on the wrap branch as the visible rescue cue. Gates: per-project `wrapAutoPrEnabled` opt-out (new project-config flag, default true), no-`origin`-remote skip, `gh`-unavailable → push-only. The wrap drawer's commit row renders the outcome (e.g. `<sha> · wrap PR auto-merge armed`). Companion fix (Critic-caught): `continuity-write` now anchors its freshness stamp and Map delta to the commit step's recorded `{commitSha, branch}` from `previousResults` instead of HEAD (`_resolveCommitAnchor`) — without it, the close-loop's checkout-back would have made the post-wrap `main...HEAD` delta empty and recorded the wrong sha/branch in the continuity resume index. Tests: `test/wrap-step-commit-autopr.test.js` (full success, opt-out, no-remote, push/create/merge-arm failures, gh-missing, label best-effort, throw degradation, feature-branch/allowDirectToMain null) + drawer detail cases + continuity anchor cases. Docs: ADR 0002 amendment, user-guide "Wrapping a Session".

## [4.1.0] - 2026-07-03

### Fixed

- **Ingress basic_auth credential is now durable — no more single-copy-in-the-Caddyfile lockouts (#397, 2026-07-03 incident).** On 2026-07-03 the operator was locked out of remote access when the live Caddyfile's `basic_auth` hash was replaced during the v4 upgrade window. Investigation correction for the record: **v4.0.0 has no startup Caddyfile-regeneration path and no code that generates a random credential** (verified: `writeCaddyfile`/`buildCaddyfileContent` are reachable only from `scripts/ingress-cutover.js` and `reset-admin`'s in-place patch; every hash originates from an operator-supplied password) — the runbook §1b theory doesn't match the code, and the writer that night remains unidentified. The *structural* root cause is real regardless: the working credential existed ONLY inside the hand-edited Caddyfile, so any regeneration lost it, and with an empty config a cutover would have emitted an **ungated** ingress (worse than lockout).
