Fixes, all fail-closed: **(1) boot-time adoption** — in caddy mode the server adopts the live Caddyfile's credential (and remote-HTTP shape) into canonical config at startup, READ-ONLY on the file, never overwriting an existing config credential, refusing ambiguous multi-user files (`caddy.adoptCredentialIntoConfig`, called from server boot; cutover runs it too with the mode-gate lifted); **(2) refuse-to-ungate** — `planCutover` now throws rather than replace a gated Caddyfile with an ungated one; **(3) the remote plain-HTTP catch-all shape is codified** — new `caddyRemoteHttp` config key + `remoteHttpCatchAll` generator option emit the Basic-Auth-gated `http:// { ... }` site + `auto_https disable_redirects` (the 2026-06-23 hand-edit that a cutover would have destroyed), with the generator throwing on an ungated catch-all (open-door guard); output without the option is byte-identical to before. `scripts/reset-admin.js` already synced config (verified, no change needed). Tests: `test/auth-credential-durability.test.js` — extraction from both file shapes, adoption (adopt/no-overwrite/ambiguous/idempotent/read-only), byte-for-byte hash re-emission through regenerate→extract→regenerate, refuse-to-ungate, catch-all emission + open-door guard. Docs: `deploy/INGRESS.md` "Credential durability" section; the machine-local EMERGENCY-RECOVERY.md §1b corrected in place.

### Changed

- **OpenClaw no longer appears in the project engine picker (#459).** Assigning an OpenClaw connection as a project's engine never gave a local project an LLM — it opened a portal to the remote agent working in the REMOTE workspace, so presenting it as a peer of "Claude Code" in the LLM dropdown misled (and the base profile rendered as "OpenClaw (not installed)" noise, since `detection: null` can never succeed). Both entry kinds are gone from the picker: the base profile (new declarative `pickerHidden: true` profile flag, filtered in `engines.listWithAvailability`) and the per-connection virtual engines (`openclaw:<connId>` — the `availableAsEngine` appending block removed; the flag is now vestigial, its checkbox/badge/detail-row dropped from the connection UI, and the DB column persists untouched with no migration). Registered instances remain reachable through the top-bar OpenClaw panel — connections, tunnels, ClawBridge, and wrap capture are all unchanged, and `getWithAvailability('openclaw:<id>')`/base-profile resolution still work for launch plumbing. The shared `buildEngineOptions` builders (ui.js/session.js) lost the dead optgroup branch and gained a hardening fallback: a project bound to an engine the server no longer lists (hidden or retired) renders its current selection as "(unavailable)" instead of silently showing the wrong choice. Verified live pre-change: zero projects were bound to any `openclaw:*` engine. Tests: `test/openclaw-engine.test.js` picker-exclusion block (per-connection + base + launch-path resolution retained); docs (engine-guide, openclaw-setup) updated.

### Removed

- **Gemini CLI engine retired (#457).** Google sunset Gemini CLI for individual accounts on 2026-06-18 (Antigravity is the successor); the bundled profile pointed at a dead service. `data/engines/gemini.json` deleted, and a new **retired-engine tombstone pass** in `store.js#_syncBundledEngines` (`RETIRED_ENGINE_IDS`) removes the stale synced copy from `~/.tangleclaw/engines/` on boot — without it, the union semantics of #251 would have silently promoted the leftover file to an immortal "operator profile" (the ADR-0001 asymmetric-gate hazard flagged in the issue). The three gemini-bound projects (gemtest, Kobold, Medusa) were migrated to `antigravity` live via the API before removal (operator-ratified manual migration; `.antigravity.md` configs regenerated on PATCH). The `gemini-md` generator and `_generateGeminiMd` markdown builder STAY — antigravity's `antigravity-md` case reuses the builder, and the generator name remains valid for custom profiles. The co-author strip hook keeps `gemini` in its vendor list (historical commits still matter). Gemini-profile-specific tests retired with the engine (yolo-parity flags, `.gemini/` subdirectory filename); profile-independent coverage ported to antigravity; parity lists now assert gemini does NOT resurface.
- **genesis placeholder engine removed (#458).** Non-functional profile (`command: null`, `launch: null`, null detection target) that showed up as a selectable "(not installed)" engine option. Same tombstone mechanism as #457. The "engine with no config file → skipped" code path stays (OpenClaw uses it); genesis badge CSS dropped from `session.css`; parity/status/API tests now assert absence. Zero projects were bound to it.

### Added

- **Antigravity engine (#456).** Google's Gemini CLI successor (`agy`) is now a built-in engine — Gemini CLI stopped serving individual accounts on 2026-06-18, leaving TC with no working Google-engine path. New bundled profile `data/engines/antigravity.json`: detection `which agy`, session-based launch in tmux, prime prompt via the generic tmux-typed injection, and launch modes pinned to the real agy v1.0.10 flag surface — Interactive (default), Sandbox (`--sandbox`), Bypass (`--dangerously-skip-permissions`, warning-gated); Gemini's Auto-Edit/Plan-Only modes were deliberately NOT carried over (agy has no `--approval-mode`). Config generation targets `.antigravity.md` at the project root (Antigravity's recommended context file, precedence over its `GEMINI.md`/`AGENTS.md` compat reads) via a new `antigravity-md` generator case that reuses the gemini-md markdown builder with a parameterized header — gemini output stays byte-identical (regression-pinned). Status monitoring reuses the `google-incidents` adapter with `productName: "Gemini"` (agy fronts Gemini models; model-serving incidents carry that name). Also: engine badge color in `session.css`, `antigravity` added to the co-author strip hook's vendor list (installed hooks refresh on next sync via content-drift detection), engine-guide + README updated (Gemini CLI marked sunset, pointing at #457 for retirement). Tests: `test/antigravity-engine.test.js` (profile contract, launch-mode flag pins, config-gen header + gemini regression, CSS surface) + parity/status-parity/API list assertions + strip-hook trailer test; suite 3711/0/1.

### Internal

- **README rewritten for the 4.0 release.** The storefront was frozen at the v3.15 era (title still said "TangleClaw v3"; no mention of continuity, auth, Project Master, orchestration profiles, session rules, or Project Map). Rewrite covers the full 4.x surface: new "What TangleClaw Does" feature list with 4.0 callouts, a "How Do I…?" task-to-doc quick-reference table (links into `docs/user-guide.md` anchors, `deploy/INGRESS.md`, and the rest of `docs/`), a rewritten Security section reflecting the Caddy ingress option (the "no authentication exists" claim is no longer the whole story), the ingress in the architecture diagram, refreshed counts (3,600+ tests, 115+ routes; were 1,314/62), the one-click Update & restart path, a rename note for pre-4.0 clones, the stale "#139 Chunk 11c lands" wrap-V2 section dropped (long since default; ADR 0002 remains the contract home), and a roadmap refresh (shipped items removed; Switchboard/Master-actions/cross-model governance added). Doc-only; no behavior change.

## [4.0.0] - 2026-07-03

### Changed

- **BREAKING: repo renamed `TangleClaw-v3` → `TangleClaw` (chunk R / #183 — the last 4.0 box).** The vestigial `-v3` suffix is dropped as the 4.0 identity reset. Executed per the pre-flight inventory (`.claude/plans/r-rename-preflight-inventory.md`): disk root moved to `~/Documents/Projects/TangleClaw` (the GitHub repo/remote already carried the new name), the Claude auto-memory dir re-keyed to the new path key (the old key retained as the plan-mandated backup), and the TC DB `projects` row migrated. Product code needed **zero changes** — paths are relative/`__dirname`-based throughout; the one hardcoded absolute was fixed in the #451 pre-step, and its regression guard keeps `public/*.js` clean. A compat symlink `TangleClaw-v3 → TangleClaw` bridges the ~13 managed projects whose `.claude/settings.json` SessionStart hooks still carry the old absolute path — `syncEngineHooks` rewrites each at that project's next session launch (lib/sessions.js), after which the symlink can be dropped. Non-repo stores updated in place: `~/.tangleclaw/EMERGENCY-RECOVERY.md` (backup kept), `.claude/priming/build-session.md` (history note added), `.prawduct/project-state.yaml` + continuity-index titles. Verified from the new root: session launch + memory recall + server cwd, launchd plists/engine configs/`config.json` clean, suite **3696/0 (1 skipped)**. Breaking for anything outside TC's regeneration reach that holds the old absolute path or clone URL.

### Fixed

- **Self-update prompt no longer hardcodes the install path (#183, chunk R pre-step).** `buildUpdatePrompt` in `public/session.js` embedded a literal `cd ~/Documents/Projects/TangleClaw-v3` — wrong the moment the checkout is renamed or relocated (the #183 rename would have shipped stale self-update instructions). The `/api/update-status` payload now carries `repoRoot` (resolved from `__dirname` in `lib/update-checker.js`, which also consolidates its two ad-hoc `path.join(__dirname, '..')` git-cwd computations onto the same constant), and the client derives the `cd` step from it — degrading to "ask the operator for the path" if the field is ever absent rather than inventing a location. This was the ONLY hardcoded install path in product code (pre-flight inventory, `.claude/plans/r-rename-preflight-inventory.md`); a new regression guard fails the suite if any `public/*.js` grows one again. No `CACHE_NAME` bump — `session.js` is network-first (same rationale as #431), so a plain reload delivers it (Critic-caught: the first draft bumped it on the false "precached" premise). Tests: `test/update-prompt-path.test.js` (structural + the no-hardcoded-path sweep) + `repoRoot`-presence behavioral assertions in `test/update-checker.test.js`.

## [3.32.0] - 2026-07-03

### Added

- **Project Master — slice 3 (final): the in-session drawer + the shared terminal-frame pipeline (chunk G / #331; UI-4C7R).** The master's second surface completes the ratified "reach it without leaving a session" requirement (D7): a **🧠** button in the session banner opens a bottom drawer (peek-drawer pattern — backdrop, handle, 60vh terminal) embedding the same attach-only ttyd iframe onto `tangleclaw-master`, with the identical **ensure-then-attach** contract as the landing pane: opening POSTs `/api/master/ensure` (idempotent; refreshes the master's `CLAUDE.md` identity), the status dot walks pending→live/down, and the iframe src is set **only after ensure succeeds** (ttyd attaches to existing sessions only); failures surface the real server error (`api.lastError`) with a Retry button; re-entrancy + attach-once guards; **no polling** (no-UI-timers rule #98/#268). Closing only hides the surface — the master session persists (launch on first open, then persist). Alongside it, **backlog UI-4C7R lands in full**: the per-page xterm theme palettes (`XTERM_THEMES` in session.js / `MASTER_XTERM_THEMES` in ui.js) and the *triplicating* readiness-retry wiring collapse into `public/api-helper.js` — `TC_XTERM_THEMES` + `tcApplyTerminalTheme` (single palette source), `tcEnableLocalSelectionOverride` (the #431 ⌥+drag override, moved verbatim from session.js), and **`tcWireTerminalFrame(win, frame, getTheme)`**: ONE load-listener + readiness-retry pipeline applying theme + the #431 override + the #443 touch-scroll shim + #445 drag-copy to every terminal surface (session terminal, landing Master pane, new drawer). Per-page copies of this loop are what let #443's dead shim ship on two surfaces — structural tests now pin that they cannot return. Live theme switches repaint the drawer terminal too (`applyTerminalTheme` iterates both frames). `CACHE_NAME` v3-34→v3-35. **Docs:** new **ADR 0008** (the master session model — harness-session singleton, dedicated home, no `sessions` row — and the *instructional* v1 read-only boundary, with enforcement explicitly deferred to G2); `operational-spec.md` gains the master singleton in the service architecture; `data-model.md` records the deliberate no-DB-footprint decision. **Tests:** new `test/master-drawer-frontend.test.js` (structural: src-less iframe, ensure-before-attach ordering, close-persists guard, no-`setInterval`, exact SW pin) + new `test/terminal-frame-wiring.test.js` (behavioral — api-helper.js binds to `globalThis` under Node, so the real helpers run against fake frame/term/doc: palette fallback, retry cadence + bounded budget, cross-origin survival, mouseup-copy gating); the #431/#443/#445 structural suites re-pinned at the helpers' new home (guards moved, never weakened). VRFs consolidated into `VRF-g-master` (pane + drawer + copy/scroll parity). Completes chunk G — the last 4.0 box before R (#183).

### Internal

- **Terminal-gesture math extracted into pure functions with real unit tests (backlog UI-9J3F).** The #443 touch-scroll quantization and the #445 selection math were inline in the wiring closures, covered only by regex-on-source assertions — which catch deletion but not an off-by-one. Three pure functions in `public/api-helper.js` now own the math, each delegated to by the (unchanged-behavior) wiring: `tcQuantizeScrollDelta(accum, deltaY, lineHeight)` (line quantization with sub-line remainder carry and symmetric truncation), `tcCellFromPoint(point, rect, cols, rows, viewportY)` (finger→buffer-cell mapping: edge clamp + viewport scroll offset), `tcSelectionSpan(from, to, cols)` (anchor swap for backward drags + endpoint-inclusive length). New `test/terminal-math.test.js` (18 behavioral: remainder round-trip across a slow multi-move drag, flick batching, direction reversal, boundary/edge clamps, viewportY buffer-row mapping, both drag directions, row-first swap ordering). The behavioral pass immediately caught one real API wart: `Math.trunc` returns `-0` for sub-line upward totals — harmless inline (`-0 !== 0` is false) but wrong as a return value; normalized with `|| 0`. Structural pins re-pointed at the new homes (never weakened) + new delegation pins. No behavior change; no CACHE_NAME bump needed (`api-helper.js` is network-first; the precached `ui.js` is untouched).

## [3.31.0] - 2026-07-03

### Added

- **Project Master — slice 2: the landing-page Master pane (chunk G / #331).** The master session (slice 1) gets its first surface: a **🧠 Master** button in the landing header opens a collapsible panel embedding the verified ttyd terminal stack as an iframe onto the reserved tmux session `tangleclaw-master` — the Claude Code TUI IS the chat UI, no new chat transport. **Ensure-then-attach:** opening the panel POSTs `/api/master/ensure` (idempotent; also refreshes the master's `CLAUDE.md` identity) and sets the iframe src **only after ensure succeeds** — ttyd attaches to existing sessions only. Failure paths surface the real server error (`api.lastError`) with a Retry button. A **status dot** (header button + panel row) shows live/pending/down; a one-shot `GET /api/master/status` probe at page load colors it before the panel is ever opened — **no polling** (no-UI-timers rule #98/#268). The pane applies the same terminal enhancements as the session page (thin duplicate per the spec): operator theme pushed into the iframe's xterm instance, the #431 ⌥+drag local-selection override so copy reaches the browser clipboard, and the mobile touch-scroll shim (`term.scrollLines` in line increments — Critic-caught parity gap; iPhone Safari is the primary platform). `public/sw.js` `CACHE_NAME` bumped v3-31→v3-32 (no new script file — the logic lives in the precached `ui.js`). Tests: new `test/master-pane-frontend.test.js` (15 structural assertions: src-less iframe, ensure-before-attach ordering, re-entrancy guard, #431 override, touch-scroll shim, no-`setInterval` guard, SW bump). VRF enqueued (`VRF-g2-master-pane`).
- **Plain-drag terminal copy to the CLIENT clipboard + long-press selection on touch (#445).** Operators are mostly remote, and the #432 remedy (Option+drag) was verified working but undiscoverable ("a non standard way to do things"), while touch devices had NO selection path at all. New shared `tcWireTerminalDragCopy(win, term, doc)` in `public/api-helper.js` funnels the natural gestures into the already-verified #432 force-selection pipeline (local xterm selection → ttyd copy-on-select ✂ → the #431 mouseup re-copy): **desktop** — a capture-phase rewriter re-dispatches plain button-0 drags with BOTH force-selection modifiers set and lets xterm's own platform check pick the one it honors (`shouldForceSelection`: `altKey` on Mac gated by `macOptionClickForcesSelection`, `shiftKey` elsewhere — and xterm classifies iOS as NOT-Mac, the on-device discovery that killed alt-only synthetics) while the terminal app owns the mouse (`term.modes.mouseTrackingMode !== 'none'`); real modifier gestures, right-click, and non-tracking terminals pass through untouched; `altClickMovesCursor` forced off so rewritten clicks can't become arrow-key spam; a `buttons===0` hover guard disarms the rewriter after an off-iframe release (Critic-caught phantom-selection edge); a 1s **ghost-mouse suppression window** after any touch activity swallows iOS's synthesized post-lift mouse events, which otherwise re-selected one cell and clobbered the copied text. **Touch (7 on-device iterations — synthetic-mouse approaches failed on iOS)** — long-press (450ms, 12px slop) enters select mode and drives xterm's public `select(col,row,length)` API directly from finger→buffer-cell math (viewportY-adjusted, both drag directions); the touch-scroll shim (#443) yields via `doc.tcTouchSelectActive`; releasing surfaces a native-iOS-style **Copy pill** (44px touch target) whose TAP performs the clipboard write — Safari refused every touchend-time write, and a real click in the same document is the #435-proven flow; `tcCopyToClipboard` gained an optional `targetDoc` param because Safari scopes gesture permission to the touched FRAME (parent-document writes were silently refused). Pill lifecycle is state-driven — tap copies+hides, the next terminal touch dismisses — no timers (#98/#268). `-webkit-touch-callout: none` keeps iOS's magnifier out of the way. Both surfaces wired (session page + Master pane). **Verified on-device:** iPhone Safari select→pill→paste (operator, 2026-07-02) + elkaholic Chrome plain-drag→auto-copy→paste. **Design note:** issue #445's sketched `/api/host-clipboard` bridge (option B) was NOT built — the pure client-side rewrite achieves the same UX with no new API surface and none of the host-clipboard security exposure the issue flagged. **Trade-off (deliberate):** while the app tracks the mouse, plain clicks/drags no longer reach the TUI — selection wins; Claude Code's own host-side drag-copy no longer triggers. `CACHE_NAME` v3-33→v3-34. Tests: new `test/terminal-drag-copy.test.js` (structural: platform-modifier pins, no-rewrite-loop guard, tracking-mode gate, phantom-selection disarm, long-press mechanics, scroll-shim yield, both call sites, SW bump).

### Fixed

- **Terminal touch-scroll was dead on iOS — on BOTH the session page and the new Master pane (#443).** Caught on-device during `VRF-g2-master-pane` (the #435-class blind spot working exactly as designed): one-finger drag on the terminal scrolled the *browser page*, never the terminal. Two defects in the old per-page shims: (1) **wrong target** — listeners attached to `.xterm-viewport`, but xterm's screen layer (`.xterm-screen`, later in DOM order) paints above it, so touches never reached them; (2) **passive listeners** — `{ passive: true }` can't stop iOS's native pan from claiming the gesture, so the outer page scrolled instead. Fix: ONE shared `tcWireTerminalTouchScroll(win, term, doc)` in `public/api-helper.js` (the both-pages base, home of the #430 copy helper) — listens on `.xterm-screen` (→ `.xterm` → `body` fallbacks), non-passive `touchmove` + `preventDefault()`, injects `touch-action: none` on the terminal layers, and translates the drag into **synthetic wheel events** dispatched at the touch target in line-sized batches — the exact pipeline desktop scrolling uses, so it inherits xterm's mode handling (tmux `mouse on` → wheel reported to tmux → server-side copy-mode scrollback; mouse tracking off → xterm local scrollback). A first on-device iteration used `term.scrollLines()` (xterm's local buffer only) and moved nothing — the wheel path is the one proven daily on desktop. The single-touch guard runs before `preventDefault`, so pinch-zoom is untouched. Both surfaces now delegate: `session.js` wires it from the terminal readiness retry (the old shim also raced xterm init at iframe-load time) and drops `setupTerminalTouchScroll`; `ui.js` drops `wireMasterTouchScroll` — partially delivering backlog UI-4C7R (touch-scroll is now shared; theme + copy override extraction remains for chunk G slice 3). `CACHE_NAME` v3-32→v3-33. **Verified on-device** (iPhone Safari, operator, 2026-07-02; a mid-iteration "page won't load" scare was the phone's service worker wedged between the two same-day cache-generation bumps — cleared via Settings → Safari → Website Data, not a code defect). Tests: new `test/terminal-touch-scroll.test.js` (11: target-chain pin with a no-`.xterm-viewport`-listener guard, non-passive + `preventDefault` ordering, wheel-event construction in the iframe realm with a no-`scrollLines`-resurrection guard, `touch-action` injection, idempotency, both-call-sites delegation, SW bump + network-first pin).

## [3.30.0] - 2026-07-01

### Added

- **Project Master — the global read-only assistant, slice 1: the session singleton + API (chunk G / #331).** ONE persistent AI assistant **above all projects** — a read-only cross-project control plane ("which projects have open PRs?", "what's stale?") — begins landing. Architecture (ratified 2026-06-16, spec `.prawduct/artifacts/g-project-master.md`): **harness-session-backed** — a persistent Claude Code session in the reserved tmux session **`tangleclaw-master`**, NOT a TC-owned LLM chat loop, and deliberately **not a `sessions` row or project** (the wrap pipeline, idle watchdog, dashboard cards, and ownership objects all key on projects; none apply — a structural test pins that the module never touches the sessions store). Its home is **`~/.tangleclaw/master/`** — a dedicated data directory, never a repo clone (which would share git HEAD with dev sessions). New `lib/master.js`: `ensureMasterSession()` (idempotent — creates the home, **regenerates a TC-generated `CLAUDE.md` identity on every call** so guide/token changes propagate, and launches the default engine in the tmux session only when absent; refuses with a typed error when the engine binary is missing) + `getMasterStatus()` (liveness truth straight from tmux — no DB row to drift) + pure `buildMasterClaudeMd()` (the identity: read-only administrator role and hard rules, the TC API base URL from config, a read-endpoint quick reference, and — when the AUTH-4 M2M gate is on — the bearer-token Authentication block for the gated PortHub/shared-docs surfaces). Two operator routes in `server.js` (outside the M2M-gated set): `POST /api/master/ensure` and `GET /api/master/status`. **Lifecycle (operator-chosen):** launch on first open, then persist — no boot-time launch from the launchd daemon context. **v1 read-only boundary is instructional** (CLAUDE.md rules + no project checkout by construction), not API-enforced — enforcement via a scoped token is a G2+ concern, documented rather than silently claimed. **Out of scope (later slices):** the landing-page pane (slice 2), the in-session drawer + ADR/docs (slice 3); actions/session-relay are G2 (needs Switchboard #333). **Tests:** new `test/master.test.js` (13: identity marker/role/read-only rules, base-URL from config, token-block gating both ways, ensure create/idempotent-regenerate, the full refusal matrix — engine unavailable, engine profile not found, no launch command (no bare-shell master), tmux create-false and thrown — the no-sessions-row structural guard, tmux-truth status, and both routes over real HTTP with the ensure handler stubbed — tests must never launch a real engine).

## [3.29.0] - 2026-06-30

### Added

- **Index auto-describe + Feature-Index self-heal parity (PIDX / #425, #426).** The two AI-orientation indexes only deliver value once their description stubs are *filled* — the descriptions **are** the product. Two changes close that gap. **(A) Feature-Index self-heal (#425):** `features-toc` now mirrors the Project Map's #423 self-heal — when `featureIndexEnabled` is on but `FEATURES.md` is missing, it **creates** the file from `projects.FEATURE_INDEX_TEMPLATE` (then appends any session drift onto the seed) instead of skipping forever; the wrap commit body reads `- Feature Index: created [(N stub(s) appended)]`. **Why:** the toggle — not file deletion — is the off-switch, so a missing index under an enabled toggle is an anomaly to recover (fresh clone where it wasn't committed, delete-to-regenerate, a toggle path that didn't seed), not a permanent skip. **(B) Auto-describe (#426):** a new non-blocking `index-describe` wrap step (`lib/wrap-steps/index-describe.js`, wired into `STEP_DISPATCH` + the prawduct template after `project-map`, before `memory-update`) drives the live session's AI to fill **only the empty `<!-- describe -->` stubs** in the enabled index file(s) with a one-line note based on each directory's / feature's actual contents — curation-preserving (already-described entries are never overwritten, no entries added/removed). It reuses the existing `ai-content` send→poll machinery (the AI edits files directly; the commit's `git add -A` picks the edits up), then re-scans each file to report the **honest filled count** (`- Index: described N stub(s)`). **Decision — clobber-avoidance:** `features-toc`/`project-map` *stage* their writes for the commit-step flush, so `index-describe` **skips any file with a pending staged write this wrap** (the flush would otherwise overwrite the AI's descriptions); brand-new stubs added this wrap get described on the *next* wrap — a self-converging one-wrap lag. Both index files keep their own toggle; the step no-ops when neither is on or no enabled file has empty, non-pending stubs. **Tests:** new `test/wrap-step-index-describe.test.js` (`+18`: stub-count/prompt purity, gate + clobber-avoidance skips, happy-path delegate→re-scan→count, honest partial-fill count, never-blocks-on-ai-failure, commit body line) + `test/wrap-step-features-toc.test.js` self-heal create paths + the two `created` body lines; prawduct pipeline step-list pins updated 10→11 across `wrap-pipeline`/`sessions`/`skills` tests. Also corrected **2 stale source-assertion tests** orphaned by #430 (`test/upload-modal-frontend.test.js`, `test/openclaw-setup-readme.test.js`): #430 routed the copy sites through the shared `tcCopyToClipboard` helper but their `navigator.clipboard.writeText(...)` regex pins weren't updated, so they were red on `main` — re-pinned to `tcCopyToClipboard(...)`. Full suite **3573 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/index-auto-describe.md`. Closes #425, #426.

- **Project Map: self-heal — create the index on wrap when it's missing (#423).** The `project-map` wrap step previously *skipped* when `PROJECT-MAP.md` was absent (the file was only ever created at toggle-on). Now, when the toggle is on and the file is missing, the step **creates** it from the current top-level skeleton + group membership (staged through the commit flush), and the wrap commit body reads `- Project Map: created (N dir(s))`. **Why:** the toggle is the operator's intent and the *off-switch* — file deletion is not — so a missing index is an anomaly to recover (fresh clone where it wasn't committed, delete-to-regenerate, a toggle enabled through a path that didn't seed), not a permanent skip. Matters when enabling Project Map across many/large projects, where a silently-missing map defeats the point. The create is as cheap as a refresh — **one top-level `readdir`, no tree walk, no file reads** — so it stays millisecond-scale even on a 300k-line repo (`lib/wrap-steps/project-map.js` `created` branch; `commit.js:_buildBodyLines` "created" line; `_buildProjectMapContent` reused). **Tests:** `+2` `test/wrap-step-project-map.test.js` (self-heal create path + the "created" commit body line); the prior "skips when missing" assertion is replaced by the create contract. Full suite **3557 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. ADR 0007 updated (self-heal + the top-level-only compute property). Closes #423.

- **Project Map: freshness wrap-step (PIDX slice 3 / #360, #356).** A new `project-map` wrap step (`lib/wrap-steps/project-map.js`, wired into `STEP_DISPATCH` + the prawduct template after `features-toc`) keeps `PROJECT-MAP.md` current on every wrap — the "self-regulating file-map" half of #360. It refreshes the `## Structure` skeleton (top-level dirs added/removed) and the `## Shared directories / doc groups` snapshot (current group membership) against the **live filesystem + store** (no git, unlike `features-toc`, since a directory added directly on disk should surface even if no tracked file changed). The refresh is **section-scoped, curation-preserving, and idempotent** (ADR 0007): surviving directories keep their hand-written descriptions verbatim, new dirs get `<!-- describe -->` stubs, vanished dirs are dropped, and the header comment + any operator-added sections are left untouched — pure helpers `_refreshProjectMapContent` / `_mergeStructureBody` / `_replaceSectionBody` / `_parseStructureDirs` in `lib/projects.js`. Idempotence makes the drift check a plain `newContent === existing` compare: no change ⇒ the step skips and the file's mtime stays stable; a change ⇒ the new content is staged through the commit step's single-transaction `_flushStagedWrites` and the wrap commit body carries a `- Project Map: refreshed (+A/-R dir(s))` audit line (`commit.js:_buildBodyLines`, `mapRefresh` duck-type). `lib/wrap-steps/project-map.js` lazy-`require`s `../projects` inside `run()` to break the `projects → sessions → wrap-pipeline → wrap-steps/project-map` module cycle (`features-toc` sidesteps it by never requiring `../projects`). **Tests:** `+18` `test/project-map.test.js` (parse/merge/replace/refresh incl. byte-idempotence, curation + operator-section preservation, membership refresh, add/drop dirs) + new `test/wrap-step-project-map.test.js` (gate skips, no-drift skip, staged shape, both commit body lines); prawduct pipeline step-list pins updated 9→10 across `wrap-pipeline`/`sessions`/`skills` tests. Full suite **3556 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Docs: ADR 0007 (section-scoped freshness); `VRF-pidx-slice3-project-map-freshness` enqueued; closes #360 + #356 (via PR). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/pidx-project-map.md`.

- **Project Map: shared-dir / doc-group membership (PIDX slice 2 / #356).** The `PROJECT-MAP.md` "Shared directories / doc groups" section is now populated from the project's actual shared-doc group membership instead of a placeholder: on toggle-on, `_collectProjectGroups(projectId)` reads `store.projectGroups.getByProject` + `store.sharedDocs.getByGroup` and `_buildSharedDirsSection(groups)` renders each group as `- **<name>** → \`<absolute sharedDir>\`` with its registered docs nested beneath (with honest "(no shared directory)" / "(no docs registered)" / "not a member of any shared-doc group" fallbacks) — so the agent stops filesystem-hunting for where shared docs live. `_buildProjectMapContent`/`_seedProjectMapFile` gained an optional `groups` param (backward-compatible — structure-only callers unchanged). The membership is a point-in-time snapshot at toggle-on; the slice-3 freshness wrap-step keeps it current. **Verified the #356 secondary concern (on-launch sync):** the launch-time `syncFromDirectory` re-scan (`lib/sessions.js`, pre-existing) already picks up newly-added `.md` files — pinned by a new regression test (register doc A, add doc B to the same shared dir, re-sync → B registers, A is skipped) — so no fix was needed, only the guard. **Tests:** `+7` `test/project-map.test.js` (section rendering incl. empty/no-dir/no-docs, `_collectProjectGroups` mapping + non-throw, content embedding, the seed-on-toggle-with-real-membership integration) + `+1` `test/store-shareddocs.test.js` (the #356 incremental re-scan regression). Full suite **3534 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/pidx-project-map.md`.

- **Project Map index — "where things live" (PIDX slice 1 / #360, #356).** A new per-project `PROJECT-MAP.md` at the project root: a structural "go here first" map the agent consults before grepping or filesystem-hunting, distinct from FEATURES.md (which maps features→paths; this maps the layout itself). New engine-agnostic `projectMapEnabled` toggle (Settings, mirrors the Feature Index toggle); on toggle-on, `_seedProjectMapFile` (`lib/projects.js`) seeds `PROJECT-MAP.md` with an auto-generated top-level-directory skeleton (`_listTopLevelDirs` filters `node_modules`/`dist`/`build`/`coverage`/`.git`/hidden dirs) — each directory a `<!-- describe -->` stub — plus a placeholder shared-directories section (populated in slice 2). Idempotent (never overwrites a curated file; toggle-off does not delete it). The SessionStart prime emits a **reference pointer** — a `## Project Map` section telling the agent the file exists and to consult it first — rather than inlining the map body (a deliberate difference from FEATURES.md: the map grows with the project, so spending prime budget echoing it every session is wasteful; #360 point 3). Same symmetric gate as the Feature Index (`projectMapEnabled && silentPrime && supportsSilentPrime`), and the pointer is emitted only when the file exists and is non-empty. `CACHE_NAME` `v3-25`→`v3-26`. **Decision:** new additive index, not a unification of the three index artifacts (FEATURES.md/structure/shared-dir) — unify deferred and documented to avoid reworking shipped #207 machinery mid-4.0. **Out of scope (later slices):** shared-dir/doc-group membership population (#356, slice 2), the freshness wrap-step (slice 3). **Tests:** `+15` `test/project-map.test.js` (toggle default, dir-skeleton filtering, seed content + idempotence + non-throw, updateProject validation/persistence/seed-on-toggle/no-delete-on-off, enrichProject surface) + `+4` `test/sessions.test.js` (the prime pointer gate + the reference-not-inline assertion). Full suite **3526 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/pidx-project-map.md`.
- **OpenAI-compat assertion: pin the guarantee (TB-4 / #359).** Makes "every orchestration-profile endpoint is OpenAI-compat" a checked guarantee rather than a coincidence, so a future LangGraph endpoint (semantic-route, Monad #35) drops into the same profile mechanism unchanged and swapping a profile's `base_url` between two OpenAI-compat endpoints requires no harness change. New pure `assertOpenAICompatEndpoint(baseUrl)` in `lib/orchestration.js` validates that an endpoint is a well-formed absolute `http(s)` base URL with a host — the invariant TC can enforce at resolve time, since TC injects only `OPENAI_API_BASE`/`OPENAI_API_KEY`/`--model` and the harness appends `/chat/completions`. Wired into `resolveLaunchProfile` as a new refusal case (after the null-baseUrl "not yet landed" check): a bound-but-non-compat endpoint **refuses to inject** (honest degradation, no silent fallback — matching every other TB-1 refusal), so every endpoint TC actually injects is OpenAI-compat by construction. **Decision:** the `/v1` suffix is the near-universal convention (LiteLLM, vLLM, OpenRouter) but is deliberately **not** hard-required — refusing on it would false-reject a valid compat server mounted at a different base path; the validator enforces scheme + host and treats the path leniently. The "nothing engine-specific leaks" half of the guarantee is pinned by the overlay being engine-agnostic (no new URL construction added to TC — it never POSTs the endpoint, so a `chatCompletionsUrl()` helper would be dead code). **Tests:** `+9` `test/orchestration.test.js` (validator accept/refuse matrix incl. empty/non-string/unparseable/non-http-scheme; the new resolve-time refusal distinct from the null case; the acceptance — swapping `base_url` between two compat endpoints changes only `OPENAI_API_BASE`, with only the three generic knobs injected and no profile/engine leak). Full suite **3509 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/tb-4-openai-compat-assertion.md`.
- **Escalation-signal recognizer (TB-3 / #358).** Wires the TangleBrain seam by which a local OpenAI-compatible endpoint signals "this needs frontier." New pure `lib/escalation.js`: `recognizeEscalation(response)` matches a **namespaced top-level `tanglebrain` marker** (`{ escalate: true, reason, detail, suggested_tier }`) on a parsed chat-completion response or SSE terminal chunk — deliberately **not** `finish_reason` (SDKs enum-validate that; a custom value breaks strict parsers), so the marker rides alongside a still-valid `finish_reason` and standard clients drop the unknown key. The recognizer is strict (`escalate === true`), normalizes the snake_case wire field to `suggestedTier`, and **never throws** on malformed input (declines to `null`); `recognizeEscalationFromSSELine(line)` covers the streamed terminal-chunk path (skips `[DONE]`, comments, non-`data:` lines, and parse errors). `surfaceEscalation(escalation, context, deps)` is the hook: it logs the signal (structured, non-blocking) and returns `{ surfaced, routed: false }`. **Stub scope — no routing, no cloud call** (`routed` always `false`; honors TangleBrain invariant #3: TC/Monad never broker the cloud hop). The marker key is pinned to `tanglebrain` (exposed as `MARKER_KEY`; the Monad #35 emitter must match). **No live call site by design** — nothing emits the marker today and TC isn't in the chat-completion path, so the exported recognizer *is* the seam, ready for a future LiteLLM-callback / response-proxy tap to compose `surfaceEscalation(recognizeEscalation(response), context)`. **Out of scope:** the emitter (Monad #35) and the actual signal-up routing; TB-4 (#359). **Tests:** `+23` `test/escalation.test.js` (valid/declined markers, strict-true, snake_case normalization, never-throw totality, single-SSE-line recognition, the hook's log+no-route contract, the object + SSE acceptance paths, and a structural guard that the module imports no HTTP client). Full suite **3500 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/tb-3-escalation-recognizer.md`.

### Fixed

- **Clipboard copy works on iOS Safari over plain HTTP (#435).** The #427 plain-HTTP fallback (`tcCopyToClipboard` in `public/api-helper.js`) selected via a `readonly` textarea + `.select()` before `document.execCommand('copy')` — a pattern that copies nothing on **iOS Safari**, so every copy button (setup prompt, SSH command, service token, upload path, wrap report) silently failed on an iPhone reaching TangleClaw over the plain-HTTP Tailscale URL (`http://host:8080`, not a secure context, so the native Clipboard API is `undefined`). Desktop browsers tolerated the readonly+select fallback, which is why #427 looked complete. The fallback now selects the text the iOS-compatible way — a non-readonly / `contentEditable` element, a `Range` + `Selection.addRange`, and `setSelectionRange(0, len)` — which copies on iOS **and** desktop. The durable fix (a real secure context on the phone via a trusted Tailscale HTTPS cert, which also restores the native Clipboard API and the service worker) is tracked in #434. **Tests:** new `test/clipboard-copy.test.js` (`+4`: secure-context native path skips execCommand; the plain-HTTP fallback uses Range+setSelectionRange and never bare `.select()`, with the temp element cleaned up; execCommand-failure returns false; the secure-API-rejects-then-recovers path). Full suite **3578 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Follow-up: `CACHE_NAME` `v3-30`→`v3-31` so a client whose service worker predates the network-first carve-out for `api-helper.js` is still forced to pull the fixed helper on next load (belt-and-suspenders delivery for already-installed phones). Closes #435.

- **Terminal drag-copy never reached the remote browser's clipboard — ⌥(Option)+drag now forces a real local selection (#431).** Selecting terminal text showed a highlight and a "copied N chars to clipboard" message, but pasting on the viewing device produced nothing (or stale content). Root cause — established by live headless repro against the real ttyd/tmux stack: the highlight, the toast, and the copy are all **Claude Code's built-in drag-to-select** (the toast template `copied ${n} ${r} to clipboard` is in the CC binary). CC enables xterm mouse tracking, so the drag never reaches xterm's selection engine; CC copies the text on the **host** (pbcopy on the TC machine + a tmux buffer — verified byte-accurate with all spaces), and **no channel exists to the browser's clipboard**: ttyd's bundled xterm registers no OSC 52 handler, and xterm's force-local-selection modifier is dead on macOS because it requires Option(⌥)+drag **and** `macOptionClickForcesSelection`, which defaults to false (Shift+drag, the non-mac gesture, is ignored on Mac by xterm's design). A remote operator therefore had *no* working copy gesture at all. (The previous root-cause theory — browser accessibility mode selecting a `.xterm-accessibility-tree` overlay — was disproven: that overlay only exists when `screenReaderMode` is on, which nothing in TC/ttyd enables, and it carries `pointer-events:none`; the earlier `user-select:none` injection was inert and is removed.) **Fix:** `public/session.js` flips `macOptionClickForcesSelection` on the xterm instance in the terminal iframe (`enableLocalSelectionOverride`, inside the existing `setupTerminal` theme retry loop), so **holding ⌥ while dragging** produces a native xterm selection — themed highlight, and **Cmd+C copies the real buffer text** (xterm's copy handler). Because Chrome can refuse ttyd's own copy-on-select (`execCommand('copy')` fired from xterm's async selection-change emit, after the transient user activation is spent), the same helper also re-runs the copy inside a real `mouseup` gesture — auto-copy-on-⌥-drag to the **browser's** clipboard, full text with spaces, works over plain HTTP (verified headlessly against a mouse-capturing TUI; ⌥+drag→green highlight→Cmd+C verified live by the operator). Plain drag keeps Claude Code's own select/copy behavior untouched (the gesture hook no-ops when xterm holds no selection). Touch devices (no ⌥ key) get a toolbar Copy button reading the tmux buffer in a follow-up (#438). No `CACHE_NAME` bump needed — `session.js` is already network-first, so a plain reload delivers it. **Tests:** `test/terminal-selection-fix.test.js` (5: the option flip, null-safety, wiring into `setupTerminal`, and a guard that the inert a11y-overlay injection stays removed). Also re-pinned **2 stale source-assertions orphaned by #430** (`test/openclaw-setup-readme.test.js`, `test/upload-modal-frontend.test.js` still asserted `navigator.clipboard.writeText(...)` after #430 routed those sites through `tcCopyToClipboard` — red on `main`).

- **Copy buttons work over plain HTTP (secure-context clipboard fallback, #427).** Every copy button — wrap report, upload path, OpenClaw SSH command, setup prompt — failed with "Could not copy — select … manually" whenever TangleClaw was accessed over plain HTTP (e.g. `http://host:8080` over Tailscale), forcing operators to hand-select text (acute for a blocked-wrap report). Cause: `navigator.clipboard` is only defined in a **secure context** (HTTPS/localhost), so over plain HTTP it's `undefined` and `writeText` throws. New shared `tcCopyToClipboard(text)` in `public/api-helper.js` (the base helper loaded on both pages) tries the async Clipboard API when `window.isSecureContext`, else falls back to a hidden-`<textarea>` + `document.execCommand('copy')` which works over HTTP; all four call sites (`public/session.js`, `public/ui.js`) route through it and keep accurate toasts. `api-helper.js` joins the service worker's **network-first** set so the shared helper never serves stale (#271 pattern). `CACHE_NAME` `v3-29`→`v3-30`.

- **Project Settings modal: fits the viewport + multi-column layout (no more page-zoom).** The modal was a single 400px column that grew taller than the screen with no internal scroll, so the Save button fell off the bottom and operators had to zoom the page out to ~67% to use it. Now: the Settings modal is widened to 680px and capped at `90vh` with the **body scrolling internally while the title and Save/Cancel stay pinned** (`public/style.css`, `public/index.html` — a dedicated `.modal-content.settings-modal` two-class selector that outranks the base `.modal-content` width regardless of source order; the base `.modal-content` also gained a `max-height:90vh`/`overflow-y:auto` safety net for any tall modal). The dense controls are laid out in responsive `auto-fit`/`minmax` grids that collapse to one column on narrow viewports: the four capability toggles 2-up, the eight wrap-summary pills 3-up, and the three rule editors side-by-side (`public/ui.js`). **Also fixed the root cause of UI changes not reaching the browser:** `ui.js` and `style.css` were served **cache-first** by the service worker, so every dashboard/CSS change stayed invisible behind an active worker until a `CACHE_NAME` bump — they now join `session.js` in the **network-first** set (`public/sw.js`, the #271 pattern), so a plain reload always gets fresh UI. `CACHE_NAME` `v3-26`→`v3-29`.

## [3.28.0] - 2026-06-29

### Added

- **Key-ref hygiene: detect the master-key footgun (TB-2 / #189).** TB-1 made a harness's secret deliverable via an orchestration-profile `keyRef` (`file:`/`env:`) resolved at launch — TC stores only a *reference*, never writing the secret into a config. The footgun this closes is the opposite: a LiteLLM key (originally the unrestricted **master** key) pasted directly into an engine config's static `launch.env.OPENAI_API_KEY`, inherited by every session that launches that engine. New pure `detectHardcodedKeys(engineProfile)` in `lib/orchestration.js` scans a **static, pre-overlay** engine config and flags an env entry whose value matches a LiteLLM key shape (`^sk-[A-Za-z0-9_-]{16,}$`) **or** whose name is `LITELLM_MASTER_KEY` (non-empty), returning **redacted** findings — it never throws and never blocks. Wired at the `lib/sessions.js` launch seam: each finding emits a redacted, non-blocking `log.warn` naming the engine, env var, and remediation (use a profile keyRef); the launch proceeds. Three deliberate choices (ADR 0006): **detect literals, not "the master key value"** (TC never holds the master key — any `sk-…` literal in a config is wrong because the sanctioned path is a keyRef); **scan pre-overlay** so the legitimately-resolved scoped key that `applyLaunchOverlay` injects is never flagged; **warn, not refuse** (the operator owns their engine configs; a hard-block could brick a deliberate setup). The detector is exported for a future refuse mode / load-time call site. **Out of scope:** editing the operator-owned runtime `aider.json` or fetching the secret (operator action → `VRF-tb-2-scoped-key`); minting keys from TC (Monad-gated); generalizing scoped keys to other engines. **Tests:** `+8` `test/orchestration.test.js` (literal flagged + redacted with the raw secret absent from the finding, `LITELLM_MASTER_KEY` by name, empty/non-key/keyRef-style values clean, no-throw on null/no-launch, and a sanctioned-path-silent-while-footgun-warns case spanning all three acceptance criteria). Full suite **3477 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/tb-2-key-ref-hygiene.md`; ADR 0006.
- **Launch-binder: per-project orchestration profiles (TB-1 / #357).** A project can now bind to an *orchestration profile* that points its engine at a different OpenAI-compatible endpoint (LiteLLM `direct`, a future `smart-fallback` group, or a `semantic-route` LangGraph host) **per project**, without editing the global engine config. Two stores, no DB registry: an operator-owned flat file `~/.tangleclaw/orchestration-profiles.json` (seeded once from bundled `data/orchestration-profiles.json`, then never overwritten — unlike engine profiles it carries operator-edited endpoints + key refs) maps each profile to `(baseUrl, model, keyRef)`; a nullable `orchestration_profile` column on `projects` (schema **v21→v22**) holds the binding (`NULL` = unbound = byte-identical to today, zero injection). New pure `lib/orchestration.js`: `resolveKeyRef` (`file:<path>`/`env:<NAME>` — TC stores only a *reference*, resolves the secret at launch so a rotated key needs no config change; full master-key retirement is TB-2/#189), `resolveLaunchProfile` (returns the resolved `(baseUrl, model, apiKey)` triple, or a typed **refusal** — unknown profile / `null` baseUrl for a not-yet-landed endpoint / missing model / unresolvable key — so a bound-but-broken profile launches with **no** injection rather than silently falling back to a different endpoint), and `applyLaunchOverlay` (returns a **clone** of the engine profile with `--model` appended to `launch.args` + `OPENAI_API_BASE`/`OPENAI_API_KEY` merged into `launch.env`; never mutates the shared cached profile). Wired into `lib/sessions.js` at one seam — both the launch command and the tmux env read the overlay; the secret rides in env, never the command line. Optional per-(project,profile) key override via `projConfig.orchestrationKeyRef` for isolated metering/revocation. Endpoints use Tailscale MagicDNS names, never raw IPs. **Out of scope (later TB chunks):** scoped-key minting / master-key retirement (TB-2), escalation-marker recognizer (TB-3), OpenAI-compat assertion (TB-4); `smart-fallback`/`semantic-route` ship stored-but-provisional (selectable once Monad #33/#35 land, no further TC change). **Tests:** `+24` `test/orchestration.test.js` (key-ref resolution, the full refusal matrix, the overlay no-mutation contract, overlay→launch-command integration) and `+8` `test/orchestration-profiles-store.test.js` (seed-if-missing, operator-edit preservation, load/cache/degrade-on-malformed, the v22 column round-trip). Full suite **3468 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/tb-1-launch-binder.md`.
- **Service-token management + fleet reach (AUTH-4 slice 4b).** AUTH-4a shipped the gate; 4b makes it usable. **Reveal/rotate:** `GET /api/service-token` reveals the raw fleet token for the Settings display (`404 NO_SERVICE_TOKEN` when the gate is off/unset — the redacted config API never carries it) and `POST /api/service-token/rotate` issues + persists a new token (`409 SERVICE_TOKEN_DISABLED` when off); both are operator endpoints, deliberately *outside* the M2M-gated path set so a service caller can't reveal or rotate its own credential. **Fleet injection** (`lib/engines.js`): when the gate is on, every project's generated config (CLAUDE.md, Gemini, Codex YAML, aider) carries an `Authorization: Bearer <token>` block right after the API base URL (new `_serviceTokenAuthLines` helper, markdown + `#`-comment forms) so sessions authenticate automatically; when off it injects nothing — the config is byte-for-byte its pre-AUTH-4 form (the reversibility contract). **Settings UI** (`public/ui.js` + `style.css`): a "Service Token (M2M API)" panel in Global Settings — enable toggle plus Reveal + Rotate buttons (shown when the saved gate is active) rendering the token into a monospace, selectable field; rotate confirms first. `CACHE_NAME` `v3-24` → `v3-25`. **Guides:** `data/porthub-guide.md` and `data/shared-docs-guide.md` gain an Authentication section documenting the bearer requirement and per-session injection. **Invariant centralization** (carried 4a Critic note): the "enabled ⇒ token present" rule now lives once in `service-token.ensureTokenWhenEnabled(config)`, shared by the PATCH enable path and the rotate writer. Rotating invalidates the old token — live sessions holding it lose API access until they relaunch and pick up the re-injected value. **Out of scope (4c):** ADR 0005 + security docs + `VRF-auth-4-service-token`; the AUTH-4 Status box stays unchecked until 4c. **Tests:** `+5` `test/service-token.test.js` (the `ensureTokenWhenEnabled` matrix), `+6` `test/api-service-token.test.js` (reveal/rotate over real HTTP, including the old token failing the gate after a rotate), `+5` `test/engines.test.js` (token surfaced only when enabled, all four configs carry the header, none when off, static-guide content). Full suite **3436 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-4-service-tokens.md`.
- **M2M service-token gate on the PortHub + shared-docs APIs (AUTH-4 slice 4a / #1).** The PortHub (`/api/ports*`) and shared-docs (`/api/shared-docs*` plus a group's `/sync`) endpoints were reachable unauthenticated on the direct localhost listener — AUTH-2's Caddy `basic_auth` only gates *remote* callers, and local fleet callers hit `localhost` directly, bypassing Caddy. AUTH-4a adds a TC-level bearer-token gate on exactly those surfaces. New pure `lib/service-token.js`: `generateToken()` (a `tcsk_`-prefixed token with 32 bytes of entropy, zero-dep via node `crypto`), `requiresServiceToken(pathname)` (a pathname-prefix predicate — gates `/api/ports*`, `/api/shared-docs*`, `/api/groups/:id/sync`, and is fail-safe for any future sub-route), and `validateRequest(headers, config)` (constant-time comparison via `crypto.timingSafeEqual`, fail-closed). Two new `DEFAULT_CONFIG` fields — `serviceTokenEnabled` (master switch, **default off** so existing local callers keep working — opt-in and reversible) and `serviceToken` (the raw fleet token, **redacted** from the config API as a `serviceTokenConfigured` boolean and **auto-generated on first enable**). The gate runs once in the central `handleRequest` dispatch (a no-op until enabled, so the surfaces stay byte-for-byte open until the operator opts in); denied requests are logged (method/path/code, never the token). **Out of scope (later slices):** the reveal/rotate endpoints + Settings UI and the per-session token injection into project config guides (4b); ADR + security docs (4c). **Tests:** new `test/service-token.test.js` (16 — generation, the gated-path predicate, and the full fail-closed/fail-open validation matrix) and `test/api-service-token.test.js` (10 — the dispatch gate over real HTTP: default-off pass-through, auto-generate-on-enable, config redaction, 401 without/with a wrong token, 200 with the right one on both surfaces, a non-gated route staying open, and reversibility on disable). Full suite **3421 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-4-service-tokens.md`.

### Internal

- **Service-token docs + governance (AUTH-4 slice 4c).** Doc-only close-out of the AUTH-4 chunk (no code or test change): **ADR 0005** (`docs/adr/0005-service-tokens.md`) records the design — single fleet token, default-off reversible, auto-generate + reveal/rotate, raw-at-rest + redacted, pathname-prefix gate, management endpoints outside the gated set — plus consequences and alternatives. `SECURITY.md`, `security-model.md` (§1/§2/§4), `operational-spec.md` (§2/§3), and `data-model.md` (§2 config schema + field reference) gain service-token sections; the data-model update also closes a pre-existing gap where the canonical config schema omitted the AUTH-1/2/3 ingress + auth field family. `VRF-auth-4-service-token` enqueued (consolidating the former `VRF-auth-4b-service-token-ui` — same live flow, promoted to the chunk-level acceptance). Closes the AUTH track. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-4-service-tokens.md`.

## [3.27.0] - 2026-06-29

### Added

- **TangleClaw attributes the logged-in user (AUTH-3 / #1 — proxy identity → session owner).** With the AUTH-2 `basic_auth` gate live, Caddy now forwards the authenticated username to TC and TC consumes it. The Caddyfile generator adds `header_up X-Auth-User {http.auth.user.id}` to each gated `reverse_proxy` block (`{http.auth.user.id}` is populated by `basic_auth` after a successful challenge; `header_up` uses **set** semantics, so it overwrites any client-supplied value — a forged header can't reach the app through the proxy). TC trusts that header **only** when the gate is actually live (`ingressMode === 'caddy'` AND `authEnabled`): the new pure `lib/auth-identity.js` `resolveRequestUser(headers, config)` is the trust gate — in direct mode (no authenticating proxy in front) the header is ignored entirely, so it can't be spoofed against TC's localhost listener, and an ambiguous/duplicate header fails closed. Two consumers: (1) `GET /api/server-info` returns `currentUser`, and the dashboard shows a **"👤 ⟨user⟩"** chip ("Logged in as", hidden in direct mode, refreshed on the existing 60 s server-info poll); (2) each launched session records the user in a new nullable **`sessions.owner`** column (schema **v20→v21**; NULL for every pre-AUTH-3 session and for any direct-mode launch — unauthenticated == NULL, no backfill needed), threaded through both the tmux and webui launch paths, and surfaced on the #347 session-ownership object (`_toOwnership.owner`). This is **attribution, not enforcement** — single operator, no per-user restriction yet (AUTH-4+). On a **hand-edited** live Caddyfile that TC doesn't regenerate (the Cursatory ingress), the operator adds the one `header_up` line by hand for identity to flow; until then `currentUser` is null (honest degradation, never a fabricated identity). Realizes the original AUTH-track "identity flow" decision (planned as an Authelia `Remote-User` header) on the shipped Path-A gate. **Tests:** new `test/auth-identity.test.js` (9 — trust gate: live/direct/gate-off, missing/empty/whitespace, array fail-closed, null-safety), `test/api-auth-identity.test.js` (3 — `currentUser` over a real HTTP request: gated/direct/no-header), `+3` `test/caddy.test.js` (`header_up` on gated local + both sites, none ungated), `+1` `test/session-ownership.test.js` (owner surfaced/null), `+1` `test/store.test.js` (the v20→v21 `owner` migration on a real old-schema DB). `header_up` syntax verified against real **caddy 2.11.4** (`Valid configuration`). Full suite **3395 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-3-proxy-identity.md`; ADR 0004 follow-on note; `VRF-auth-3-identity` enqueued.
- **Break-glass admin password reset — `scripts/reset-admin.js` (AUTH-2 slice 3, the no-permanent-lockout guarantee).** An operator who loses the Caddy `basic_auth` admin password can always recover from a terminal **on the host** — the gate runs in Caddy locally, so physical/SSH access is a sufficient recovery path and no working remote login is ever required. The script resolves the admin user from the live Caddyfile (`--user <name>` disambiguates when more than one is present), prompts for a new password (hidden, entered twice; or `--password-stdin` for scripting), validates it with the **same** slice-2b rules (≥12 chars, weak-password denylist, no-username-match, no control chars), hashes it via `caddy hash-password`, and **patches the credential line(s) in place** — it does **not** regenerate the Caddyfile, so a hand-edited live file (its remote-access block, snippet form, comments) is preserved rather than clobbered. It is **fail-closed**: the patched file is `caddy validate`d before the reload and a **timestamped `.bak`** is restored if the patch is invalid, so a recovery run can never itself break the ingress; on success it reloads Caddy (`launchctl kickstart`) and syncs the persisted `authEnabled`/`basicAuthUser`/`basicAuthHash` so a later cutover stays consistent. `--dry-run` previews the user + steps without touching anything. New `lib/caddy.js` primitives back it: **`replaceBasicAuthCredential`** (matches the credential *line* — the bcrypt-hash shape — so it patches both the generated inline gate and a hand-edited snippet alike; re-stamps the integrity header **only** when the input was already a generated file, so a hand-edited file is never silently converted into a cutover-clobberable one) and **`listBasicAuthUsers`**. The recovery procedure is documented in the machine-local `~/.tangleclaw/EMERGENCY-RECOVERY.md` (new "§4.G — forgot/lost the admin password" section + a manual fallback) and, for fresh clones, in `deploy/INGRESS.md`. **Tests:** `+9` in `test/caddy.test.js` (generated single/dual-site re-stamp, hand-edited snippet patch with header untouched, multi-user `--user` disambiguation, absent-user / no-credential / bad-hash throws, `listBasicAuthUsers`) and a new `test/reset-admin.test.js` (`+12`: arg parsing, user resolution, reload argv, and the fail-closed write→validate→restore guard). Full suite **3378 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. **AUTH-2 slice 4** (ADR 0004, `SECURITY.md`/`operational-spec.md`, the `VRF-auth-2-login` live verification, final Critic) closes out the chunk.
- **The first-run setup wizard now forces an admin login when running behind the Caddy ingress (AUTH-2 slice 2b).** In caddy ingress mode the wizard gains a mandatory **Admin Login** step (username + password + confirmation) and the **Skip** button is hidden — there is no default login. The password is validated server-side (**minimum 12 characters**, a bundled weak-password denylist, no-username-match, no control characters) and hashed with **`caddy hash-password`** (bcrypt, fed on stdin so it never appears in `ps`) via a new `lib/caddy.js` helper; only the hash is persisted (into slice 2a's `basicAuthUser`/`basicAuthHash`, with `authEnabled` flipped on). The gate is enforced **server-side, not just in the UI**: both `POST /api/setup/complete` and `PATCH /api/config { setupComplete: true }` (the Skip path) refuse to finish setup in caddy mode without an admin credential (`ADMIN_REQUIRED`), so the login gate can't be bypassed. The live Caddyfile is **not** regenerated by the wizard — completion returns a warning steering the operator to run `node scripts/ingress-cutover.js --to caddy` to activate the gate at a terminal (where rollback is available), keeping the risky launchd/TLS reload in the one tested, fail-closed primitive that already owns it. Direct-mode setup is unchanged (the admin step never appears). The generated-Caddyfile header drops its `AUTH-1` version tag (cosmetic; integrity hashing unchanged). **Tests:** `+15` in `test/caddy.test.js` (password-rule + bcrypt-hash helpers), `+10` in `test/auth2-setup-admin.test.js` (endpoint gate, both paths, direct-mode pass-through), `+9` in `test/auth2-wizard-admin.test.js` (caddy-only step insertion, client gate, completion payload). Full suite **3357 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**. **No break-glass recovery yet** — `scripts/reset-admin.js` + the lockout-recovery runbook are slice 3.
- **The ingress can now be password-gated with Caddy `basic_auth` (AUTH-2 slice 2a — config-driven).** Three new config fields — `authEnabled` (default `false`), `basicAuthUser`, `basicAuthHash` — make slice 1's generator capability reachable: set a username + a **bcrypt hash** (from `caddy hash-password`) and flip `authEnabled`, then run the ingress cutover, and the regenerated Caddyfile gates every path except `/api/health` behind HTTP Basic auth. `PATCH /api/config` validates the trio and **fails closed**: enabling auth requires *both* a user and a hash (symmetric with the generator's both-or-neither guard, so the config can never hold `authEnabled=true` with a missing credential), and `basicAuthHash` must be a real bcrypt string — a plaintext password is rejected rather than silently stored as if hashed. The hash is persisted **as-is** (it is already hashed — unlike `deletePassword`, it is never re-hashed) and is **redacted** from `GET`/`PATCH /api/config` responses (a `basicAuthConfigured` boolean is exposed instead — a stored credential hash never leaves the server, consistent with `deletePassword`). `scripts/ingress-cutover.js` passes the credential to the generator only when `authEnabled` is set (the generator's guard backstops a hand-edited `config.json`, throwing rather than emitting an ungated ingress). Default-OFF, so an existing ingress is byte-identical until an operator opts in. **No first-run wizard yet** — that, plus password rules and break-glass recovery, is slice 2b; this slice is the config + cutover wiring usable via the API today (it formalizes the live hand-edited-Caddyfile setup). **Tests:** `+8` in `test/api-config.test.js` (defaults, hash-stored-as-is, enable with creds, fail-closed on no-credential + half-set, bcrypt-shape guard rejects plaintext, non-boolean reject, empty→null normalization) and `+3` in `test/ingress-cutover.test.js` (ungated when the flag is off despite creds present, gated when enabled, throws on a half-set config). Full suite **3327 pass / 0 fail / 1 skip**.
- **Single-command install — `install.sh` auto-installs every dependency (AUTH-1 clean-Mac durability).** A fresh Mac now needs only `bash deploy/install.sh`: the script detects any missing runtime dependency and installs it via Homebrew — and **bootstraps Homebrew itself** (official non-interactive installer + `brew shellenv` PATH priming) when it's absent — instead of hard-exiting with a `brew install X` hint and making the operator come back. Two new helpers (`ensure_homebrew`, `ensure_dep <cmd> <formula>`) cover **node** (installed when missing; an existing too-old node still errors rather than being silently upgraded), **ttyd**, **tmux**, **mkcert**, and **caddy** (so the AUTH-1 ingress cutover works out of the box; direct mode doesn't use it). Crucially, install.sh now also runs **`mkcert -install` to trust the local CA** while it has an interactive terminal — the **privileged** step (`sudo` / `security add-trusted-cert`) that the headless launchd server structurally cannot perform. Surfaced live by `VRF-auth-1-cutover` on a clean Mac: the first-run HTTPS wizard previously failed with `mkcert -install failed: … a terminal is required to read the password`, because `lib/https-setup.js` `generateCerts` attempted the privileged CA trust-install **from the server**. Fixed on the server side too: `generateCerts` now only attempts `mkcert -install` when the CA is **absent**, and treats a failure as **non-fatal** — (unprivileged) cert generation proceeds regardless, and `caInstalled` from `/api/setup/https-check` is the wizard's signal to flag an untrusted CA. So the trust-install lives in the interactive installer, never the daemon. **Tests:** `test/install-sh.test.js` (a real `bash -n` syntax gate on the bootstrap additions; `ensure_homebrew`/`ensure_dep` helpers; non-interactive Homebrew bootstrap + `brew shellenv`; ttyd/tmux/mkcert/caddy auto-install; node-when-absent; the `mkcert -install` CA-trust step), `test/https-setup.test.js` (generateCerts skips `-install` when the CA is already trusted; does not throw when `-install` fails — cert still generated).
- **Caddy reverse-proxy ingress, behind a reversible flag (AUTH-1, #395) — TC-side, in progress.** Groundwork for putting [Caddy](https://caddyserver.com) in front of TangleClaw as the single ingress (the prerequisite for the AUTH-2 forward-auth gate), landed **behind a new `ingressMode` config flag that defaults to `direct` — today's behavior, unchanged**. In `direct` mode TC terminates its own HTTPS (mkcert via `lib/https-setup.js`) and binds all interfaces exactly as before; nothing about a running install changes until an operator deliberately cuts over. In `caddy` mode TC drops to plain HTTP bound to `127.0.0.1` (Caddy terminates TLS — reusing the existing mkcert cert for `localhost`, so local HTTPS is identical, with an ACME/Let's-Encrypt site block generated when a `publicDomain` is set) and ttyd rebinds to a Unix domain socket so it is unreachable except via the proxy chain. New `lib/caddy.js` detects the Caddy binary, generates + validates the Caddyfile (non-privileged `https_port`/`http_port` so Caddy runs as a no-sudo user LaunchAgent, `admin off`, `0600`, generated-not-hand-edited; `reverse_proxy` carries WebSocket upgrades transparently), and resolves the ttyd connect target per mode (`ttydConnectTarget`); `server.js` consumes it at the three ttyd-coupled sites (`/api/health` probe, `/terminal` HTTP + WS proxies) and forces plain-HTTP + localhost binding in caddy mode. `ttyd-watcher` needed no change (it recycles via `launchctl`, not a port probe). The reversible cutover is `scripts/ingress-cutover.js` (`--to caddy` / `--to direct` / `--rollback` / `--dry-run`): it regenerates the Caddyfile + the ttyd plist (TCP↔Unix-socket via a templated bind arg) + a `com.tangleclaw.caddy` LaunchAgent, **`caddy validate`s before any launchd reload (fail-closed)**, flips `ingressMode`, reloads the jobs, restarts the server, and health-checks — printing the one-command rollback. `install.sh` keeps its direct path unchanged and points at the cutover. Configurable `caddyHttpsPort`/`caddyHttpPort` (default `8443`/`8080`); `publicDomain` adds an ACME site block. The 443/80 + root-LaunchDaemon path and the Linux/systemd seam are documented in `deploy/INGRESS.md`. **Live cutover is operator-driven and reversible (`VRF-auth-1-cutover`).** Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-1-caddy-ingress.md`. **Tests:** `test/caddy.test.js`, `test/ingress-cutover.test.js` (pure plan/arg/template logic; launchctl is VRF), `test/ttyd-plist.test.js` (templated bind), config validation in `test/api-config.test.js`.
- **Typed-wrap trigger parity — the wrap sentinel (CC-7, Slice C).** Typing "wrap" (or "let's wrap up", "end the session", …) inside a live session is now a second front door to the **same wrap drawer the Wrap button opens** — cross-model and cross-transport, no Claude-only skill lock-in. The NL variation is absorbed by the **AI** (instructed via the prime prompt): on recognizing wrap intent it emits a fixed, render-safe marker — the bare token `TANGLECLAW_WRAP` on a line by itself. TC's side is deterministic: a new boot-time monitor (`lib/wrap-sentinel.js`, wired into `server.js` alongside the other watchers) polls each live session's output for that token and, on a fresh emission, raises a per-project flag. The session view's existing status poll (`GET /api/sessions/:project/status` now carries `wrapRequested`) sees the flag and calls the same `openWrapModal()` the button does, then acks it (`POST /api/sessions/:project/wrap-sentinel/ack`). **No auto-commit, no auto-kill** — the drawer is the operator's review/confirm surface (the spec's safety). Detection works on **both transports** — tmux (`capturePane` tail) and the ClawBridge gateway (`getOutput` cursor delta) — because a plain alphanumeric token is the one form the B1 spike proved survives Claude Code's TUI render on both. **Two false-positive guards** keep a mere *mention* of the token (the prime instruction names it) from tripping a wrap: detection matches only a standalone whitespace-delimited word (the instruction phrases it backticked / period-terminated, so it never matches), and the monitor baselines past each session's backlog (gateway: starts at the live cursor edge; tmux: records the token already-present at first sight) and flags only a later absent→present transition, at most once per session. All state is in-memory and ephemeral (a restart simply re-baselines). **Tests:** new `test/wrap-sentinel.test.js` (detection + both false-positive guards isolated; tmux baseline→fresh-emission, prime-echo-never-flags, once-per-session + ack, vanished-pane resilience, end-of-session prune; gateway cursor-baseline + fresh-output flag, transient-error, no-sidecar; lifecycle) + `test/sessions.test.js` (prime carries the instruction AND does not self-trip the monitor) + `test/api-sessions.test.js` (status `wrapRequested` + ack round-trip). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-7-degraded-wrap.md` Slice C. **CC-7 is now complete — A + B0 + B1 + C all shipped.**

- **WebUI/gateway wrap capture over ClawBridge (CC-7, Slice B1).** WebUI/OpenClaw wrap sessions can now capture structured AI judgment over the ClawBridge gateway instead of silently skipping it (the #334 honest-skip), so a webui wrap can reach tier-1/2 (`full`/`no-plugin`) rather than always degrading to `mechanical-only`. **New `clawbridge.getFile({project, path, consume})`** consumes ClawBridge #18's `GET /v2/session/file` (shipped v1.9.1) to read a session-relative captureFile's **raw** bytes back over the bridge — `## Heading` and newlines survive verbatim, which the PTY output stream does not (Slice B1 spike: the paint stream mangles `##` and collapses line structure, so structured capture can't come from the output stream). **`lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` gains a webui branch (`_runGatewayCapture`):** for a step with both `captureFields` and a `captureFile` it sends the wrap prompt via `clawbridge.send`, polls `clawbridge.getStatus` until the AI turn completes (`inputReady`, bounded by the existing 5-min cap; `waiting_for_permission` is surfaced as an honest blocked step, never a hang), then reads + consume-once the captureFile via `getFile` and parses it with the **same** `_parseFields` the tmux path uses — staging the identical `{capturedText, parsedFields}` shape so `continuity-write` sees `hadCapture:true`. Steps without a captureFile, and sessions with no ClawBridge sidecar (`bridgePort`), return an honest `skipped` with a reason (Slice A then flags the judgment empty) — never a fabricated capture. memory-update-style steps that write their own files stay out of scope (the AI writes the remote tree; `commit` reconciles the local one). No schema change, no new store/endpoint/UI. **Tests:** `test/clawbridge.test.js` (`getFile` raw round-trip, consume literal `"true"`, empty-body preservation, 400/404/unreachable) + `test/wrap-step-ai-content.test.js` (gateway happy path, no-sidecar skip, no-captureFile skip, missing-field block, unreadable-file block, permission block, timeout, send failure, non-openclaw engine). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-7-degraded-wrap.md` Slice B1.
- **Per-methodology wrap contract — depth presets (CC-8, #386).** A methodology can now declare its default wrap-section depth in `template.json` via a new optional `wrap_contract: { sections: [...] }` field (a subset of the eight fixed `WRAP_SECTIONS`), so a lightweight methodology (e.g. grant-writing) wraps with fewer sections than a software methodology without each project's operator having to configure it by hand. This completes the wrap-section precedence chain begun in CC-6: `continuity-write` resolves the rendered set as **per-project `project.wrapSections`** (CC-6 operator override — wins) → **methodology `wrap_contract.sections`** (CC-8 default — used when no per-project override) → **all 8** (the deep fallback). `Next action` is always forced in by `effectiveWrapSections` regardless of layer. The methodology field is validated in `lib/methodologies.js` `validateTemplate` against the **same** `continuity.WRAP_SECTIONS` vocabulary the per-project gate uses (symmetric gates), so an invalid section name fails template load loudly; resolution in `lib/wrap-steps/continuity-write.js` is best-effort (an unresolvable template falls through to the deep default, never halts a wrap) and the methodology lookup is injected via `_internal.getMethodologyTemplate` for testability. **Prawduct deliberately omits `wrap_contract` ⇒ stays deep (all 8), so no existing project regresses** — no schema change, no migration, no new store/endpoint/UI. **Tests:** `test/methodologies.test.js` (valid subset / omitted / non-object / non-array / unknown-section-name) + `test/wrap-step-continuity-write.test.js` (methodology default used when no per-project override; per-project override wins; deep fallback when the methodology declares no `wrap_contract`). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-8-methodology-wrap-contract.md`.
- **One-click self-update — the "Update & restart" action (#228/#229, UB).** The update pill that detects a newer release (24h release-tag poll → `/api/update-status`) now carries an **Update & restart** button, closing the last manual step: previously the badge only *injected an AI prompt* telling the agent to `git pull` + restart on the box. Clicking it (with a confirm) fetches the release and moves the checkout to the **latest release tag** (consistent with the tag the pill advertised), then chains the existing #235 restart (`POST /api/server/restart` → launchd `KeepAlive` relaunch → poll `/api/server-info` → reload onto the new assets). **New `lib/update-applier.js`** performs the git half with safety guards that **fail closed**: refuses on a **dirty working tree** (never clobbers local changes), when **no update is available** (no silent no-op), when **HEAD isn't on `main` or a release tag** (never moves a dev's feature branch — detached-at-a-tag is allowed for a prior self-update), or when it's **not a git checkout**; an unexpected git failure mid-flow returns the pre-update `fromSha` so recovery is a one-line `git checkout <fromSha>`. **New route `POST /api/update/apply`** (200 on success with `fromSha`/`toRef`/`toSha`; **409** + a stable `code` on a refused guard; **500** on a git error) — it does **not** restart itself, so the proven flush-202-then-kill path stays in one place. Git runs argv-form (`execFileSync`), so a tag ref can't shell-inject. The button degrades honestly when no restart mechanism exists (code lands on disk; the operator restarts manually → the #199 stale-server banner). **No auto-rollback in v1** (documented: `fromSha` is logged for manual recovery); the in-session AI prompt (`public/session.js`) stays as the no-mechanism fallback. **Tests:** new `test/update-applier.test.js` (every guard: no-git / no-update / dirty-tree / wrong-ref / no-tag / git-error; happy path from main + from a detached release tag; `_headState`) + `test/api-update-apply.test.js` (route 200/409/500 mapping). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/ub-self-update-action.md`.
- **Degraded-wrap tiers — honest labeling of how much a wrap could capture (CC-7, Slice A).** Every session wrap now records which **tier** ran into both the continuity index and the per-session wrap summary's freshness stamp: **`full`** (AI judgment captured + plugin-governed → reflection fold), **`no-plugin`** (judgment captured, not plugin-governed), or **`mechanical-only`** (no AI channel → only the server-side floor). On a `mechanical-only` wrap the uncaptured judgment sections are now flagged **with the reason** (`_⚠ not captured (no AI channel)_`) instead of a bare marker, so the next session reads *why* a section is empty rather than mistaking an honest gap for "nothing happened" — the contract's "missing judgment is flagged-empty, never fabricated" rule made legible. The reason is derived from the prior `ai-content` step's skip cause (no AI channel / operator skip / generic). The session-resume prompt surfaces a non-`full` tier (`Wrap tier: no-plugin (judgment may be thin — verify)`) to ground its freshness check. `lib/continuity.js` `renderWrapSummary` gains a `tier` frontmatter key + an `uncapturedReason` flag; `renderIndex`/`parseIndex` round-trip a `tier` freshness bullet; reason-bearing flags still collapse to empty on parse (round-trip preserved). No new store, no schema change, server-side only — webui sessions stop silently dropping judgment. (Slices B/C — the gateway AI channel + the `<<TANGLECLAW_WRAP>>` trigger-parity sentinel — follow.)
