- **version-bump bumps `package.json` when there's no `version.json` (closes #298).** `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` now resolves the version source — preferring `version.json`, falling back to `package.json` (Node projects) — so wrapping a Node app actually bumps its version instead of skipping. Of 34 registered projects only 4 had a `version.json`; ~14 are `package.json`-versioned and were silently skipped every wrap with "version.json not found". The `package.json` write is **surgical** — only the top-level `"version"` value is swapped (anchored on the current value), byte-preserving the hand-maintained file's formatting, key order, and dependency versions; a defensive normalized-rewrite fallback covers unusual formatting. `version.json` stays preferred + normalized (TangleClaw and the other 3 `version.json` projects are unchanged). When **neither** file exists the skip reason is now the clearer "not version-tracked (no version.json or package.json …)" instead of the alarming "version.json not found", and the wrap-drawer detail names the source (e.g. `1.4.2 → 1.5.0 (minor, package.json)`). The commit-body "Bumped …" line shape-matches the staged metadata, so package.json bumps render with no commit-step change. **Tests.** New `test/version-bump-package-json.test.js`: source resolution (version.json preferred, package.json fallback, neither → skip, missing/non-semver version → skip), the surgical swap preserves siblings and does NOT touch a coinciding dependency version, and a `run()` e2e bumping package.json + promoting the CHANGELOG. Updated the "skips when missing" + detail-format pins in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`. Full suite 2666/2667 (1 pre-existing skip).

## [3.23.0] - 2026-06-02

### Added

- **OpenClaw connection panel shows the instance version per connection (closes #296).** Each OpenClaw connection's expanded panel now displays the running OpenClaw version inline (alongside Host / Port / SSH User / Local Port), read from the instance's pinned image tag (`OPENCLAW_IMAGE=ghcr.io/openclaw/openclaw:<tag>` in its `.env`) over SSH. The version isn't exposed by the gateway's HTTP endpoints / headers / JS bundle, and `docker`/`podman` aren't on the SSH user's PATH, so the `.env` is the viable source (discovered while chasing the tunnel incidents). Adds an optional **`instanceDir`** connection field (host path of the instance stack, e.g. `~/openclaw-tilt`) — set it to enable the version row; unset connections show no row. New `GET /api/openclaw/connections/:id/version` reads + parses the tag over SSH, **cached per connection** (5-min TTL) so repeated panel renders don't each SSH; `?force=1` bypasses the cache, and the cache is invalidated on connection update. `lib/openclaw-version.js` validates `instanceDir` against a metacharacter-free shape before interpolating it into the remote command (shell-injection guard). Schema migration **v15→v16** adds the `instance_dir` column. **Tests.** New `test/openclaw-version.test.js` (tag parse; `instanceDir` safety incl. injection rejection; fetch + cache + `force`; no-dir / unsafe / ssh-fail / missing-tag paths); `test/store-openclaw.test.js` round-trips `instanceDir` + asserts the v16 column survives the v15 rebuild; schema-version pins bumped 15→16 across the store/session/portlease tests. `CACHE_NAME` `v3-16`→`v3-17` so operators get the new panel + modal field. Full suite 2659/2660 (1 pre-existing skip). **Follow-up:** the per-connection "Update" button (#297) — TC shelling out to a durable `openclaw-update` host-helper over SSH (the host `docker` lives at `/usr/local/bin`, just off the non-interactive PATH) — is filed separately.
- **Wrap drawer operator guidance: status tooltips + "How to fix this" remediation (closes #222, #223).** Two affordances from the post-#220 dogfood feedback ("I'm not clear on what these things do") land together since they share the drawer-rendering code. **Status tooltips (#222):** each step's status badge (DONE/SKIPPED/BLOCKED/PENDING/RUNNING) now carries a plain `title` tooltip explaining what the status means — e.g. SKIPPED = "Step ran but had nothing to do… Not a failure.", PENDING = "Step queued but didn't run because a blocker:true step earlier in the pipeline failed." Text is centralized in `STATUS_META` (`public/wrap-drawer.js`) and surfaced via `buildStepRow().statusTooltip`; no JS, no dependency, accessible. **Remediation (#223):** step handlers can now return an optional `output.remediation` string — a handler-authored "how to fix this" — which the drawer renders as a collapsible **"How to fix this"** disclosure under the blocked row (and `buildReportText` appends a `How to fix:` line to the copied report). Absent/blank `remediation` falls through to the existing raw-blocker rendering (back-compat). Retrofitted the primary blocked path of each handler that genuinely blocks: `priming-roll` (multiple/no/unresolvable plan — the motivating #226 case — and no-chunk-headings), `test` (non-zero exit, points at the skip-tests override), `lint` (errors, suggests `--fix`), `critic-check` (blocking findings, points at `/critic verify-resolutions` and the override; merged into the existing `output` without clobbering `blockingFindings`), and `commit` (pre-commit hook rejection — the #268 motivating case). `pr-check` is intentionally untouched: it is always-ok by design (gh-missing/auth → `status:'skipped'`, never blocks), so it has no blocked-return to remediate; rarer secondary blocks in `commit`/`ai-content` deliberately fall through to raw-blocker rendering to keep the change scoped. **Tests.** `test/wrap-drawer.test.js` +6 (every status carries a tooltip; unknown-status empty-tooltip fallback; remediation surfacing with trim + blank/non-string/absent → null back-compat; `buildReportText` includes/omits the How-to-fix line). Regression assertions added to the existing blocked-path tests for `test`, `lint`, `priming-roll` (×2), `critic-check`, and `commit` in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pinning each handler's `output.remediation`. Full suite 2622/2623 (1 pre-existing skip; net +6). `CACHE_NAME` bumped `v3-14` → `v3-15` so operators get the new drawer assets.
- **priming-roll auto-disambiguates multiple build plans instead of always blocking (closes #226).** A long-lived project accumulates `.md` files in `.claude/plans/` (shipped plans, in-progress plans, advisory plans), and `priming-roll` used to BLOCK whenever it found more than one — forcing the operator to name `step.planPath` or clean the directory after every plan completed (the post-#220 dogfood pain point: 9 plans, "I'm not clear what these do"). The handler now resolves the plan by precedence: (1) `step.planPath` (methodology config, unchanged); (2) **new** `activePlan: "<filename>"` in `.tangleclaw/project.json` — an operator escape hatch whose bare filename resolves under `.claude/plans/` (with the same project-root containment guard as `step.planPath`); (3) exactly one `.md` plan → use it; (4) **among several, the single _in-progress_ plan** — one with an undone `### Chunk N` heading per `_parseChunks`/`_selectPointer` — is auto-picked. If **zero** plans are in progress (all chunks ✅ or chunk-less) the step now **skips** (`status: 'skipped'`, "No in-progress plan … nothing to roll") rather than blocking, so a finished project's wrap isn't held up; if **more than one** is in progress it blocks with `output.remediation` (the #223 drawer surface) naming the three disambiguation options (`step.planPath`, `activePlan`, or clean up `.claude/plans/`). New exported helpers `_isPlanInProgress` and `_readActivePlan`. **Tests.** +5 in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`: auto-pick the single in-progress plan among complete ones, skip when all complete, `activePlan` escape hatch resolves the named plan, `activePlan`→missing-file blocks with remediation, and the multiple-in-progress block (replacing the old always-block-on-\>1 test). Full suite 2635/2636 (1 pre-existing skip; net +4).

### Changed

- **version-bump refuses to bump when `version.json` trails the CHANGELOG's top released heading (closes #203).** `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` now guards the computed `newVersion` against the newest dated `## [X.Y.Z]` heading already in the changelog: if the bump wouldn't be strictly greater (a drift scenario — botched manual edit, out-of-order merge, or a force-push that rolled `version.json` back but not the CHANGELOG), the step returns `skipped` with a diagnostic reason (`refusing to bump: newVersion (X) is not strictly greater than CHANGELOG top released (Y); version.json may have drifted; reconcile manually before re-wrapping`) instead of promoting an out-of-order heading. Skips rather than blocks, per the ADR 0002 step-kind contract ("never blocks") — the wrap pipeline proceeds, the operator reconciles before re-wrapping. This catches the bad shape *before* the wrap commit lands, where `test/changelog-structure.test.js`'s descending-order invariant would only flag it post-commit. New helpers `_topReleasedVersion` (first dated heading) and `_compareSemver`. **Tests.** +5 in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`: `_compareSemver` ordering, `_topReleasedVersion` (first-heading + nullish-safe), the drift skip case (version.json 3.16.0 vs top released 3.16.2 → patch 3.16.1 ≤ 3.16.2 → skip, no writes staged), and the +1-patch boundary that correctly proceeds. Full suite 2629/2630 (1 pre-existing skip; net +5).

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw tunnels: end-to-end health + adaptive IPv6 forward target + reliable kill (closes #288, #291).** Two compounding tunnel defects left OpenClaw instances stuck at `BAD_GATEWAY` with no self-recovery (diagnosed live on the TiLT Claw / RentalClaw connections). **(1) Health was binding-based (#288):** `ensureTunnel` and `detectTunnel` treated a tunnel as up whenever the local port was *bound*, but under `ExitOnForwardFailure=yes` an `ssh -f -N -L` keeps the socket bound after its transport dies — a zombie forwarding into a void — so `POST .../tunnel` returned `alreadyUp` and never rebuilt while the proxy hung. **(2) Forward target hardcoded `127.0.0.1` (#291):** Docker Desktop for Mac republishes container ports IPv6-only after a restart, so `ssh -L <port>:127.0.0.1:<port>` dead-ends (`[::1]` answers, IPv4 loopback resets) — bound-but-dead from the first second; Linux/dual-stack hosts were unaffected, which is why only Mac-Docker hosts broke. **Fix:** new `httpRoundTrip(localPort)` does a real HTTP round-trip (ANY status = alive) and is the liveness truth source — `detectTunnel.active` and `ensureTunnel`'s already-up check are now end-to-end, so a zombie reports **down** and rebuilds. `ensureTunnel` spawns adaptively (`_spawnTunnelOnce` per attempt): tries forward target `127.0.0.1`, and if the round-trip fails, tears down and retries `[::1]`, keeping whichever carries traffic. **(3) `killTunnelByPort` made reliable + async (#288 defect 2):** resolves the PID actually holding the LISTEN socket via `lsof -t -iTCP:<port> -sTCP:LISTEN` (scoped to our `ssh -L <port>:` signature so it never kills an unrelated holder), escalates SIGTERM→SIGKILL, and **verifies the port is released** before returning `released` + the real `pid` — the old ps+grep resolver returned `pid:null` against zombies, so the documented "delete + recreate" recovery was a no-op against exactly the state needing it. The `DELETE .../tunnel` route awaits the now-async kill. **Tests.** `test/tunnel.test.js` +8 (`httpRoundTrip` any-status-alive / silent-zombie-dead / no-listener; `detectTunnel` zombie→inactive; `_findSshPidByPortLsof` scopes out non-ssh holders; `FORWARD_TARGETS` order; async `killTunnelByPort` release flag) plus the existing already-up/active tests upgraded from bind-based to end-to-end servers. Full suite 2647/2648 (1 pre-existing skip). **Live-verify caveat:** the IPv4-vs-IPv6 selection and lsof kill are exercised via real-socket fixtures; the true half-dead-SSH-transport path still needs verification against an actual Docker-Desktop-for-Mac instance (the TiLT Claw connection on `192.168.20.10` that surfaced this).
- **Wrap `memory-update` step no longer blocks every wrap on valid AI output (closes #287).** The step declared `captureFields: [summary, nextSteps, learnings]` and parsed them out of the tmux pane via `_parseFields`'s `/^##\s+/` match — but `tmux capture-pane -p` returns the *TUI-rendered* pane (escapes stripped), and Claude Code renders `## Summary` as a styled heading **without** the literal `##`, so the regex never matched and every wrap blocked with `Required captureField "summary" missing or empty` even though the AI emitted the blocks correctly (confirmed empirically: 0 lines start with `## ` across 2000 lines of a live Claude Code pane). It's the only `ai-content` step that parses pane output rather than just editing a file, so its siblings (`changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`) were unaffected. **Fix:** an `ai-content` step may now declare `captureFile` (a project-relative path); when set, the AI writes the structured `## Heading` block to that file (raw markdown, `##` preserved) and the handler parses the file instead of the pane, then removes it (consume-once — a later wrap can't read a stale summary if the AI fails to rewrite it). The bundled prawduct `memory-update` step gains `captureFile: ".tangleclaw/.wrap-summary.md"` and its prompt now instructs writing the block there; `schemaRevision` bumps `1`→`2` so existing installs pick up the framework-owned step change via the #275 reconcile on next boot. Steps without `captureFile` keep the original pane-parse path unchanged (back-compat); a missing/unreadable file blocks with a clear, actionable message. **Tests.** New `test/wrap-step-ai-content.test.js`: `_parseFields` parses raw `## ` blocks and (documenting the failure mode) returns empty on TUI-rendered headings; `run()` parses fields from the `captureFile` despite a hash-stripped pane, removes the file after read, blocks clearly when the file is missing, and the back-compat pane path still parses when no `captureFile` is set. `test/prawduct-aicontent-prompts.test.js` gains a lockstep guard pinning `memory-update.captureFile` and that the prompt references it. Full suite 2640/2641 (1 pre-existing skip; net +9 vs the prior `[Unreleased]` baseline).
- **Wrap blocked-report drawer no longer auto-closes before the operator can read it (closes #268).** When the wrap pipeline halted at any step (commit-hook failure, lint/test failure, Critic blocking finding), the blocked report — the operator's primary source of truth for *why* a wrap stopped — was visible only "for a few seconds" and then vanished. Root cause was a race, not a timer on the drawer itself: the wrap-block drawer (`public/session.js` `openWrapDrawer`) is sticky and has no self-dismiss, but when the underlying session subsequently went inactive, the status poller's `handleSessionEnded()` started its 10-second auto-redirect `countdownTimer` and navigated the whole page to `/`, taking the open drawer with it. **Fix:** `openWrapDrawer`/`closeWrapDrawer` now track `sessionState.wrapDrawerOpen`, and `handleSessionEnded` gates its countdown through a new pure helper `tcWrapDrawerHelpers.shouldStartEndedCountdown({wrapDrawerOpen})` — while the drawer is open the redirect is suppressed (the ended bar shows with no countdown; the operator dismisses the drawer and uses the manual "Back to Projects" themselves). Consistent with the no-timer-driven-UI-lifecycle stance (#98, #268) — the fix removes/guards the timer rather than lengthening it. **Copyable report:** new "Copy report" button in the drawer actions copies the full report (status banner + every step's label, status, detail, and complete blocker output) to the clipboard via a new pure serializer `tcWrapDrawerHelpers.buildReportText(pipelineResult)`, so operators can paste a halt into an issue or share it. **Not clipped:** `.wrap-step-blockers` now renders with `white-space: pre-wrap; word-break: break-word` so multi-line failure output (e.g. husky + jest output) wraps and stays readable inside the already-scrollable (`max-height: 80vh`, `flex` column) drawer rather than being truncated. **Tests.** 4 new tests in `test/wrap-drawer.test.js`: `buildReportText` serializes a blocked pipeline with full step output + tolerates a malformed/empty result; `shouldStartEndedCountdown` suppresses the countdown when the drawer is open and allows it when closed/absent. **SW delivery:** `/wrap-drawer.js` added to `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS` (it's the pure-helper sibling of the already-network-first `session.js`; a stale cached copy against a fresh `session.js` would throw on the new helpers) and `CACHE_NAME` bumped `tangleclaw-v3-13` → `tangleclaw-v3-14` so operators evict the old cache on next SW activation; pinned in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js`. Full suite 2616/2617 (1 pre-existing skip; net +4).

### Internal

- **CHANGELOG: reconstructed orphaned v3.2.3–v3.2.9 release sections; removed buried duplicate `## [Unreleased]` (closes #281).** A stray second `## [Unreleased]` heading sat mid-file (between `[3.3.0]` and `[3.2.2]`) holding the entire OpenClaw build's release notes — they were never stamped with their version numbers when v3.2.3–v3.2.9 shipped (2026-03-21), so the changelog was missing those seven dated sections and carried a duplicate `[Unreleased]`. The orphaned content was **not** a duplicate of any released section (the original mis-diagnosis on #281); deleting it would have lost history. Reconstructed faithfully using the unambiguous chunk/test-count→version mapping from the release commit subjects: `[3.2.9]` PortHub regression fixes; `[3.2.8]` standalone access (viewer, auto-pair, HTTPS, proxy auth); `[3.2.7]`–`[3.2.4]` Web UI/tunnel/integration Chunks 6→3; `[3.2.3]` build plan + connection-registry Chunks 1–2. Entry text preserved verbatim; only regrouped under dated headers in descending order. **Guard:** `test/changelog-structure.test.js` gains invariant #5 (exactly one `## [Unreleased]` heading) + a detector test for the buried-duplicate shape, so this can't recur silently.
- **Wrap drawer: skip detail keyed off canonical `status`, not `output.skipped` (closes #204).** `public/wrap-drawer.js:deriveDetail` checked `output.skipped` per kind (pr-check/test/priming-roll/commit/version-bump), but only `version-bump` ever set that flag — the branch was dead code for every other handler, and the renderer happened to fall through to kind defaults. Replaced the per-kind `output.skipped` branches with a single hoisted check on `stepResult.status === 'skipped'` (the canonical signal `buildStepRow` already carries), returning the handler's `detail`/`reason`. This eliminates the convention-drift class permanently — future handlers need no extra flag — and uniformly surfaces skip reasons for kinds that previously had no skip branch (lint/critic-check/ai-content). Dropped the now-redundant `output.skipped: true` from the only two writers (`lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js`, `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js`). Chose this over the issue's recommended "backfill the flag everywhere" (Option A) because keying off the canonical status removes the drift rather than requiring every present and future handler to remember a redundant flag. Incidental UX: a skipped `commit` now reads its reason (`no changes to commit`) and a skipped `test`-override reads `user opted to skip tests` instead of hardcoded drawer strings. **Tests.** `test/wrap-drawer.test.js`: skip-detail-from-status across kinds incl. those with no prior skip branch, bare-skip → `Skipped`, and a guard that a stale `output.skipped` on a non-skipped step is ignored; `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pins `output.skipped === undefined` on the skip path. `CACHE_NAME` `v3-15` → `v3-16`. Full suite 2631/2632 (1 pre-existing skip; net +2).

## [3.22.0] - 2026-05-30

### Changed

- **Wrap pipeline safety: auto-branch on `main` + halt on Critic blocking findings (closes #264).** Two paired safety layers ship together to close the failure mode that produced the `631acb5` regression on 2026-05-26 (a session-wrap commit landed directly on main with a Critic-blocking framework regression, the wrap pipeline neither branched nor halted). **Fix 1 — auto-branch in `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js`:** when wrap fires on `main`/`master`, the commit step now creates `wrap/<YYYYMMDDHHmmss>-<project-slug>` and switches to it BEFORE staging+committing — so the wrap commit lands on a feature branch rather than directly on the protected branch. Operator escape hatch: `context.options.allowDirectToMain === true` bypasses entirely (for trivial doc edits / hot-fixes per CLAUDE.md's "direct main commits only for trivial doc edits or incident hot-fixes" carve-out). Output adds `autoBranched` + `originalBranch` so the wrap drawer UI surfaces "Wrap committed on branch X (auto-branched off main)" — feature branches are untouched. A failed `git checkout -b` halts cleanly (rather than silently committing to main against the operator's intent) and the blocker message surfaces the escape-hatch option. **Fix 2 — halt-on-blocking in `lib/wrap-steps/critic-check.js`:** the step now scans `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` entries on the current branch and filters by `ranAt: "actual"` + `severity: "blocking"` (case-insensitive). Any blocking finding → `ok: false, status: 'blocked'` with the per-finding summary surfaced in `blockers[]`. The bundled prawduct template's critic-check step flips `blocker: false` → `blocker: "errors-only"` so the runner's `step.blocker === "errors-only" && !ok` halt condition fires. Operator override: `options.criticBlockingOverride === true` + `options.criticBlockingOverrideReason` proceeds anyway but stages an `overrideBlockingFindings` entry; `_buildBodyLines` adds an audit-trail commit-message footer line "Critic-override: \<reason\> (\<N\> blocking finding(s) ignored)" so the override survives in `git log` and `gh pr view` for future reviewers. Backward-compat preserved: `ranAt: "ack"` entries and pre-#267 entries (no `ranAt`) still satisfy the `criticRan` predicate (suppress the heuristic warning) but NEVER trigger the halt — only #267-era real-invocation entries with structured findings can halt. Cross-branch blockers don't bleed (only current-branch entries are scanned). The misconfigured-project path stays `ok: true status: skipped` so probe failures don't accidentally halt wraps. **ADR 0002 amended** to document the new contract under "Extended 2026-05-30 (#264 — wrap-pipeline safety)" — explicitly notes that methodology authors retain control via the `blocker` field (a custom template with `blocker: false` on critic-check restores warning-only semantics). **Tests.** 15 new tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`: 7 commit-step tests (auto-branch on main, auto-branch on master, `allowDirectToMain` opt-out, feature-branch no-op, auto-branch failure blocks cleanly with escape-hatch hint, override body-line render with/without rationale) + 8 critic-check tests (halt on blocking, case-insensitive severity match, ack-only & no-ranAt backward-compat, non-blocking findings preserved, cross-branch blockers don't bleed, operator override flips back to ok:true + stages audit entry, override-without-rationale still bypasses, warning+blocking coexist independently) + bundled-template-contract pin for prawduct's new `blocker: "errors-only"`. Full suite 2604/2605 (net +16 vs main); 1 pre-existing skip.
- **Addressed Critic-blocking finding on #267 PR (engine field read).** Independent Critic review of `feat/run-critic-button-upgrade` returned 1 BLOCKING + 4 WARNINGs. BLOCKING: the engine guard at `lib/actions/invoke-critic.js` read `session.engine || session.engineProfile?.id`, but the production session record from `store.sessions.getActive` exposes `engineId` (see `lib/store.js:_rowToSession:4210`) — so in production both fields were undefined, the guard never fired, and non-Claude sessions (Gemini, Codex, `openclaw:*`) would have sent `/critic` and burned the full 5-minute `MAX_WAIT_MS` before falling back via `noFindingsFile`. Fix: read `session.engineId || session.engine || session.engineProfile?.id`, treat any non-`"claude"` value (including engine prefixes like `openclaw:<connection>`) as degraded, and report `degradedEngine:unknown` on a corrupt/partial session record. **WARNINGs addressed:** (a) added `test/actions-dispatcher.test.js` regression-pin "injects the active session from store.sessions.getActive into handler options (#267)" using a real `store.sessions.start()`-created session — would have caught the BLOCKING bug; (b) gated the success toast on no-fallback case in `public/session.js:invokeMethodologyAction` — previously toast read "Critic completed for X — 0 finding(s)" alongside the panel reading "ack-only fallback," which was contradictory; (c) added a bounded `AbortController` to the front-end POST with `ACTION_TIMEOUT_MS = MAX_WAIT_MS + 30s`, replacing the previously-unbounded `apiMutate` call — protects VPN / flaky-connection operators from a spinner-of-doom if the server stalls. **WARNINGs deliberately deferred:** the test-evidence-stale finding (informational; full suite 2588/2589 pass on the fix commit is empirically true; updating `.prawduct/.test-evidence.json` is a separate Prawduct concern). **NOTEs (smart quotes, CHANGELOG paragraph length) skipped** as cosmetic. Re-ran `/critic verify-resolutions` per the Critic protocol; resolutions verified before merge.
- **"Run Critic" button actually invokes a Critic now (closes #267, supersedes #266).** Previously the prawduct methodology's action button was labeled "Mark Critic Run" and recorded an operator ack to `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` so the wrap pipeline's `critic-check` step could detect that an external Critic review happened. Operators kept reading the label as "this runs a Critic" and were surprised when it didn't. This PR closes the gap by upgrading the handler at `lib/actions/invoke-critic.js` to actually spawn a Critic: it sends `/critic` to the project's active Claude tmux session, polls `sessions.detectIdle` (reusing the wrap pipeline's `ai-content` step pattern), reads structured findings from `.prawduct/.critic-findings.json` (the path the Critic skill documents as its output target), and persists them inline in `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` alongside the ack entry. The schema is additive — entries gain optional `ranAt: "actual" | "ack"`, `criticFindingsRef`, and `findings: [...]` fields; the wrap pipeline's read contract is unchanged (any entry on current branch → `criticRan: true`). **Engine matrix deferred to ADR 0002 Chunk 12** — when the active engine is not Claude (e.g. Gemini, Codex on a project like Medusa), the handler falls back to ack-only with a structured `fallbackReason` (`degradedEngine:<engine>`, `noActiveSession`, `tmuxSendFailed`, `idleTimeout`, `noFindingsFile`, `idleDetectFailed`) so the UI surfaces *why* no findings appeared. The `lib/actions.js` dispatcher is now async-aware (handler results are awaited via `Promise.resolve(...)` — sync handlers continue to work unchanged) and looks up the project's active session via `store.sessions.getActive` so handlers don't need to depend on the session store directly. **Findings UI surface.** `public/session.js` gains `renderActionFindings` and `renderActionFallback` panels that anchor at the bottom-right of the viewport, **stay open until explicitly dismissed** (intentional contrast with the auto-closing toast — addresses the same operator-readability concern as #268), and render per-finding severity badges (blocking/warning/note), message, recommendation, and location. Toast also gains a `{findingCount}` placeholder alongside the existing `{branchName}` substitution. **Tests.** 7 new tests in `test/actions-invoke-critic.test.js` covering: ack-only fallback when no session is provided, `degradedEngine` fallback for non-Claude engines, explicit `ackOnly` opt-out, real invocation with mocked tmux+findings-file (verifies parsed findings flow), `noFindingsFile` fallback when the Critic doesn't write, `tmuxSendFailed` fallback when sendKeys throws, and a backward-compat round-trip pin that old entries (no `ranAt`) coexist with new entries without breaking the wrap pipeline's `branchName` filter. **What this PR explicitly does NOT do** (to keep scope tight): does not amend ADR 0002 to halt the wrap pipeline on blocking Critic findings — that's the deferred work in #264. Does not implement engine matrix support for Gemini/Codex Critic invocation — that's Chunk 12 of ADR 0002. Does not change the wrap pipeline `critic-check` step's `blocker: false` contract. Full suite 2583/2584 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +7).

### Fixed

- **Framework-owned template subtrees now propagate value-changes, reorders, and renames to existing installs (closes #275, #266; activates #264 on existing installs).** The bundled→runtime methodology-template reconcile (`store._mergeBundledTemplate`, run on every server boot) was **purely additive** — `addMissing` adds absent keys, `_reconcileMergeBy` appends entries with a new `idKey`, `_reconcileSetUnion`/`_reconcileOrderedSubset` add absent members — and **never updated a matched entry's field, reordered an array, or dropped a renamed-away entry**. So three bundled changes that shipped green were inert on every existing install: #264's `critic-check.blocker` `false`→`"errors-only"` (matched by id → field left stale, so a BLOCKING Critic finding never halted the wrap), #264's `commit`-after-`critic-check` reorder, and #230's `"Mark Critic Run"`→`"Run Critic"` action rename (matched by label → appended the new label, left the old as a vestigial duplicate button — that *is* #266). Verified live: this machine's `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` carried all three stale shapes, and a server restart could not heal them. **Fix:** new `_reconcileFrameworkSubtrees` in `lib/store.js` replaces the framework-owned subtrees (`FRAMEWORK_OWNED_PATHS` = `wrap_pipeline.steps` + `actions`) wholesale from bundled, gated by a monotonic integer `schemaRevision` on the bundled template. It fires only when `bundled.schemaRevision > live.schemaRevision` (a missing/un-revisioned bundled template keeps the exact pre-#275 additive behavior — opt-in by construction, so `minimal` and others are untouched), fires **exactly once per bump** (stamps `live.schemaRevision` after syncing — bounding the clobber to one event per revision with an auditable stamp), and never deletes a path absent from bundled. The live revision is captured **before** `addMissing` runs, because `addMissing` would otherwise copy `schemaRevision` into live and pre-close the gate. The bundled `prawduct` template gains `schemaRevision: 1`, so existing installs self-heal on next boot: `critic-check.blocker` → `"errors-only"`, step order corrected (`critic-check` before `commit`), and the vestigial "Mark Critic Run" action dropped. **Design trade-off (ADR 0001 amended):** these subtrees are framework-owned — the supported customization path is forking a new methodology `id` via `templates.save`, not hand-editing the canonical template's steps/actions in place — so a `schemaRevision` bump overwriting an in-place edit to them is accepted. **Tests.** 7 new tests in `test/store.test.js` (`framework-owned subtree sync — schemaRevision gate (#275)`) exercise the canonical stale-install shape through `_mergeBundledTemplate` (the runtime-load path the inert fixes never tested): the full incident shape (reorder + blocker flip + action rename-dedupe), un-revisioned bundled = no-op (pre-#275 behavior preserved), one-shot-per-bump (equal revision = no re-sync even over a user edit), re-fire on a subsequent bump, stamp-when-already-matching, never-delete-absent-path, and the gate-closed direct-call. Full suite 2612/2613 (1 pre-existing skip; net +7).

### Internal

- **SW NETWORK_FIRST extended to core UI assets to prevent stale-UI bug recurrence (closes #271).** The #267 verification pass on 2026-05-30 surfaced that the new "Run Critic" findings panel didn't render until the operator did `Cmd+Shift+R` — the SW served a stale `public/session.js` from cache. Same pattern bit on #246 (openclaw-cache.js) and #258 (CACHE_NAME bump propagation); this is the third recurrence in two weeks. **Structural fix:** added `/session.js`, `/session.css`, `/landing.js` to `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS` in `public/sw.js`. Updated the in-source comment to document the broadened scope (two categories now accepted: cache-invalidation scripts AND core UI assets where stale-serve has historically hidden feature changes). Bumped `CACHE_NAME` from `tangleclaw-v3-12` → `tangleclaw-v3-13` so existing operators evict the old cache on next SW activation. **Trade-off:** every page load now incurs a network round-trip for each of these three assets (~50ms × 3 = ~150ms latency added). Bounded and predictable; the unbounded "operator concludes the feature is broken when in fact the new code never reached the browser" cost is what we were paying without it. **Test pin:** new test in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js` asserts all three paths are present in the SW source — future SW-edits can't silently drop the carve-out. **`/landing.css` deliberately omitted** per the post-merge Critic review: no `public/landing.css` file exists today (the landing surface uses `style.css`); a pin for a non-existent asset would have locked dead config. Re-add when/if the asset materializes. Full suite stays green.
- **`.gitignore`: fold the second `# Prawduct session files` header block into the first.** Two consecutive `# Prawduct session files` section headers existed at lines 39 and 54 — first block held 13 entries, second held only `.prawduct/.sync-pending` and `.prawduct/.advisories.json`. Same coherence finding the Independent Critic raised against both prawduct-test's working tree and this repo's working tree during the #267 verification pass. Two-line deletion (the duplicate header + blank line); the two entries from the second block now live in the first block alongside the other session files. Zero behavior change — `.gitignore` semantics are unchanged. Prevents drift if a future framework sync adds another `# Prawduct session files` block.

## [3.21.0] - 2026-05-27

### Internal

- **`serviceWorker.register('/sw.js', { updateViaCache: 'none' })` to speed `CACHE_NAME` bump propagation (closes #258)** — without `updateViaCache: 'none'`, the browser uses the default `'imports'` mode and respects HTTP `Cache-Control` on the top-level SW script. Server already sends `Cache-Control: no-cache` on the SW response, but aggressive intermediate proxies or browser-quirk edge cases can hold the old SW for up to 24h. Setting `updateViaCache: 'none'` forces a network fetch on every update check, so a bumped `CACHE_NAME` (the immediate-unblock tool for any future SW-cache-related bug — see #246) propagates without waiting on TTL. **Belt-and-suspenders relative to #246's structural `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS` carve-out** — the structural fix already protects cache-bust-critical script delivery; this option makes the `CACHE_NAME` mechanism itself faster for any other cache class. One-line change in `public/landing.js:1041` plus a source-level test pin in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js`. Full suite 2576/2577 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +1).

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw cache-bust now reaches operators with an active service worker (closes #246)** — root cause was the service worker (`public/sw.js`) serving `openclaw-cache.js` from its cache-first branch. When PR #245 shipped escape-form coverage on `clearStaleOpenclawCache`, operators with an active SW kept getting the pre-#245 script from cache. The cache-bust regex was correct — the new version of it never reached the browser. The user-visible symptom was the issue's repro: stale `openclaw.control.settings.v1` localStorage entry persisting after navigating to a different OpenClaw connection, despite a `currentConnId` mismatch the regex should have caught. **Two-part fix.** (1) Bump `CACHE_NAME` from `tangleclaw-v3-11` to `tangleclaw-v3-12`. The SW's `activate` handler filters out non-matching cache names, so the bump triggers a one-time eviction of every operator's stale cache on next SW install. This is the immediate unblock. (2) Add a `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS` set containing `/openclaw-cache.js`. The fetch handler now routes these paths through the same network-first branch as `/api/` and navigation requests, so every future change to the script reaches operators immediately. Reserved for scripts whose ENTIRE PURPOSE is cache invalidation — serving a stale copy from the SW cache is by definition wrong, since the operator just shipped a new version precisely because the old one had a cache-related bug. **Diagnostic instrumentation.** `clearStaleOpenclawCache` now emits a `console.warn('[oc-cache] removed <N> stale entries for connId <X>')` when `removed > 0`. Quiet on the common case (zero entries) so normal page loads don't spam the console. This was the issue's "Next investigation step" suggestion — even with the SW fix in place, the breadcrumb makes future cache-bust failure modes diagnostically loud rather than silent. **Tests.** 5 new tests in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js`: (1) `CACHE_NAME` version pin (≥ v3-12, source-level regex) — catches a future hand-edit reverting the bump; (2) `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS` declaration pin; (3) fetch-handler wiring pin (asserts the routing decision actually consults `NETWORK_FIRST_PATHS.has(url.pathname)`, not just declares it as dead code); (4) instrumentation fires with correct count + connId when entries removed; (5) instrumentation stays quiet on zero-removed common case. Full suite 2575/2576 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +5).

- **`PUT /api/rules/global` body cap raised from 10 KB to 256 KB (closes #212)** — the default `MAX_BODY_SIZE` of 10 KB was below the size of the canonical `data/global-rules.md` file (14 KB at HEAD, growing as new conventions land), so every PUT returned 413 "Request body too large". This silently broke the landing-page global-rules editor (which calls the same endpoint) since the bundled defaults first crossed the 10 KB threshold. **Fix.** Add a per-route `maxBodySize: 256 * 1024` override on `PUT /api/rules/global` (`server.js:817`) using the same pattern as other large-body routes (`server.js:1567`, `:2827`). 256 KB gives ~18x headroom over current size; even a 10x growth in the ruleset stays well under the limit. **Tests.** Two new cases in `test/api-globalrules.test.js`: (1) explicit 50 KB synthetic-payload PUT to pin the new cap above the old default, with a precondition assert that the payload exceeds 10 KB so the test stays meaningful as defaults shift; (2) round-trip against the actual bundled `data/global-rules.md` (GET → PUT → GET) — the issue's canonical reproduction — with a precondition assert that the bundled content exceeds 10 KB so future ruleset shrinkage doesn't silently nullify the test. Round-trip assertion accounts for #100's trailing-whitespace normalization. Full suite 2569/2570 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +2 from this PR).

- **Engine profile updates now reach existing installs (closes #251)** — replaces the pre-existing add-missing-only merge in `lib/store.js#_copyBundledFiles` / `#_mergeBundledProfile` with a canonical-source sync (`#_syncBundledEngines`). On every `store.init()`, every bundled `data/engines/*.json` is reconciled against its on-disk counterpart at `~/.tangleclaw/engines/`: structurally-equivalent files short-circuit; drifted files get a `log.warn` followed by an overwrite from bundled. **Why.** PR #250 surfaced the gap by flipping `openclaw.json#launchModes.*.disabled` from `true` → `false`. Existing installs that already had the file at `~/.tangleclaw/engines/openclaw.json` from a prior session never received the value change — the merge ran but skipped keys that already existed in the live file, leaving the launch-mode picker UI cosmetically active but functionally inert. Every PR since the seed-once logic landed that has modified an existing engine field has had the same silent-strand failure mode (#211, #249, #250 confirmed; older PRs likely affected). **Design choice (canonical-source vs field-level merge).** Engine profiles have no UI/API edit surface — `store.engines.save` exists as a primitive but is never called outside tests. The "preserves user customizations" contract the prior merge was written for is theoretical: there is no documented path by which an operator creates such customizations. The same structural ambiguity #240 settled for `data/global-rules.md` applies here, in mirror image — repo file wins, on-disk drift is logged then overwritten. **Operator hand-edits (e.g. someone forking a Claude binary and customizing `preKeys` for it) now get clobbered with a `log.warn` breadcrumb** pointing at the source-of-truth path (`data/engines/`). The #119 stale-bypass-preKeys prune is subsumed by the same mechanism — bundled file has no `preKeys` on `bypassPermissions`, so the canonical overwrite achieves the prune's end state without a special-case branch. **Files in user-local with no bundled counterpart are preserved** — an operator who manually drops a custom engine profile into `~/.tangleclaw/engines/` doesn't lose it; the runtime dir is a union of bundled + operator-added. **Structural-equivalence compare.** `_engineProfileEquivalent` parses both sides as JSON and compares the canonicalized stringification, so whitespace, key order, and trailing-newline differences from older TC versions do NOT trigger spurious drift warnings. Malformed JSON on either side returns false (fail-open), so corrupted on-disk profiles self-heal on next startup. **Tests.** 9 new tests in `test/engine-profile-sync.test.js` covering drift propagation (nested `launchModes.*.disabled` — the #250 root case + a top-level key analog), fresh-install seeding parity, operator-added profile preservation, structural-equivalence short-circuit (no spurious rewrite on whitespace differences), corrupted-on-disk self-heal, idempotence across reboots, and the snapshot the issue specifically called for (every bundled `openclaw.json` key/value reaches `store.engines.get`/`#list` after init). Three pre-existing `#119` tests in `test/store.test.js` updated to reflect the new contract (`canonical-source clobbers operator-customized bypass preKeys` replaces `preserves user-customized bypass preKeys`; prune-specific assertions retargeted at canonical-source end-state); two `add-missing` merge tests replaced with explicit drift/clobber tests. Methodology templates (`_copyBundledTemplates`) deliberately scoped out — they have a richer reconciler (`#155`/`#158` array + hook-entry handling) tied to operator-customizable methodology surfaces, and the same canonical-source flip there would be a separate design decision. Full suite 2566/2567 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +9 from this PR).

### Added

- **AI co-author strip extended to ALL repos via global git template (#252)** — companion to #247 (per-project commit-msg hook). When `globalSettings.stripAiCoauthors === true`, TC now ALSO installs `strip-ai-coauthors.sh` into `~/.tangleclaw/git-template/hooks/commit-msg` and points `git config --global init.templateDir` at the template root. Every `git init` or `git clone` on the host — including repos created outside TC's project root (`~/code`, `/tmp/scratch`, sibling project trees) — inherits the hook automatically, closing the structural gap surfaced by the 2026-05-27 `openclaw-ebay-research` incident where a Claude session committed a `Co-Authored-By:` trailer into an unregistered repo. **Why.** A user's intent when toggling `stripAiCoauthors` ON is "Claude shouldn't be credited on ANY of my work" — the per-TC-project layer alone doesn't satisfy that. **Three-case `init.templateDir` detection.** (1) Unset → TC sets it to the template root and writes a sentinel file at `<templateDir>/.tc-init-templatedir-owned` (kept at the dir root, NOT inside `hooks/`, so it doesn't leak as a stray dotfile into every `git init`'d repo's hook directory). (2) Already pointing at TC's path → no-op for the global config; sentinel is ensured for clean future revert. (3) Operator-set custom path (e.g. dotfiles, commitlint template) → emit `log.warn`, do NOT clobber, do NOT write sentinel; the hook file is still written to TC's template dir (so per-project installs still work) but the global flip is skipped until the operator resolves the conflict manually. **Toggle-off behaviour.** Removes the hook from TC's template dir; reverts `init.templateDir` ONLY when the sentinel confirms TC claimed ownership (`git config --global --unset init.templateDir`); the sentinel is removed regardless so a future install sees a fresh decision point. If the operator changed the value out from under TC in between install and uninstall, the value is left alone and the result reports `templateDirAction: 'value-changed-by-operator'`. **What changed.** New `lib/git-template.js` (`syncGlobalTemplate`, `installGlobalTemplate`, `uninstallGlobalTemplate`). Wires into `lib/projects.js#syncAllProjects` (startup — single global sync alongside the existing per-project loop, using the same hoisted config snapshot so the toggle value is identical across both surfaces) and `server.js` `PATCH /api/config` (toggle handler — fires once globally after the per-project walk completes). Reuses the same `data/hooks/strip-ai-coauthors.sh` source the per-project installer ships, so a future hook update lands in one place. Atomic tmp+rename writes with 0755 perms — same SIGKILL-safe pattern as `lib/git-hooks.js`. **Known limitation (carried forward by design).** `init.templateDir` only fires on `git init` / `git clone` — existing on-disk repos don't auto-acquire the hook. Two follow-ups deferred out of this PR: (1) a `TC Setup > Apply hook to all git repos` sweep button that walks `find ~ -type d -name .git` and runs `git init` in each parent so the template's commit-msg lands; (2) extending the unregistered-repo surface to suggest the sweep. For now: existing TC-managed repos are covered by #247's per-project installer; existing non-TC-managed repos need the operator to re-run `git init` in-place (or wait for the sweep follow-up). **Tests.** 20 new tests in `test/git-template.test.js` covering fresh install (hook write + templateDir set + sentinel placement at dir root not inside hooks/), idempotence (second install reports `idempotent`; mtime unchanged), drift refresh of stale hook content, operator-owned non-TC `init.templateDir` (no clobber, no sentinel, hook still written), uninstall when TC owned the value (hook removed + templateDir unset + sentinel removed), uninstall without sentinel (hook removed, value left alone), uninstall with operator-changed value (value preserved + sentinel cleaned), idempotent uninstall, dispatcher round-trips for null/empty/explicit true/explicit false config, toggle round-trip (install → uninstall → install leaves no orphan state), source-missing fallback, and an end-to-end `git init` test confirming the hook actually copies into a fresh repo's `.git/hooks/` when the sandboxed `init.templateDir` is active. Tests sandbox `GIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL` (git 2.32+) and `__setTemplateDir` so the real `~/.gitconfig` and `~/.tangleclaw/git-template/` are never touched. Closes #252.

## [3.20.0] - 2026-05-26

### Added

- **Launch-mode picker for OpenClaw connections — propagates `permissionMode` to ClawBridge end-to-end (#210 Phase 2, closes #210)** — completes the multi-phase #210 build started by Phase 1 (PR #249). When the operator picks a launch mode for an OpenClaw connection that carries a `bridgePort`, TC now pre-creates the bridge session with the matching `permissionMode` BEFORE the iframe loads, so the chat UI's own session/start attaches to the existing session via ClawBridge v1.7.0's `attachIfExists: true` idempotent attach. Pick `default` to surface ClawBridge's structured permission-review channel (4 permission events vs 0 with no mode set, per the sibling's smoke-test data); pick `bypassPermissions` for unattended execution in containers; etc. The same six modes that ClawBridge accepts (`default`, `acceptEdits`, `bypassPermissions`, `auto`, `plan`, `dontAsk`) are now selectable. **What changed.** New `lib/clawbridge.js` — thin `node:http` client for `POST /v2/session/start` through the SSH-tunneled `bridgePort`. The POST body is `{project, permissionMode, attachIfExists: true}` — `instruction` is intentionally omitted per ClawBridge v1.6.0's orchestrator pre-create pattern (when omitted, claude spawns as `claude --session-id <uuid> --permission-mode <X>` and enters interactive mode; subsequent user input flows via `POST /v2/session/send`). Bridge auth via `Authorization: Bearer <bridgeToken>` when the connection record carries one. 5s timeout, non-fatal on failure: a failed pre-create falls back to the chat UI's own session/start (no mode propagation) so the iframe URL is always returned. `lib/sessions.js#launchWebuiSession` calls the helper after tunnel-up + health-check, before constructing the iframe URL. `data/engines/openclaw.json` flips all six `launchMode.disabled` flags to `false`. `public/landing.js`'s picker gate (added in Phase 1) now passes the filter and the modal renders for OpenClaw connections. `server.js` forwards `body.launchMode` into the webui launch options. `store.sessions.start` records the chosen mode in the `launch_mode` column for both webui and tmux sessions (was previously only tmux). **Cross-repo coordination (closed).** This is the third PR of a three-repo coordination established this session — ClawBridge v1.6.0 added `permissionMode`, v1.7.0 added `attachIfExists`. The OpenClaw chat-UI session's attach-on-load behaviour question is now moot: `attachIfExists: true` makes the bridge idempotent regardless of whether the chat UI attaches-or-creates. **Connections without `bridgePort`** (Volta is the canonical example in our deployments) launch identically to before this PR — the picker may show modes but the pre-create no-ops, and the chat UI handles session/start as it always did. **Tests.** +9 new tests in `test/clawbridge.test.js` covering happy paths (POST shape + body, attached:true return shape, omitted Authorization header when no token, fallback to `id` field) and error paths (4xx with parsed error, 5xx with synthesized message, connection refused, timeout, non-JSON response body). Contract test in `test/engines.test.js` updated: assertion `disabled === true` → `disabled === false` with the Phase 2 docstring naming what changed. Full suite 2536/2537 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +9 from this PR).

### Internal

- **OpenClaw `launchModes` engine-profile scaffold (#210 Phase 1)** — adds the six modes ClawBridge v1.6.0 accepts on `POST /v2/session/start` (`default`, `acceptEdits`, `bypassPermissions`, `auto`, `plan`, `dontAsk`) to `data/engines/openclaw.json`, each with `disabled: true` and a `bridgePermissionMode` field that downstream code will read when Phase 2 lands. **No user-visible behaviour change** — the launch-mode picker gate in `public/landing.js` was updated to count only non-disabled modes, so the modal still doesn't render for OpenClaw connections; openclaw launches today are byte-for-byte identical to before this PR. **Why ship now.** Decoupling the engine-profile shape from the propagation work lets the OpenClaw chat-UI session (the third repo in the three-repo coordination established this session: TC / ClawBridge / OpenClaw chat UI) verify its session attach-on-load behaviour against the documented profile while TC's Phase 2 work (lib/clawbridge.js HTTP helper + `launchWebuiSession` POST through the SSH tunnel before iframe URL return) lands separately. **Test contract.** The pre-existing sentinel "openclaw intentionally has no launchModes yet (#209)" was retired and replaced with a contract test that asserts (a) every openclaw mode key is one of ClawBridge's accepted enum, (b) every entry declares a string `bridgePermissionMode` also in the enum, (c) every entry has `disabled: true` while Phase 1 ships without propagation. Comment in the test names the four-step Phase 2 plan that will update the `disabled === true` assertion to `=== false`. **Tracking.** ClawBridge v1.6.0 contract notes captured in `~/.claude/projects/.../memory/reference_clawbridge_architecture.md`. Cross-repo coordination notes captured on #210 (three comments: original assumption, three-repo correction, sibling-confirmed Phase 1 plan). Full suite 2527/2528 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +0 from this PR — the existing sentinel test was retargeted, not added).

### Added

- **Global setting: strip AI co-author trailers from commits (#247)** — new `stripAiCoauthors` global config field (default **ON**) installs a `commit-msg` git hook in every TC-managed project that strips `Co-Authored-By:` trailers naming an AI coding assistant (Claude, Opus, Sonnet, Haiku, GPT-N, ChatGPT, Gemini, Copilot, Aider, Cursor) before commits land. **Forward-only by design** — git's `commit-msg` hook fires only on new commits; existing history is never touched. Human co-authors pass through, including humans at AI-vendor email domains (the regex anchors to the display-name region BEFORE the `<email>` bracket so `Co-Authored-By: Alex Engineer <alex@anthropic.com>` is preserved). **Accepted trade-off:** humans whose display name CONTAINS an AI vendor token as a full word (e.g. "Anna Sonnet", "Sage Haiku") get stripped — keeping the rule mechanical is preferred over false negatives; humans whose name contains an AI token as a substring ("Claudette Smith", "Cursorial Wright") are preserved by the word-boundary anchor on both sides of the vendor token. **Why.** The advisory layer (`feedback_no_coauthor` memory entry — *"user considers AI work-for-hire"*) was already in place but models forget; mechanical enforcement at the git layer makes the rule unbypassable regardless of model context-window state. **What changed.** New `data/hooks/strip-ai-coauthors.sh` (POSIX sh, two-pattern `grep -ivE` filter with tmp+atomic-rename + `trap`-based cleanup on EXIT/INT/TERM/HUP for SIGKILL safety; carries a `TC-OWNED-HOOK:` marker for drift-aware uninstall). New `lib/git-hooks.js` (`syncGitHooks`, `installCommitMsgHook`, `uninstallCommitMsgHook` — install refuses to clobber a foreign `commit-msg` hook (commitlint, gitlint, operator scripts); uninstall refuses to remove a foreign hook; worktree/submodule `.git`-pointer-files AND symlinked-`.git` setups treated as no-git in v1 (`lstatSync` is load-bearing); ownership marker check is anchored at start-of-line in the first 20 lines so foreign hooks that merely mention the marker text in a comment are not misclassified; refresh of drifted TC-owned hooks emits a `log.warn` BEFORE clobber per the #240 drift-aware-write contract; refresh uses tmp+atomic-rename so a SIGKILL between write and chmod can't leave an unexecutable hook). `DEFAULT_CONFIG.stripAiCoauthors = true` in `lib/store.js`. PATCH `/api/config` whitelists the new boolean field; toggling it iterates EVERY registered project (including archived ones, so a toggle-OFF doesn't leave orphan hooks on archived projects) and re-syncs — gated on actual value change so a Save click that didn't touch the toggle doesn't trigger an N-project filesystem walk. New UI section in Global Settings modal → *Commit hygiene*. **Lifecycle wiring** — symmetric with `engines.syncEngineHooks` per `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates`: `createProject`, `attachProject`, `syncAllProjects` (startup), `updateProject` engine/methodology/silentPrime branches, and `launchSession` all call `gitHooks.syncGitHooks(projectPath, config)`. The `syncAllProjects` startup loop hoists `store.config.load()` out of the per-project loop — single FS read + pinned snapshot avoids the half-on/half-off race if a PATCH /api/config fires mid-sync. **Pattern details (Critic-driven hardening).** Vendor token alternation enforces word boundaries (POSIX ERE workaround: requires non-letter character before and whitespace/`<`/EOL after); `gpt-[0-9]+` covers multi-digit version numbers; trailer prefix tolerates leading whitespace (indented continuation lines) and zero-space-after-colon (editors that strip trailing whitespace). Second pattern matches bot-shaped localparts (`noreply`, `bot`, `ai`, vendor-name + variant) at AI vendor email domains for trailers with empty or generic display names. When EVERY non-blank line matches the strip pattern, the hook refuses to overwrite with an empty commit message and emits a stderr breadcrumb naming itself instead of silently triggering git's confusing "empty commit message" abort. **Tests.** 56 new tests: `test/strip-ai-coauthors-script.test.js` (33 cases — every canonical AI-vendor trailer, multi-digit GPT versions, empty/generic display names, no-space-after-colon variants, leading whitespace tolerance, word-boundary preservation of Claudette/Cursorial/Anna-as-not-a-vendor-token, prose-mentioning-AI-name preservation, would-be-empty refusal with stderr breadcrumb, multi-trailer stripping, missing-arg/missing-file resilience) and `test/git-hooks.test.js` (22 cases — install/uninstall/sync behaviour, TOCTOU-safe `.git` detection, symlink rejection (F8), anchored-marker classification of foreign hooks that mention TC-OWNED-HOOK text in comments (F9), marker-beyond-header-line-limit rejection, drift-aware refresh of TC-owned hooks, foreign-hook preservation on both install and uninstall, `.git`-pointer-file handling, idempotence, default-ON semantics for null/empty/missing config, source-missing fallback) and 3 new cases in `test/api-config.test.js` (PATCH boolean validation, default-ON via GET, accept-and-restore round-trip). Full suite 2527/2528 pass (1 pre-existing skip; net +59 from this feature). Closes #247.

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw cache-bust now catches JSON-escaped / URL-encoded / unicode-escaped slashes (#162-followup)** — `public/openclaw-cache.js#clearStaleOpenclawCache` previously matched the raw substring `/openclaw-direct/<connId>` only. The OpenClaw dashboard bundle (`openclaw.control.settings.v1*` keys) serializes its `gatewayUrl` through `JSON.stringify` and some downstream encodings emit `\/`, `%2F`, or `/` instead of a raw forward slash. A stale URL stored in any of those escape forms slipped through the cache-bust, so opening the Volta viewer after a RentalClaw session left the iframe's dashboard auto-filled with RentalClaw's wss URL — Connect then produced the OpenClaw UI's "Protocol mismatch" banner because the Volta-served Control UI bundle tried to handshake against RentalClaw's gateway. **Fix.** Normalize those three escape forms to `/` before running the existing `OPENCLAW_DIRECT_REF` regex. Stale-detection semantics unchanged: composite values containing the current connId in any escape form are still preserved (Critic MAJOR-2 contract). The scope-honesty note in the original #162 commit explicitly called this followup out as the next failure mode. **Tests.** +4 cases in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js` covering JSON-escaped, URL-encoded, unicode-escaped stale entries (all classified stale → removed), plus a symmetric preservation case for same-connection escape-form encodings. Full openclaw-cache suite 21/21 pass.

## [3.19.0] - 2026-05-23

### Fixed

- **CLAUDE.md regeneration no longer silently clobbers PR-driven rule edits (closes #240)** — `data/global-rules.md` (renamed from `data/default-global-rules.md` and populated with the full 191-line ruleset) becomes the single canonical source for global rules. `store.globalRules.load/save` read/write the tracked file directly; the legacy `~/.tangleclaw/global-rules.md` is ignored with a one-time warn + auto-backup to `*.pre-240-backup`. New `engines.writeEngineConfig` helper wraps every engine-config write with drift detection — warns loudly when the on-disk file differs from regenerated content, surfacing the silent-clobber failure mode at all four write sites (`createProject`, `syncAllProjects`, `updateProject` engine-switch, `launchSession`). Comparator normalizes CRLF→LF + trims so Windows editors and auto-formatters don't false-positive. Helper returns `{skipped: true, ...}` for engines without config files (openclaw, genesis) so callers don't surface spurious errors. **Going forward:** PR-driven rule changes edit `data/global-rules.md` and commit; UI/API edits land in the same file. The competing-sources-of-truth class of bug is structurally impossible. Reset button in the Global Rules editor is now a no-op pending UI cleanup in #243. Full suite 2463/2464 pass.

- **Recover global rules from #234 + #236 silently clobbered by CLAUDE.md regeneration (#240)** — `lib/engines.js#_generateClaudeMd` regenerates `CLAUDE.md` from the DB-stored global rules on every session launch / engine PATCH / startup sync, overwriting the on-disk file in place. PR-driven raw-file edits to `CLAUDE.md` (e.g. via `git`) are silently discarded the next time TC restarts — the content lives on in `git log` but is functionally absent from the live ruleset. Two PRs this session were affected: **#234** (the versioning bump-level decision table) and **#236** (the stale-plan archive rule + `gh issue view <N> --json state` issue-state check). Both rule blocks were clobbered after the first TC restart following each merge; the celebrated "structural lessons codified in CLAUDE.md" claim in those PR descriptions was technically true in git history and functionally false in the running ruleset. **Recovery procedure run this session:** read the live DB content via `store.globalRules.load()`, splice the two missing rule blocks back into their respective sections (`Build Plans & Chunks` for #236, `Releases & Versioning` for #234) preserving sibling content, write back via `store.globalRules.save(merged)` (which normalizes and persists to `_globalRulesPath()`). Verified end-to-end: the regenerated `CLAUDE.md` is now byte-for-byte identical to HEAD (diff is empty), so the next TC restart produces no surprise drift. **Defensive comment added** to `lib/engines.js#_generateClaudeMd` documenting the regeneration contract and pointing future readers (or automated agents tempted to commit directly to `CLAUDE.md`) at the durable edit paths: landing-page editor, `PUT /api/rules/global` (10 KB body cap), or `store.globalRules.save()` from a node script. The same regeneration pattern applies to Codex / Aider / Gemini config files — same trap, less commonly hit because TC-v3 itself uses Claude. Public diagnostic + recovery procedure for any other cloner who is affected is documented in #240. Structural fix (preventing the trap from ever firing again — likely either a tracked-file canonical source with startup sync, or an append-only marker pattern that regeneration preserves) is tracked in #240 as separate work.

### Changed

- **"Run Critic" button: clarify the contract via label + confirm dialog + toast (#230)** — the methodology-action button on prawduct projects was previously labeled `Run Critic` with `confirm: false`, so clicking it skipped any dialog and silently POSTed to `/api/projects/:name/actions/invoke-critic`. The handler only appends an entry to `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json`; it never *runs* a Critic. New operators clicked the button expecting an automated review, saw the toast `Run Critic: recorded`, and reasonably concluded the button was broken (it wasn't — the contract was mislabeled). **What changed.** (1) Label renamed `Run Critic` → `Mark Critic Run` (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json:106`) so the imperative is honest about what the click does. (2) `confirm: false` → `confirm: true` so the contract-clarifying dialog actually fires. (3) Two new optional per-action wording fields added to the methodology template schema — `confirmMessage` and `successToast` — used by `public/session.js#invokeMethodologyAction` when present, falling back to the generic `Run "<label>" for this project?` / `<label>: recorded` when absent. (4) The Critic action's `confirmMessage` reads: *"Confirm an Independent Critic review was completed for this branch. This button does NOT run a Critic automatically — it records that you (or a separate review agent) have completed one, so the wrap step's critic-check passes. Continue?"* — addressing the misread head-on. (5) Its `successToast` reads: *"Critic review recorded for this branch"*. **API surface change.** `lib/projects.js:enrichProject` (line 602 region) extends the methodology-action allow-list to surface `confirmMessage` and `successToast` when present and non-empty; absent fields stay absent (the handler's `typeof === 'string' && length > 0` guard tolerates both shapes). Per `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates`, the inline comment now documents that the allow-list is intentionally restrictive and lists every field it exposes. **Tests.** `test/api-actions.test.js`'s `prawduct project response includes actions[]` case extended from 2 assertions to 7: label is the new value, confirm flipped to true, confirmMessage and successToast are present-and-non-empty strings on the wire. Other test files that reference `Run Critic` as a fixture string (e.g. `test/store.test.js:896-1402`) are not load-bearing for the rename — they test store-layer merge logic against synthetic data, not the prawduct template — so they're left alone. Full suite 2445/2446 pass (1 pre-existing skip on this case-insensitive host). Closes #230.

### Added

- **"Restart TangleClaw" button in stale-server banner + Global Settings → Diagnostics (#235)** — adds a one-click restart path so operators don't have to drop to a terminal for `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$UID/com.tangleclaw.server` every time the stale-server banner (#199) lights up. **Two surfaces, same handler.** (1) The stale-server banner (`public/index.html:287`) now renders a *Restart TangleClaw* button alongside the warning text — visible only when the server reports a non-null `restartMechanism`. (2) The Global Settings modal (gear icon → "Diagnostics" section, `public/ui.js#openGlobalSettings`) carries the same button as an always-available alternative. Both wire to `triggerServerRestart()` in `public/landing.js`, which confirms via dialog, POSTs to the new endpoint, displays a "Restarting…" state, polls `/api/server-info` until `startedAt` advances, then reloads the page. Double-clicks (banner + modal) coalesce via `state.restartInFlight`. **Backend.** New `POST /api/server/restart` route in `server.js` returns 202 Accepted *before* shelling out (so the response actually flushes before the SIGKILL), then `setTimeout(() => execSync('launchctl kickstart -k gui/$(id -u)/com.tangleclaw.server'), 80)`. Returns 501 with a descriptive error when no mechanism is available — the frontend reads `restartMechanism: null` from `/api/server-info` and hides the button cleanly, so 501 is a defensive path that should never reach an operator. **Mechanism detection.** `lib/server-info.js#detectRestartMechanism()` returns `'launchctl'` when the host is macOS (`os.platform() === 'darwin'`) AND the per-user plist exists at `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.tangleclaw.server.plist`; returns `null` otherwise. Cached on first call — the plist location is install-time-fixed, so re-stating it on every poll would be wasted. **Linux support is a deliberate follow-up** — `systemctl --user restart tangleclaw.service` is the equivalent invocation but only applies when TC is installed via systemd, which today's installer doesn't yet do. The mechanism-detection seam (`buildRestartCommand(mechanism)`) is structured so adding a `'systemctl'` branch is a self-contained change. **Tests.** 12 new cases. `test/server-info.test.js`: 5 cases for `detectRestartMechanism` (macOS+plist → `'launchctl'`; macOS-no-plist → `null`; Linux → `null`; unknown platform → `null`; caching pin), 2 cases for `buildRestartCommand` (exact command shape; null for unknown mechanism), 2 cases for `getServerInfo` surfacing the field. `test/api-system.test.js`: 3 cases for the route (501 when no mechanism; 202 + body when mechanism present, using `'true'` shell builtin as the no-op command so the test process survives; 500 when detection and builder disagree — defensive pin). Full suite 2457/2458 pass (1 pre-existing skip). Closes #235.
- **`### Internal` CHANGELOG subsection + tightened minor-bump trigger (#231)** — `version-bump` wrap step now recognizes a new `### Internal` subsection in `[Unreleased]` for refactors, test-only changes, dev tooling, CI tweaks, and doc-only edits that don't change user-facing behavior. Entries logged there still appear in `CHANGELOG.md` (full auditable history) but are intentionally excluded from `MINOR_TRIGGER_SUBSECTIONS`, so a release made up entirely of internal churn stays at a patch bump instead of inflating the minor counter. Mixed with `### Added` or `### Changed`, the user-visible subsection still wins and minor fires — `### Internal` does not "veto" a real feature. **What changed.** `SUBSECTION_RE` in `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js:72` now matches `Internal` alongside the existing Keep-a-Changelog set; the JSDoc precedence list (lines 19-25) and `_decideBumpLevel`'s docstring document the new bucket. The `MINOR_TRIGGER_SUBSECTIONS` set is unchanged — `Internal` is parsed but deliberately not included, so the patch-fallthrough path in `_decideBumpLevel` catches it. **Tests** (in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s existing `wrap-step version-bump — pure helpers` block): one new `_parseUnreleased` case pinning that `Internal` surfaces in `subsections[]` alongside `Added`; one new `\`### Internal\` subsection (#231)` sub-describe with five cases covering Internal-only → patch, Internal+Fixed → patch (both orderings), Internal+Added → minor (both orderings; user-visible wins), Internal+Changed → minor, and BREAKING+Internal → major (BREAKING precedence unchanged). Full suite 277/277 pass. **Operator-facing doc.** `CLAUDE.md` Global Rules → Releases & Versioning section now carries the bump-level decision table verbatim, so future sessions pick the subsection by user-visible impact rather than file footprint. The next wrap that contains only `### Internal` (or `### Internal` + `### Fixed`) entries will demonstrably bump to patch instead of minor — the closed loop the issue called for. Closes #231.
- **Feature Index dogfooded on TC-v3 (#207 Chunk 4)** — closes out the four-chunk Feature Index build. `featureIndexEnabled` is now `true` on TC-v3's own project config, and `FEATURES.md` ships at the repo root with hand-authored pointer entries across UI / Web, Server / API, Methodologies / Engines, and CLI / Tooling. The Chunk-1 stub-seeding helper was verified end-to-end via a `PATCH /api/projects/TangleClaw-v3 {"featureIndexEnabled": true}` API call: the seed template lands when the toggle flips, and the hand-authored content replaces the placeholder sections. **Verification deferred.** Two parts of the plan's verification matrix can only run in *future* sessions and are intentionally not part of this PR: (1) starting a fresh Claude Code session on TC-v3 to confirm the Chunk-2 SessionStart injection actually pastes `## Feature Index` into the prime context, and (2) producing a PR that touches a brand-new file to confirm Chunk-3's `features-toc` wrap-step appends a TBD stub. Both will happen organically as the project continues; if either misbehaves, the regression is captured in a follow-up issue rather than blocking the dogfood landing. **Cross-references.** `MEMORY.md` gains a `reference_features_index.md` entry pointing at `FEATURES.md` as the canonical "where does feature X live?" lookup, so future sessions know to consult it before spawning Explore agents.

### Internal

- **Stale-plan hygiene rule + `.claude/plans/archive/` convention** — adds two paragraphs to `CLAUDE.md` Build Plans & Chunks section codifying that plan files whose chunk has shipped get moved to `<project-root>/.claude/plans/archive/` (preserves the design rationale without polluting the active listing) AND that sessions starting work on a "next chunk" must verify the referenced issue's state via `gh issue view <N> --json state` before treating any plan as canonical. Both halves are needed: archiving is the convention, the issue-state check is the contract that protects across clones (the `.claude/` directory is gitignored, so archives are local-only). **Why now.** The 2026-05-23 session recommended #137 as the next chunk because `build-plan.md` was present at the repo root; the issue had been closed 18 days prior. The trap was structural — "plan exists" was treated as "work is ready" — and now the rule explicitly requires the issue-state check. **Local cleanup performed this session (not in this PR diff because `.claude/` and `build-plan*.md` are gitignored):** 19 stale plan files moved to `.claude/plans/archive/` — 13 from `.claude/plans/` covering closed issues #103, #131, #139, #144, #145, #155, #158, #165, #207, plus three unnumbered plans self-marked closed (`prawduct-aicontent-prompts.md` via PR #200, `version-bump-handler.md` via PR #202, `replicated-coalescing-journal.md` whose `syncAllProjects()` shipped at `lib/projects.js:728`), and 6 stale `build-plan*.md` files at the repo root (including the #137-specific `build-plan.md` that triggered this whole janitor pass). Active plans directory is now empty; future planning sessions start from a clean slate.

## [3.18.0] - 2026-05-23

### Fixed

- **Case-insensitive project identity for orphan-port import banner + every identity-creating gate (#221, closes #188)** — the landing page's `checkPortImports` (`public/landing.js:732-762`) compared lease project names against TC project names case-sensitively. A PortHub lease registered as `monad-1` (lowercase, from a programmatic registration) against a TC project named `Monad-1` (mixed-case, from a human-typed create) was falsely advertised as an "unregistered project" — clicking Import would have created a duplicate. Dogfooded today; the user spotted the false banner and asked whether the bug was on the PortHub side or the TC side. **Fix.** New `_canonicalProjectName(name)` helper in `public/landing.js` normalizes to lowercase. `checkPortImports`'s `Set` membership check, ignored-list check, and conflict-detection cross-reference now all run through it on both sides. Lease bucketing preserves the original casing (the banner shows the lease's wire-form name, not a normalized form). **Symmetric gate audit (#188 closure scope, Critic-driven expansion).** Added `store.projects.getByNameCaseInsensitive(name)` (SQL `WHERE name = ? COLLATE NOCASE`). Per `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates`, every gate around the same conceptual flag (project-name identity) must check the same predicate, so every identity-CREATING site was migrated together: `createProject`'s duplicate-check, `updateProject`'s rename-collision check, `attachProject`'s already-registered check (`lib/projects.js:1119`), `listAllProjects`'s filesystem-scan unregistered-filter (`lib/projects.js:1619`), the startup project-sync warning (`server.js:642`), and the `POST /api/projects/import` warning (`server.js:969`). Without this audit, attach + import + startup-sync would have remained back doors that could introduce the very case-collisions the new validator rejects. **Error message format.** When `existing.name === requested.name` exactly, the legacy error format is preserved (no spurious "case-insensitive match" suffix). When they differ in case, the error cites the existing project's actual casing so the operator can find it — e.g. `Project "foo-1" already exists (case-insensitive match for "Foo-1")`. Same pattern across create, rename, attach, sync, and import paths. **Self-rename allowance.** `updateProject`'s rename-collision check uses an `existing.id !== project.id` guard so case-only self-rename (`foo-1` → `Foo-1` on the same project) stays legal at the validator layer. The filesystem-side directory rename is a separate concern that case-insensitive filesystems (macOS APFS-CI, Windows) silently absorb anyway. **Deliberately out of scope.** Auto-lowercasing existing project names at storage. Project names are filesystem-coupled (`<projectsDir>/<name>`) and display-coupled (modal headers, tmux session names, pill text); renaming `Monad-1 → monad-1` would touch directories, tmux sessions, port leases, engine configs, `.claude/settings.json` hooks, and `.tangleclaw/project.json` files — high blast radius for marginal payoff. Preserve original casing for display; canonicalize only at comparison sites. `store.projects.getByName` stays case-sensitive — only identity-check call sites opt into the looser match via the new `getByNameCaseInsensitive`. URL-lookup routes (`GET /api/projects/:name`, status queries) also stay exact-case — the URL is the identity, surprising substitution would be worse than the false-match. **Test coverage:** 3 new tests in `test/projects.test.js`'s `createProject` block (case-collision rejection both directions, error-message correctness, exact-case back-compat), 3 new tests in a new `updateProject` rename-collision sub-describe (case-only self-rename allowed at validator layer with case-insensitive-FS skip, cross-rename rejected with case-collision cite, exact-case rename-target legacy error format), 1 new attach-collision test (case-insensitive-FS skip pattern matching the rename test), 4 new `test/store-projects.test.js` tests for `getByNameCaseInsensitive` (cross-case match, exact-case match, null on absent, distinct-from-getByName regression pin). Full suite 2438 / 2438 pass with 1 skipped on this case-insensitive host (net +11 from this fix). Closes #221 + #188.

### Added

- **Stale-server detection + banner (#199)** — new `lib/server-info.js` captures the git HEAD SHA at server boot and exposes a snapshot-comparison API. New `GET /api/server-info` route returns `{startupSha, currentDiskSha, isStale, commitsAhead, startedAt, uptimeSeconds}`. The landing page's init sequence fetches this in parallel with the other background loads, **polls every 60s** so the banner surfaces mid-session when the operator merges/pulls with a tab open, and renders a danger-coloured banner above the projects grid when `isStale === true` — the text shows the short SHAs of both states, the commit count between them, the running-since duration (e.g. "Running for 3h 12m"), and instructs the operator to restart TC. Wired into the existing `.orphan-banner` class shape via a `.stale-server-banner` colour variant (danger red instead of amber) so the two banners read distinctly when both surface together. **Why this matters.** Node caches required modules at process start. When the operator pulls or merges code while TC is running, the on-disk source advances but the running process keeps using its in-memory copy until restart. The browser fetches fresh static assets each page load — so the front-end shows the latest UI while the server still runs old behaviour. Silent-mismatch bugs follow: the canonical incident this issue was filed for was the Feature Index toggle clicked in a post-#208 UI, sent to a pre-#208 backend that doesn't recognize `featureIndexEnabled` and silently drops it on save (toggle appears to revert on the next read). Dogfooded today during the #207 series merge. **No-git fallback.** TC run outside a git checkout (tarball install, packaged distribution, CI) returns null for both SHAs; `isStale` reduces to `false` and the banner never fires. Detection is opt-in via the presence of a `.git` directory. Dirty-tree detection (uncommitted changes) is deliberately out of scope for v1 — only merged-since-startup commits surface.
