Auto-restart and per-module hot-reload are deferred. **XSS-defensive UI.** `renderStaleServerBanner` clamps `commitsAhead` to a non-negative integer (`Math.max(0, Number(x) | 0)`) and `esc()`-passes every string before assignment to `innerHTML` — matches the rest-of-file convention; a future server bug that leaks a non-numeric `commitsAhead` cannot inject markup. **Test-only reset export.** The module exposes `__unsafeResetForTest` (double-underscore + `unsafe` token) instead of the more conventional `_resetForTest`, so accidental production usage is grep-loud at review time. **Test coverage:** new `test/server-info.test.js` with 17 tests — capture/idempotence/no-git-fallback for `captureStartup`; clean-state, stale-state, degraded-state semantics for `getServerInfo` (matched SHAs, null SHAs, mid-runtime git removal, non-numeric rev-list output, exec timeouts via ETIMEDOUT); detached-HEAD scenario (real SHA returned, stale detection still works); pure-helper coverage for `_countCommitsAhead` (null inputs, identical SHAs that short-circuit without shelling out). Full suite 2427 / 2427 pass (net +17 from this feature). Closes #199.

### Changed

- **Extracted `todayIsoLocal` to shared `lib/wrap-steps/_date.js`** — post-#216 / post-#215 refactor that closes the duplication called out in both PRs' CHANGELOG entries. The local-zoned date formatter (`Date#getFullYear` / `getMonth` / `getDate`) previously lived inline in BOTH `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` (#216's fix for `## [version] - YYYY-MM-DD` headings) and `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js` (#215's `## TODO (auto-stubbed YYYY-MM-DD)` heading); duplicating it meant a future "fix it" patch could silently regress one call site. **Refactor shape:** new `lib/wrap-steps/_date.js` (underscore-prefixed filename signals "internal helper, not a step kind that `STEP_DISPATCH` dispatches to") exports a single `todayIsoLocal()` function. Both handlers now `require('./_date')` and bind their `_internal.todayIso` to the shared export. The pre-existing public names `versionBump._todayIsoLocal` and `featuresToc._todayIsoLocal` are preserved as **re-exports** of the shared function — referentially identical to `_internal.todayIso` and to `dateUtil.todayIsoLocal`. This keeps every existing wiring-pin test passing untouched (no test file changes required for #216 or #215's coverage to stay valid) while collapsing the implementation to one source of truth. **Test coverage:** new `test/wrap-steps-date.test.js` with 7 tests — shape pin (YYYY-MM-DD, 10 chars, separators), local-vs-UTC behavior pin (uses a `global.Date` subclass to pin a UTC moment whose local projection differs by date; skips gracefully on UTC-host CI where the distinction is unobservable), and 5 wiring/identity pins asserting that `dateUtil.todayIsoLocal`, `versionBump._internal.todayIso`, `versionBump._todayIsoLocal`, `featuresToc._internal.todayIso`, and `featuresToc._todayIsoLocal` ALL resolve to the same function reference. The all-five-references-identical pin is the core refactor invariant — if anyone ever copies the helper back inline to "fix it in one place," this test fails on the very next suite run. Full suite 2410 / 2410 pass (net +7 from this refactor).

### Fixed

- **`_parseFields` now accepts natural-English heading variants (#201)** — `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js:_parseFields` previously required exact-string equality (after `.toLowerCase()`) between the `## Heading` text and the declared `captureField` name. This silently rejected the most natural Markdown a human or AI would write: `step.captureFields: ['nextSteps']` would match `## nextsteps` but NOT `## Next Steps` (space-separated), `## next-steps` (kebab), `## NEXT_STEPS` (screaming snake), or `## Next.Steps`. The handler then returned `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['Required captureField "nextSteps" missing or empty in AI response']}` and halted the wrap pipeline. Surfaced as Critic n1 on PR #200; the workaround there was to harden the `memory-update` prompt with explicit "use these exact spellings" instructions — works, but every prompt edit is one slip away from re-introducing the block. **Fix:** new `_normalizeFieldKey(s)` helper lowercases and strips every non-`[a-z0-9]` character, applied symmetrically to both sides of the comparison. After normalization, `Next Steps`, `next-steps`, `next_steps`, `NEXT.STEPS`, and `nextSteps` all collapse to the same match key `nextsteps`. Output map keys remain the DECLARED `captureField` name (not the normalized form) so downstream consumers (`_completeV2Wrap`'s summary deriver, the prawduct lockstep / inverse-drift pins in `test/prawduct-aicontent-prompts.test.js`) do not have to also normalize. Normalization is a strict superset of the prior equality contract — every input the old parser matched still matches; only the previously-rejected variants now also match. **Test coverage:** 11 new tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s `_parseFields` describe block — natural-English variants (`## Next Steps`, kebab, screaming snake, dotted), canonical form still works (regression pin against over-correction), multiple mixed-style headings in one response, output-key contract (declared name, not normalized form). Plus a dedicated `_normalizeFieldKey` describe block covering non-alphanumeric stripping, case folding, digit preservation, and defensive inputs (empty, null, undefined, number coercion). The prawduct lockstep / inverse-drift tests are intentionally left untouched — they enforce a STRICTER convention than the parser (single-word PascalCase headings) as a style guide for bundled methodology prompts; the parser is the safety net for community-authored methodologies and for AI responses that drift from canonical. Full suite 2360 / 2360 pass (net +11 from this fix). Closes #201.

### Added

- **YOLO mode in the launch picker for Gemini / Aider / Codex (#209)** — extends the session-launch mode modal beyond Claude Code so every engine with a documented skip-permissions / unattended-execution flag exposes it as a picker option. **Gemini CLI** gains four modes mirroring Claude's structure: `Interactive` (default), `Auto Edit` (`--approval-mode auto_edit`), `Plan Only` (`--approval-mode plan`), and `YOLO` (`--yolo` — auto-approve all actions). **Aider** gains `Interactive` + `YOLO` (`--yes-always`). **Codex** gains `Interactive` + `Full Auto` (`--full-auto` — sandboxed automatic execution, not true YOLO; the label and description call out the distinction). The modal's render gate at `public/landing.js:470` (`Object.keys(launchModes).length > 1`) means each engine needs ≥2 modes to surface the picker, which all three satisfy. Backend wiring (`lib/sessions.js:_buildLaunchCommand`) is already engine-agnostic — no JS changes required, only data. **OpenClaw** was deliberately scoped out: it's TC's in-house wrapper with no upstream YOLO flag to map, so its `launchModes` semantics need to be designed deliberately (follow-up tracked at [#210](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/210)). **Per-engine flag rationale:** all four CLIs (`claude --dangerously-skip-permissions`, `gemini --yolo`, `aider --yes-always`, `codex --full-auto`) verified against the locally installed binary's `--help` output before wiring. **Test coverage:** new `launchModes parity across engines (#209)` describe block in `test/engines.test.js` pinning (a) each engine's YOLO flag args exactly, (b) presence of `warning` text on every YOLO mode, (c) `defaultLaunchMode` key exists in `launchModes`, (d) every engine with `launchModes` has >1 mode so the modal renders, (e) sentinel pin asserting OpenClaw intentionally has no `launchModes` until [#210](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/210) is resolved. Full suite 2349 / 2349 pass (net +6 from this PR).

- **Feature Index — `features-toc` wrap-step handler (#207, Chunk 3)** — third sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. New `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js` handler appends stub entries to `<projectPath>/FEATURES.md` for files touched on the current branch that are not yet referenced anywhere in the index. Inserted into prawduct's `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` between `next-session-prime` and `memory-update` (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`); registered in the dispatch table at `lib/wrap-pipeline.js`. **Never blocks** (matches the ADR 0002 step-kind contract + `version-bump` precedent): every degraded condition — missing `FEATURES.md`, toggle off, base branch not resolvable, empty diff, all-touched-files-already-indexed, all-touched-files-filtered — returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` with `reason` / `detail` in `output` for the wrap drawer. **Gate (ADR 0001 symmetric, write-side scope):** only `projConfig.featureIndexEnabled === true` is checked here; the engine-capability + `silentPrime` predicates are injection-site concerns (Chunk 2) — gating the wrap-side handler on engine capability would falsely deny index writes on engines that maintain the file without injecting it. **Single-transaction discipline:** the handler stages content under `staged['features-toc:append'] = {primingPath, newContent, changed:true, addedCount, addedFiles, todoDate}` — `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js:_flushStagedWrites` already duck-types on `{primingPath, newContent, changed}` so the write happens during the commit step's flush, never inside this handler. **Commit body line:** new duck-type case in `_buildBodyLines` matches `{addedCount, addedFiles, todoDate}` — emits `- Feature Index: N stub(s) appended (file1, file2, file3, +M more)` so wrap commits surface the index churn in `git log`. **Drift detection:** `_extractIndexedPaths` scans existing `FEATURES.md` for path-like tokens using a single regex against the same extension allowlist; the matcher is intentionally permissive (matches inside backticks, free text, comments) so an entry written `` `lib/foo.js:42` `` or `lib/foo.js (line 42)` both register the file. Bias is toward over-skipping — a missed stub is recoverable, a false-positive duplicate would pollute the index. **Filter:** extension allowlist (`.js .jsx .ts .tsx .json .md .html .css .yaml .yml .sh`), prefix exclusion (`node_modules/`, `dist/`, `coverage/`, `build/`, `.git/`, `.tangleclaw/`), leading-dot-segment exclusion, basename exclusion (`CHANGELOG.md`, `README.md`, `FEATURES.md`). Set is intentionally moderate; Chunk 4 dogfood will surface whether tightening is needed. **Base branch resolution:** tries `main`, falls back to `master`, skips when neither resolves locally — uses `git diff --name-only <base>...HEAD` three-dot syntax so only branch-introduced changes (not mainline drift since branch point) are scanned. **Idempotence on re-wrap:** after a successful flush, the appended paths are present in `FEATURES.md`; the next wrap's drift scan finds them and skips with `reason: 'no drift'`. No explicit "this run" marker is needed — drift detection is naturally idempotent against the cumulative index state. **Migration note for existing prawduct installs.** `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` is reconciled by `_reconcileMergeBy:id` (ADR 0001), which is **additive-only AND end-appending** — bundled entries with a new `idKey` are pushed to the end of the live array, not inserted at the bundled position. On existing installs with a cached `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` predating this PR, `features-toc` will land AFTER `commit` rather than between `next-session-prime` and `memory-update`. Because `commit` is the flusher, this means the stub append silently no-ops on cached installs until the cache is refreshed. Workaround mirrors the v3.17.0 ai-content prompts recipe: (a) stop the TC server, delete `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (or the full `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/` directory), then restart — `_copyBundledTemplates` re-copies from `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` only when the cached dir is missing; or (b) wait for a future chunk that introduces position-aware reconciliation. The dogfood pass in Chunk 4 will exercise this refresh path. **UTC-date parity (#205, applied in-chunk).** The `## TODO (auto-stubbed YYYY-MM-DD)` heading date uses a `_todayIsoLocal` formatter (`Date#getFullYear`/`getMonth`/`getDate`) instead of `Date#toISOString().slice(0,10)` so the date reflects the operator's local clock, not UTC — same bug pattern as `version-bump` was fixed for in #216. Both call sites should ultimately share a util module; deliberately duplicated here to keep this chunk's surface contained, with the shared-util refactor tracked as a follow-up after #216 + #215 merge. **Test coverage:** new `test/wrap-step-features-toc.test.js` with 31 tests across pure helpers (`_isIndexableCandidate`, `_extractIndexedPaths`, `_appendTodoSection`, `_todayIsoLocal`), handler skip semantics (every degraded path), happy-path stage shape (6-field assertion), single-transaction discipline (no filesystem write inside the handler), idempotence (re-run after simulated flush yields no new appends), commit-body line emission (truncation, defensive zero-count, duck-type precedence), and UTC-date parity (shape, local-vs-UTC behavior with host-aware skip, wiring pin). Cached-install regression test in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pins `_reconcileMergeBy:id` end-append behavior so future drift here is caught at unit-test level. Step-count + step-order pins updated in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (3 assertions: STEP_DISPATCH expected list, step-id order, kind order; runWrapPipeline step count 8→9), `test/sessions.test.js` (V2 lifecycle step-count 8→9; legacy NL prompt `Wrap steps:` string), and `test/skills.test.js` (`getWrapSkill('prawduct').steps[]`). **What's deferred to Chunk 4 (the final chunk):** TC-v3 itself gets a populated `FEATURES.md` hand-authored from the Explore findings; a small test commit touching a new file → wrap → confirms `features-toc` stubs it; CHANGELOG + MEMORY.md gain pointers to `FEATURES.md` as a discoverable surface. Full suite 2381 / 2381 pass (net +23 from this chunk — Chunk 3 base 28 tests + cached-install regression pin + 3 UTC-parity tests). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

- **Feature Index — SessionStart injection (#207, Chunk 2)** — second sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. When `featureIndexEnabled === true` AND `silentPrime === true` AND the engine profile has `capabilities.supportsSilentPrime === true`, `generatePrimePrompt()` in `lib/sessions.js` reads the project's `FEATURES.md` from the project root and pushes its trimmed contents into the prime prompt under a `## Feature Index` heading. Injection slots between the Last Session Summary and Eval Audit Mode blocks so it's adjacent to other session-dynamic state (Active Learnings, Last Session). **Symmetric gate (ADR 0001):** all three predicates must be true — asymmetric gates leak orphan state (the lesson pinned by `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates` after PR #125's Critic-caught regression). **Defensive shape-checks:** `engineProfile` and `engineProfile.capabilities` are explicitly null-checked before `supportsSilentPrime` is read, so a synthesized / minimal profile (the integration-test path and any future engine that omits the capabilities object) skips cleanly. **Graceful skip on read failure:** missing / unreadable `FEATURES.md` is caught silently — absence must never block session start (the file is opt-in scaffolding seeded by Chunk 1 only when the user toggles on). **Whitespace short-circuit:** a file containing only whitespace produces no section in the prime, so a freshly-seeded but un-edited template doesn't surface an empty heading. **Truncation preserved:** the existing `template.prime.maxTokens` truncation at `lib/sessions.js:408-413` still runs after the section is appended, so an oversize `FEATURES.md` cannot blow the prompt budget — surfaced as a `[Prime prompt truncated]` marker matching every other prime-state addition. **Test coverage:** 8 new tests in `test/sessions.test.js`'s `generatePrimePrompt` describe block — happy path (all three gates true → section present with body); each gate's negative case (toggle off / silentPrime off / engine capability false / missing capabilities object entirely); missing FEATURES.md graceful skip; whitespace-only file produces no section; truncation budget honored against an oversized FEATURES.md. **What's deferred to remaining chunks:** the `features-toc` wrap-step handler that auto-appends stubs for PR-touched files not in `FEATURES.md` (Chunk 3); dogfooding TC-v3 itself with a populated index (Chunk 4). Full suite 2357 / 2357 pass (net +8 from this chunk). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

- **Feature Index — per-project toggle + template seeding (#207, Chunk 1)** — first sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. Introduces an opt-in `featureIndexEnabled` field in `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG` (default `false`) plus a settings-modal toggle that, when flipped on, seeds a `FEATURES.md` template at the project root if the file does not already exist. The seed helper `_seedFeatureIndexFile` is idempotent — never overwrites pre-existing content, never deletes on toggle-off (the file is a user-owned, git-tracked artifact). **What this chunk does:** persists the flag, surfaces it through `enrichProject`, renders the toggle in `public/ui.js`'s settings modal (engine-agnostic, always shown — the file + future wrap-step parity are engine-independent), and seeds the template stub. **What's deferred to later chunks:** SessionStart prime-prompt injection of `FEATURES.md` contents (Chunk 2, engine-capability-gated at the injection site per ADR 0001 symmetric-gate principle); the `features-toc` wrap-step handler that auto-appends stubs for PR-touched files not in `FEATURES.md` (Chunk 3); dogfooding TC-v3 itself with a populated index (Chunk 4). **Validation placement** mirrors the `silentPrime` precedent (`lib/projects.js:1169`): boolean type-check runs pre-mutation so a rejection drops cleanly without partial-state corruption. **API surface:** `PATCH /api/projects/:name` accepts `featureIndexEnabled: boolean`; `GET /api/projects/:name` and `GET /api/projects` return `featureIndexEnabled` on each project. **Test coverage:** new `test/feature-index.test.js` with 15 tests across DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG default, helper idempotence (create / preserve existing / non-throwing on error), updateProject validation (5 non-boolean shapes rejected), seeding behavior on toggle-on / toggle-off / idempotent true→true save, enrichProject surface, and PATCH-body independence (combo updates persist both fields; rejection isolation). Full suite 2343 / 2343 pass (net +15 from this chunk). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

### Fixed

- **`version-bump` handler now stamps the release heading with the operator's LOCAL date instead of UTC (#205)** — `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js:_internal.todayIso` previously called `new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)`, which always returns UTC. When the wrap ran after the operator's local-zone day had ended but before midnight UTC (e.g. 5pm PT on 2026-05-22 = 00:25 UTC on 2026-05-23), the new `## [version] - YYYY-MM-DD` heading came out one day ahead of every other entry in the file. Surfaced the evening this PR landed when cutting v3.17.0 itself: handler stamped `## [3.17.0] - 2026-05-23` against a local 2026-05-22, requiring a manual patch before the release shipped — Critic n4 of that release flagged the inconsistency. **Fix:** extracted a named `_todayIsoLocal` formatter using `Date#getFullYear` / `getMonth` / `getDate`, no timezone-database dependency, exported it so tests can pin the wiring. `_internal.todayIso` now points to `_todayIsoLocal`. **Test coverage:** three new regression tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s `wrap-step version-bump — pure helpers` describe block — (1) YYYY-MM-DD shape pin (10 chars, separators at indices 4 and 7, regex match); (2) local-vs-UTC behavior pin using a `global.Date` subclass that pins the wall clock to a known local moment and asserts the formatter returns the local date regardless of host TZ; (3) wiring pin asserting `_internal.todayIso === _todayIsoLocal` so a future refactor cannot silently regress to a UTC-emitting default. All existing handler tests already stub `_internal.todayIso` to a deterministic literal, so the fix is purely internal to the default factory — no test plumbing churn elsewhere. **Note on `features-toc` (#207 Chunk 3, PR #215):** the new handler ships the same `todayIso: () => new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)` pattern; it inherits the same bug until either #215 is rebased against this fix post-merge or a follow-up applies the same change to `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js`. Both call sites should ultimately share a single utility; deferred so this fix stays surgical and #215 can land on its own merits. Full suite 2347 / 2347 pass (net +3 from this fix).

## [3.17.0] - 2026-05-22

### Changed

- **Prawduct `ai-content` step prompts populated (open-queue #2 post-#139)** — `data/templates/prawduct/template.json`'s three `ai-content` steps (`changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`, `memory-update`) gain real prompts. Prior to this change the steps shipped with `prompt: ""` and surfaced as `skipped` rows in every V2 wrap drawer post-Chunk-11c — functional, but produced no user-visible session output. New prompts instruct the AI to: (`changelog-update`) read `git log <lastWrapSha>..HEAD` + working tree, then edit CHANGELOG.md `[Unreleased]` per Keep-a-Changelog style with a `## Result` tail; (`learnings-capture`) reflect on non-obvious takeaways and append to `.tangleclaw/memories/learnings.md`, or write `no novel learnings` rather than fabricating signal; (`memory-update`) demote prior `Last Session` block to `wrap-log.md`, write a new block to `MEMORY.md`, then emit `## Summary` + `## NextSteps` + `## Learnings` heading blocks that `_parseFields` in `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` parses against the step's `captureFields` and `_completeV2Wrap`'s summary deriver consumes for the wrap commit subject. **Migration note for existing prawduct projects:** the methodology template is cached at `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (via `_copyBundledTemplates` at `lib/store.js` on TC server boot). `_reconcileMergeBy:id` (ADR 0001) is additive-only on existing step ids, so cached templates with `prompt: ""` keep their empty prompts on every subsequent boot. To pick up the populated prompts on an existing install: (a) stop the TC server, delete `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (or the full `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/` directory), then restart — `_copyBundledTemplates` re-copies from `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` only when the cached dir is missing; or (b) wait for a future chunk that introduces per-field reconciliation of `step.prompt`. The per-project `.tangleclaw/project.json` is the per-project *config*, NOT the methodology template cache — deleting it does not refresh the bundled prompts. New test file `test/prawduct-aicontent-prompts.test.js` pins the prompt invariants (>=200 chars each, `## Summary` / `## NextSteps` / `## Learnings` instructions in memory-update, `captureFields` lockstep) and the minimal-methodology empty-prompt anchor (Chunk 11c contract still exercised by bundled methodology). ADR 0002 Status line carries the extension marker.

- **`DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2: false → true` (#139, Chunk 11c)** — **closes the #139 series.** The Session Wrap button now drives the server-side `wrap_pipeline` runner by default; the legacy NL-prompt-via-tmux flow is reachable only via explicit per-project opt-out (`wrapV2: false` in `<project>/.tangleclaw/project.json`). Combined with Chunk 11a (V2 lifecycle transition) and Chunk 11b (`invoke-critic` action producer) that landed earlier in the day, V2 is now a quality default: sessions wrap-to-completion correctly, the `critic-check` step has a real producer for `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json`, and prawduct's bundled pipeline runs the full step set (`open-pr-check` + `critic-check` are wired in here for the first time).
  - **`lib/store.js`** — `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2: false → true`. The block comment that previously documented the opt-in is replaced with the opt-out semantics + migration recipe. `projectConfigApi.load`'s deep-merge is unchanged, so existing projects with an explicit `wrapV2: false` in their on-disk config preserve the legacy path with no further intervention; only projects without a `project.json` (brand-new) or whose `project.json` predates the field (legacy installs that never touched the field) pick up the new V2 default.
  - **`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`** — `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` gains two leading steps: `{id: "open-pr-check", kind: "pr-check", blocker: false}` and `{id: "critic-check", kind: "critic-check", blocker: false}`. Chunks 7 + 8 deliberately did not wire these into prawduct's pipeline so the legacy NL prompt's byte-equal pin could keep passing through Chunks 4–10; the wiring lands now alongside the flag flip so V2 prawduct projects get the full surface (PR-state surfacing + Critic warning) immediately. Order: PR-check first (surfaces session-scoped PRs before any heavy steps so the user can act on the drawer's per-PR resolution dropdowns); critic-check second (its warning state needs to be staged before the `commit` step's body-builder runs). Both are `blocker: false`.
  - **Legacy NL prompt's `Wrap steps:` list changes** as a side effect of the prawduct-template change (`lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate` flattens every `step.id` into the legacy `steps` array). The post-Chunk-11c legacy prompt for prawduct reads `Wrap steps: open-pr-check, critic-check, version-bump, changelog-update, learnings-capture, next-session-prime, memory-update, commit`. This is intentional — both the V2 pipeline and the legacy NL prompt (for opt-out projects) reflect the same authoritative step list from the methodology template. The byte-equal regression pin in `test/sessions.test.js` and `test/skills.test.js` is updated to reflect the new list.
  - **Two `wrapV2`-related test semantics inverted.** (1) `wrapV2 absent from projConfig (older on-disk state)` was previously pinned to "absent → legacy fallback" because pre-flip the default was `false`; post-flip absent → V2-routing, so the test is reframed and rewritten to assert the new contract. (2) `wrapV2:false (default)` is renamed to `wrapV2:false (explicit opt-out) uses the legacy NL-prompt path with the post-Chunk-11c step list` and pinned against the new step list (the legacy path's prompt structure — prefix, separator, capture-fields suffix — is byte-equal to pre-Chunk-11c; only the comma-joined steps inside `Wrap steps:` differ, and that's a function of the methodology template, not the legacy path's behavior).
  - **Test scaffolding fallout.** The `triggerWrap (methodology-driven)` describe block in `test/sessions.test.js` gains a `wrapV2: false` baseline in its `beforeEach` so the (numerous) legacy-asserting tests inside it stay focused on legacy behavior without each one having to repeat the projConfig write. The V2-routing tests inside the same block already write `wrapV2: true` per-test, so the baseline doesn't collide. **Two new tests** pin the Chunk 11c default-flip contract: `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2 is true` (direct invariant pin against `lib/store.js`); `a fresh project (no on-disk config) routes to the V2 path` (deletes the on-disk `project.json` to assert the fresh-project default; stubs `runWrapPipeline` to avoid exercising real-handler state on the tmp project). Step-count assertions in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` and `test/sessions.test.js` for prawduct change from 6 → 8 to match the new wired-in surface.
  - **Migration docs.** README's `Configuration` section now carries a `Session Wrap (V2 default, opt-out path)` block with the per-project opt-out recipe. ADR 0002's Status line carries a `Default flipped to V2 on 2026-05-19 via #139 Chunk 11c` marker; the Chunk 11c entry in the migration-path enumeration is expanded with the post-flip contract.
  - **What stays.** Legacy `triggerWrap` NL-prompt branch (one-release-cycle deprecation window). Back-compat shim in `lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate` (same window). Inert `wrap.steps` / `wrap.captureFields` reconciler entries in `ARRAY_RECONCILERS` (same window).
  - **What's gone.** The original Chunk 12 "cross-engine prompt-template parity" was marked optional in the build plan; it's now tracked as a separate follow-up to be filed when the codex / gemini-side roadmap firms up. The #139 series itself can close after this PR merges — the seven gaps it set out to fix (janitor pass, Critic compliance, test gating, durable memory updates, priming-pointer roll, structured-output derivation, multi-step-commit leak) are all server-side-deterministic now.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (2 MAJOR + 6 MINORs + 3 NITs addressed; YELLOW → GREEN — per user directive that every finding land before merge).** (M1) README oversold V2 by listing `lint`, `tests`, and `version-bump` as deterministic V2 steps — but `version-bump` is still the Chunk-3 no-op stub and `lint` / `test` aren't wired into prawduct's pipeline. Reworded the README's `Session Wrap (V2 default, opt-out path)` block to describe **only** what prawduct's pipeline actually runs today: `pr-check` + `critic-check` + `version-bump` (placeholder) + three `ai-content` placeholders (`changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`, `memory-update` with empty prompts that surface as `skipped`) + `priming-roll` + `commit`. Methodology authors can opt in `lint` / `test` via their own templates. (M2) Three prawduct `ai-content` steps ship with `"prompt": ""` and the pre-#139-Chunk-11c handler at `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js:154` returned `{ok: false, status: 'blocked'}` on empty prompts. Pre-flip this was harmless (V2 was opt-in); post-flip every prawduct V2 wrap would surface three `blocked` rows in the drawer. Changed the handler's contract: **empty or whitespace-only `step.prompt` → `{ok: true, status: 'skipped', output: null, blockers: []}`**. Methodology-author intent of an empty prompt is "placeholder, no work to do today" — `skipped` matches the intent. Three new tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pin the new behavior (empty string; whitespace-only; missing-entirely). The pre-flip `'blocks when step.prompt is empty'` test is rewritten as `'skips cleanly when step.prompt is empty (#139 Chunk 11c — placeholder semantics)'`. (N1) Stale comments in `lib/sessions.js:716-721` (`_triggerWrapV2` doc) and `:910-916` (entry-point `triggerWrap` gate) referenced the pre-flip default in future tense — both rewritten to describe the post-flip state. The gate-comment now explicitly notes the strict-equality `=== true` defensive contract. (N2) CHANGELOG cited `lib/store.js:420` for the `wrapV2` field; actual line is `426` post-comment-expansion. Dropped the line number — field name is unique. (N3) README referenced `v3.17` but `version.json` is `3.16.2`. Replaced with version-agnostic "After #139 Chunk 11c lands" / "this release". (N4) Local plan at `.claude/plans/issue-139-methodology-aware-wrap.md` Status line still read "Discovery complete. Ready to start Chunk 2" — replaced with a series-closing summary marker dated 2026-05-19. (N5) Added three round-trip persistence tests to `test/store.test.js`'s `projectConfig` describe block: explicit `wrapV2: false` survives deep-merge against the default-true config; explicit `wrapV2: true` round-trips; absent `wrapV2` defaults to `true` post-flip. These pin the migration guarantee at the unit level (the existing integration tests cover the through-`triggerWrap` path). (N6) Added a minimal-methodology variant of the opt-out test that asserts the legacy NL prompt for minimal contains `Wrap steps: learnings-capture, memory-update, commit`. (T1) Removed the redundant `projectConfig.save` from the fresh-project test's `finally` block — the outer `beforeEach` re-establishes the baseline before each test, so the inline restore was double-bookkeeping. Comment rewritten. (T3) Hoisted the duplicated `runWrapPipeline` stub literal into a frozen module-scope `EMPTY_V2_RESULT` constant shared by the absent-flag and fresh-project tests. (T4) Post-merge: delete the self-deleting auto-memory `project_issue_139_methodology_wrap.md` and prune the index line in `MEMORY.md` (per CLAUDE.md Memory Hygiene rule — the series-closed condition triggers cleanup). Tracked separately from this PR since auto-memory lives outside the repo.
  - Full suite: 2274 / 2274 pass (was 2266 at end of 11b; net +8 from Chunk 11c: +2 flip-pin tests, +2 new ai-content placeholder-semantics tests (the original `blocks-when-empty` test was rewritten as `skips-when-empty` — net replacement, not addition), +3 round-trip persistence tests in `test/store.test.js`, +1 minimal-methodology opt-out variant).

### Fixed

- **`tmux.createSession` env vars now reach the launch command's process (#190)** — `lib/tmux.js:createSession` was calling `tmux set-environment` AFTER `tmux new-session -d -s <name> <command>`, so the spawned command (e.g. an engine launcher reading from `~/.tangleclaw/engines/<id>.json` `launch.env`) inherited the original parent process env without the supplemented values. `set-environment` only affects subsequently-spawned child processes — the launch command itself was already running. Net effect: every engine override using `launch.env` to inject runtime variables (API keys, base URLs, env-keyed model selectors) silently did nothing. Surfaced via the Aider engine override → LiteLLM gateway integration: `OPENAI_API_KEY` never reached the spawned `aider` process, producing `litellm.AuthenticationError: OpenAIException - The api_key client option must be set either by passing api_key to the client or by setting the OPENAI_API_KEY environment variable`. **Fix**: use `tmux new-session -e KEY=VALUE` flags (tmux ≥ 2.8) so env is applied at session-creation time BEFORE the initial command spawns. Post-create `set-environment` loop removed (redundant once `-e` is in place, and removing it eliminates a second-source-of-truth for the same values). Each `-e VALUE` is wrapped via `_escapeArg` so values with shell metacharacters (spaces, quotes, `$`, `;`) reach the child byte-intact. **Test coverage**: `test/tmux.test.js` had zero coverage for `options.env`; added two regression pins — (1) launch command actually inherits the env vars (dump to file, read back, assert) and (2) tricky values with shell metacharacters survive the escape unchanged. **Blast radius**: any engine override using `launch.env` was silently broken; today only the Aider override exercised the path, but future env-keyed engine integrations (LiteLLM-routed codex, env-keyed gemini variants, etc.) would have hit the same trap. Full suite: 2226 / 2226 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +2). Independent corroboration: Monad-1 session identified the same tmux server / session env-cache hypothesis from their side without seeing the TC patch — diagnoses converged on `-e per-session` as the proper fix.

### Added

- **Real `version-bump` wrap-step handler (open-queue #3 post-#139)** — `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` replaces the #139 Chunk-3 no-op stub with a full handler that reads `CHANGELOG.md` `[Unreleased]` + `version.json`, decides a bump level, promotes `[Unreleased]` to a dated release, and bumps the semver. Closes the last remaining no-op stub in `lib/wrap-steps/`. **Bump-level precedence:** `options.bumpLevel` override (`patch`|`minor`|`major`) wins outright; otherwise `BREAKING` marker anywhere in the [Unreleased] body forces `major`; otherwise `### Added` / `### Changed` / `### Removed` / `### Deprecated` present → `minor`; otherwise (only `### Fixed` / `### Security`) → `patch`. **Single-transaction discipline + composite-staged-keys.** Handler never writes the filesystem; it stages TWO entries under composite keys (`'version-bump:version-json'` and `'version-bump:changelog'`) so the Chunk-9 `commit` step's `_flushStagedWrites` (already duck-typed on `{primingPath, newContent, changed}`) flushes both with no dispatch-table edit. Establishes the multi-file write-staging convention for any future step that needs to stage more than one file. **Commit body line.** `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js:_buildBodyLines` gains a new duck-type matching `{oldVersion, newVersion, bumpLevel}` — emits `- Bumped <old> → <new> (<level>)` once per pipeline run (deduped via a local flag since both staged entries carry the metadata). **Never blocks** (matches the ADR 0002 step-kind contract): every degraded condition — missing `version.json`, malformed `version.json`, non-semver `version` field, missing `CHANGELOG.md`, missing `[Unreleased]` section, `[Unreleased]` with no entries — returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` with a `reason` / `detail` in `output` for the wrap drawer to render inline. **Idempotent on re-wrap:** after a successful bump the `[Unreleased]` body is empty (just the heading); the next wrap observes no entries and skips. **Banner emoji NOT auto-injected** — `> 🛟` (bug-fix) / `> 🚀` (feature) leading banners stay a curated operator decision per the project's CHANGELOG convention; the handler promotes `[Unreleased]` body byte-for-byte under the new dated heading and the operator adds the banner manually. **Output for the drawer:** `output.from`, `output.to`, `output.bumpLevel`, `output.detail` (the pre-formatted "from → to (level)" string) — matches the existing `wrap-drawer.js:deriveDetail`'s `version-bump` case (`if (output.from && output.to)`), no drawer change required. **Test coverage:** 39 net new tests across `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (pure-helper decision tables for `_parseSemver` / `_bumpSemver` / `_parseUnreleased` / `_decideBumpLevel` / `_promoteUnreleased`; handler tests for every skip path + happy path + idempotency + override + BREAKING-marker + never-blocks contract sweep; commit-body-line duck-type + dedupe pin). The Chunk-3 `wrap-pipeline step stubs` describe block now marks its `kinds` array empty with a sentinel pin so a future stub-introducing chunk has to update the list. **ADR 0002** Status line extended with the open-queue-#3 marker.

- **V2 wrap session-lifecycle transition (#139, Chunk 11a)** — first sub-chunk of the original Chunk 11 (split into 11a / 11b / 11c during this session's scope review). Resolves [#186](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/186): a successful V2 wrap that produced a commit now transitions the session record (`status: 'wrapped'`), kills tmux, releases doc locks, and clears idle + wrap-pane caches — symmetric with the legacy `completeWrap` teardown minus `_autoCommitIfDirty` (V2's `commit` step already flushed). Pre-#186, V2 wraps left the session `active` indefinitely; the drawer's "Done" only closed the drawer. Halted / thrown / clean-session (`ok` + `null` SHA) runs still leave the session active per spec so the user can retry or continue. **Scope:** this is pre-flip plumbing — the flag flip itself moves to Chunk 11c so V2 is a quality experience before becoming the default; `invoke-critic` action producer (Chunk 11b) and prawduct template wiring (Chunk 11c) remain follow-ups.
  - **`lib/sessions.js`** — new helpers `_completeV2Wrap(active, pipelineResult)` and `_deriveV2WrapSummary(pipelineResult)`. The completion helper calls `store.sessions.wrap(active.id, summary)`, then independently runs each teardown step inside its own `try/catch` so a failure in one (e.g. tmux already gone, lock-release threw) cannot block the others. The summary deriver resolves in order: (1) first step output with `parsedFields.summary` (a non-empty trimmed string) — the prawduct `memory-update` shape; (2) first step output with `capturedText` — other `ai-content` steps; (3) `pipelineResult.summary` — reserved for a future `summary-derive` step per `lib/wrap-pipeline.js`; (4) `null` so `store.sessions.wrap` keeps the column NULL rather than writing an empty string.
  - **Gate predicate.** `_triggerWrapV2` calls `_completeV2Wrap` only when `pipelineResult.ok && pipelineResult.commitSha`. Clean-session wraps (`ok && !commitSha`, e.g. user clicked Wrap on a truly clean tree → `commit` step returned `status: 'skipped'`) preserve the session by design — there was nothing to wrap. Halted runs (`!ok`) and runner-thrown errors leave the session active so the user's Retry click re-enters from the same state.
  - **Plan + ADR split.** `.claude/plans/issue-139-methodology-aware-wrap.md` and `docs/adr/0002-wrap-pipeline-contract.md` now describe the Chunk 11 → 11a / 11b / 11c split with per-sub-chunk Scope / Acceptance / Critic sections. Rationale recorded inline so future-self / Critic understands why a bare flag flip wasn't the right shape.
  - **Tests** (+11 in `test/sessions.test.js`, new `V2 lifecycle transition (#139 Chunk 11a)` block under `triggerWrap (methodology-driven)`): (1) `ok + commitSha → wraps the session and runs full teardown` — pins `getActive → null`, the wrapped row's `status` + `wrapSummary`, plus `tmux.killSession` / `documentLocks.releaseBySession` were called with the right args; (2) `ok + null commitSha (clean session) → session stays active`; (3) `halted (!ok) → session stays active` even when `pipelineResult.commitSha` is populated (the halt gates the wrap, not the SHA); (4) `runner thrown → session stays active`; (5) `summary: parsedFields.summary wins over capturedText`; (6) `summary: capturedText is fallback when no parsedFields.summary`; (7) `summary: null when no step output carries summary signal`; (8) `tmux.killSession failure is non-fatal — session still wraps`; (9) `releaseBySession failure is non-fatal — session still wraps`; (10) `store.sessions.wrap failure is non-fatal — teardown still runs` (each teardown step's try/catch isolates the others, addressing Critic minor coverage gap); (11) `second triggerWrap after a successful V2 wrap returns "No active session"` (pins the idempotency contract at the call-site level — after the first wrap, the entry-point pre-check rejects before reaching the runner). Stubs `wrapPipeline.runWrapPipeline` to return fixed structured results so the lifecycle behavior is pinned without exercising real step handlers. Full suite: 2235 / 2235 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +11).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (3 MINOR addressed; YELLOW → GREEN):** (M1) Coverage gap on `tmuxSession === null/empty` defense-in-depth branch — added a comment block on `lib/sessions.js:855–860` explaining `triggerWrap`'s entry-point pre-check makes the guard unreachable via the normal V2 flow, but kept the guard so the helper remains safe to call from future callers. (M2) No idempotency test — added test 11 above. (M3) No test for `store.sessions.wrap` throwing — added test 10 above. NIT findings on gate-predicate type narrowing and `clearIdleCache` indentation asymmetry declined as not load-bearing (runner contract guarantees `commitSha` type; cache-clear placement is intentional — no cache to clear when there's no tmux session).

- **`invoke-critic` action producer (#139, Chunk 11b)** — second sub-chunk of the original Chunk 11 (split into 11a / 11b / 11c during 11a's session-start scope review). Wires the prawduct `invoke-critic` action button (previously a no-op declaration in `data/templates/prawduct/template.json:84`) so clicking "Run Critic" writes an entry to `<project>/.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` per Chunk 7's read contract: an array of `{branchName: string, timestamp: ISO 8601, ...}` entries. Without this writer, the `critic-check` wrap step always emitted `warning: true` on medium+ work because no producer existed for the file it reads. With Chunks 11a + 11b shipped, the only remaining work to flip `wrapV2: true` by default is Chunk 11c (flag flip + prawduct template wiring + migration docs + test updates).
  - **`lib/actions/invoke-critic.js`** — the handler. Resolves the current branch via `git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD` (sync, so a single Node process can't interleave concurrent read-modify-write windows); returns `null` for detached HEAD / non-repo / missing git, which the handler surfaces as `ok: false` with a specific error. Reads existing `critic-runs.json` via a tolerant loader symmetric with the Chunk 7 reader (missing file / malformed JSON / non-array contents all degrade to `[]` so a corrupted file is silently rebuilt on next write). Appends `{branchName, timestamp: new Date().toISOString()}` to the array. **Atomic write:** tempfile + `fs.renameSync` within the same filesystem so a concurrent reader sees either the pre-write content or the full post-write content, never a half-written file. Caller-injection seams: `options.branchName` (skips git resolution), `options.now` (deterministic timestamps for tests).
  - **`lib/actions.js`** — the dispatcher. Maps action `command` → handler module via `ACTION_DISPATCH`. Validates that the project's methodology declares the command in its `actions[]` block before dispatching: the methodology template is the authorization surface, so a frontend that POSTs a command not declared by the project's methodology gets a 404 rather than executing. Handlers that throw are caught and surfaced as `{ok: false, error: 'action handler threw: ...'}`. Separate from the wrap-pipeline dispatch table (`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:STEP_DISPATCH`) so user-clicked actions and pipeline-runner steps don't accidentally couple — adding a new action is a one-line entry plus a sibling module under `lib/actions/`.
  - **`POST /api/projects/:name/actions/:command`** (`server.js`). Body is the handler's `options` (object-only; arrays / strings / numbers / null all coerce to `undefined` so the handler's default-param governs — symmetric with the wrap endpoint's body-parsing contract). Status codes: `200` ok or handler-soft-fail (detached HEAD, missing project path, etc — frontend surfaces the error inline); `404` for unknown project or undeclared action command; `500` for handler-thrown.
  - **`lib/projects.js:enrichProject`** — methodology object now carries `actions[]` (filtered to entries with string `label` + `command`; `confirm` coerced to boolean). The frontend reads this from the `GET /api/projects/:name` response to decide which action buttons to render, so no second round-trip to `/api/methodologies/:id` is needed.
  - **Frontend wire-up** (`public/session.html`, `public/session.js`, `public/session.css`). New `<span id="methodologyActions">` slot in the banner-actions row; `renderMethodologyActions(actions)` populates it after `loadProject`. Click handler: optional `window.confirm` when the action declares `confirm: true`, then `apiMutate POST /api/projects/.../actions/<command>` with the request body `{}`. Inline disable + label-change ("Run Critic…") for the duration of the request so a user can't double-fire. Brief banner-anchored toast (`#methodologyActionToast`) confirms success/error; hides after 3.5s.
  - **Tests** (+31): `test/actions-invoke-critic.test.js` (15 — new-file create, append to existing, malformed JSON recovery, top-level-object recovery, caller-supplied branchName, detached HEAD failure, non-git directory failure, empty/missing project.path validation, `now()` injection seam, no `.tmp.*` remnants after success, idempotency across multiple invocations, `.tangleclaw` exists as regular file (post-Critic), `_redactProjectPath` strips absolute path (post-Critic), `_redactProjectPath` no-op when projectPath empty/null (post-Critic), round-trip pin against the Chunk 7 reader's shape filter). `test/actions-dispatcher.test.js` (7 — runs invoke-critic for prawduct, rejects undeclared action on minimal, rejects unknown command, returns "not found" for unknown project, validates inputs, forwards options to handler, catches handler throws). `test/api-actions.test.js` (9 — 200 ok, 404 unknown project, 404 undeclared action, 404 unknown command, body forwarded as options, non-object body coerced, soft-fail returns 200 ok:false, prawduct project response includes actions[], minimal project response has empty actions[]). Full suite: 2255 / 2255 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +31).
  - **Out of scope (deliberately):** no frontend unit tests for `renderMethodologyActions` / `invokeMethodologyAction` / `showMethodologyActionToast` — they're DOM-coupled glue (~80 lines) that don't justify extracting a separate helper module the way `wrap-drawer.js` did for the multi-step drawer's view-model logic. **Per CLAUDE.md frontend-testing rule: the dev server was NOT run to validate the button in a browser — manual smoke test required at user review.** Server-side request/response is well-pinned via the API tests; frontend integration is straightforward glue (`apiMutate → result.ok → toast`).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (1 MAJOR + 3 MINORs + 1 NIT addressed; YELLOW → GREEN).** (M1, MAJOR) `public/session.js:254` accessed `api.lastError.message` to render the error toast — but `api.lastError` is a **string** per `public/api-helper.js` (lines 2030 and 2170 in the same file consume it as a bare string, confirming the pattern). Result: every server-returned 4xx error showed the literal "Run Critic: failed" toast instead of the real reason. Fixed by dropping `.message`. No coverage caught this because the disclaimed frontend test gap left the toast string the user sees unpinned. (M2) `execSync('git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD')` had no timeout — a pathological FS hang or git-lfs prompt could stall the single-process server's event loop. Added `timeout: 5000`. (M3) Error messages from `fs.mkdirSync` / `fs.writeFileSync` / `fs.renameSync` leak the project absolute path into the HTTP response (low impact for a single-user dev tool but reachable via the public API). Added `_redactProjectPath` helper that replaces the project's absolute path with the literal `<project>` placeholder; applied to both fs error paths. (M4) Test gap on `.tangleclaw` existing as a regular file — `mkdirSync({recursive: true})` throws EEXIST in that case; pinned with a new test that verifies the surfaced shape + redaction. (N1) `document.querySelector('.methodology-action-btn[data-command="..."]')` used unescaped template interpolation; defended with `CSS.escape` fallback to a manual escape so methodology-template-supplied command strings containing selector-syntax characters can't break the button-disable behavior. Declined: (MINOR) substring-based error → HTTP-status routing in `server.js` is fragile but not regressing today — a follow-up to add a `code` field to `runAction`'s return contract is filed conceptually but not pinned to a chunk; (MINOR) `confirm: true` action-path coverage — acknowledged scope gap, scope-disclaimed alongside other frontend tests; (NIT) `ACTION_DISPATCH` single-entry table — deliberately overbuilt for one entry per the module doc's scope-discipline rationale; (NIT) temp filename `${filePath}.tmp.${pid}.${Date.now()}` — single-process sync I/O makes collision impossible, no need for `crypto.randomBytes`.
  - **Bonus follow-up.** Chunk 7's open question — "where does `critic-runs.json` get written?" — is now answered. The Chunk 11c flag flip can ship without `critic-check` defaulting to `warning: true` on every prawduct project's medium+ work, because the Run Critic button has a real producer.

- **Frontend multi-step wrap progress drawer (#139, Chunk 10)** — tenth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the single-button confirm modal with a drawer that renders each pipeline step's status (`pending` / `running` / `done` / `blocked` / `skipped`) plus inline interactive recovery widgets for blocked or warning steps. The legacy `wrapV2:false` modal flow is unchanged byte-for-byte; the drawer only opens when the server response carries a `pipelineResult` (V2 path). With Chunk 10 landed, the wrap UX is functional end-to-end against the Chunks 4–9 step handlers; Chunk 11 (default flip) is now validatable against a real interactive flow.
  - **New `public/wrap-drawer.js` helper module** (mirrors `public/api-helper.js` pattern). Exposes `window.tcWrapDrawerHelpers` with seven pure functions — `buildStepRow`, `deriveDetail`, `summarizePipelineStatus`, `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep`, `warningWidgetForStep`, `prCheckResolutionWidget`, `collectOptionsFromAccessors`. All DOM-free so they're testable in a Node vm sandbox; `session.js` consumes the view-models and owns the DOM. Module pattern matches the existing api-helper factory: attaches to `window` in the browser, exports via `module.exports` for tests.
  - **`public/session.html`** — new drawer markup after the existing wrap modal: `#wrapDrawerBackdrop`, `#wrapDrawer` (with `.wrap-drawer-header`, `#wrapDrawerStatus`, `#wrapStepList`, `#wrapDrawerDecision`, action buttons `#wrapDrawerCancelBtn` / `#wrapDrawerRetryBtn` / `#wrapDrawerDoneBtn` / `#wrapDrawerCloseBtn`). Drawer hidden until `openWrapDrawer(pipelineResult)` is invoked. `wrap-drawer.js` script tag added before `session.js` so the helpers are available at page-script init.
  - **`public/session.css`** — full drawer style block. Reuses the existing `.drawer-backdrop` / `.drawer-handle` styles (peek drawer pattern); adds `.wrap-drawer`, per-step row grid (`.wrap-step-row` + `.wrap-step-main` + `.wrap-step-status`), status-pill color tones (`pending` / `running` / `done` / `blocked` / `skipped`), warning + blocker row backgrounds, decision-widget styles for checkbox / textarea / pr-list shapes.
  - **`public/session.js`** — `confirmWrap` now branches on response shape: V2 (`data.pipelineResult` present) → `openWrapDrawer(data.pipelineResult)`; V1 (legacy `{ok, status:'wrapping'}`) → existing `showWrappingState` + polling loop, byte-equal to pre-Chunk-10. New functions: `openWrapDrawer` / `closeWrapDrawer` / `renderWrapDrawer` (orchestrates status banner + step list + decision widget + action-button visibility) / `renderStepRow` (`<li>` per result) / `renderDecisionWidget` (checkbox or textarea) / `renderPrResolutionWidget` (per-PR dropdown row) / `retryWrap` (collects decision-widget values via accessor functions and re-POSTs to `/wrap` with `{options}`). Action-button visibility logic: `Retry` shows when `blockedAt` is set OR a warning/pr-list widget rendered; `Done` shows on clean `ok:true`; `Cancel/Close` always present; close-affordances wired (X button, Cancel button, backdrop click). The `currentPipelineResult` module-level variable retains the most recent result so a retry's response replaces it.
  - **Decision widgets — three shapes, one collection path.**
    - **`test` blocked** (`blocker:true` + `allowOverride:true`) → checkbox "Override: skip tests and record the override in the commit body" → on retry sends `options.skipTests:true`.
    - **`critic-check` warning** (`blocker:false` step with `output.warning === true`) → textarea "Skip rationale (recorded in commit body — required to clear the warning):" → on retry sends `options.criticSkipRationale:<trimmed text>` (whitespace-only text is dropped so a user can't bypass the gate by typing spaces).
    - **`pr-check` unresolved session-scoped PRs** (`output.sessionScoped.length > 0` and not in `output.resolutions`) → per-PR `<select>` with `merge` / `defer` / `ignore` → on retry sends `options.prHandling: {[prNumber]: 'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'}` (empty selections filtered out; full-map dropped if no PR has a resolution).
    - **`lint` blocked + `commit` blocked** intentionally have NO recovery widget — the user fixes outside the drawer (lint errors → edit code; pre-commit hook rejection → fix the hook-rejected issue) and clicks Retry to re-run the pipeline. `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep` returns `null` for these kinds; drawer still shows the row with blockers surfaced inline.
  - **Server-side options threading** — `lib/sessions.js`: `triggerWrap(projectName, options)` now accepts a second arg (V2-only — ignored on the legacy NL-prompt path so existing call sites stay back-compat). `_triggerWrapV2(project, active, options)` passes through to `wrapPipeline.runWrapPipeline(name, options)`. The runner already accepted `options = {}` since Chunk 3; Chunk 10 closes the loop from the frontend to the runner. **`server.js`**: `POST /api/sessions/:project/wrap` reads `body.options` (object-only; arrays / strings / numbers / null all coerce to `undefined` so the runner's default-param governs), passes to `sessions.triggerWrap`, and surfaces `pipelineResult` on the response. **HTTP semantics for V2 blocked pipelines: `200 OK` with `status:'blocked'` (not `500`).** A blocked pipeline is an expected outcome the drawer renders — the runner produced a structured result, the endpoint returns it. `500` is reserved for the runner throwing (no `pipelineResult` present); `404` still for missing project / session.
  - **No live progress updates yet.** TangleClaw has no WebSocket / SSE infrastructure today (only ttyd's terminal proxy). The pipeline runs synchronously in the request; the drawer renders the final state, not in-progress. Adding live updates means a new SSE channel + per-pipeline run IDs — a separate chunk, tracked as a Chunk-11-or-later follow-up. The drawer's "Running…" status banner is a brief flash during the in-flight POST; the result paint happens once on response.
  - **Out of scope (deliberately):** `invoke-critic` action button still has no implementation (Chunk 7's known follow-up); pipeline pause-mid-run (current model is fail → collect options → retry, which matches the runner's request/response contract); custom-methodology decision widgets beyond the three above (kinds without a widget show the row with raw blockers and rely on user-side fix + retry).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (4 MAJOR + 3 MINOR + 1 NIT addressed; YELLOW → GREEN):** (M1) Retry POST omitted the password — broke `deleteProtected` installs. Fixed by caching the password from the initial confirm modal on `openWrapDrawer` and replaying it on retry. The replaced dead-state variable `currentPipelineResult` (N2, never read after assignment) repurposed as `currentWrapPassword`. (M2) ADR 0002 extended with the Chunk-10 entry — Status line + Migration-path Chunk 10 + Chunk 11 sections cover the runner-API surface change (`triggerWrap(name, options)` second arg), HTTP 200-on-blocked semantics, the three decision widgets' shape contract, the warning-state re-run trade-off, password replay on retry, the no-live-updates deferral, and scope-discipline note on bundled templates. (M3) `retryWrap` silently swallowed `apiMutate → null` (403/404/500/network). Added `renderWrapDrawerError(message)` that surfaces the inline error via the `wrapDrawerStatus` element with `--error` tone, reading the message from the side-channel `api.lastError`. (M4) Critic-warning state hid the Done button so a user with a passing-but-warned wrap had only Retry (re-runs the pipeline → second commit) or Close (no rationale recorded). Fixed by showing Done alongside Retry on warning-only state ("accept warning as-is") and surfacing the trade-off inline as a `.wrap-decision-note` in the pr-check resolution widget. (M5) PR-resolution roundtrip had no test — frontend → server → runner for `prHandling` was unverified. Added `test/api-sessions.test.js` "threads prHandling map verbatim from request body to runner" pinning both the shape (`{string-pr-num: enum}`) and the key-type contract (string, matching `_normalizeHandling`'s `String(key)` lookup). (N5) `deriveDetail` had no case for `ai-content` or `version-bump`. Added both — ai-content surfaces "captured N fields" or "captured" fallback; version-bump surfaces `from → to` or skipped reason. +5 tests for the new cases. (N6) Renderer loop iterated `H.buildStepRow` twice per step (once for the step list, once for the decision widget). Hoisted into a single `rows` array with `{row, raw}` tuples consumed by both loops. (T3) PR-row title was a `<span>` with the URL only in the tooltip. Made it an `<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">` when the URL is present, falling back to span when absent. (N1) Filed [#185](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/185) — "Live wrap pipeline progress via SSE" — for the deferred WebSocket/SSE phase. (N7) Filed [#186](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/186) — "V2 wrap success doesn't transition session lifecycle" — Chunk 11 will fold the fix into the default-flip work; logged in ADR 0002's Chunk 11 entry. Declined: (N4) `aria-modal` toggle pattern is a pre-existing peek-drawer convention; (T1) `status:'wrapping'` field name is misleading for V2 success but the drawer ignores `status` so impact is zero; (T2) `Object.freeze(options)` comment lie is Chunk-4 debt.
  - **Tests** (+40 after Critic fixes; was +34 pre-Critic): 11 cases for `buildStepRow` (done step with commit detail; blocked step gets `isBlocker:true` + `blocked` tone; warning row from `output.warning`; unknown kind falls back to raw kind; missing output handled gracefully; pr-check detail singular/plural; priming-roll target chunk surfaced; ai-content N-fields plural; ai-content singular; ai-content text-only fallback; version-bump from→to; version-bump skipped reason — last five added in Critic fixes), 6 for `summarizePipelineStatus` (success with sha; success without sha; blocked + reason; warning when ok:true with warning step; error when top-level error without blockedAt; null/undefined input → error tone), 4 for `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep` (test gets checkbox; non-blocker null; lint blocker → null since no recovery; null/undefined input), 3 for `warningWidgetForStep` (critic-check textarea; warning:false → null; unknown kind → null), 5 for `prCheckResolutionWidget` (returns prs when session-scoped + unresolved; filters out resolved; null when no session-scoped; null when all resolved; null for non-pr-check kinds), 8 for `collectOptionsFromAccessors` (skipTests true collected; false omitted; rationale trimmed + included; whitespace-only rationale omitted; prHandling filters empties; full-empty prHandling omitted; all-three combined; missing accessor keys tolerated). API-layer (+5 in `test/api-sessions.test.js`, +1 from Critic M5): options threading from request body → `runWrapPipeline`; blocked pipeline returns `200` with `pipelineResult`; thrown pipeline returns `500`; non-object options bodies coerced to `undefined`; `prHandling` map round-trips verbatim with `string`-typed keys. Lib-layer (+1 in `test/sessions.test.js`): `triggerWrap` options-threading contract pinned for both present and absent cases. Full suite: 2224 / 2224 pass (was 2179 at end of Chunk 9; net +45 from Chunk 10).

- **Wrap pipeline `commit` step real handler + single-transaction orchestration (#139, Chunk 9)** — ninth and load-bearing chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js` with the real flush + commit + `lastWrapSha`-stamp orchestrator. This is the chunk every prior step has been staging *for*: priming-roll's `newContent`, ai-content's `capturedText`, critic-check's `owedRationale`, pr-check's `resolutions` — all of it lands in one git commit (or no commit on a truly clean session) at the end of the pipeline. With Chunk 9 landed, 7 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`, `pr-check`, `commit`) have real handlers; only `version-bump` remains as a Chunk-3 stub. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. Chunks 10 (frontend) + 11 (default flip) are now validatable against an end-to-end functional wrap.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/commit.js`**: orchestrates four phases — (1) flush staged filesystem writes (currently only `priming-roll` produces these; duck-typed on shape `{primingPath, newContent, changed}` so any future write-producing step that mimics the shape Just Works without a dispatch-table edit), (2) detect "anything to commit?" via `git status --porcelain` — empty output → `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'no changes to commit', commitSha:null}}` so a session that ran the pipeline but produced no real edits stays a no-op at the git level, (3) `git add -A` + `git commit -m <session-derived message>` (the user clicking Session Wrap is opting into "everything in my working tree belongs to this session" — Chunk 10's UI will surface the file list so the user can cancel before this step runs), (4) capture commit SHA via `git rev-parse HEAD` and stamp `lastWrapSha` on `projConfig` so Chunks 4 (lint scope) + 7 (critic-check range detection) can drop their `HEAD~10..HEAD` fallback in a future chunk.
  - **Single-transaction discipline.** A pipeline failure before this step leaves whatever the AI / priming-roll already put into the working tree, but produces NO commit. The user fixes the blocker and retries; on the next attempt this step picks up everything still in the working tree plus the fresh-run staged writes. Re-running the wrap is idempotent at the commit level — the runner produces zero or one commit per invocation.
  - **Blocker contract: `blocker:true` (real, not always-ok).** Unlike Chunks 5–8 which all returned `ok:true` regardless of internal probe failures, this step is the load-bearing transactional gate. `git status` failure, `git add` failure, or `git commit` failure (typically a pre-commit hook rejection) → `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}` with the git/hook output surfaced in `blockers[]`. The runner halts the pipeline; the user fixes the hook-rejected issue and retries the wrap. We do **NOT** pass `--no-verify` (per CLAUDE.md's Git Safety Protocol) — the pre-commit hook is the user's intentional gate.
  - **Commit message strategy: `session-content`.** Subject derived from a chunk-tag regex on the current branch (`chunk-9-…` → `Session wrap (chunk 9)`; dotted/lettered ids like `chunk-10c.2` are honored to match the priming-roll / critic-check chunk-id grammar) with a branch-name fallback (`Session wrap on feat/some-feature`) and a generic fallback for detached HEAD (`Session wrap`). Body assembled from shape-typed staged entries: priming-roll's `pointer.current` → `- Priming rolled to Chunk N — Title` (with `(blocked on: …)` on the next line when present), ai-content's `capturedText` → `- AI content (<step-id>): captured` or `- AI content (<step-id>): captured fields [a, b, c]` if `parsedFields` is non-empty, critic-check's `owedRationale` → `- Critic skip rationale: <text>` (or `- Critic warning: medium+ work without Critic dispatch (no rationale provided)` when warning fired without a rationale), pr-check's `sessionScoped` + `resolutions` → `- Open session-scoped PRs: N` + `  - PR #<num>: merge|defer|ignore` per resolution. Subject capped at `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN = 72` chars with `…` truncation marker so `git log --oneline` stays readable. Anything not matching a known shape is silently skipped — extra staging keys aren't an error.
  - **`lastWrapSha` stamping is non-fatal on failure.** The commit already landed by the time we reach this stamp; the stamp is a hint for later steps' range detection. We `log.warn` and continue, surfacing the outcome on `output.stamped: boolean` so the Chunk 10 UI can render "stamp failed — Chunks 4/7 will keep using the HEAD~10 fallback next wrap" inline rather than producing a runner-level blocker. A clean session that skipped the commit does NOT stamp (no SHA to record).
  - **Bundled templates updated**: `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` and `data/templates/minimal/template.json` each declare `"blocker": true` on their `commit` step. (`data/templates/tilt/template.json` carries the same change locally but is gitignored — `.gitignore:24` lists it as an "Unreleased methodology template" — so it doesn't ride along in this PR; the matching tilt-blocker test is gracefully skipped when the file isn't on disk.) The back-compat shim (`lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate`) reads only `step.id` and `step.captureFields[]`, so adding `blocker` to an existing step does NOT change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal output — the regression pin in `test/sessions.test.js` continues to pass. This is the first chunk that DOES touch a bundled template's `wrap_pipeline` schema; doing so explicitly (vs. an implicit "commit kind is implicitly blocker:true" rule in the runner) keeps the runner shape-dumb and the methodology template the single source of truth for the contract.
  - **Runner threading**: `lib/wrap-pipeline.js:runWrapPipeline` now reads `commitSha` from any step result whose `output.commitSha` is a non-empty string, populating the top-level `result.commitSha` field. The threading is step-id-agnostic (any step with an `output.commitSha` populates it; first-wins) so a future methodology with a renamed commit step still surfaces the SHA without a runner edit. Halted pipelines and clean-session skips leave `result.commitSha = null`.
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG`** gains `lastWrapSha: null` — round-trips through `projectConfig.load` / `.save` and merges with on-disk configs that pre-date this field (the deep-merge loop in `projectConfigApi.load` propagates the default for missing keys). Chunks 4 and 7's range detection will switch to `<lastWrapSha>..HEAD` in a future chunk when they read this field; for now they keep the `HEAD~10..HEAD` fallback that's authoritative on never-wrapped projects.
  - **Six pure helpers exported** for testability: `_flushStagedWrites(staged)` (idempotent — `changed:false` is a no-op; missing `changed` defaults to "needs write"; returns array of `{stepId, path}` for the run output), `_buildSubject(branch)` (chunk-tag → branch-name → generic fallback; truncates over `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN`), `_buildBodyLines(staged)` (shape-typed across the four producers; returns `[]` for null/empty/unknown shapes), `_buildMessage(staged, branch)` (subject + blank + body assembly; subject-only when body is empty), `_stampLastWrapSha(projectPath, sha)` (returns `boolean`; `log.warn`s on failure and continues — the commit already landed), plus the `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN` constant.
  - **Three `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (thin `execFile`-based Promise wrapper that never throws on non-zero exit — matches the pr-check / critic-check pattern), `writeFileSync`, `mkdirSync`. `execFile` rather than `exec` — argv-style arg passing means multi-line messages with quotes pass through to `git commit -m` byte-intact without any shell-quoting math.
  - **Test scaffolding pollution fix (Chunk 3 → 9).** Several Chunk-3-era tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` and `test/sessions.test.js` ran the full pipeline against tmp-dir projects that aren't git repos — they passed in Chunks 3–8 because every step was either a stub or always-ok. Now that `commit` is a real blocker handler, those tests would hit `git status` failure on a non-repo and return `ok:false`. Fix: the affected tests now monkey-patch `STEP_DISPATCH['commit']` to the canonical no-op for the duration of their assertion (with `finally`-block restore), keeping each test focused on what it actually asserts (runner skeleton, blocker semantics, options threading, V2 routing) rather than accidentally exercising the real commit handler. The Chunk-9 commit-handler tests stand up real git repos via `execSync('git init ...')` in `beforeEach`.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 9 entry) with the full contract — flush order, single-transaction discipline, blocker:true semantics, message-builder strategy, `lastWrapSha` stamping, bundled-template `blocker:true` addition, and the byte-equal-pin compatibility note.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes:** 1 MAJOR + 4 MINORs addressed before this PR opened. (MAJOR-1) `data/templates/tilt/template.json` is gitignored as "Unreleased methodology templates" — the test asserting `blocker:true` would have broken on a clean clone. Fixed by making the tilt assertion gracefully skip when `store.templates.get('tilt')` returns null, and noting the locally-vs-tracked split in CHANGELOG + ADR 0002. (MINOR-1) Comment in `commit.js:_internal.exec` claimed `-F -` (stdin) but the code uses `-m` (argv) — comment rewritten to accurately describe the argv-style execFile-handling. (MINOR-2) Silent-swallow on `priming-roll` staged entries with `pointer:{current:null, allDone:false}` — the file was being flushed but the commit body produced no line; added an explicit "Priming refreshed: plan has no parseable chunks" branch in `_buildBodyLines`. (MINOR-3, 4, 5) Three missing failure-path tests added: `_stampLastWrapSha` throwing → `output.stamped:false` with `ok:true` (commit landed; stamp is a hint); `git rev-parse HEAD` failing AFTER commit landed → `output.commitSha:null` with `ok:true`; `git add -A` failing → blocked with the third path in the three-path git matrix (status / add / commit) now covered. **Consistency NIT addressed:** `_buildSubject`'s chunk-tag regex now uses `\bchunk` to mirror priming-roll + critic-check's CHUNK_TAG regex shape per ADR 0002 (prevents `junkchunk-9` matching). **Concurrent-wrap NIT addressed:** `_stampLastWrapSha` JSDoc now documents the lock-free load → mutate → save sequence relies on the runner's no-concurrent-wraps assumption.
  - **Tests** (+44, after Critic fixes): 5 cases for `_buildSubject` (chunk-tag extracted from `feat/chunk-N-…`; dotted/lettered chunk ids like `10c.2`; branch-name fallback; generic fallback on null branch; truncation at MAX_SUBJECT_LEN with ellipsis), 9 for `_buildBodyLines` (priming-roll pointer; priming-roll `blockedOn` surfaces under the pointer; priming-roll allDone; priming-roll `{current:null, allDone:false}` no-parseable-chunks line — Critic MINOR-2 pin; ai-content with `parsedFields` lists the fields; ai-content without `parsedFields` minimal form; critic-check skip rationale; critic-check warning without rationale; pr-check sessionScoped count + per-PR resolutions; unknown-shape entries skipped silently; null/undefined/empty staged → `[]`), 2 for `_buildMessage` (subject-only when body empty; subject + blank + body assembly), 5 for `_flushStagedWrites` (skips entries without primingPath/newContent; skips `changed:false`; writes when `changed:true`; writes when `changed` is missing as defensive default; null/undefined staged → `[]`), 13 handler-level cases against a real git repo (blocks on missing project.path; skips with no commit when working tree is clean + no staged writes; skips when staged priming has `changed:false` and tree is clean; flushes a priming-roll write + produces one commit + captures hex SHA; picks up an AI-style MEMORY.md edit the AI made before commit step ran; stamps lastWrapSha on projConfig after a successful commit; blocks on pre-commit hook rejection with hook output surfaced — `--no-verify` is NOT passed; blocks with explanatory message when `git status` fails — non-repo simulation; surfaces flush errors as blockers, never as runner exceptions; session-content message includes priming pointer + AI captureFields + critic rationale on a real commit; generic subject on detached HEAD; `_stampLastWrapSha` throwing leaves `ok:true` with `stamped:false` — Critic MINOR-3 pin; `git rev-parse HEAD` non-zero after commit lands leaves `ok:true` with `commitSha:null` — Critic MINOR-4 pin; `git add -A` non-zero exit blocks with stderr surfaced — Critic MINOR-5 pin), 3 for runner `commitSha` threading (surfaces from `output.commitSha` at the top level; null on a `skipped` commit step; null when the pipeline halts before commit), 3 for bundled-template `blocker:true` on commit step (prawduct, minimal, tilt-when-present), 2 for projConfig `lastWrapSha` (DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG default `null`; round-trips through load/save). Test-scaffolding updates: stub-conformance test (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`) — `commit` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; only `version-bump` remains pinned. Full suite: 2179 / 2179 pass (was 2135 at end of Chunk 8).

- **Wrap pipeline `pr-check` step real handler (#139, Chunk 8)** — eighth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/pr-check.js` with a real `gh pr list` integration that surfaces open authored PRs to the wrap UI, partitioned into "this session's PR" and "other open PRs you might want to think about." Behavior fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`. With Chunk 8 landed, 6 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`, `pr-check`) have real handlers; only `version-bump` and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 stubs.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/pr-check.js`**: shells out to `gh pr list --state open --author @me --json number,title,headRefName,baseRefName,url,createdAt,isDraft,author`. JSON fields kept narrow on purpose — the commit-step + UI need just enough to identify and link the PR; adding fields without a downstream consumer is dead surface area. Parses JSON, filters drafts (unless `step.includeDrafts === true`), partitions into `sessionScoped` (PRs whose `headRefName` matches the current branch) and `otherOpen` via `_partitionPrs`. **Session-scope filter is intentionally minimal:** `headRefName === currentBranch` is the single source of truth — more elaborate matching (PR title chunk-tag, issue number cross-reference, base-branch heuristic) is Chunk-10 UI territory; overly-clever filtering at the handler level produces false positives the user can't easily undo. **`gh` availability gate:** `gh --version` (no auth required, no network round-trip) up front; missing → `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'gh CLI not available'}}`. **`gh pr list` failure modes** (no auth via `gh auth login`, repo isn't on GitHub, API hiccup, malformed JSON, non-array JSON) all degrade to skipped — the first 200 chars of `stderr`/`stdout` are surfaced in `output.detail` so the UI can render the recovery hint inline rather than just "gh failed." **Draft filtering:** drafts hidden by default; unfiltered count exposed in `output.counts.rawTotal` so the UI can render "N drafts hidden" without re-calling gh.
  - **Caller-supplied resolution (Chunk 10 hand-off)**: `options.prHandling` accepts two shapes — a string shortcut (`'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'`) applied to every session-scoped PR, or a per-PR object map (`{prNumber: 'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'}`). Both string and number keys are normalized to string before lookup, so a UI that emits `{42: 'merge'}` and one that emits `{"42": 'merge'}` resolve identically. Invalid shortcuts (`'squash-bomb'`), invalid map values (`'rebase-and-pray'`), unknown PR numbers (resolution references a non-session-scoped PR), and bad shape (`prHandling` is an array) are all surfaced via `output.invalidHandling[]` with a human-readable descriptor — the UI prompts the user to fix and re-submit rather than silently dropping the choice. The handler validates but does NOT act on resolutions; the Chunk 9 `commit` step reads `context.staged[step.id]` to embed the choices in the wrap commit body / MEMORY block.
  - **Blocker contract: always `ok:true`** (matches the Chunk 7 always-ok pattern). The handler wraps ALL `_internal` probes (`isGhAvailable`, `getCurrentBranch`, `listOpenPrs`) in a single outer `try/catch` — thrown probes (child_process spawn failure, OOM from maxBuffer, etc.) degrade to `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'pr-check probe failed', error}}` rather than runner-level "step threw" blockers. Even on a misconfigured project (missing `context.project.path`) the handler returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` to honor the same contract — a session with an open PR isn't a structural failure.
