  - **Single-transaction discipline (matches Chunks 5–7)**: handler reads only — never mutates git, never writes the filesystem. `context.staged[step.id] = {branch, sessionScoped, resolutions, invalidHandling}` only when `sessionScoped.length > 0 || resolutions has entries` (no PRs + no resolutions = nothing for the commit step to do). Invalid-only handling (caller passed a resolution for a PR that doesn't exist) does NOT stage — pinned by test so a future refactor that always-stages doesn't accidentally make the commit step think there's work to do.
  - **Three pure helpers exported**: `_filterPrs(prs, step)` (draft filter; missing `isDraft` treated as not-a-draft); `_partitionPrs(prs, currentBranch)` (split into sessionScoped + otherOpen; null currentBranch → everything in otherOpen — fail-soft); `_normalizeHandling(prHandling, sessionScoped)` (returns `{resolutions, invalid}`; handles undefined / null / string shortcut / object map / array / unknown enum / unknown PR number, all pinned). Constants exported: `VALID_HANDLINGS` (Set), `GH_PR_JSON_FIELDS` (the gh JSON field list — pinned so a downstream consumer can rely on the shape).
  - **Four `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (thin Promise wrapper for `node:child_process.exec`), `isGhAvailable`, `getCurrentBranch`, `listOpenPrs`. Each stubbable per-test (matches Chunk 7's pattern). The defaults never throw on non-zero exit — gh exits non-zero on the no-auth path, no-repo path, and many other recoverable cases, so blanket-rethrow would defeat the never-blocks contract.
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `pr-check` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining two stubs (`version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll`/`critic-check`/`pr-check` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore). **Test-pollution fix:** the new `wrap-step pr-check — handler` describe gets an `after()` hook restoring `_internal` to its true originals so the sibling `defaultListOpenPrs JSON handling` describe captures clean state rather than the previous suite's last-test stubs (caught during test authoring; pinned so other handler suites can follow the pattern when they grow sibling test groups).
  - **Scope discipline**: bundled prawduct template intentionally NOT extended with `{kind: "pr-check"}` in this chunk (matches Chunks 4 / 5 / 6 / 7's strict pattern — would change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal pin). A future chunk paired with the Chunk-11 default flip will wire prawduct's pipeline.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 8 entry) with the full contract — gh availability gate + failure-mode handling + session-scope filter + resolution staging + scope-discipline note.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (MINOR):** `_normalizeHandling` string-shortcut branch now writes string keys symmetrically with the object-map branch (both produce `{string: enum}` maps so the Chunk 9 commit step + Chunk 10 UI iterate with predictable key types); `defaultListOpenPrs` non-zero-exit `reason` field appends `…` when the raw gh stderr/stdout was longer than the 200-char truncation cap, so the UI knows there's more to see; added `_partitionPrs` regression pin for `headRefName: null` / empty (gh can return this for orphaned PRs whose source branch was deleted — defensive against a future `pr.headRefName.startsWith(...)` refactor); added `GH_PR_JSON_FIELDS` snapshot pin so a rename / reorder of the gh JSON shape forces a CHANGELOG conversation rather than silently breaking downstream consumers.
  - **Tests** (+29): 3 cases for `_filterPrs` (drafts dropped by default; kept on opt-in; missing isDraft treated as not-a-draft), 4 for `_partitionPrs` (headRefName match; null branch → everything in otherOpen; empty input; null/empty headRefName → otherOpen — Critic MINOR pin), 1 snapshot pin on `GH_PR_JSON_FIELDS` (downstream-consumer contract — Critic MINOR pin), 8 for `_normalizeHandling` (undefined/null → empty; string shortcut applies to every session-scoped PR; unknown shortcut → invalid; per-PR object map; unknown PR number flagged; bad handling value flagged; array shape rejected; numeric-vs-string key normalization), 9 handler-level cases (always ok:true — even on missing project.path; gh missing → skipped; gh non-zero with reason; no PRs → empty buckets, nothing staged; session-scoped PR surfaces + stages; draft hide/include via includeDrafts; options.prHandling threading; invalid-only handling does NOT stage; isGhAvailable throws → skipped via outer try/catch; null currentBranch → everything in otherOpen, nothing staged), 4 for `defaultListOpenPrs` JSON handling (non-zero exit + reason; malformed JSON; non-array JSON; happy path). Full suite: 2135 / 2135 pass (was 2106 at end of Chunk 7).

- **Wrap pipeline `critic-check` step real handler (#139, Chunk 7)** — seventh chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/critic-check.js` with a real session-history heuristic + Critic-dispatch detector that warns (never blocks) when medium+ work landed without an Independent Critic review. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. With Chunk 7 landed, 5 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`) have real handlers; only `pr-check`, `version-bump`, and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 stubs.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/critic-check.js`**: heuristic for "medium+ work that should have had an Independent Critic review." **Three trip conditions (any-of):** commit count ≥ `step.commitThreshold` (default 10), total line changes (insertions + deletions) ≥ `step.lineChangeThreshold` (default 500), or a chunk-tag regex (`\bchunk[\s\-_]?N(?:\.N[a-z]?)*\b`, case-insensitive) matches the current branch name or any commit subject in the session range. **Branch wins over commit subjects** when both match — more specific to the session — and the matched id (e.g. `7` from `chunk-7`) is exposed in `output.heuristic.chunkTag` so the Chunk 10 UI can show "this looks like Chunk N work" in the warning. Separator-tolerant: matches `Chunk 7`, `chunk-7`, `chunk_7`, `chunk7`, and dotted sub-ids like `chunk-10c.2`. The id regex shape mirrors `priming-roll`'s (Chunk 6) so a chunk a priming-roll knows about is also a chunk-tag this heuristic detects. **Session range** resolved via `git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD` → main branch; range spec `<main>..HEAD`. Degraded fallback: `HEAD~10..HEAD` when the symref is missing, current branch is the main branch (work-directly-on-main case), or HEAD is detached — `output.rangeDegraded` + `output.rangeDegradedReason` surface the degradation so the Chunk 10 UI can render "the heuristic is operating in degraded mode" instead of silently producing weird numbers. Chunk 9 will replace this with a `lastWrapSha`-stamped range once the `commit` step starts recording it on project records. **Critic-dispatch detection** reads `<project>/.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` — an array of `{branchName: string, timestamp: ISO 8601, ...}` entries — and filters to entries whose `branchName` matches the current branch. Any match → `criticRan: true`; otherwise `false`. Missing file / malformed JSON / non-array contents / no current-branch entries → `false`. Entries are defensively filtered to those with a string `branchName` to guard against partial writes or schema drift. **The producer is intentionally NOT shipped in Chunk 7** — the `invoke-critic` action button in methodology templates (`actions[]`) currently has no implementation, and the frontend wiring lives in Chunk 10. Chunk 7 ships only the read contract so the pipeline can produce meaningful output today via test fixtures, and the write side can land in any later chunk without re-touching this handler.
  - **Blocker contract: always `ok:true`** (Critic MAJOR-1 pre-merge fix). The spec from #139's Discovery says missing-Critic is a methodology rule the user can knowingly skip with rationale, not a structural failure that halts the pipeline. The handler wraps ALL `_internal` git probes (`getCurrentBranch`, `getMainBranch`, `getCommitCount`, `getDiffStats`, `getCommitSubjects`) in a single outer `try/catch` so any throw (git missing, exec timeout that isn't a clean non-zero exit, fs permission, OOM from maxBuffer) becomes a structured `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'git probe failed', error}}` rather than a runner-level "step threw" blocker. Matches the priming-roll / ai-content explicit-catch pattern from Chunks 5 + 6 — drift would re-create the Chunk-7 Critic incident class. Even on a misconfigured project (missing `context.project.path`) the handler returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` to honor the same contract.
  - **Rationale staging (matches Chunk 5 / 6 single-transaction discipline)**: when `warning === true` AND `options.criticSkipRationale` is a non-empty trimmed string, the rationale is staged at `context.staged[step.id] = {warning, owedRationale, branchName, isMediumPlus, criticRan, heuristic}` for the Chunk 9 `commit` step + Chunk 5 `memory-update` prompt to consume. Whitespace-only rationale is treated as no rationale (`owedRationale → null`); the warning still surfaces and the Chunk 10 UI is expected to prompt the user before letting the pipeline commit. No warning → nothing staged. The handler reads only — no git mutations, no filesystem writes; staging is the sole side effect.
  - **Configurable thresholds** via `step.commitThreshold` / `step.lineChangeThreshold` (positive integers, default 10 / 500). Surfaced back through `output.heuristic.commitThreshold` / `lineChangeThreshold` so the UI can render the threshold inline ("12 commits exceed the 10-commit threshold"). **Footgun protection (Critic MAJOR-2 pre-merge fix):** `0` and negative values fall back to the defaults — without the clamp, `commitThreshold: 0` would trip medium+ on every wrap (`0 ≥ 0` is true), training users to dismiss the warning. Floats / NaN / strings / `null` / objects also fall back via `Number.isInteger` (not `Number.isFinite`). The chunk-tag regex is intentionally NOT exposed as a `step.chunkTagRegex` — exposing regex strings via methodology JSON is a footgun (escaping pitfalls, no validation surface).
  - **Seven `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (the thin Promise wrapper for `node:child_process.exec`), `getCurrentBranch`, `getMainBranch`, `getCommitCount`, `getDiffStats`, `getCommitSubjects`, `loadCriticRuns`. Each can be independently stubbed per test (matches Chunk 4's `execShell` + `detectChangedFiles` + Chunk 5's `sendKeys` + `detectIdle` + `capturePane` + `sleep` patterns). The defaults are thin wrappers around real git / fs calls that never throw on non-zero exit — they return `null` / `0` / `[]` so callers branch on intent rather than catching at every site.
  - **Four pure helpers exported**: `_detectChunkTag(branchName, subjects)` (branch wins; subjects searched in declaration order; `null` when neither matches; returns `{tag, source, match}` so the UI gets both the id alone for templating and the full match text for highlighting), `_isMediumPlus({commits, lineChanges, chunkTag, commitThreshold, lineChangeThreshold})` (any-of disjunction across the three signals; pinned at each boundary), `_pickRange(branch, mainBranch)` (returns `{rangeSpec, degraded, reason}`; degraded paths are pinned individually so a future refactor that drops a fallback case fails the test), and `_selectRecentRuns(entries, n)` (sorts critic-runs by `timestamp` descending — newest first — and slices `n`; entries with missing or non-string timestamps sort to the bottom; ISO 8601 string compare matches chronology for any well-formed timestamp). Sorting by timestamp instead of file-insertion order means a future producer that trims or re-sorts the file in-place can't accidentally change the "recent runs" the UI surfaces.
  - **Scope discipline**: bundled prawduct template is intentionally NOT extended with `{kind: "critic-check"}` in this chunk. Doing so would change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal behavior (the back-compat shim flattens `wrap_pipeline.steps[].id` into the legacy `wrap.steps[]` list that the NL prompt enumerates). Matches the strict scope policy from Chunks 4 / 5 / 6, where the bundled template was untouched and the new handler was wired in only via tests. A future chunk (likely paired with the Chunk-11 default flip) will wire prawduct's pipeline to include `critic-check` as part of the methodology-and-UI rollout — at that point the legacy NL-prompt byte-equal pin gets a Chunk-7-explicit baseline update.
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `critic-check` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining three stubs (`pr-check`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll`/`critic-check` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without standing up a real git history.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 7 entry) with the full contract — heuristic + thresholds + range resolution + Critic-runs.json schema + blocker:false contract + rationale staging + scope-discipline note.
  - **Tests** (+43): 8 cases for `_detectChunkTag` (neither matches → null; branch matches; commit subject matches when branch doesn't; branch wins over commits when both match; dotted sub-id `10c.2`; separator variants — space/dash/underscore/none; case-insensitive; null/empty inputs), 6 for `_isMediumPlus` (commits boundary 10/10 trips, 9/10 does not; line-changes boundary 500/500 trips, 499/500 does not; chunkTag truthy alone trips; custom thresholds honored), 4 for `_pickRange` (happy `<main>..HEAD`; degraded on branch=main; degraded on detached HEAD; degraded on missing origin symref), 3 for `_selectRecentRuns` (empty/non-array → `[]`; descending-by-timestamp ordering pinned regardless of input order; missing/non-string timestamps sort to bottom), 18 handler-level cases (always ok:true / never blocks — even on missing project.path; baseline warning=false; commit-count trip with staging; line-change trip; chunk-tag-in-branch trip; chunk-tag-in-commit trip; critic-run on current branch suppresses warning; critic-run only on OTHER branches still warns — filter pinned; rationale stages when warning + non-empty string; whitespace-only rationale → null; custom thresholds honored; rangeDegraded on main branch; rangeDegraded on missing symref; `criticRunsRecent` sorts by timestamp descending regardless of file-write order — Critic MINOR pin; thrown git probe → structured skipped — Critic MAJOR-1 pin; commitThreshold:0 falls back to default — Critic MAJOR-2 pin; negative thresholds fall back; non-integer thresholds (3.7 / NaN / "5" / null / undefined / {}) fall back; non-string criticSkipRationale (number / array / object / true / null) staged as null — typeof-guard pin), 4 for `defaultLoadCriticRuns` (missing file → `[]`; malformed JSON → `[]` no throw; non-array → `[]`; filters out entries missing `branchName`). Full suite: 2106 / 2106 pass (was 2063 at end of Chunk 6).

- **Wrap pipeline `priming-roll` step real handler (#139, Chunk 6)** — sixth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js` with a real plan-parser + managed-block roller. Pure server-side filesystem reads + a staged (deferred) write — no AI handoff and no tmux interaction. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. With Chunk 6 landed, only `pr-check`, `critic-check`, `version-bump`, and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 no-op stubs; the dispatch table for V2 pipelines is now real for 4 of 8 kinds.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js`**: parses `<project>/.claude/plans/<plan>.md` for the active chunk pointer and rolls forward a managed block in `<project>/.claude/priming/build-session.md`. **Plan format** matches the convention TangleClaw's own #139 build plan already uses: `### Chunk N: Title` headings, with `✅` anywhere on the heading line marking that chunk done. Chunk ids tolerate dotted / lettered sub-chunk numbering — `1`, `2a`, `10c.2`, `12.3a.4` all parse (regex: `[0-9]+[a-z]?(?:\.[0-9]+[a-z]?)*`). **CRLF tolerance:** the parser splits on `/\r?\n/` and strips any trailing `\r` so Windows-authored / cross-edited plans parse byte-identical to LF-only ones (Critic MAJOR pre-merge fix — repro: a CRLF plan was returning `[]` and bricking the wrap). The "current" chunk is the first un-done heading in document order; the "next" chunk is whatever follows it (or `null` when current is the tail). A `✅` body line does NOT promote a sibling chunk to done — done-state is decided on the heading line only, so embedding ✅ inside a chunk's prose stays safe. **Malformed `### Chunk Foo:` headings** (id slot non-numeric) are skipped from the chunk list but emit a `log.warn` with the line number and a 120-char tail — the user has a recovery path instead of silent confusion (Critic MAJOR pre-merge fix; the parser stays strict, the user just sees what was dropped). **Blocker annotations:** the first `**Blocked on:** <text>` line in a chunk body (case-insensitive) is captured into the rolled pointer so the next session sees the blocker inline rather than discovering it by re-reading the plan; additional `**Blocked on:**` lines in the same chunk are ignored (the first wins). **Plan path resolution:** `step.planPath` (project-relative or absolute) wins when set; otherwise the handler scans `<project>/.claude/plans/*.md` and requires exactly one match — zero or two+ → `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}` with a "set step.planPath to disambiguate" message that names the colliding files. Project-relative `step.planPath` values get a containment check (`path.resolve` + `startsWith(projectRoot + sep)`) so `../escaped.md`-style traversal is refused — defense-in-depth for the Chunk 11 default-flip and any future user-editable methodology authoring (Critic MINOR pre-merge fix). Absolute paths are accepted as-is on the assumption an author writing an absolute path knows what they're pointing at (e.g. a shared corporate plan archive). **Priming-file managed block:** the handler edits a region of `.claude/priming/build-session.md` (overridable via `step.primingPath`) delimited by `<!-- TANGLECLAW:PRIMING-ROLL:BEGIN -->` / `<!-- TANGLECLAW:PRIMING-ROLL:END -->`. The rest of the priming file is sacrosanct — user-authored content surrounding the managed block is preserved byte-for-byte. When the markers don't exist yet, the handler appends a fresh managed block separated by a blank line; when the file itself doesn't exist yet, the handler stages a brand-new file at the priming path. **Out-of-order markers** (END before BEGIN, indicating a corrupted file) are defensively treated as "no managed block" → fresh-append, doubling the markers rather than silently corrupting the file via wrong slice math (regression-pinned with a "user content between misordered markers survives" assertion). **Duplicated managed blocks** (user copy-pasted) edit only the first BEGIN/END pair; the orphan second pair is left as inert content — pinned by test so a future "find all markers" refactor is intentional, not accidental.
  - **Single-transaction discipline (matches Chunk 5 `ai-content`)**: the handler does NOT touch the filesystem itself. It stages `context.staged[step.id] = {primingPath, newContent, changed, pointer, planPath}` for the Chunk 9 `commit` step to flush. A re-run against an unchanged plan + already-rolled priming file produces an unchanged `newContent` and reports `output.changed === false` — the commit step is expected to skip writes when `changed === false`, so idempotent wraps stay no-op (pinned by the "reports changed=false when the rolled content matches existing file exactly" test). The single-transaction inertness pin from Chunk 3 (`runner is transactionally inert — every stub receives an empty staged scratch`) still passes because that test monkey-patches every dispatch entry.
  - **Six pure helpers exported** for testability and Chunk 9 commit-step contract: `_parseChunks(planContent)` (returns `[{id, title, done, blockedOn, lineNo}]` in document order; tolerates the ✅-in-title case by stripping it from the rendered title while still using its presence to mark done; tolerates `### Chunk N (suffix): Title` heading variants like the plan's own "Chunk 12 (optional): …"), `_selectPointer(chunks)` (returns `{current, next, allDone}`; first un-done wins; `next` is `null` when current is the tail; both `null` when allDone), `_renderPointerBody(pointer, planRelPath)` (markdown rendering of the rolled pointer — no nested code fences so it nests safely inside a surrounding markdown body), `_replaceManagedBlock(prior, body)` (replaces in place when markers found; appends fresh block separated by a blank line when not; defensively appends on out-of-order markers), `_resolvePlanPath(projectPath, step)` (the disambiguation logic described above), `_resolvePrimingPath(projectPath, step)` (absolute-path resolver). Marker constants and default paths also exported: `BEGIN_MARKER`, `END_MARKER`, `DEFAULT_PRIMING_PATH`, `DEFAULT_PLANS_DIR`.
  - **`_internal`** holds `readFileSync`, `existsSync`, `readdirSync` so tests can stub disk failures (matches the `_internal.execShell` / `_internal.sendKeys` pattern from Chunks 4 and 5). The handler intentionally does NOT expose `writeFileSync` — there's no write path to mock because there's no write path at all (the commit step in Chunk 9 owns that).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `priming-roll` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining four stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without standing up a real plans dir.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path section) with the Chunk 6 entry pinning the plan-format, managed-block-delimiter, and staged-write contracts so downstream chunks (Chunk 9 commit step, Chunk 10 progress drawer) can rely on them.
  - **Known follow-up (multi-plan disambiguation):** TangleClaw's own `.claude/plans/` already holds 10 plans; the prawduct bundled template's `next-session-prime` step ships without a `planPath` override. A wrap on TC-v3 itself with `wrapV2: true` would block with the disambiguation message until `step.planPath` is set per-project. This is gated entirely behind the Chunk-3 opt-in flag (default `false`), so no existing wrap is affected — but Chunk 11 will need a smarter default-resolution strategy (most-recently-modified plan, an active-plan symlink convention, or a project-level "current plan" pointer) before the default flip lands. Captured here so it doesn't get lost.
  - **Tests** (+42): 11 cases for `_parseChunks` (basic id+title; ✅-anywhere done detection with ✅-in-title strip; body ✅ does NOT promote; dotted/lettered sub-chunk ids `1`, `10c.2`, `12.3a.4`; **Blocked on:** capture; first-wins on multiple **Blocked on:** lines; case-insensitive match; empty/null input → `[]`; `(suffix):` heading tolerance; CRLF parses byte-equivalent to LF — Critic MAJOR-1 regression pin; malformed `### Chunk Foo:` heading skipped while well-formed siblings still parse — Critic MAJOR-2 regression pin), 4 for `_selectPointer` (first-undone wins; tail current → next=null; all-done; empty input), 5 for `_replaceManagedBlock` (in-place replace preserves surround; append-with-separator when no markers; no separator when prior empty; defensive double-append on out-of-order markers AND user content between misordered markers survives — Critic MINOR pin; duplicated managed blocks edit only the first pair — pin for refactor intentionality), 4 for `_renderPointerBody` (active + on-deck; blockedOn surfaces on active; allDone explicit; "no headings" fallback), 17 handler-level cases (missing project.path → blocked; no plans dir → blocked; empty plans dir → blocked; multiple plans → blocked with disambiguation; `step.planPath` honored; `step.planPath` missing file → blocked; project-relative `step.planPath` escaping project root → blocked — Critic MINOR path-traversal defense pin; absolute `step.planPath` outside project root is accepted — pinning the "absolute is trusted" branch; no chunk headings in plan → blocked; fresh priming file → managed block created in stage with `changed=true` AND no real disk write — single-transaction pin; existing managed block replaced while user surround preserved byte-for-byte; idempotent re-roll → `changed=false`; allDone reflected in pointer + rendered body; **Blocked on:** carries into rolled pointer; `step.primingPath` honored; plan-read throw → blocked; priming-read throw with successful plan-read → blocked). Full suite: 2063 / 2063 pass (was 2021 at end of Chunk 5).

- **Wrap pipeline `ai-content` step real handler (#139, Chunk 5)** — fourth implementation chunk. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` with a real send-prompt → poll-idle → capture-pane → validate-fields handler. The same handler powers both prawduct's `memory-update` step (AI writes the session block to `.tangleclaw/memories/MEMORY.md` via its own file tools — TangleClaw owns the *prompt*, not the write) and `summary-derive` (AI emits `## Heading` blocks that the handler parses against `step.captureFields`). One substitution token is supported in this chunk: `{previousMemoryBlock}` interpolates the captured text of the prior step whose `stepId === 'memory-update'`, enabling `summary-derive` to deterministically reference the memory block the AI just produced (instead of trusting the AI to re-read its own scrollback). Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js`**: defensive blocks on missing `context.session.tmuxSession` or empty `step.prompt`. Sends the interpolated prompt via `_internal.sendKeys(tmuxSession, prompt, {enter:true})`. Sleeps an initial settle window (`INITIAL_SETTLE_MS = 3000`), then polls `_internal.detectIdle(tmuxSession)` every `POLL_INTERVAL_MS = 2000` until idle is reported (`detectIdle` defines idle as ≥10s of unchanged pane output — pinned in `lib/sessions.js`). Total wait capped by `MAX_WAIT_MS = 5 min`; exceeded → `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['AI did not return within Xs']}`. On idle, captures full pane scrollback via `_internal.capturePane(tmuxSession, {full:true})` and validates. If `step.captureFields[]` is set, each field must appear as a `## Heading` (case-insensitive) with non-empty content; otherwise the handler asserts only that the AI returned ≥`MIN_RESPONSE_CHARS = 20` chars (catches no-ops and rare premature-idle captures). Successful captures are staged in `context.staged[step.id] = {capturedText, parsedFields}` for the eventual `commit` step (Chunk 9) to consume. Failures of `sendKeys` / `detectIdle` / `capturePane` are caught and surfaced as blocker entries rather than thrown — the runner already converts thrown handlers to blocked results, but explicit handling produces sharper error messages.
  - **`lib/sessions.js` import: lazy via `require('../sessions')` inside `defaultDetectIdle`** to break the module-load cycle `sessions.js → wrap-pipeline.js → wrap-steps/ai-content.js → sessions.js`. At call time the cycle is fully resolved, so `sessions.detectIdle` is always defined. `lib/tmux.js` has no back-edge to sessions and is eager-required as before.
  - **Two pure helpers exported** for testability: `_interpolatePrompt(promptTemplate, previousResults)` (single-token substitution; unrecognized braces pass through; null prompt → empty string; non-`status:'done'` prior memory steps are ignored — symmetric with the runner's halt-aware aggregation) and `_parseFields(rawOutput, captureFields)` (returns the `{field: content}` map; mirrors `lib/sessions.js:parseWrapSummary`'s parsing but without the flattened-string return shape, so the handler can validate field-by-field for missing-or-empty cases).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `ai-content` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining five stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `priming-roll`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without re-implementing tmux state in the harness.
  - **Tests** (+20): 5 cases for `_interpolatePrompt` (token substitution; missing prior step → empty; unrecognized braces pass through; null prompt; non-`done` prior step ignored), 5 for `_parseFields` (case-insensitive matching; absent captureFields; empty rawOutput; non-matching headings skipped; multi-field parse), 10 for the handler (missing session blocks, missing prompt blocks, happy path no-captureFields, short-response no-captureFields blocks, captureFields-all-present succeeds with staged output, missing-or-empty captureFields surfaces per-field blockers, `{previousMemoryBlock}` interpolation snapshot, idle timeout via `Date.now` monkey-patch, `sendKeys` throws → blocker, `detectIdle` throws → blocker, `capturePane` throws → blocker). Full suite: 2021 / 2021 pass.

- **Wrap pipeline `lint` + `test` step real handlers (#139, Chunk 4)** — third implementation chunk. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stubs at `lib/wrap-steps/test.js` and `lib/wrap-steps/lint.js` with real server-side handlers that shell out to the project's configured commands and surface exit-code + tailed stderr/stdout. `lib/wrap-pipeline.js` extends to (a) thread caller-supplied `options` into each step's `context` so handlers can read overrides like `skipTests`, and (b) honor `blocker: "errors-only"` as a halt condition (was `"errors-only resolved inside the handler"` in Chunk 3 — collapsed the contradiction with the build plan's "blocks on lint errors but not warnings" wording). Default opt-in remains `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so this chunk produces zero behavior change on any existing project — only sessions explicitly opting in see the real handlers fire.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/test.js`**: reads `projConfig.testCommand`; `null` → `{status:'skipped', output:{reason:'no testCommand configured'}}`. With `step.allowOverride === true` AND `options.skipTests === true` → `{status:'skipped', output:{override:true,reason:…}}` and the command never runs (Chunk 9's `commit` step will record the override in the wrap commit body). Otherwise shells out via the internal `_internal.execShell` (10-min timeout, 10 MiB buffer cap); exit 0 → `{ok:true, status:'done', output:{exitCode:0}}`; exit ≠ 0 → `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['Tests failed (exit N)', last-50-lines of stderr-or-stdout]}`. Timeouts surface as exit code 124. The `_internal` object is exported so tests can override `execShell` without spawning real processes (matches the Chunk 3 `STEP_DISPATCH` monkey-patch idiom).
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/lint.js`**: reads `projConfig.lintCommand`; `null` → skipped. Computes "in-session" file set via `_internal.detectChangedFiles(cwd)` (parses `git status --porcelain` — staged + unstaged + untracked-but-tracked, deletes excluded, rename arrows resolved to destination, porcelain-quoted paths unquoted). Empty file set → skipped with `output.reason: 'no in-session changes to lint'`. Otherwise builds `<lintCommand> -- <quoted-files…>` — the `--` POSIX end-of-options separator prevents a git-legal filename starting with `-` (e.g. `-rf.js`) from being interpreted as a flag by the lint binary (Critic-MINOR-1); each file is then single-quote-escaped via the standard `'\''` close-reopen idiom (exposed as `_shellQuote`, unit-pinned against filenames with spaces and embedded single quotes) and the whole string is handed to `exec`. Blocker semantics: `blocker:"errors-only"` (or `true`) + exit ≠ 0 → `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}`; `blocker:false` + exit ≠ 0 → `{ok:true, status:'done', output.warnings: tail}` (informational only — pipeline continues). Chunk 9 will widen the in-session scope to "since last wrap commit" once the `commit` step starts stamping `lastWrapSha` on project records.
  - **`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:_buildStepContext`** now accepts and forwards `options` from `runWrapPipeline(name, options)` into the step context's new `context.options` field. Defaults to `{}` (handlers can read `context.options.skipTests` etc without guarding against undefined). Block-condition broadened from `step.blocker === true` to `step.blocker === true || step.blocker === "errors-only"` — the runner now halts on either form when the handler returns `!ok`. JSDoc updated to document the broader contract; the previous "enum-style blockers resolved inside the handler" wording was load-bearing in Chunk 3's no-op world but contradicted #139's pipeline-blocking requirement once real handlers landed. **ADR 0002** updated in this PR (Status line, Runner contract section, Migration-path Chunk 4 entry) to reflect the broadened halt condition (Critic-MAJOR-1).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `lint` and `test` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining six stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned to the canonical shape so a half-inlined implementation on any of them fails this test.
  - **Tests** (+18): six per-handler `test` cases (no command → skipped; passing → done with exitCode 0; failing → blocked with stderr tail; allowOverride+skipTests → skipped with override flag; skipTests without allowOverride → still runs; shell command observed exactly), seven `lint` cases (no command → skipped; no in-session files → skipped; `errors-only` + exit 1 → blocked with file count and shell-quoting verified; `errors-only` + exit 0 → done with warnings surfaced; `blocker:false` + exit 1 → informational ok:true; `_shellQuote` unit test against `simple.js` / `with space.js` / `it's.js`; real-git integration against a throwaway repo that exercises the actual `git status --porcelain` parser end-to-end). Two runner-level `"errors-only"` block-condition tests (halts on `!ok`; ignores unrecognized enum values). Two `options`-threading tests (forwards through `context.options`; defaults to `{}` when caller omits options). Full suite: 2001 tests pass.

- **Wrap pipeline runner skeleton + `projConfig.wrapV2` opt-in (#139, Chunk 3)** — second implementation chunk. Ships the server-side pipeline runner (`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:runWrapPipeline`), the eight per-kind step modules under `lib/wrap-steps/`, and the opt-in flag that routes `lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap` to the new path when `projConfig.wrapV2 === true`. Default is `false` through Chunk 10 — every existing wrap continues on the legacy NL-prompt path byte-equal to pre-#139 behavior (regression-pinned in `test/sessions.test.js`). Chunk 11 will flip the default.
  - **`lib/wrap-pipeline.js`** (NEW, ~190 lines): the runner. Reads `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` from the methodology template, dispatches each step by `kind` to a handler module via `STEP_DISPATCH`, threads a single-transaction `runState` (`results` + `staged` scratch space — only the `commit` step in Chunk 9 will flush `staged` to git), and returns `{ok, blockedAt, results:[{stepId, kind, status, output, blockers}], commitSha:null, summary:null, error:null}`. Block-true semantics: a step declared `blocker: true` whose handler returns `!ok` halts the pipeline immediately, and every subsequent step is reported as `'pending'` so the Chunk 10 UI can render where the pipeline froze. Enum-style blockers (e.g. `"errors-only"`) stay inside handlers — the runner only knows boolean. Unknown step kinds skip (forward-compat with future bundled changes); thrown handler errors are caught and surfaced as `blockers[]` entries on a synthesized `'blocked'` result.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/`** (NEW subdir): eight files — `pr-check.js`, `lint.js`, `test.js`, `critic-check.js`, `ai-content.js`, `priming-roll.js`, `version-bump.js`, `commit.js`. Each exports `async function run(context)` returning the canonical no-op `{ok:true, status:'done', output:null, blockers:[]}` and JSDoc'd with the future-chunk contract. Real implementations land in Chunks 4–9.
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG`**: three new fields — `wrapV2: false` (the opt-in flag), `testCommand: null`, `lintCommand: null` (explicit declarations the `test` and `lint` step kinds will shell out to in Chunk 4; auto-detection is rejected as a monorepo-class footgun).
  - **`lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap`**: now `async`. Reads `projConfig.wrapV2` from `store.projectConfig.load(project.path)`; on `true` delegates to the new `_triggerWrapV2` helper (invokes the runner, returns the canonical wrap shape + a `pipelineResult` field carrying the runner's structured output, does NOT send any tmux command since the runner is server-side). On `false` (default) the legacy NL-prompt path runs unchanged. All callers updated to `await`: `server.js:POST /api/sessions/:project/wrap` and existing `test/sessions.test.js` cases.
  - **ADR 0002** updated with a Chunk 3 status line noting the runner skeleton landed behind the flag.
  - **Tests** (+22): `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (NEW) — dispatch-table covers every contract kind; dispatch covers every kind referenced by bundled prawduct + minimal templates; runner runs all stubs end-to-end and returns ok:true; preserves step ID order; attaches `kind` to each result; preflight errors (unknown project, missing `wrap_pipeline`); block-true halts and marks subsequent steps `pending`; blocker:false `!ok` does NOT halt; thrown handler error surfaces as blocker; unknown-kind skips without dispatch; each of the eight step stubs pinned to the canonical no-op shape. `test/sessions.test.js` — V2-opt-in test (no tmux command sent, pipelineResult attached) + V2:false byte-equal regression pin against the Chunk 2 NL prompt.

- **Wrap pipeline schema migration + back-compat shim (#139, Chunk 2)** — first implementation chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the legacy `wrap: {command, steps, captureFields}` block in bundled methodology templates with a typed `wrap_pipeline: {schemaVersion, promptTemplates, steps[]}` schema. Each step is an `{id, kind, ...}` object that the runner (Chunk 3+) will dispatch via a typed dispatch table — kinds enumerated in ADR 0002. Bundled methodology templates migrated: `prawduct` (6 steps) and `minimal` (3 steps); the gitignored `tilt` template migrates symmetrically when present locally. No runtime behavior change in this chunk: `lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap` continues to fabricate the legacy NL prompt byte-equal to pre-migration via a back-compat shim.
  - **`lib/skills.js`**: new exported helper `wrapShapeFromTemplate(template)` synthesizes the legacy `{command, steps, captureFields}` shape from either schema. When `wrap_pipeline` is present, `steps` is the ordered list of `pipeline.steps[].id`, `captureFields` is the flattened deduplicated union of every step's `captureFields[]`, and `command` is `null` (custom overrides will move to `promptTemplates.<engine>` once the runner honors them in later chunks). Falls back to the legacy `wrap` block verbatim for installs that haven't yet picked up the new bundled schema. `getWrapSkill` is a thin wrapper over `wrapShapeFromTemplate(store.templates.get(id))` — the helper is the single read-point so callers can't drift into asymmetric reads of the two schemas (ADR 0001).
  - **`lib/eval-audit.js:scoreWrapQuality`** routes through the new shim instead of reading `methodology.wrap.steps` directly. Both `triggerWrap` and `scoreWrapQuality` now answer "what are the wrap steps?" through the same predicate — symmetric capability gates per ADR 0001.
  - **`lib/store.js:ARRAY_RECONCILERS`** gains `wrap_pipeline.steps` with `mergeBy:id` policy (the #155 Chunk 2 reconciler) so new bundled steps with a new `id` value propagate additively to live runtime templates on init. Legacy `wrap.steps` and `wrap.captureFields` entries remain in the table as inert safety nets during the migration window — bundled templates no longer ship those paths, so the policy short-circuits on missing bundled arrays, leaving any legacy `wrap` blocks on live templates untouched.
  - **ADR 0002 — Wrap Pipeline Contract** (`docs/adr/0002-wrap-pipeline-contract.md`) documents the schema, the step-kind dispatch table, the runner contract (`runWrapPipeline` signature, step return shape, single-transaction semantics), the back-compat shim semantics, the reconciler choice, and the phased Chunks 3 → 11 rollout via `projConfig.wrapV2`. ADR 0001 updated to cross-link to ADR 0002 as an instance of the "one read predicate per conceptual state" rule.
  - **Tests**: +6 in `test/skills.test.js` (byte-equal legacy shape for all three migrated templates pinning behavior preservation; `wrap_pipeline` → legacy synthesis with captureFields union; legacy fallback; `wrap_pipeline` preferred when both present; null/empty input handling; defensive skip of malformed entries), +5 in `test/store.test.js` (`wrap_pipeline.steps` mergeBy:id append; user-added step preserved; field-overwrite forbidden on matched entries; user-removed re-add limitation pin per ADR 0001; inert-legacy-reconciler safety-net behavior when bundled drops the `wrap` block), +1 in `test/eval-audit.test.js` (`scoreWrapQuality` works against a `wrap_pipeline`-shaped methodology object — proves the shim routing). The #136 init-glue integration test in `test/store.test.js` updated for the new world: legacy `wrap` block on live is preserved untouched while `wrap_pipeline` is propagated from bundled.
  - **Scope discipline**: this chunk lands schema + shim + reconciler + ADR only. No runner, no step kinds, no UI, no `wrapV2` opt-in flag — those are Chunks 3–11. The legacy NL-prompt code in `triggerWrap` is unchanged; `triggerWrap` continues to fabricate the exact same prompt it did before this PR via the shim. Out-of-scope items pinned in ADR 0002: auto-Critic-dispatch, tombstone-based step removal, branch-protection push flow, methodology authoring UX, per-step retry. The self-deleting bridging auto-memory `project-issue-139-methodology-wrap.md` continues to point at the build plan; deletion is gated on #139 closing.

- **Template-array reconciliation extends to object-keyed arrays (#155, Chunk 2)** — `lib/store.js:ARRAY_RECONCILERS` policy table grows to nine paths total. Chunk 2 adds the `_reconcileMergeBy(live, bundled, idKey)` policy and wires five previously-drifting object-keyed arrays through it: `phases` (idKey=`id`), `evalDimensions.tier1`, `evalDimensions.tier2`, `evalDimensions.tier3` (idKey=`id`), and `actions` (idKey=`label` — prawduct's `actions` entries don't have an `id` field, the `label` field is the natural identifier). The policy matches by string equality on `entry[idKey]` and appends bundled entries whose key value is absent from live; matched entries are left untouched (additive only, never overwrites). Appended entries are deep-cloned so in-process reuse of the same bundled object across multiple live targets cannot leak mutations.
  - **ADR 0001 extended**: new section "Generalized template-array reconciliation (#155 extension)" documents the full pattern (table + policies + driver), the three policies' behavior at-a-glance, and the user-removed-entry acknowledged limitation that's symmetric across `orderedSubsetReplace` and `mergeBy`. A new rule in the ADR captures the operational follow-through: when adding a new array to any bundled template, add a one-line `ARRAY_RECONCILERS` entry in the same PR — the cost of forgetting it is exactly the incident-then-patch cycle #119, #136, and #158 each paid.
  - **Driver change**: the inner loop in `_mergeBundledTemplate` now passes `entry.idKey` to the reconciler, allowing each path to declare its own identifier field. Log payload simplified from per-entry `added` list (only meaningful for primitive arrays) to `addedCount` (works uniformly across string and object arrays).
  - **Acknowledged limitation (re-add on user-removed entry)**: symmetric with `_reconcileOrderedSubset`. `_reconcileMergeBy` cannot distinguish "user removed entry X" from "user is on an older bundled version that never had entry X" — both produce a live whose id-set is a subset of bundled's. The policy choice is to re-add, documented in the reconciler's JSDoc and pinned by a regression test (`treats user-removed object-keyed entry as stale and re-adds it`). Tombstones would solve it but are out of scope for #155.
  - **Tests**: +22 in `test/store.test.js` — 13 unit tests on `_reconcileMergeBy` (additive append; live order preserved; null when in sync; user-added preserved; field-overwrite forbidden on matched entries; deep-clones appended entries; empty live → bundled copy; empty bundled → null; non-array inputs → null; missing/empty idKey → null; non-`id` key names supported via `'label'`; bundled entries without idKey skipped; bundled internal duplicates protected) + 9 integration tests on `_mergeBundledTemplate` (phases append by id; phases user-added preserved; phases field-overwrite forbidden; evalDimensions.tier1 append by id; actions append by label; deep-clone integration; multi-path single-pass spanning string and object arrays; no-op mtime pin; user-removed re-add limitation pin). The Chunk 1 phases-untouched pin is replaced with a generalized "unregistered path stays alone" pin (`customCategory.items` — outside the table, must not be reconciled). All 1927 prior tests continue to pass — 1949 total.

- **Template-array reconciliation generalized beyond `wrap.steps` (#155, Chunk 1)** — `lib/store.js:_mergeBundledTemplate` now drives plain-array reconciliation through a declarative policy table (`ARRAY_RECONCILERS`) instead of hardcoding `wrap.steps`. Three previously-drifting paths join the table in this chunk: `prime.sections` (orderedSubsetReplace, same policy as wrap.steps), `wrap.captureFields` (setUnion, additive set merge), and `init.directories` (setUnion). Adding a newly-tracked array path is now a one-line registry entry — no driver change. The original wrap.steps inline code from #136 migrates into the same table-driven loop; all existing wrap.steps tests pass unchanged, proving the refactor is behavior-preserving.
  - **New pure functions**: `_reconcileOrderedSubset(live, bundled)` (extracted from the original #136 inline logic) and `_reconcileSetUnion(live, bundled)` (new). Both return a new array OR `null` meaning "leave alone" — uniform shape lets the driver dispatch identically across every policy. `_getAtPath(obj, dotPath)` resolves nested array references for both bundled and live sides.
  - **Policy choices**: `setUnion` preserves `live`'s element order at the front and appends bundled-only entries at the end in bundled-iteration order. `orderedSubsetReplace` carries forward the #136 acknowledged limitation verbatim — a user-removed entry that leaves the array as a strict subset of bundled is indistinguishable from "user is on an older version missing that entry", and is treated as stale-older (re-added). This policy now applies uniformly to `wrap.steps` AND `prime.sections`; if either ever needs different semantics, the table makes the wiring split explicit.
  - **Scope discipline**: `hooks.<engine>.<event>[]` continues to flow through `_mergeBundledHookEntries` (#158) — match-by-matcher semantics don't fit the plain-array driver and the existing hook-entry path is unchanged. Object-id-keyed arrays (`phases`, `evalDimensions.tier1/tier2/tier3`, `actions`) are explicitly NOT in the table — they're deferred to Chunk 2 along with `_reconcileMergeById` and the ADR 0001 update documenting the full generalized pattern. A pinning test asserts the Chunk 1 driver leaves `phases` alone even when drifted, locking the scope boundary against future drift.
  - **Tests**: 22 new in `test/store.test.js` — 6 for `_reconcileOrderedSubset` (subset → returns bundled copy; identical → null; user-customized → null; reordered → null; non-array inputs → null; result is not the bundled reference), 8 for `_reconcileSetUnion` (appends bundled-only entries in order; preserves live order at front; null when live is superset; preserves user-added entries; empty live returns bundled copy; empty bundled returns null; non-array inputs → null; no duplication when bundled has repeats live already covers), 8 integration in the existing `_mergeBundledTemplate (#136)` block (prime.sections subset reconcile; prime.sections user customization preserved; wrap.captureFields additive merge; wrap.captureFields user-added preserved with bundled appended; init.directories additive merge; no-op when every array is in sync — pinned via mtime; multi-array reconcile in single pass; pinning test that `phases` stays untouched in Chunk 1). All 1927 prior tests still pass (was 1905 pre-chunk).

- **CHANGELOG.md structural-invariants test (#168)** — `test/changelog-structure.test.js` asserts four structural invariants on `CHANGELOG.md`: every release banner (`> 🛟` / `> 🚀`) is inside a `## [X.Y.Z] - YYYY-MM-DD` section (catches the PR #166-class regression where a heading was silently consumed); released-version headings appear in descending semver order (catches cherry-pick / backport misorderings); no released-version heading appears twice (catches bad merge resolutions); the top released-version heading agrees with `version.json` (the load-bearing invariant — would have caught PR #166 directly, where the cache self-heal then propagated `3.16.0` to dashboards on every install). Invariant detectors are factored as pure functions so a second describe block exercises them against a synthesized post-#166 / pre-#167 file shape, proving the regression is detected. ~180 lines, 9 tests, runs in < 40ms inside the standard `node --test 'test/*.test.js'` sweep — no new tooling. Structural-only; lints body content of release entries is intentionally out of scope (style / completeness remains Critic territory).

## [3.16.2] - 2026-05-13

> 🛟 **Recommended bug-fix release.** Two patch-class fixes since v3.16.1: **ttyd-watcher actually fires on macOS** (#144) — closes a 6+-month silent regression where the watcher's `pgrep -c` proxy exited 2 on every BSD invocation, leaving #94's session-killing PTY-exhaustion bug unprotected since #95 merged; users had been manually `launchctl kickstart`-ing ttyd on every incident. The replacement measures `kern.tty.ptmx_max` vs `/dev/ttys*` directly and trips at 85% pool saturation. **Dashboard project-version label self-heals on enrichment** (#165) — closes the stale-label gap where external version bumps (release-PR merges, manual `version.json` edits) didn't reach the dashboard until the next TC-managed session launch or wrap on the same project. Anyone on v3.16.1 will get the update-pill notification with a clickable link to this release page.

### Fixed

- **ttyd-watcher now actually fires on macOS — measures PTY pool, not broken `pgrep -c` proxy (#144)** — `lib/ttyd-watcher.js` shipped in PR #95 to auto-recover from #94's session-killing PTY-exhaustion bug. It has been a silent no-op on every macOS install since merge. `_countTtydChildren` invoked `pgrep -c -P <pid>` — but BSD `pgrep` (`/usr/bin/pgrep` on macOS) has no `-c` flag and exits 2 with `illegal option -- c`. The catch only special-cased `err.status === 1` (no matches), so exit 2 fell through to a `pgrep failed` warn that has been logged every 5 minutes since at least 2026-05-02. The kickstart never fired; users have been manually running `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$UID/com.tangleclaw.ttyd` to recover from every incident. The PR #95 unit tests stubbed the runner via `_setRunner`, so the production code path against real BSD `pgrep` was never exercised by CI — three defects compounded into a silent regression that took 6+ months to surface.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_isPtyPoolExhausted(thresholdRatio)`** — new function replacing `_countTtydChildren`. Measures the actual exhausted resource: `sysctl -n kern.tty.ptmx_max` (cap) vs `sh -c 'ls /dev/ttys* 2>/dev/null | wc -l'` (used). Returns `{ exhausted, used, cap, ratio }`. The pool measurement counts both live and zombie PTY-holding processes because it asks the kernel rather than introspecting a process tree — closing the second compounding defect (BSD `pgrep` filters out zombies). Fail-safe: any non-numeric reading, throwing binary, or `cap <= 0` returns `{ exhausted: false, used: 0, cap: 0, ratio: 0 }` and the watcher never kickstarts on a failed measurement.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_countTtydZombies(pid)`** — new diagnostic-only function using `ps -A -o ppid=,stat=` (which unlike BSD `pgrep` DOES include zombies). Counts rows where `ppid == pid` AND `stat` contains `Z`. **Never gates the kickstart decision** — captured purely for diagnostic logging so production logs on the next incident carry the data that answers "how many zombie children did ttyd have when we kickstarted?" with a grep rather than a guess. Returns 0 on any error.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_check`** — rewired to gate kickstart on `_isPtyPoolExhausted` (pool-only, per the #144 issue body's explicit proposal). Trigger log line moves from `'ttyd child count above threshold, kickstarting'` to `'ttyd PTY pool exhausted, kickstarting'` and carries `{ ttydLabel, pid, used, cap, ratio, zombies, threshold }`. The below-threshold debug log carries the same fields so verbose operators can watch the pool fill over time. Zombie count is included in both log lines as diagnostic-only data.
  - **API change**: `DEFAULT_THRESHOLD = 50` (child count) → `DEFAULT_PTY_THRESHOLD = 0.85` (pool ratio). `_check` opt `threshold` → `ptyThresholdRatio`. `start()` opt `threshold` → `ptyThresholdRatio`. Only caller in the repo (`server.js:3123`) invokes `start()` with no options, so the rename is fully internal.
  - **Design call: pool-only gate (not hybrid pool+zombies AND gate)**. The issue body explicitly proposed pool-only ("trip kickstart when used/cap crosses ~0.85"). Simpler. If unrelated PTY saturation produces false-positive kickstarts in practice (no observed case yet), can add a hybrid gate as a follow-up — easier to add a gate later than to remove one. A test pins the policy: pool exhaustion alone triggers kickstart even when zombie count is 0.
  - **Production-runner smoke test (closes the test gap that hid this bug for 6+ months)** — `describe('production runner smoke test (darwin only)')` block calling `_isPtyPoolExhausted(0.85)` AND `_countTtydZombies(1)` against the real host shell (no `_setRunner` patch). Gated on `process.platform === 'darwin'`. Asserts both functions return finite values without throwing. Pre-#144 the entire watcher was tested only against a stubbed runner; the same regression class — a wrong-flag invocation that silently fails on macOS — would slip through CI again without this. Closes the issue's "Test gap to close" requirement.
  - **Tests**: -3 in `test/ttyd-watcher.test.js` (`_countTtydChildren` describe block removed — function gone). +9 (`_isPtyPoolExhausted`: trips at threshold; trips at canonical #94 incident shape used=527 cap=511; doesn't trip below threshold; doesn't trip at floor-1 (off-by-one boundary lock, Critic NIT 1); fail-safe on non-numeric sysctl; fail-safe on sysctl throw; fail-safe on ls/wc throw; fail-safe on cap≤0; uses DEFAULT_PTY_THRESHOLD when no arg). +6 (`_countTtydZombies`: counts only ppid-match AND Z-stat rows; returns 0 when no rows match parent; returns 0 when all matching rows are live; fail-safe on ps error; empty ps output; skips malformed rows). +2 `_check` tests (still kickstarts when zombies=0 — pins the pool-only design call; doesn't kickstart on fail-safe measurement and short-circuits to the new measurement-failed warn — Critic MINOR 1). +2 production-runner smoke (darwin-gated). 1896 total passing (was 1880).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 0 MAJORs / 2 MINORs / 4 NITs. MINORs + 3 NITs addressed in-chunk. **M1** (fail-safe `{ cap: 0 }` fell through to the "PTY pool ok" debug log so operators grepping `ratio: 0.000` couldn't distinguish "pool empty" from "measurement broken") — `_check` now branches early on `cap === 0`, emits a `warn` with `'ttyd PTY pool measurement failed (fail-safe — no kickstart)'` carrying `{ ttydLabel, pid, zombies, threshold }`. New regression test asserts the branch is reachable from a thrown sysctl and that no kickstart fires. **M2** (CHANGELOG test-count off by one — enumeration listed 8 `_isPtyPoolExhausted` tests but the count said `+7`) — corrected to `+9` after also adding the boundary-lock test from NIT 1; total now sums correctly at 1896. **N1** (boundary lock missing) — added a `used = floor(cap*threshold) - 1` test asserting `exhausted === false` to pin the `>=` vs `>` predicate from drifting in either direction; pairs with the existing `used = floor(cap*threshold)` trip test. **N2** (test body had six lines of working-out-loud commentary about macOS ps STAT codes) — collapsed to a one-line `// Expected: rows 3 and 4 match. Others either lack Z or wrong ppid.` comment. **N4** (JSDoc on `_check`'s `ptyThresholdRatio` typed as bare `number` and could mislead a future caller into passing `85` instead of `0.85`) — added `/* 0..1 fraction, not percent */` inline comment to the type signature; pulled the better wording in `start()`'s JSDoc through. NIT 3 (whether to keep the unconditional `ps -A` per tick — Critic recommended keeping it for diagnostic continuity) accepted as-is; the measurement is microseconds and the symmetric log payload across exhausted/ok branches is more valuable than the saved cycle.
  - **Backwards compatibility**: TC restart picks up the new watcher behavior on launch. The watcher remains macOS-only (Linux installs are unaffected — `start()` short-circuits in the existing platform guard). No data migrations.

- **Dashboard project-version label self-heals on enrichment (#165)** — The project-version label shown in the dashboard project list (e.g. `TangleClaw-v3 v3.X.Y`) is sourced from each project's `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt` cache file via `lib/projects.js:_detectProjectVersion`. Pre-#165 the cache file was only rewritten by `lib/project-version.js:recordVersion`, which is called from two narrow triggers — session launch (`lib/sessions.js:145`) and session wrap (`lib/sessions.js:765`). When a project's on-disk version source changed outside of a TC-managed session (release-PR merge via `gh`, external `git pull`, manual edit of `version.json`), the cache stayed stale and the dashboard kept rendering the pre-bump number until the next launch/wrap. Manifested live on 2026-05-13 when cutting v3.16.1: the TC-v3 project's `version.json` and `CHANGELOG.md` both reflected the new version, but the dashboard label still read `v3.14.0` because no TC-managed session had launched on the TC-v3 project itself since 2026-05-05.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_detectProjectVersion`** — semantic inversion. Pre-#165 the cache was the highest-priority source and a divergent on-disk source never reached the label. Post-#165 the function reads both the cached value AND the live chain (CHANGELOG.md → version.json → package.json) on every call; if live is present and differs from cached, it rewrites the cache with the live value + correct source label and returns live. Live's absence (no source files match) preserves the cached value — this is load-bearing for git-tag-derived caches that `lib/project-version.js:recordVersion` may have written via its richer detection chain, which `lib/projects.js`'s live readers can't reproduce.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_detectLiveVersion`** — new helper exposing the live half of the detection chain as `{ version, source } | null`. Separated from `_detectProjectVersion` so the self-heal write can label the source correctly (`'CHANGELOG.md'`, `'version.json'`, `'package.json'`) rather than re-detecting source post-facto.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_writeVersionCacheFile`** — new helper mirroring `lib/project-version.js:_formatCacheFile`'s output byte-for-byte (`version: …\nrecorded_at: …\nsource: …\n` with ISO-without-ms recorded_at). Write is best-effort via try/catch; logs at warn on failure but returns silently so enrichment never crashes on a read-only filesystem or permission-denied `.tangleclaw/`. Creates `.tangleclaw/` if missing.
  - **Why the write helper lives in `lib/projects.js` rather than calling `projectVersion.recordVersion`**: `lib/project-version.js` already requires `lib/projects.js` for its own readers (`_readChangelogVersion` etc.). A back-require would close a cycle. The cache file format is plain text and stable across the codebase; duplicating the four-line write is cheaper than reorganizing the module graph.
  - **Cost**: every enrichment call now does up to ~3 extra small text-file reads (CHANGELOG.md / version.json / package.json) when the cache is present. Previously the chain short-circuited on cache hit. Filesystem-cache-warm reads are sub-millisecond; no measurable dashboard-refresh slowdown.
  - **Tests**: 1 inverted in `test/projects.test.js` (`layer 1: live source overrides stale cache and self-heals` — was the pre-#165 `cache file should win over CHANGELOG, version.json, and package.json` test, asserting `1.0.0-from-cache`; now asserts `2.0.0-from-changelog`). 9 new in a dedicated `describe('_detectProjectVersion self-heal (#165)')` block: rewrites on version.json mismatch (asserts cache file contents + source label + recorded_at shape); rewrites on CHANGELOG mismatch (verifies live-chain priority — CHANGELOG over version.json); steady-state byte-equal preservation (no rewrite when cache matches live, filesystem-agnostic); cache preservation when no live source (git-tag-derived caches survive); read-only-directory fail-open (chmod 0o500 forces write failure, function still returns live value); creates `.tangleclaw/` if missing; non-existent path returns null without throwing; `_detectLiveVersion` returns null when no live source; `_detectLiveVersion` source labels match the reader that hit (CHANGELOG / version.json / package.json). 1880 total passing (was 1871).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 1 MAJOR / 3 MINORs / 2 NITs. MAJOR + 2 MINORs addressed in-chunk. **M1** (fail-open test passed for the wrong reason) — original test seeded an existing cache file then `chmod 0o500`'d the directory, but POSIX `O_WRONLY|O_TRUNC` on an *existing* file succeeds inside a r-o directory (the test silently exercised the success path, not the catch block). Rewrote the test to stub `fs.writeFileSync` so it throws unconditionally; added positive assertions that the stub was invoked exactly once AND that no cache file was created. The stub-based approach is also cross-platform robust (chmod-based fail-open tests no-op when run as root). **N1** (`_readVersionCacheFile` JSDoc was doubly stale) — comment still referenced "AI on session start and wrap once the session-lifecycle hook lands in #55 chunks 2+" from before #101 made TC the writer. Refreshed to document both current TC-side writers (`lib/project-version.js:recordVersion` for the rich chain incl. git-tag, `lib/projects.js:_writeVersionCacheFile` for the #165 self-heal). **N2** (preserve-cached-when-live-null trade-off not documented in-code) — added a sentence to `_detectProjectVersion`'s JSDoc explaining the accepted trade-off: a project whose only live source was deleted will keep showing the pre-deletion value until the next session launch's `recordVersion` rewrites the cache with `source: fallback`. The alternative (clobber on null) would regress git-tag-only projects on every enrichment, which is worse. N3 (test pollution risk from chmod permission failures) accepted as-is — N1 fix removed the chmod entirely, so the concern no longer applies. NITs (CHANGELOG count framing, duplicated JSDoc rationale) accepted as-is.

## [3.16.1] - 2026-05-13

> 🛟 **Recommended bug-fix release.** Three OpenClaw / methodology-hook fixes since v3.16.0: **chunk-1 orphan-hook protection now reaches pre-#146 runtime templates** (#158) — closes the session-killing infinite Stop-hook loop that resurfaced on TC-v3 itself when chunk-1's `requires` filter silently no-op'd on pre-v3.15.0 runtime templates; **OpenClaw connection flow fixes** (#160) — surfaces real save errors, fixes Bridge Port silently defaulting to 3201 for non-ClawBridge deployments, and replaces the generic "check SSH connectivity" message with the actual SSH failure (local-bind conflict, auth failure, network error); **OpenClaw Web UI cached-WS-URL routing fix** (#162) — clicking a second OpenClaw connection's Web UI button no longer loads the first connection's dashboard via stale localStorage cache. Anyone on v3.16.0 will get the update-pill notification with a clickable link to this release page.

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw Web UI: clicking a second connection's Web UI button loaded the first connection's dashboard via cached localStorage WS URL (#162)** — When TC proxies multiple OpenClaw connections through `/openclaw-direct/<connId>/...` on the same TC origin, the iframe-loaded OpenClaw dashboard caches its derived WebSocket URL in localStorage (e.g. `wss://192.168.10.99:3102/openclaw-direct/<connId>`). Because the dashboard reads localStorage on subsequent loads instead of re-deriving from the iframe URL, the second OpenClaw's Web UI button would silently route WebSocket traffic to the *first* OpenClaw's tunnel. Symptom: clicking Claw-Node-01's Web UI button opens RentalClaw's dashboard. The iframe URL is correct; the dashboard's WebSocket connection is wrong.
  - **Scope honesty (Critic MAJOR-4)**: this fix targets the **observed manifestation** — cached values whose string content contains the proxy path `/openclaw-direct/<otherId>/`. The TC parent page can detect and remove those entries before the iframe loads. If a future OpenClaw dashboard caches its WS URL under a key whose value contains no proxy-path substring (e.g. origin-only `wss://host:port` or a structured `{host,port}` JSON), the fix as shipped does NOT clear it and the bug recurs. That broader case is acknowledged-out-of-scope here; would file as a #162-followup needing either a TC-side proxy HTML injection or a coordinated change with OpenClaw upstream.
  - **Fix in `public/openclaw-cache.js`** — new helper module `tcClearStaleOpenclawCache(connId, storage)`. Walks `localStorage`, uses `matchAll` to extract every `/openclaw-direct/<id>` reference inside each value, and deletes the entry only when EVERY reference is for a different (case-insensitive) connId than the current one. Composite values that reference both the current connection AND a stale one are PRESERVED — the dashboard's legitimate current-connection state shouldn't be lost just because the value also mentions an old id. Loaded via a new `<script src="/openclaw-cache.js">` tag in `openclaw-view.html` (positioned between `api-helper.js` and `openclaw-view.js` so the helper is defined before `openclaw-view.js`'s `init()` calls it). Uses the same UMD-ish factory pattern as `api-helper.js` — exposes on `window` for the browser and `module.exports` for tests.
  - **Wiring in `public/openclaw-view.js`** — new `setFrameSrc(frame, url)` helper is the only writer of `terminalFrame.src` in the file; it runs `tcClearStaleOpenclawCache(connId)` then sets `frame.src`. Both writer sites (`init()` initial load and the post-pairing auto-approve reload) route through this helper, so the cache-bust is symmetric (Critic MINOR-1 + MINOR-2). The iframe is same-origin with the parent (TC proxies under `/openclaw-direct/`), so localStorage is shared — clearing entries from the parent makes the dashboard JS running inside the iframe fall through to deriving its URL fresh from the iframe's own `location` (for the in-scope value shape). Call is guarded by `typeof tcClearStaleOpenclawCache === 'function'` so a missing helper script doesn't crash navigation.
  - **Policy decisions**: (a) **Composite-value safety** — `matchAll` + "hasStale && !hasCurrent" predicate: only delete when no reference inside the value matches the current connId (Critic MAJOR-2). (b) **Case-insensitive connId comparison** — UUIDs are case-insensitive per RFC 4122 §3; both extraction and comparison are normalized to lowercase so a value emitted with mixed case (uppercase / mixed canonical form) doesn't get misclassified as stale and over-deleted (Critic MAJOR-3). (c) Only entries whose VALUES reference `/openclaw-direct/<otherId>/` are touched — TC's own per-project settings under `tc_<project>_<key>` and other unrelated keys are preserved. (d) Same-connection cache is preserved (the dashboard's prior session state survives navigation away and back, including across case differences). (e) Idempotent — calling twice with the same connId does nothing the second time. (f) Storage walk goes BACKWARDS so live mutation via `removeItem` doesn't skip keys (regression-tested). (g) Tolerant of incognito/disabled storage — wrapped in try/catch, returns 0 on any thrown access. (h) Defensive against missing/empty/malformed `currentConnId` — UUID-shape validation (`/^[0-9a-fA-F-]{16,64}$/`) means an accidental empty/typo input returns 0 without touching storage (Critic MINOR-4).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 3 MAJORs / 4 MINORs / 3 NITs. All MAJORs + actionable MINORs addressed in-chunk. **M2** (composite-value over/under-deletion) — original match-first-occurrence semantics could either over-delete (first match stale → whole value gone even if it also referenced current) or under-delete (first match current → preserves entry even if it referenced an old id elsewhere). Rewrote to `matchAll` + "hasStale && !hasCurrent" predicate; composite values containing the current connId are preserved. **M3** (case-policy backwards) — original strict-equality comparison would over-delete legitimate same-connection state if OpenClaw ever emitted a mixed-case UUID. UUIDs are case-insensitive per RFC 4122 §3; both extraction and comparison are now `.toLowerCase()`-normalized. Test that previously asserted "case difference treated as mismatched" was rewritten to assert the correct "case differences are NOT stale" contract. **M4** (CHANGELOG scope honesty) — added a "Scope honesty" sub-bullet acknowledging the fix targets the observed manifestation only; cached values whose strings don't contain the proxy path would need a follow-up issue. **Min1 + Min2** (symmetric clearing) — pre-Critic, only the initial `init()` write to `frame.src` cleared the cache; the post-pairing auto-approve reload was an un-cleared direct `frame.src = frame.src`. Extracted a `setFrameSrc(frame, url)` helper that's the only writer of `terminalFrame.src` in the file; both call sites route through it. Wiring test asserts there are NO direct `frame.src` writes outside the helper body. **Min4** (malformed connId) — added a UUID-shape regex `/^[0-9a-fA-F-]{16,64}$/` so a malformed input returns 0 without touching storage; regression test pins the contract. NITs (comment length, count-claim verification, CHANGELOG phrasing) accepted or addressed inline.
  - **Tests**: 17 new in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js`. Behavioral coverage against a mock `Storage` shim (13 cases): removes mismatched connId entries; preserves matching connId entries (incl. mixed-case); preserves unrelated entries (TC settings, third-party widgets); handles multiple stale entries in one pass; walks backwards so removeItem-during-iteration doesn't skip; tolerates non-string values; returns 0 on null/throwing storage; refuses to touch anything when `currentConnId` is empty/missing/malformed (UUID-shape validation); composite-value with mixed stale + current refs is preserved; all-stale composite is removed. Source-level structural assertions (4 cases): `openclaw-view.html` loads `openclaw-cache.js` BEFORE `openclaw-view.js`; `setFrameSrc` is the only `frame.src` writer outside its own body; `setFrameSrc` is called from at least 2 sites (init + post-pairing reload); the cache-bust call is guarded by `typeof === 'function'`. 1849 total passing (was 1832 at #161 merge).
  - **Backwards compatibility**: TC's own localStorage entries (per-project session settings, update-pill dismissal state, etc.) all use the `tc_*` prefix and don't carry `/openclaw-direct/` substrings — they're untouched by the helper. Users who have only ever opened one OpenClaw connection see no behavior change. Cross-connection users who currently see the bug get the fix on next openclaw-view.html load.

- **OpenClaw connection flow: misleading save errors + Bridge Port silently defaulting to 3201 + tunnel "check SSH connectivity" hiding the real failure (#160)** — Three compounding UI/UX bugs that made non-ClawBridge OpenClaw connections (any deployment without a ClawBridge sidecar — e.g. a fresh Docker-based OpenClaw on a Linux host) effectively unusable until the user manually PATCHed the record via the REST API. All three closed in one PR.
  - **Bug 1 — Save toast now surfaces the real server error.** Pre-#160, the New / Edit Connection modal hardcoded `"Save failed. Name may already exist."` for any non-2xx response. The actual error (PORT_CONFLICT, BAD_REQUEST, CONFLICT, etc.) lived in the JSON response body's `error` + `code` fields but never reached the UI. `public/ui.js:saveConnection` now uses `api.lastError` + `api.lastErrorCode` (the side-channel exposed by `public/api-helper.js` since PR #84 / issue #80) to render the real message. Falls back to the previous generic message only when no error payload was returned (e.g. network failure mid-save). Backend tests pin the contract that PORT_CONFLICT responses carry both `error` (string) and `code: 'PORT_CONFLICT'` so the frontend can disambiguate.
  - **Bug 2 — Blank Bridge Port now persists as null.** Pre-#160, an empty Bridge Port field in the modal silently saved as `3201` (the ClawBridge default) for three reasons: (a) `public/ui.js:saveConnection` serialized `parseInt(value, 10) || 3201`; (b) `lib/store.js:openclawConnections.create` ran `const bridgePort = data.bridgePort || 3201;`; (c) `lib/store.js:_rowToConnection` coerced null read-back to 3201. Every non-ClawBridge connection carried 3201 in its DB row, which then drove server.js to ask `lib/tunnel.js` for a `-L 3201:127.0.0.1:3201` SSH forward — and with `-o ExitOnForwardFailure=yes` set, any local-port conflict on 3201 killed the entire tunnel. Fixed at all three layers: form submit sends `null` on empty; create accepts null verbatim; row read-back preserves null. PATCH-to-clear (sending `bridgePort: null` or `bridgePort: ''` in PUT) now actually clears. Persisted non-null values (e.g. 4501) still round-trip unchanged — only the falsy → 3201 coercion went away.
  - **Bug 3 — Tunnel failure messages now name the actual problem instead of "check SSH connectivity".** Pre-#160, `lib/tunnel.js:ensureTunnel` spawned SSH with `stdio: 'ignore'`, discarding stderr. When `tcpProbe` saw the tunnel didn't come up, the only available message was a generic "SSH tunnel spawned but port not connectable" — which `server.js` then wrapped as "Tunnel failed: …", indistinguishable from a real SSH connectivity issue. The local-bind conflict (the canonical #160 incident shape) is invisible in this message. Fixed by switching stdio to `['ignore', 'ignore', 'pipe']`, buffering stderr (4 KB cap), and routing it through a new `_formatTunnelError(stderr, extraForwards)` helper that recognizes the load-bearing failure modes — local-bind conflict (with a special hint when the conflicting port matches a secondary forward like Bridge Port), `Permission denied`/`publickey` auth failures, `Connection refused`/`No route to host`/`Could not resolve hostname` network failures — and renders them with actionable text. Unrecognized stderr falls back to surfacing the first non-empty line so the user has something to grep.
  - **Schema migration v14 → v15 (`lib/store.js`)**: `openclaw_connections.bridge_port` was `INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 3201` pre-#160. SQLite can't `ALTER COLUMN` to drop NOT NULL, so the migration recreates the table preserving every existing row's data verbatim — rows that already have 3201 keep 3201 (the migration changes only the column constraint, not existing values). Wrapped with explicit `BEGIN; ... COMMIT;` SQL (the runtime DB engine is `node:sqlite`'s `DatabaseSync`, which doesn't expose a `.transaction()` wrapper). Postcondition check verifies `PRAGMA table_info` reports `notnull=0` before advancing `schema_version` — if the recreate step silently failed for any reason, the migration throws rather than marking the DB v15 with a v14 schema still in place (Critic MAJOR-3). Best-effort `ROLLBACK` in the catch block if a BEGIN landed without COMMIT. Fresh `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` also updated for new installs.
  - **Docs**: `docs/openclaw-setup.md` updated — the Bridge Port row in the connection-fields table now says "leave blank for non-ClawBridge OpenClaw deployments" rather than presenting `3201` as the default (Critic MAJOR-4). The "How it works" section also clarifies that the Bridge Port forward is conditional on the field being set.
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 4 MAJORs / 4 MINORs / 2 NITs. All MAJORs + actionable MINORs addressed in-chunk. (M1 — `Warning: Permanently added` first-connect noise was leaking into the auth/network/fallback messages) `_firstLine` now filters lines matching `/^Warning: Permanently added/i` before picking the first meaningful line; auth + network + fallback branches all render the real error line, not the host-key Warning. (M2 — original "migration preserves data" test was actually testing API round-trip on a fresh v15 DB, not the migration code path) Added a real migration regression test that opens a fresh tmpDir, seeds it directly via `node:sqlite` with the pre-#160 schema (`bridge_port INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 3201`) + `schema_version = 14` + two pre-existing rows (one with `3201`, one with `4501`), then calls `store.init()` to fire `_runMigrations` and asserts (a) `schema_version` advanced to 15, (b) `PRAGMA table_info` reports `notnull=0` + `dflt_value=null`, (c) both pre-existing row values survived verbatim, (d) post-migration inserts with `bridgePort: null` now succeed. (M3 — silent migration-failure → false v15) Postcondition check throws if `bridge_port` isn't nullable after the recreate step; `schema_version` advancement is gated on the throw not firing. (M4 — `docs/openclaw-setup.md` still claimed 3201 as the default) See "Docs" bullet above. (Min1 — IPv6 bind-conflict regex) Bind-pattern regex broadened to `/bind\s+(?:\[[^\]]+\]|[^:\s]+):(\d+):\s*Address already in use/i` so `bind [::1]:port` matches the same way `bind [127.0.0.1]:port` does; regression test added.
