Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 0 MAJORs / 2 MINORs / 4 NITs, MINOR 2 + NIT 1 + NIT 2 addressed in-chunk: the Eval Audit Mode block now carries an inline comment explaining why it's intentionally kept in the prime (so a future refactor doesn't blindly delete it as "yet another duplicate"); CHANGELOG corrected on the Methodology Archives justification (they ARE in CLAUDE.md, not just findable on disk — the deletion is correct but the original framing was inaccurate); CHANGELOG clarified on shared-docs injection (it's content for inline mode, references for reference mode, not uniformly "full content"). Other 1 MINOR (no test asserts presence of dropped blocks IN CLAUDE.md to lock in division of concerns) + 3 NITs (engineProfile param unused, truncation logic untested, learnings test doesn't assert CLAUDE.md absence) accepted — all are coverage-completeness improvements that don't change the implementation's correctness. The `engineProfile` parameter to `generatePrimePrompt()` is left in place since the only call site already passes it; removing both isn't worth the diff churn. 1622 total tests passing (was 1620).

## [3.13.5] - 2026-04-30

### Fixed

- **First user message of every bypass-mode session is a stray `2` (#119)** — When a session was launched in `bypassPermissions` mode (`--dangerously-skip-permissions`), the first user-message turn the AI received was the literal text `2` instead of the prime prompt or the user's input. The bundled `data/engines/claude.json` declared `preKeys: ["2", "Enter"]` for that mode, originally added to dismiss Claude Code's old "press 2 to confirm dangerous mode" confirmation dialog. The current Claude Code CLI no longer presents that confirmation, so `2` + `Enter` typed via tmux `send-keys` landed straight in the chat input as the first submitted message. Fix is two-part because `_mergeBundledProfile` only adds missing keys (never removes): (1) the bundled profile no longer declares `preKeys`/`preKeyDelay` on `bypassPermissions` so new installs are clean; (2) a one-shot prune in `_mergeBundledProfile` removes the stale value from existing live profiles when it equals exactly `["2","Enter"]` — equality match preserves any user-customized preKeys (e.g. a forked binary that still requires confirmation). The prune is keyed on filename (`claude.json`) rather than `live.id === 'claude'` so a profile whose `id` field has drifted from a hand-edit still self-heals. Independent Critic flagged 2 MAJORs and 1 doc parity issue, all addressed in-chunk: (M1) the prune guard switched from `id`-field to filename per the above; (M2) stale "press 2 to continue" reference in `_resolvePreKeys` JSDoc reworded to a generic "dismissing a confirmation dialog" example; (D1) `_mergeBundledProfile` JSDoc updated to acknowledge the targeted prune as a narrowly-scoped exception to the otherwise additive merge contract. The post-write log line now distinguishes merge-only vs prune-only paths so a pure prune doesn't misleadingly emit "Merged new bundled fields" (Critic NIT). 4 new tests in `test/store.test.js`: (1) bundled profile carries no preKeys on bypassPermissions, (2) stale `["2","Enter"]` is pruned on init, (3) custom preKeys (e.g. `["y","Enter"]`) are preserved, (4) the prune is idempotent — a second init after pruning does not rewrite the file. 1624 total tests passing (was 1620).

## [3.13.4] - 2026-04-30

### Changed

- **Record project version in TangleClaw at session launch instead of delegating to the AI (#101)** — `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt` is now written by TangleClaw itself, not by the AI session. The previous design (introduced in #55 chunk 2) injected a ~20-line "Project Version Recording" protocol into every session's prime prompt instructing the AI to inspect `CHANGELOG.md` / `version.json` / `package.json` / `git describe`, format an ISO-8601 UTC timestamp, and write the cache file in a specific key/value format. That's pure file I/O + string parsing — zero reasoning where an LLM adds value, and it produced 3–5 visible tool calls of scrollback noise on every session start plus inconsistent output across sessions (different models pick different sources, different timestamp precisions, different `source:` strings like `CHANGELOG.md` vs `CHANGELOG.md:11` vs `CHANGELOG`). New `lib/project-version.js` module: `detectVersion(projectPath) → { version, source }` runs the same fallback chain (CHANGELOG → version.json → package.json → git tag → `0.0.0-dev`) using `child_process.execFileSync` for the git lookup with a 2 s timeout and stripping a leading `v` from tags so `v3.13.3` matches manifest sources; `recordVersion(projectPath)` calls detect, formats `version: / recorded_at: / source:` lines with a millisecond-stripped ISO-8601 UTC timestamp, creates `.tangleclaw/` if missing, writes the file. Both functions are non-throwing — `recordVersion` returns `null` and logs a warning on any I/O failure so a read-only project dir or full disk never blocks session launch or wrap. Wired into `lib/sessions.js`: `launchSession()` calls `recordVersion(project.path)` before generating the prime; `triggerWrap()` calls it before sending the wrap text (captures pre-wrap state; the next session-launch record captures any version bump the wrap itself produced like a CHANGELOG promotion or git tag). Removed: the entire `## Project Version Recording` block (18 lines) from `generatePrimePrompt()`, the appended re-record instruction from `triggerWrap()`, the `projectVersionGuide` loader and all 4 generator usages in `lib/engines.js` (`_generateClaudeMd`, `_generateGeminiMd`, `_generateCodexYaml`, `_generateAiderConf`), and the now-unused `data/project-version-recording-guide.md` file (added in PR #76). The cache-file *reader* in `lib/projects.js:_readVersionCacheFile` is unchanged — `enrichProject()` still reads the file for the landing-page enrichment chain, just now with a deterministic writer behind it. Tests: new `test/project-version.test.js` (20 tests covering detectVersion's 5-layer chain with priority assertions, recordVersion's file-format + idempotence + non-string-input defensiveness, `_formatCacheFile`, and `_readGitTagVersion` with real git repos via `child_process.execFileSync`); inverted assertions in `test/sessions.test.js` (prime no longer contains `## Project Version Recording`, wrap command no longer contains `project-version.txt`/`re-check the project version`) plus 2 new positive tests asserting `triggerWrap` and `launchSession` actually write the cache file with the expected ISO-8601 UTC `recorded_at:` field; inverted assertions in `test/engines.test.js` (no generator with `supportsConfigFile` includes the section anymore, `_getRulesContent` no longer surfaces a `projectVersionGuide` field). Visible cost saved per session: ~20 lines of prime-prompt noise gone, 3–5 AI tool calls eliminated, output is now deterministic. Independent Critic flagged 1 MINOR (test isolation: the launchSession write-detection test seeded a `package.json` into a shared project dir without cleanup, which would have leaked into a future test in the same describe block) and 3 NITs, MINOR + 1 NIT addressed in-chunk: cleanup now runs in `finally` removing both the seeded `package.json` and the produced `.tangleclaw/` directory; `_readGitTagVersion`'s silent-catch now logs at `debug` level so a slow-repo `git describe` timeout is diagnosable when verbosity is raised. Other 2 NITs (millisecond strip undocumented in JSDoc; `recordVersion` doesn't reject whitespace-only path strings) accepted — millisecond format choice is locked in by tests so any future change would surface there, and a whitespace path triggers the outer try/catch + `null` return path harmlessly. 1620 total tests passing (was 1600).

## [3.13.3] - 2026-04-29

### Fixed

- **Global rules editor saves trailing whitespace and stray indentation, polluting every regenerated CLAUDE.md (#100)** — `globalRulesApi.save()` in `lib/store.js` wrote pasted content verbatim, so any cosmetic whitespace artifacts in the source (trailing spaces, uniform leading indent applied by an editor or chat client) were persisted to `~/.tangleclaw/global-rules.md` and propagated into every project's `CLAUDE.md` via `_generateClaudeMd()` on each boot regeneration. Captured live on this repo's own user file: 53 lines with trailing whitespace, body uniformly indented 2 spaces while the H1 sat at column 0 — producing visible inconsistency where some `##` section headings rendered at column 0 and others at column 2 inside the same generated CLAUDE.md. Fix: new `_normalizeRulesContent()` helper normalizes line endings (CRLF/CR → LF), strips trailing per-line whitespace **outside fenced code blocks** (` ``` ` and `~~~` — trailing whitespace inside fences can be semantic), detects a uniform leading indent across the body skipping a leading H1 (markdown convention puts the H1 at column 0 even when the rest of the doc was indented — the issue's suggested algorithm missed this and would have computed minIndent=0 for the actual polluted file, producing zero dedent), collapses runs of 3+ blank lines to a single blank line, and trims leading/trailing blank lines. Wired into `save()` and `reset()` so new content is normalized before persisting; wired into `load()` with auto-heal — if normalized content differs from raw, `load()` rewrites the file in place so legacy polluted files self-resolve on first read after deploy without requiring a separate migration step. Trade-off accepted: users who deliberately added trailing whitespace to global rules content (outside code fences) lose it (premise of the bug fix). The dedent logic preserves nested list indentation correctly because the strip is uniform — a parent at indent 2 and child at indent 4 dedent to indent 0 and 2 respectively, keeping the relative hierarchy; same applies to code inside fences (uniform shift preserves intra-fence indent structure). Independent Critic flagged 1 BLOCKER (CRLF not normalized — Windows / GitHub web editor pastes carry CRLF that survived `split('\n')` and propagated into CLAUDE.md) and 1 MAJOR (trailing whitespace inside fenced code blocks stripped unconditionally, causing semantic loss in code samples), both addressed in-chunk: CRLF/CR normalized via `replace(/\r\n/g, '\n').replace(/\r/g, '\n')` up front; trailing-ws strip now tracks fence state via a per-line `^[ \t]*(```|~~~)` toggle and skips body lines while inside a fence (the fence delimiters themselves still get their own trailing whitespace stripped). Critic also flagged 1 MINOR (multiple-H1 docs not handled — only the first H1 is skipped during indent scan; accepted as defensive, won't fix since global rules use single-H1 structure) and 1 NIT (CHANGELOG tone — accepted). 23 new tests in `test/store-globalrules.test.js` covering: trailing-ws strip, H1-skip indent detection, no-H1 indent detection, refusal to dedent when body has any column-0 line (treats indent as intentional), 3+ blank-line collapse, leading/trailing blank trim, idempotence, empty/whitespace-only/non-string defensive cases, nested-list preservation, save→on-disk normalization, save→load round-trip idempotence, load() auto-heal of dirty files, load() no-op on clean files (mtime unchanged), reset() default-normalization, plus 6 Critic-driven tests: CRLF→LF, lone CR→LF, fence content preservation (` ``` ` and `~~~`), fence-line trailing-ws strip, and combined fence + uniform-dedent (relative indent preserved). 1 new test in `test/api-globalrules.test.js` covering the API-level PUT-then-GET round-trip with the exact pollution shape from the live user file. 1600 total tests passing (was 1576).

## [3.13.2] - 2026-04-29

### Fixed

- **Kill button does nothing once a session enters `status='wrapping'` — orphan tmux + stuck DB row, project becomes un-relaunchable (#105)** — `DELETE /api/sessions/:project` returned `404 NOT_FOUND` for any session in `status='wrapping'` because `killSession()` only matched `status='active'` rows. Once the wrap-idle modal landed (#93/#98) and live wraps regularly held the row in `wrapping` for longer windows, this gap turned every wrap-stuck session into a brick: tmux still alive, DB row in `wrapping` indefinitely, kill button useless, next launch attempt failing with `"Session is currently wrapping for"`. Manual recovery required `tmux kill-session` plus a direct `UPDATE sessions SET status='killed'` — captured live on session 330 (`RentalClaw-Project`, wrapping for 10 days). Fix has three parts: (1) `killSession()` now targets `getActive() OR getWrapping()` so the kill button is a real force-stop again — when neither row exists but tmux still has a session under the project's expected `tmuxName`, it kills the orphan tmux and returns `{ reconciled: true }` so the API can render a 200 instead of 404; (2) `launchSession()` gains a stale-wrapping recovery path — when a wrapping row's `wrap_started_at` (or `started_at` for legacy rows) is older than `STALE_WRAPPING_THRESHOLD_MS` (1 hour), the launch kills the stale tmux, marks the row killed, and proceeds with a fresh launch instead of refusing; recent wraps still block as before so a long-running session that just initiated wrap can't be killed mid-flight; (3) new schema v14 column `wrap_started_at` populated by `setWrapping()` so the launch-guard can distinguish "session started 8 hours ago, just wrapped 5 seconds ago" (recent — block) from "session has been wrapping for 8 hours" (stale — recover) without false-positives off the unrelated `started_at` field. Server handler in `server.js` updated to surface `result.reconciled` as a 200 success body instead of crashing on the missing `result.session.id`. New `_parseSqliteUtcMs()` helper in `lib/sessions.js` interprets SQLite's TZ-less `'YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS'` output as UTC explicitly — a latent bug since `new Date(...)` parses TZ-less strings as the runtime's local time, which would have made the threshold check wrong by the local TZ offset on every non-UTC machine. The same helper was applied to the two pre-existing `durationSeconds` math sites in `getSessionStatus` so the UI's session timer is now correct on non-UTC hosts (Critic MAJOR follow-up). Independent Critic flagged 2 MAJORs + 3 MINORs, all addressed in-chunk: (M1) latent TZ bug fixed in `getSessionStatus`'s two `Date(active.startedAt)` callsites; (M2) added 2 api-level tests in `test/api-sessions.test.js` covering both DELETE-handler success paths (wrapping-row kill returns sessionId+status, orphan reconcile returns reconciled:true with no sessionId); (Mn4) stale-recovery test now uses distinct tmux names (`stale-wrap-OLD` on the wrapping row, `stale-wrap` on the canonical project name) so the recovery-kill is distinguishable from the pre-launch orphan-kill that fires later in `launchSession`; (Mn5) added fail-safe direction for unparseable `wrap_started_at`/`started_at` — the launch guard now treats NaN as stale (recover) instead of fresh (block), since blocking is the exact bug class #105 was filed for. Wrap pane cache (`_wrapPaneCache`) is now cleared during kill so a re-launched session starts clean. 15 new tests across `test/sessions.test.js` (13: 6 in `killSession recovers wrapping + orphan tmux (#105)` + 7 in `launchSession stale wrapping recovery (#105)`) and `test/api-sessions.test.js` (2 covering both DELETE handler success branches). Schema-version assertions in `test/store.test.js`, `test/store-portleases.test.js`, `test/store-session-mode.test.js`, and `test/sessions-webui.test.js` bumped from 13 → 14 to reflect the new migration. 1576 total tests passing (was 1561).

- **Wrap-idle banner vanishes under the cursor — convert to sticky modal (#98)** — The wrap-idle banner from PR #93 had two practical problems users hit during real wraps: (1) the inline-banner placement was easy to miss visually ("I never got the pop-up modal we discussed"), and (2) PR #93's Critic-MAJOR-2 auto-hide-on-resume kicked in on incidental events. A single 2 s status poll returning `idle: false` — caused by `detectIdle`'s pane-diff sensitivity to ttyd redraw events (mouse hover into the iframe, laptop close/reopen reattach, the engine's streaming progress indicator updating each second) — silently dismissed the banner. Live-witnessed race condition: banner appears, user moves mouse toward Return button, next poll fires before click lands, banner vanishes. This issue is **complementary to #97** (`detectIdle`'s streaming-indicator bug) — even after #97 is fixed, momentary flip-flops on iframe focus events would still happen, so the wrap-idle UI needs to be robust against them independently. Fix: convert `#sessionWrapIdle` from inline-banner pattern to the existing `.modal-backdrop`/`.modal-content` modal pattern used by `#wrapModal` and `#killModal` (HTML markup updated in `public/session.html`, banner-specific `.session-wrap-idle` CSS rule deleted in `public/session.css` since the modal classes already exist), and make it **sticky once shown** by removing the `resumeFromWrapIdle()` call from the poll handler's `data.wrapping && !data.idle` branch in `public/session.js` — once the modal appears, it stays until the user explicitly clicks one of: **Return to Projects** (POSTs `/wrap/complete`, kills tmux, navigates), **Resume working** (closes modal, resets `wrapIdleCount`), or the **backdrop** (mirrors the existing `wrapModal`/`killModal` backdrop pattern via `e.target === e.currentTarget` guard, calls `resumeFromWrapIdle`). Function `showWrapIdleBanner` renamed to `showWrapIdleModal`, state field `sessionState.wrapIdleBannerShown` renamed to `sessionState.wrapIdleModalShown`, and stale "wrap-idle banner" wording in three JSDoc/comment blocks updated to "wrap-idle modal" for parity (Critic MINOR follow-ups). The 5 `#sessionWrapIdle` `.classList.add('hidden')`/`.classList.remove('hidden')` callsites all switched to `.classList.remove('open')`/`.classList.add('open')` to match modal semantics. The backdrop click handler short-circuits with `if (sessionState.wrapCompleting) return;` (Critic NIT 3) so an outside click during an in-flight Return-to-Projects POST can't hide the modal mid-flight — the modal stays visible until either `handleWrapCompleted` runs (success) or the error toast surfaces (failure). Trade-off accepted: if the user walks away after the modal appears and the AI is still streaming, the modal sits indefinitely — same trade-off as the original banner, better than losing the user-gate to a flicker; the Kill button on the banner remains the escape hatch. Test changes in `test/session-wrapper.test.js`: rewrote the HTML structural test to assert the new modal markup (`modal-backdrop`/`modal-content`/`modal-actions`/`aria-modal="true"`), inverted the CSS test to assert `.session-wrap-idle` is **absent** (was: present), updated the handler-presence test to assert `showWrapIdleModal` (and **not** the old `showWrapIdleBanner` name), added two new structural tests asserting (a) the auto-hide-on-resume branch is gone (no `resumeFromWrapIdle()` call inside the AI-active poll branch) and (b) the backdrop click handler is wired with the `e.target === e.currentTarget` guard, the `resumeFromWrapIdle` call, and the `wrapCompleting` short-circuit (test uses brace-walked body assertion instead of a fixed-length slice so wrapping comments can't escape the window). 1561 total tests passing (was 1559).

## [3.13.1] - 2026-04-28

### Fixed

- **ttyd zombie children exhaust macOS PTY pool — every project terminal stuck on "Reconnecting…" (#94)** — ttyd does not reap its tmux child processes on macOS; after extended ttyd uptime, exited tmux clients accumulate as defunct (`?Es`) processes that pin kernel PTY slots. Once the count nears `kern.tty.ptmx_max` (default 511 on macOS), every new project terminal fails with `pty_spawn: 6 (Device not configured)` — the websocket attaches but the PTY allocation throws, the browser auto-reconnects, and the loop repeats forever. The TC API and tmux server-side sessions remain healthy throughout, so the symptom is purely browser-side: `Reconnecting…` for every project. Production captured 490 zombies and 527 `/dev/ttys*` entries before manual `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$UID/com.tangleclaw.ttyd` cleared it. Layer 1 mitigation: new `lib/ttyd-watcher.js` polls ttyd's child count every 5 minutes via `pgrep -c -P <ttydPid>` and kickstarts the launchd job when the count reaches 50 (well below the kernel limit, well above the normal 1–5 active connections). PID is read from `launchctl list <label>` and the kickstart targets `gui/$UID/<label>`. macOS-only — `start()` no-ops on other platforms. All shell-outs use `execFileSync` with a 5 s timeout; failures log at `warn` and never crash the watcher loop. Watcher start wired into `server.js` after `server.listen` succeeds; stop wired into the existing graceful-shutdown block alongside `porthub.shutdown`/`modelStatus.stopMonitor`. No new config keys, no plist changes, no upstream ttyd patching (Layer 2, tracked in #94). Independent Critic flagged 2 MAJORs + 4 MINORs, all addressed in-chunk: (M1) `_kickstartTtyd` now reads `process.getuid` defensively and refuses to invoke `launchctl kickstart` with `gui/0/<label>` (root) or an unsafe uid — root would need `system/<label>` which TC doesn't run as; (M2) the `_check` threshold test now asserts the exact `gui/<UID>/<label>` target string passed to launchctl, not just "kickstart was called", so a future refactor that routes through a different domain can't silently pass; (N3) the non-darwin lifecycle test now stubs `setInterval` and the runner to assert the no-op truly schedules no timer and makes no shell-out, replacing the previous trivial `assert.ok(true)`; (N4) `start()` now uses `??` instead of `||` for `intervalMs` and `threshold` defaults so explicit `0` values are honoured rather than silently fallback-replaced; (N5) `_getTtydPid` demoted launchctl-list failure from `warn` to `debug` so dev clones without the launchd label don't spam the log every 5 min; (N1) `_setRunner` carries a comment about the module-global seam to flag the constraint for any future concurrent test importer. 17 new tests in `test/ttyd-watcher.test.js` covering: PID parsing from launchctl output (running + loaded-but-not-running), pgrep child-count parsing (with the no-match exit-1 case treated as 0), kickstart success/failure plus the new uid=0 refusal path (Critic M1), threshold-met / threshold-exceeded / below-threshold branches in `_check` (with the new exact-target assertion, Critic M2), skip-when-no-pid, error swallowing, and start/stop idempotency including the strengthened non-darwin no-op path (Critic N3). 1559 total tests passing (was 1542 after #91 follow-up).

- **Server-side wrap timeout still kills sessions despite #91 fix (#91 follow-up)** — PR #93 / v3.13.0 fixed the three frontend timers in `public/session.js` but left intact a server-side `WRAP_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` in `lib/sessions.js:622` that fired every status poll: if the session had been in `wrapping` state for more than 120 s, `getSessionStatus` returned `wrapCompleted: true`, called `completeWrap()`, and killed tmux — exactly the behavior the frontend rework was supposed to prevent. Wraps that ran longer than 120 s (memory writes + git auto-commit + version recording + Critic) lost data on the server side regardless of the new wrap-idle banner; the banner had no opportunity to help because the server already declared the wrap finished. Fix is pure deletion: removed `WRAP_TIMEOUT_MS`, the force-complete branch previously in `getSessionStatus`'s `if (tmuxAlive)` body, the `_wrapStartTimes` map and all `set`/`delete` callsites in `triggerWrap`, `completeWrap`, and `autoCompleteWrap`, plus the corresponding `module.exports` entries. No safety net is being lost — the new wrap-idle banner from PR #93 gives the user an explicit Return-to-Projects gate, and stale wrapping sessions are already auto-cleaned on next launch via the `getWrapping(project.id)` check at `lib/sessions.js:48-56`. Test changes in `test/sessions.test.js`: deleted 4 tests that asserted the old timeout behavior (`force-completes wrapping session after timeout`, `triggerWrap records wrap start time`, `completeWrap cleans up wrap start time`, `autoCompleteWrap cleans up wrap start time`), reframed `does not force-complete before timeout` as `getSessionStatus stays wrapping while tmux is alive`, renamed the describe block from `'wrap timeout'` → `'wrap state persistence (#91)'`, dropped the `_wrapStartTimes.clear()` line from `afterEach`, and added a new structural regression test that locks in the absence of `WRAP_TIMEOUT_MS` and `_wrapStartTimes` from the module's exports — so a future edit can't reintroduce them without breaking the build. 1542 total tests passing (was 1545; 4 obsolete tests deleted, 1 added). Closes #91 for real.

- **Session wrap closes prematurely — three aggressive timers replaced with explicit user gate (#91)** — Three stacked timers in `public/session.js` could cut off a wrap before the AI finished writing memory files, committing, and completing the wrap protocol: a 120 s hard timeout (`setTimeout(...120_000)` in `showWrappingState`) force-completed regardless of progress; a ~6 s idle threshold (`wrapIdleCount >= 3` in the poll handler) declared the wrap done after 3 consecutive idle polls and POSTed `/wrap/complete` — which kills the tmux session unconditionally on the server (`lib/sessions.js:842`); a 20 s auto-redirect (`setInterval` countdown in `handleWrapCompleted`) navigated to `/` whether the user was paying attention or not. Net effect: real data loss when wraps that included git push, Critic runs, or multi-file memory updates paused long enough for the idle threshold to fire — by the time the user noticed, tmux was already gone. Fix introduces a three-state wrap flow with an explicit user gate. **State 1 (Wrapping):** unchanged — wrap clicked, banner up, AI working, kill enabled. **State 2 (Wrap-idle, NEW):** triggered after **8 consecutive idle polls (~16 s)** instead of 3 — survives brief git/Critic pauses. New `#sessionWrapIdle` banner appears with two buttons: **Return to Projects** (POSTs `/wrap/complete`, kills tmux, navigates to `/`) and **Resume working** (hides banner, resets `wrapIdleCount` to 0 — banner re-appears if AI goes idle again for another 16 s window). Tmux stays alive throughout State 2. **State 3 (Wrap completed):** triggered by either user clicking "Return to Projects" or `wrapCompleted` from server (tmux died on its own during wrap). Existing `#sessionEnded` bar shown — but `handleWrapCompleted` no longer starts the 20 s countdown, so the user must click "Back to Projects" or "Stay" themselves. The `#countdown` span is reused by `handleSessionEnded` (unexpected tmux death outside a wrap) which keeps its 10 s countdown — different code path, session is already gone there, no recovery possible, so an auto-redirect is harmless. Polling continues throughout State 2 so if tmux dies during the prompt, the UI transitions to State 3 cleanly. Trade-off accepted: if the user walks away after wrapping, the banner sits forever waiting for a click — better than losing memory writes; kill button is always the escape hatch. New banner styled in `public/session.css` (primary-coloured, mirrors `.session-wrapping` idiom). Wired up in `bindEvents()` — clicking "Resume working" while another in-flight POST is happening is guarded by the `wrapCompleting` flag. Independent Critic flagged 2 MAJORs + 2 MINORs, all addressed in-chunk: (1) `confirmReturnFromWrapIdle` would silently bounce the user to `/` even when the `/wrap/complete` POST failed (network/server error) — tmux still alive — so it now branches on `apiMutate`'s null return, re-enables both banner buttons, surfaces an error toast (using the `api.lastError` side-channel from #80), and stays put for retry; (2) banner did not auto-hide when AI demonstrably resumed work after going briefly idle — poll handler now calls `resumeFromWrapIdle()` in the `data.wrapping && !data.idle` branch when the banner was shown, so a fleeting click on Resume isn't required; (3) `handleSessionEnded` (unexpected tmux death path) defensively hides `#sessionWrapIdle` to cover the case where tmux dies while the wrap-idle banner is up but the server emits `!active` instead of `wrapCompleted`; (4) misleading comment on the Stay button reworded to clarify it cancels `handleSessionEnded`'s countdown only — wrap-completed path doesn't start one, so Stay is a no-op there. 7 new structural tests in `test/session-wrapper.test.js`: HTML-level assertion for `sessionWrapIdle` + `wrapReturnBtn` + `wrapResumeBtn`, JS-level assertions for the new threshold (`wrapIdleCount >= 8` present, `>= 3` absent), removal of the 120 s timeout (`120_000`/`wrapTimeoutTimer`/`clearWrapTimeout` all absent), presence of the three new handlers (`showWrapIdleBanner`/`resumeFromWrapIdle`/`confirmReturnFromWrapIdle`), brace-walked body assertion that `handleWrapCompleted` contains no `setInterval`/`Returning in`/`window.location.href = '/'`, brace-walked body assertion that `confirmReturnFromWrapIdle` guards navigation behind `if (!data)`, re-enables `wrapReturnBtn`, and surfaces a toast on POST failure (Critic MAJOR 1 regression), and CSS-level assertion for `.session-wrap-idle`. 1545 total tests passing (was 1538).

## [3.13.0] - 2026-04-28

### Added

- **HTTPS setup wizard integration polish (#61, chunk 3)** — Final chunk of #61 wires the install flow, config PATCH, and generated docs to the HTTPS-default world. `deploy/install.sh` now reads `~/.tangleclaw/config.json` and picks `https` + `curl -k` for the post-install health check and the "Landing page" URL when `httpsEnabled` + both cert paths are set — mirrors `createServer()`'s guard so the install-script URL matches what the server actually binds. Falls back to plain `http` when the config file is absent (first install) or any of the three fields is missing. The ttyd terminal URL stays on `http://localhost:3100` since the ttyd launchd plist does not configure TLS. `createServer()` gained a second warn-level log for the previously silent branch where `httpsEnabled: true` but `certPath`/`keyPath` are unset — existing installs upgrading to `DEFAULT_CONFIG.httpsEnabled: true` without certs see an explicit "falling back to HTTP" message pointing them at the setup wizard (the existing cert-unreadable branch's warning was also reworded for consistency). `PATCH /api/config` now mirrors `/api/setup/complete`'s HTTPS cert validation: rejects enabling HTTPS with a missing cert file, rejects enabling HTTPS with only one of cert/key set, accepts a valid pair, and allows `httpsEnabled: true` with both paths empty so the server-level graceful fallback still works for migration scenarios. Critic follow-up hardened the PATCH handler in two ways: (1) accept `null` for `httpsCertPath`/`httpsKeyPath` (not just strings) so the Settings UI can clear them — previously a 400, now normalized to `null` in persisted config; (2) normalize empty-string paths to `null` so the persisted shape is identical to `/api/setup/complete`'s (both endpoints now store `null` for "no cert", never `""`). `data/porthub-guide.md` picks up a one-line note in the API Operations preamble explaining that `https://localhost:3102` is the default, HTTP is the fallback for skipped-HTTPS installs, and `curl -k` (or installing the mkcert root CA) is needed for local HTTPS with `curl` — propagates to every generated CLAUDE.md/GEMINI.md/Codex/Aider config via the four config generators in `lib/engines.js`. 22 new tests: 8 in new `test/install-sh.test.js` (protocol detection, config-file guard, `curl -k`, URL interpolation, ttyd-stays-http) following the existing `ttyd-attach.test.js` pattern; 4 in `test/api-openclaw.test.js` under HTTPS createServer (new httpsEnabled-without-paths branch + two `process.stdout.write`-intercepting tests asserting both warn-level log messages fire); 10 in `test/api-config.test.js` covering the PATCH validator (reject missing cert file, reject single-path, accept valid pair with `requiresRestart: true`, allow no-paths migration case, plus Critic follow-ups: empty-string → null normalization parity, accept explicit `null` to clear paths, allow disabling HTTPS while paths remain set, reject asymmetric cert-exists-but-key-missing; openssl-gated via `t.skip` where a real key is needed). 1509 total tests passing.
- **HTTPS setup wizard frontend (#61, chunk 2)** — Adds the HTTPS step to the first-run setup wizard (now 7 steps, HTTPS inserted between Preferences and Confirm). On entry, the step calls `GET /api/setup/https-check` to detect mkcert and defaults the mode radio to **Automatic (mkcert)** when available, falling back to **Manual** otherwise (also on network failure — confirmed by Critic follow-up test). Three paths: **Automatic** runs `POST /api/setup/generate-cert` for `localhost`/`127.0.0.1`/`::1`, then renders the cert + key paths plus the macOS/Linux/Windows remote-trust copy-paste commands from `getRemoteTrustInstructions()` with two confirmation buttons ("I've done this on remote machines" / "I only access locally") that unblock Next; **Manual** takes cert + key paths (validated by the server at submit); **Skip** continues over HTTP with a warning about OpenClaw LAN traffic. `wizardSelectHttpsMode()` clears per-mode state on mode change so stale mkcert paths don't leak into the manual inputs (Critic follow-up). The Confirm step now includes an "HTTPS" row (Enabled mkcert / Enabled manual / Disabled / Not configured). `wizardComplete()` ships `httpsEnabled`, `httpsCertPath`, `httpsKeyPath` alongside the existing config fields; when the server responds `{ restart: true }`, a restart overlay takes over (falling back to `window.location.origin` if `redirectUrl` is missing so the normal dismiss flow never fires while the server is exiting — Critic follow-up), polls the redirect URL with `fetch(..., { mode: 'no-cors' })`, and navigates as soon as the server is reachable (or after a 20s fallback). New HTTPS step styles in `public/style.css` (status badges, mode cards, copy-paste code blocks, warning callout, restart panel). 20 new tests in `test/setup-wizard-https.test.js` cover wizard state shape, `_httpsCanAdvance` gating for all three paths, `_buildHttpsPayload` output per mode, the confirm-summary labels, the initial https-check render (success + failure + mkcert-unavailable), mode-switch state reset, `wizardGenerateCerts` success/failure, the setup-complete payload, the restart overlay branch (with and without `redirectUrl`), and `_pollRestartAndRedirect`'s navigate-on-response behaviour — exercised via a minimal `vm` + DOM-stub loader since the wizard is a plain `<script>` file with no module boundary. 1487 total tests passing.
- **HTTPS setup wizard backend (#61, chunk 1)** — Backend scaffolding for the upcoming setup-wizard HTTPS step. New `lib/https-setup.js` module wraps mkcert with five helpers: `detectMkcert()` (availability + version + CAROOT), `isCaInstalled()` (rootCA.pem presence in CAROOT), `generateCerts()` (runs `mkcert -install` + generates `cert.pem`/`key.pem` into `~/.tangleclaw/certs/`, chmod 0600 on the key, returns hosts + expiry, throws a clear error if the cert directory is not writable), `validateCertFiles()` (existence + readability + PEM parse + cert/key pair match via `crypto.X509Certificate`), and `getRemoteTrustInstructions()` (copy-paste commands for trusting the root CA on macOS/Linux/Windows remote machines). Two new endpoints: `GET /api/setup/https-check` (detection probe) and `POST /api/setup/generate-cert` (cert generation — hostnames validated against `^[A-Za-z0-9][A-Za-z0-9.\-:]*$` so `-install` or `$(cmd)` can't slip through as mkcert flags). `POST /api/setup/complete` now accepts `httpsEnabled`, `httpsCertPath`, `httpsKeyPath`, validates cert+key pairs before saving, and schedules a `process.exit(0)` restart (via overridable `_setRestartScheduler` hook so tests don't exit) whenever the effective HTTPS-serving state changes — response includes `restart: true` + `redirectUrl` so the wizard frontend (chunk 2) can show a restart overlay and redirect to the new protocol. `DEFAULT_CONFIG` now defaults `httpsEnabled: true` with `httpsCertPath: null`/`httpsKeyPath: null` — existing installs without certs fall back to HTTP automatically because `createServer()` already requires all three values to be truthy. `createServer()` also hardened (Critic follow-up): if cert/key files are configured but unreadable at boot, log a warning and fall back to HTTP instead of crashing. 36 new tests across `test/https-setup.test.js` (22), `test/api-setup-https.test.js` (13), and `test/api-openclaw.test.js` (+1 HTTPS-fallback test); 1467 total passing.

### Fixed

- **Bypass permission mode causes engines to quit immediately on launch (#89)** — When launching Claude Code with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`, the engine shows a "1=quit, 2=continue" confirmation dialog. The prime prompt injected at 2000ms collided with this dialog, either selecting "quit" or corrupting the input, causing an immediate exit. Fix: extended the `launchModes` schema to support per-mode `preKeys` and `preKeyDelay`. The `bypassPermissions` mode in `data/engines/claude.json` now defines `"preKeys": ["2", "Enter"]` which dismisses the confirmation before the prime prompt fires. New `_resolvePreKeys(engineProfile, launchMode)` helper in `lib/sessions.js` checks mode-level preKeys first, falls back to engine-level (preserving Codex's existing `["Enter", "Enter"]` behavior), and returns `null` when neither is defined. `_deferEngineInit()` now accepts and passes through the selected launch mode. Existing installs get the new fields automatically via `_mergeBundledProfile()` deep-merge on next boot. 10 new tests for `_resolvePreKeys` covering mode priority, engine fallback, delay resolution chain, empty arrays, and nonexistent mode keys. 1538 total tests passing (was 1528). Independent Critic flagged 2 MAJORs (CHANGELOG — added; missing `"Enter"` after `"2"` preKey — added) and 1 MINOR (no integration test for `_deferEngineInit` wiring — accepted, unit coverage of `_resolvePreKeys` + existing Codex behavioral parity is sufficient).
- **Remove misleading PortHub warning from installer (#59)** — `deploy/install.sh` previously checked for standalone `porthub` and printed a yellow warning when not found, causing new users to think it was a missing dependency; PortHub was fully absorbed into TangleClaw — the standalone CLI check and its associated messages have been removed.
- **Frontend swallowed server error messages as generic "Check server logs" (#80)** — When `POST /api/projects` (and other mutations) returned a 4xx with a specific, actionable body (e.g. `Directory "ClawBridge" already exists in /projects — use Attach instead`), the frontend displayed **"Failed to create project. Check server logs."** The shared `api()` helper in `public/landing.js`, `public/session.js`, and `public/openclaw-view.js` caught the thrown-with-server-message Error, logged it to the devtools console, and returned `null` — form handlers only saw the falsy result and fell back to hardcoded generic strings. Fix: attach `api.lastError` and `api.lastErrorCode` as a side channel on every call (populated from `data.error` / `data.code` on 4xx/5xx, or `"Connection lost."` / `err.message` on network failure; cleared on success). The three "Check server logs" form handlers (`ui.js:1087` submitCreate, `setup.js:588` cert-gen, `setup.js:678` setup-complete) now render `api.lastError` when the server returned a message, falling back to the generic string only when the side channel is empty. Zero churn across the other 40+ `apiMutate` call sites. 17 new tests: 15 in new `test/frontend-api-errors.test.js` exercising each of the 3 api() implementations via a vm sandbox + fetch stub (4xx with message, 5xx without body, success clears stale state, network error populates, plus 3 landing.js-specific `setConnected` integration assertions), plus 2 DOM-level assertions in `test/setup-wizard-https.test.js` that `wizardGenerateCerts` actually renders `api.lastError` into `#setupHttpsError` and falls back to the generic string when empty (Critic follow-up #6). 1527 total tests passing. Follow-ups filed: #82 (consolidate duplicated api() helpers into a shared module) and #83 (audit remaining generic error strings like "Upload failed" for server-message parity).
- **Prime prompt newlines collapsed on injection (#75)** — Session-start markdown arrived as a single run-together line because `tmux paste-buffer` replaces every LF with CR by default (tmux 3.6 man page). Fix: pass `-p` to `paste-buffer` in `lib/tmux.js` `sendKeys()` so tmux wraps the payload in bracketed-paste escape sequences when the receiving app requests them — LFs pass through literally and the full multi-line prompt arrives as a single paste event. 1 new source-level regression test in `test/tmux.test.js`; 1510 total tests passing.
- **CLAUDE.md generator strips Project Version Recording section on every boot (#77)** — The `Project Version Recording` section added in PR #64 was getting silently wiped from every project's CLAUDE.md on each TangleClaw boot. Root cause: `_generateClaudeMd()` in `lib/engines.js` composes CLAUDE.md from guide files in `data/`, but no `project-version-recording-guide.md` existed, so the section was never emitted by the generator. Same gap existed for the `GEMINI.md`, `.codex.yaml`, and `.aider.conf.yml` generators. Fix: added `data/project-version-recording-guide.md` with the canonical section body; extended `_getRulesContent()` to read it into a new `projectVersionGuide` field; wired it into all four generators (`_generateClaudeMd`, `_generateGeminiMd`, `_generateCodexYaml`, `_generateAiderConf`) so the section is preserved on every config regeneration. Behavior (prime-prompt injection in `lib/sessions.js`) was unaffected — this only fixes the static documentation drift.
- **Setup wizard scan includes all directories** — `POST /api/setup/scan` previously required at least one project marker (methodology, git, or TangleClaw config) to include a directory; plain folders were silently skipped, causing new users to miss legitimate projects; scan now returns all top-level directories with a `detected` flag — directories with recognized markers (including new common project files: `package.json`, `Cargo.toml`, `pyproject.toml`, `go.mod`, `Makefile`, etc.) are pre-selected; unrecognized directories appear in a collapsed "Other directories" section that users can expand and opt into; 2 new tests, 1426 total passing (fixes #63)
- **Fix setup wizard logo SVG not rendering** — Welcome step inline SVG used `var(--primary)` CSS custom properties which aren't resolved when the setup page loads before the theme stylesheet is applied; replaced with hardcoded `#8BC34A` hex values (fixes #60)
- **Fix OpenClaw falsely detected as available in setup wizard** — `openclaw.json` used `"strategy": "which", "target": "ssh"` which matched on every machine since ssh is ubiquitous; OpenClaw is a remote engine requiring explicit configuration, so detection is now `null` — the base profile correctly shows as unavailable, while configured OpenClaw connections still appear as virtual engines with `available: true` (fixes #60)

### Changed

- **Consolidate frontend `api()` / `apiMutate()` helper into a shared module (#82)** — The three near-identical `api()` definitions in `public/landing.js`, `public/session.js`, and `public/openclaw-view.js` (touched together by #80 / PR #84) now bind from a single source of truth. New `public/api-helper.js` exposes `window.tcCreateApi({ setConnected? })` and `window.tcCreateApiMutate(api)` factory functions; the helper script tag is loaded before each page script in `public/index.html`, `public/session.html`, and `public/openclaw-view.html`. Each page script replaces its ~45-line `api`/`apiMutate` block with a one-line factory call (`const api = window.tcCreateApi({ setConnected }); const apiMutate = window.tcCreateApiMutate(api);` — openclaw-view omits the `setConnected` hook since it has no connection banner). All 89 existing call sites in `ui.js`, `setup.js`, `session.js`, `landing.js`, and `openclaw-view.js` work unchanged because `api` and `apiMutate` remain page-level globals with the same signatures and the same `lastError` / `lastErrorCode` side-channel introduced in #80. One intentional console-only change: openclaw-view's network-error path now logs `'Connection lost.'` like the other two pages instead of the raw `err.message`; openclaw-view never reads `api.lastError`, so this is invisible to users (string normalization for parity, not a UX change). `test/frontend-api-errors.test.js` rewritten to load `public/api-helper.js` once via `vm.runInContext` and exercise both factory bindings (with/without `setConnected`) instead of regex-extracting `api()` per file — net +1 test in that file (16 vs 15) covering the no-`setConnected` branch, `apiMutate` factory, and the `window`-export shape. One structural test in `test/session-wrapper.test.js` updated to assert binding from `window.tcCreateApi` instead of grepping for `async function api(`. Independent Critic flagged 1 BLOCKER (this CHANGELOG entry, now added) and 2 MINORs (overstated framing in code comment — fixed; pre-existing `lastError` parity-preserving leakage between calls — accepted and deferred to #83 follow-up). 1528 total tests passing (was 1527).

### Added

- **Launch mode selector** — When launching a session with an engine that defines `launchModes` (currently Claude Code), a modal picker appears offering permission modes: Interactive (default), Accept Edits, Plan Only, Auto (full autonomy), and Bypass (containers only, with warning). The selected mode's args are appended to the engine's launch command. Launch mode is recorded in the session DB (`launch_mode` column, schema v13) and returned in the API response. Engines without `launchModes` launch directly as before. New `launchModes` and `defaultLaunchMode` fields on engine profiles, exposed through `listWithAvailability()` to the frontend. 5 new tests (4 `_buildLaunchCommand` mode tests + 1 `listWithAvailability` launchModes assertion), 1429 total passing (fixes #25)
- **Update-available notification pill** — Landing page banner now shows a small pill when a newer version is available (e.g., "v3.13.0 available"); fetches `GET /api/update-status` (backend already existed via `lib/update-checker.js`) on page load; dismissable via X button with localStorage persistence keyed by version so it reappears for the next update but not the same one; styled to match existing banner chrome (fixes #62)

- **Document project version convention (#55, chunk 3)** — Added "Project Version Recording" section to CLAUDE.md global rules documenting the `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt` convention: file format, when to write (session start + wrap), detection order, and how TangleClaw reads it. Doc parity sweep confirmed no stale references in README or user-guide — existing "version badge" references are generic and still accurate. Completes #55.
- **Session-lifecycle version recording (#55, chunk 2)** — The engine-agnostic prime prompt now includes a "Project Version Recording" section instructing the AI to detect the project's current version at session start and write it to `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt`. The wrap protocol also includes a re-record step so the version is updated if it changed during the session (e.g., CHANGELOG bump or git tag). Both injections are methodology-agnostic — they apply to every methodology (prawduct, minimal, custom). This completes the write side of the version detection chain from chunk 1: the AI now populates the cache file that `enrichProject()` reads as its highest-priority source. 5 new tests (prime prompt section presence for both methodologies, wrap command version instruction for both methodologies, custom-command wrap branch coverage — added after Independent Critic review). 1424 total tests passing.
- **Harden #55 chunk 1 detection helpers (Critic follow-ups)** — Post-merge Independent Critic review of PR #57 surfaced several edge cases. All addressed: (1) UTF-8 BOM now stripped at the read boundary via a new `_readTextFileNoBom()` helper so files exported from Windows or certain editors don't break anchored regexes or `JSON.parse`; (2) CRLF line endings normalized to LF in the same helper so per-line regexes don't have to account for trailing `\r`; (3) `_readVersionJsonVersion` and `_readPackageJsonVersion` now require `typeof data.version === 'string'` AND a non-empty trimmed value, defensively rejecting `{"version": 123}`, `{"version": {}}`, and whitespace-only strings; (4) `_readVersionCacheFile` rejects whitespace-only version values (`version:    ` now correctly falls through to the next layer); (5) JSDoc drift fixed — cache file comment now says "Will be written" instead of implying a writer that doesn't exist yet; (6) redundant trailing `|| null` removed from the detection chain (dead code). 11 new tests covering BOM handling (all 4 readers), CRLF, non-string version field (number and object), missing/malformed version.json, whitespace-only cache value, and a dedicated layer-4 symmetry test. Live smoke-tested on the running server — Notse still returns `0.3.0` from CHANGELOG after the refactor. 1419 total tests passing.
- **Universal project version detection chain (#55, chunk 1)** — `enrichProject()` now detects the project's current version using a layered fallback chain instead of only reading root `package.json`. Order: (1) `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt` cache file (AI-recorded, highest priority — will be written by the session-lifecycle hook in chunk 2), (2) `CHANGELOG.md` first non-`[Unreleased]` version header (Keep-a-Changelog format), (3) `version.json` at root (TangleClaw convention), (4) `package.json` at root (existing logic, now layer 4), (5) `null`. Five new helper functions exposed on `projects` for unit testing: `_detectProjectVersion`, `_readVersionCacheFile`, `_readChangelogVersion`, `_readVersionJsonVersion`, `_readPackageJsonVersion`. CHANGELOG regex enforces version shape (`^v?\d+\.\d+`) so date-style headers like `## [2026-03-31]` are correctly rejected (some projects use date headers that would otherwise leak in as fake versions). Live impact on current projects: Notse now shows `0.3.0`, TangleClaw-v3 shows `3.12.7`, and projects with both CHANGELOG and package.json (OnDeck-V2, ScrapeGoat) now correctly prefer the more recent CHANGELOG entry. 14 new tests.
- **`tmux.js` regression-prevention test coverage** — `lib/tmux.js` previously had only structural tests (validation, error cases, history-limit). Added behavioral tests for the functions that physically deliver prompts to engines, where regressions silently break user experience: `sendKeys()` round-trip via real tmux sessions (text delivery, `enter:false` behavior, single-quote preservation, special shell characters `$` `` ` `` `\`, large >4KB multi-line payloads — covers the original 3.11.0 regression that motivated #23), `sendRawKey()` (behavioral Enter delivery + missing-session error case), and `killSession()` success path (return value + session removal); 9 new tests, 40 total in `test/tmux.test.js` (closes #23)

### Changed

- **Slimmer UI chrome across all pages** — Reduced vertical space consumed by headers, toolbars, and action buttons across the session banner, OpenClaw wrapper, and landing page; banner buttons shrunk from 44px to 30px (26px on desktop), back button from 44px to 32px, landing `.btn` from 44px to 32px, dash-bar and toolbar padding tightened, card rows from 44px to 34px min-height, logo and font sizes reduced proportionally; no functionality removed — same controls, just denser (fixes #51)

### Fixed

- **Session banner shows TangleClaw version instead of project version** — `loadVersion()` was fetching `/api/version` (TangleClaw's own version); now reads the project's `version` field from `enrichProject()`, which parses the project's `package.json`; projects without a `package.json` or version field show no version badge; 4 new tests (fixes #53)
- **Tmux status bar shows raw session internals** — Status bar previously showed bare `#{session_name}` (e.g. `TangleClaw-v3`) which was easily confused with the project name; now shows literal `TangleClaw` label on the left and `HH:MM  YYYY-MM-DD` on the right; canonical config moved to `deploy/tmux.conf` and installed to `~/.tmux.conf` by `deploy/install.sh` with backup of any existing file; install.sh also reloads tmux config in any running server so existing sessions update without restart; per-session `set-option` calls in `lib/tmux.js` updated to match (covers systems where the global config differs); 6-digit hex required by tmux 3.6+ (`#777` → `#777777`, `#333` → `#333333`); 2 new tests (fixes #53)

- **Status pill misses short incidents** — `_parseAtlassian()` only checked component status, which can revert to `operational` before the next poll; now also parses the `incidents[]` array from the Atlassian summary response and checks for unresolved incidents affecting the target component; uses the worse of component status vs. active incident impact; new `_parseAtlassianIncidents()` and `_incidentAffectsComponent()` helpers with component matching by ID and name; 10 new tests

## [3.12.7] - 2026-04-05

### Fixed

- **Orphan bare shell after session ends** — `ttyd-attach.sh` used `tmux new-session -A` which silently creates a new bare shell when the engine session is gone (wrap, kill, or crash); the orphan shell had no working directory (cwd `/`), inherited ttyd's restrictive launchd resource limits (`NumberOfFiles: 4096`), triggered `.zshrc` ulimit errors, and confused TangleClaw's `hasSession()` state tracking; replaced with `tmux has-session` guard + `tmux attach-session` so the script only attaches to existing sessions and shows a "session not running" message when the session is gone; 4 new tests (fixes #47)
- **Session launch feels frozen for ~6 seconds** — `launchSession()` blocked the API response while doing synchronous sleeps for `preKeyDelay` (3s), preKeys (1s), and `startupDelay` (2s); moved preKey and prime prompt injection to background timers via `_deferEngineInit()` so the API returns immediately after creating the tmux session; frontend launch button now shows "Launching…" with disabled state for instant visual feedback; user sees the terminal loading while the engine boots in the background
- **Codex sessions crash immediately on launch** — live engine profiles at `~/.tangleclaw/engines/` were never updated when bundled profiles gained new fields (e.g. `preKeys`, `preKeyDelay`, `startupDelay`); without `preKeys` the trust dialog wasn't dismissed, so the prime prompt injection selected "No, quit" and Codex exited; `_copyBundledFiles()` now deep-merges missing fields from bundled profiles into existing ones without overwriting user customizations; 4 new tests (fixes #47)

## [3.12.6] - 2026-04-05

### Fixed

- **Peek not working for alternate-screen engines (Codex, etc.)** — TUI-based engines like Codex run in tmux's alternate screen buffer, which has no scrollback history; `capture-pane -S - -E -` could fail or return empty content for these panes; `capturePane()` now detects alternate screen mode via `#{alternate_on}` and falls back to visible-only capture; new `isAlternateScreen()` helper in `tmux.js`; peek API response includes `alternateScreen` flag; frontend shows informational notice when peek content is screen-only (no scrollback); 4 new tests (fixes #44)

## [3.12.5] - 2026-04-05

### Added

- **Project archive/unarchive** — Projects can be archived (deactivated) from the landing page; archived projects are skipped by `syncAllProjects()` on boot, hidden from the main project list, and blocked from session launch; archived projects appear in a collapsed section at the bottom of the landing page with an "Unarchive" button; new API endpoints `POST /api/projects/:name/archive` and `POST /api/projects/:name/unarchive`; `store.projects.unarchive()` added; `listAllProjects()` excludes archived projects from the unregistered filesystem scan; 10 new tests (fixes #42)
- **Attach confirmation dialog** — Clicking "Attach" on an unregistered project card now shows a confirmation modal explaining what will happen (scaffold config, generate engine files, sync on boot) before registering the project; prevents accidental project registration

### Fixed

- **Session launch blocked for archived projects** — `launchSession()` now returns an error if the project is archived, with a message to unarchive first

## [3.12.4] - 2026-04-04

### Changed

- **Slim session prime prompt** — Removed full methodology playbook from the prime prompt injected into the terminal at session start; the playbook is already in the engine config (CLAUDE.md) which the AI reads automatically; prime prompt now shows only: session header, methodology name, current phase, last session summary, active learnings, and extension rules — reducing terminal output from ~50+ lines to ~10-15 lines (fixes #40)

## [3.12.3] - 2026-04-04

### Fixed

- **Wrap button completes wrap but doesn't kill session or clear banner** — Wrap completion relied solely on idle detection (3 consecutive polls with stable terminal output), which could fail silently if captured output fluctuated; added server-side wrap timeout (120s) that force-completes wrapping sessions via `getSessionStatus`; added frontend fallback timeout (120s) in `showWrappingState()`; guarded `completeWrapFromIdle()` against re-entry with `wrapCompleting` flag; all timeouts cleaned up in `handleWrapCompleted` and `handleSessionEnded`; 6 new tests (fixes #28)

## [3.12.2] - 2026-04-04

### Added

- **Session Memory** — File-based, per-project memory system that persists context across AI sessions; `.tangleclaw/memories/MEMORY.md` created automatically on project init; session memory guide injected into all engine configs (Claude, Codex, Aider, Gemini) telling the AI to read and update memory files; engine-agnostic — works with any AI that can read files and follow instructions; 4 new tests (fixes #36)
- **Startup project sync** — `syncAllProjects()` runs on every server boot: regenerates all engine configs and backfills scaffolding (like `.tangleclaw/memories/`) for existing projects; ensures code changes (new guides, updated rules) are reflected immediately across all projects without waiting for session relaunch; 3 new tests

## [3.12.1] - 2026-04-04

### Added

- **Peek search** — Search bar in peek drawer with live case-insensitive matching, match highlighting (`<mark>` spans), next/prev navigation (buttons + Enter/Shift+Enter), match counter ("3 of 42"), Cmd/Ctrl+F keyboard shortcut when peek is open, Escape to close; performance-guarded rendering limits DOM highlights to 1000 around the active match for large buffers; 4 new tests

### Fixed

- **Session wrap notes not picked up by next session** — Added "Session Start" section to Prawduct playbook instructing agents to glob for all `build-plan*.md` files (not just `build-plan.md`) and surface incomplete chunks; updated wrap instructions to specify updating build plan files with ✅/⬜ markers as the handoff mechanism; 2 new regression tests (fixes #33)

## [3.12.0] - 2026-04-04

### Added

- **Full scrollback peek** — Peek drawer now shows the entire terminal scrollback history instead of the last 50 lines; tmux sessions are created with `history-limit 50000`; `capturePane()` supports `full: true` for full buffer capture (`-S - -E -`); peek API accepts `full=true` query param; frontend strips ANSI escape codes, auto-scrolls to bottom, supports sticky scroll (unlocks on scroll-up, re-locks at bottom), and has Jump to Top/Bottom buttons (fixes #26)

### Fixed

- **Light mode only changes splash screen, not terminal shell** — `applyTheme()` in `session.js` now propagates theme colors to the xterm.js terminal instance inside the ttyd iframe via `term.options.theme`; added xterm theme palettes for dark, light, and high-contrast modes; terminal theme is applied on iframe load (with retry for async xterm init) and on theme change; `.terminal-frame` background changed from hardcoded `#000` to `var(--bg)` (fixes #30)

## [3.11.5] - 2026-04-03

### Fixed

- **Prime prompt pastes but doesn't submit on session start** — `sendKeys()` now uses tmux `load-buffer`/`paste-buffer` for reliable delivery of large text (properly triggers bracketed paste mode), with a 500ms delay before sending Enter to let the terminal process the paste; the previous `send-keys -l` approach sent characters too fast for Claude Code to process before Enter arrived

## [3.11.4] - 2026-04-03

### Fixed

- **Kill button shows generic "Check password" instead of actual error** — session view's `confirmKill()` used `apiMutate()` which swallowed server error messages and showed a hardcoded string; now uses direct `fetch` (matching the landing page pattern) to display the actual error from the server (e.g. "Password required" vs "Incorrect password")

## [3.11.3] - 2026-04-03

### Fixed

- **Methodology playbook missing from engine config files** — `_generateClaudeMd`, `_generateCodexYaml`, `_generateAiderConf`, and `_generateGeminiMd` now inject the full playbook content (not just methodology name and description), matching what `generatePrimePrompt()` already does
- **Bundled template sync skips new files in existing directories** — `_copyBundledTemplates()` now syncs missing files into existing template directories instead of skipping the entire directory; this fixes the case where `playbook.md` was added to bundled templates but never copied to installations that already had the template directory
- **`getPlaybook()` falls back to bundled templates** — if a playbook is missing from the user's `~/.tangleclaw/templates/` directory, it now checks the bundled `data/templates/` directory as a fallback, ensuring playbook injection works reliably even before the sync runs
- 7 new tests: playbook injection for Claude/Gemini/Codex/Aider generators and cross-engine parity

## [3.11.2] - 2026-04-02

### Fixed

- **Polling burst storm on tab refocus crashes system** — replaced all `setInterval` polling in `session.js`, `openclaw-view.js`, and `landing.js` with `setTimeout` chains that don't queue callbacks when browser tabs are backgrounded; added `visibilitychange` listener to pause/resume session page polling when tabs are hidden/shown. Previously, backgrounding a session tab for ~60s caused ~35 queued interval callbacks to fire simultaneously on refocus, hammering the server with rapid tmux shell commands and overwhelming the system (fixes #19)

## [3.11.1] - 2026-04-02

### Fixed

- **Prime prompt no longer fires before Claude engine is ready** — added explicit `startupDelay: 2000` to Claude engine profile, bumped default fallback from 500ms to 1500ms (fixes #17)

## [3.11.0] - 2026-04-02

### Added

- **Methodology playbook injection in prime prompt** — `generatePrimePrompt()` now reads and injects `playbook.md` from methodology template directories, giving engines full operational procedures instead of just the methodology name and phase labels (fixes #14)
- **Extension rule definitions in prime prompt** — `defaultRules` in `template.json` now supports object form with `enabled` and `definition` fields; active rules are rendered with their definitions in the prime prompt
- **Prawduct playbook** — new `data/templates/prawduct/playbook.md` covering session discipline (one chunk per session), phase procedures (Discovery/Planning/Building), Independent Critic review protocol, Janitor Pass, and Decision Framework
- **Prawduct rule definitions** — `independentCritic`, `docsParity`, and `decisionFramework` now include concrete definitions explaining what each rule requires in practice
- 7 new tests: store `getPlaybook` (3), prime prompt playbook injection (2), rule definitions (2)
